# Rounds 9-15 — consolidated bug findings (review-only scan)

> Read-only multi-agent review. NO code changes made. Each finding is post-adversarial-verification (confirmed = held after a skeptic tried to refute it).


## Round 9 — obligations / case-banks / case-expenses

**raw 29 -> confirmed 27 / refuted 2  (High 2, Medium 7, Low 18)**

### High (2)

#### `CE-authz-1` — case_expenses INSERT/UPDATE RLS + soft-delete RPC use the LEGACY authz pattern — associated advisors are locked out of every expense write
- **File:** supabase/migrations/081_case_expenses.sql:58-94 (case_expenses_insert / case_expenses_update WITH CHECK) and :114-128 (soft_delete_case_expense RPC)
- **Evidence:** All three DB write paths gate on the pre-associated-advisor check: insert/update RLS use `(public.has_permission('edit_any_case') OR c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())`, and soft_delete_case_expense uses `public.has_permission('edit_any_case') OR (public.has_permission('edit_own_case') AND c.assigned_advisor_id = v_actor)`. No migration after 081 re-points these at the canonical guard — migration 190 explicitly canonicalized borrowers/incomes/obligations onto can_edit_case/_assert_can_edit_case but did NOT include case_expenses, and 147 only widened cases_select/cases_update/can_view_case/can_edit_case/_assert_can_edit_case (not the expense-specific policies/RPC). Meanwhile every server action (create-empty-expense.ts:21, update-expense-field.ts:54, remove-expense-receipt.ts:29, upload-expense-receipt.ts:62, delete-expense.ts:21) authorizes with `userCanEditCase` (canonical, INCLUDES associated advisors). The writes then run through the USER client (subject to the legacy RLS) or call the legacy RPC.
- **Why it matters:** An associated advisor (case_associated_advisors, mig 146/147 — a shipped role) holds edit_own_case but is NOT the assigned_advisor_id, so can_edit_case returns true. The server gate passes and the UI (canEdit threaded everywhere) shows add/edit/delete/upload affordances, but the actual DB write is silently filtered by the legacy RLS / rejected by the RPC. Result: the associated advisor can edit the case, its borrowers, incomes and obligations (all canonicalized) yet CANNOT add, edit, attach a receipt to, or delete an expense — exactly the bug class migration 190's header calls out as 'EXCLUDES an associated advisor who legitimately has can_edit_case'. This is an authz-gap + a C-036 inverse violation (affordances shown that fail at the server). UPDATE/INSERT fail silently (RLS no-op); delete returns generic 'unauthorized'.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a migration mirroring 190 for case_expenses: re-create case_expenses_insert / case_expenses_update to gate on `public.can_edit_case(case_id)` (which already encapsulates edit_any OR edit_own AND assigned/associated + case-not-deleted), and re-create soft_delete_case_expense to `PERFORM public._assert_can_edit_case(p_case_id)` instead of the inline assigned_advisor_id check. Safe-by-construction (superset of the legacy check). Self-register in schema_version.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. Migration 081 is the ONLY file defining the case_expenses write paths (Grep for case_expenses_insert|case_expenses_update|soft_delete_case_expense returns only 081). All three use the legacy pre-associated-advisor check: case_expenses_insert WITH CHECK (081:68) = `has_permission('edit_any_case') OR c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid()`; case_expenses_update USING+WITH CHECK (081:83,92) = same; soft_delete_case_expense RPC (081:122-125) = `has_permission('edit_any_case') OR (has_permission('edit_own_case') AND c.assigned_advisor_id = v_actor)`. None reference is_case_associated_advisor / can_edit_case.

Migration 190 (read in full) canonicalizes ONLY update_borrower_in_case, save_borrower_for_case_full, add_empty_borrower_to_case, soft_delete_borrower_income/obligation, and the borrower_incomes/obligations INSERT+UPDATE policies onto can_edit_case/_assert_can_edit_case — case_expenses is absent. Migration 147 widened only cases_select/cases_update/can_view_case/can_edit_case/_assert_can_edit_case (147:23-131), and these helpers DO include associated advisors via is_case_associated_advisor. Migration 146 confirms associated advisors are a real shipped role with view+edit, holding edit_own_case but NOT being assigned_advisor_id — so can_edit_case returns true for them while the legacy `assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid()` check returns false.

All five server actions gate on userCanEditCase (permissions.ts:102-122 delegates to the can_edit_case RPC = canonical, includes associated advisors): create-empty-expense.ts:21 then INSERTs via the user client (subject to legacy case_expenses_insert RLS); update-expense-field.ts:54 UPDATEs via user client (legacy case_expenses_update RLS); delete-expense.ts:25 calls the legacy soft_delete_case_expense RPC; upload-expense-receipt.ts:62 uploads the blob via the admin client but writes the row pointer via the USER client (104-116, explicitly commented "user client -> case_expenses RLS"); remove-expense-receipt.ts:29 clears the pointer via user client (45-57). Net: an associated advisor sees every add/edit/delete/upload affordance (UI threads canEdit from userCanEditCase, C-036), passes the server gate, but the DB write is silently RLS-filtered (INSERT/UPDATE no-op, no error) or RPC-rejected (delete returns generic unauthorized). This is exactly the authz gap + C-036 inverse violation migration 190's own header names ("EXCLUDES an associated advisor who legitimately has can_edit_case"). One refinement (strengthens, not refutes): upload/remove receipt actions return ok:true on the silently-no-op'd user-client UPDATE — a false success. Severity High is correct: shipped-role authz gap with affordances that silently fail server-side. Suggested fix (mirror 190 for case_expenses: re-point the two policies at can_edit_case and the RPC at _assert_can_edit_case) is safe-by-construction (superset of legacy check).

#### `R-cb-authz-1` — case_banks write RLS uses the LEGACY guard — excludes associated advisors (canonicalization invariant violation)
- **File:** supabase/migrations/024_rls_layer2_and_constraints.sql:88-125 (case_banks_insert / case_banks_update); set_primary_bank is SECURITY INVOKER so it inherits these (supabase/migrations/118_set_primary_bank_no_delete.sql:25)
- **Evidence:** case_banks_insert / case_banks_update WITH CHECK/USING = `public.has_permission('edit_any_case') OR (public.has_permission('edit_own_case') AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())`. Migration 190 canonicalized borrower_incomes/borrower_obligations + borrower RPCs onto public.can_edit_case but did NOT re-point case_banks. No migration after 024 re-creates these policies (grep for CREATE POLICY "case_banks_insert/update" returns only 022+024).
- **Why it matters:** This is exactly the legacy pattern the project invariant flags as a bug: `assigned_advisor_id = actor OR edit_any_case` EXCLUDES associated advisors. An associated advisor (case_associated_advisors, mig 146/147) passes the server-action userCanEditCase gate — which delegates to can_edit_case (superset incl. associated) — but is then silently rejected at the case_banks RLS layer for add/edit/delete/set-primary. The UI surfaces a generic 'saveFailed'/'unknown' with no recovery: a legitimate role cannot manage banks on a case they can otherwise fully edit (broken core flow). Server gate and DB authority disagree.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a migration re-pointing case_banks_insert and case_banks_update at public.can_edit_case(case_id) (mirror migration 190's incomes/obligations policy rewrite, which already encapsulates edit_any OR edit_own AND (assigned OR associated) + the not-deleted check). Soft-delete already rides on case_banks_update, so it is covered by the same fix. Re-run the two-advisor verification with an ASSOCIATED advisor.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. (1) case_banks_insert/case_banks_update in migrations/024 (lines 88-125) use the LEGACY guard `has_permission('edit_any_case') OR (has_permission('edit_own_case') AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())` — no associated-advisor branch. (2) grep for CREATE POLICY "case_banks_insert"/"case_banks_update" returns ONLY migrations 022 and 024; migration 039 (the only later policy edit) re-creates just case_banks_SELECT. No migration after 024 re-points the write policies. (3) Migration 190 (read in full) canonicalizes borrower_incomes/borrower_obligations INSERT+UPDATE onto public.can_edit_case and re-points the borrower RPCs onto _assert_can_edit_case, but never touches case_banks — exactly as the finding states. (4) can_edit_case (mig 147 lines 81-101) IS the superset: edit_any OR (edit_own AND (assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid() OR is_case_associated_advisor(c.id))). (5) set_primary_bank is SECURITY INVOKER (mig 118 line 25) with no DELETE on case_banks, so it inherits the legacy policies. (6) Server/DB disagreement is concrete: addCaseBankAction, updateCaseBankFieldAction, save-case-bank, delete-case-bank all gate on userCanEditCase (permissions.ts:102-122 → delegates to the can_edit_case RPC, the associated-inclusive superset) and then write DIRECTLY to from('case_banks') via createClient() (server.ts: ANON key + session cookies = RLS-enforced user client, not admin). So an associated advisor with edit_own_case passes the server gate, then the case_banks legacy RLS silently rejects insert/update/soft-delete/reactivate/set-primary; UI returns generic 'unknown'/'already-failed' with no recovery. This is the same canonicalization-invariant violation that migration 190 fixed for incomes/obligations, left un-fixed for case_banks. Severity: it is over-restrictive (denies a permitted role), not a privilege escalation or data leak, but it fully breaks a core edit flow for a legitimate role with no UI recovery — matching the High treatment this codebase gave the identical legacy-guard class in the R8/mig-190 fix. Suggested fix (re-point both policies at can_edit_case, mirroring mig 190) is correct and covers soft-delete since it rides on case_banks_update.

### Medium (7)

#### `R9-obl-1` — Inline obligation cells are editable for view-only users (C-036 UI edit-gate violation)
- **File:** src/features/obligations/components/obligation-table-row.tsx:33-85, 94-228; src/features/obligations/components/case-obligations-client.tsx:109-138,211-219
- **Evidence:** ObligationTableRow receives `canEdit` but only uses it to gate the delete button (line 70 `{canEdit && (...Trash2...)}`). The editable cells (TextCell/NumberCell/DateCell) take NO canEdit/disabled/readOnly prop and always render live `<input>`s wired to `onSaveField`. CaseObligationsClient.saveField is always passed to every row (`onSaveField={(field, value) => saveField(ob.id, field, value)}`) regardless of canEdit; only `canAdd = canEdit && primaryBorrowerId !== null` gates the Add button.
- **Why it matters:** A user who can view a case but not edit it (e.g. secretary with view_all on an unassigned case, the exact persona contract C-036 was written for) sees fully interactive loan-amount / monthly-payment / end-date / months / lender inputs. Typing + blur fires updateObligationFieldAction, which correctly rejects at the server (userCanEditCase + RLS), but the UI shows edit affordances that silently fail — the precise pattern Round 6's C-036 invariant bans. Incomes/banks/expenses thread a read-only gate into their cells; obligations does not.
- **Suggested fix:** Thread `canEdit` into ObligationTableRow's Cell editors and render read-only (disabled input or plain text) when false — mirror the case-banks/incomes read-only cell treatment. At minimum pass `disabled={!canEdit}` to each input in TextCell/NumberCell/DateCell and skip onSave when not editable.
- **Verify:** Core finding CONFIRMED by reading the code. obligation-table-row.tsx:39-68 — the inline Cell editors (TextCell/NumberCell/DateCell, defined lines 94-228) take no canEdit/disabled/readOnly prop and always render live <input>s wired to onSaveField; canEdit is used only to gate the delete button (line 70 `{canEdit && (...Trash2...)}`). case-obligations-client.tsx:211-219 passes onSaveField to every row unconditionally; only canAdd (line 70: `canEdit && primaryBorrowerId !== null`) is gated. case-obligations-block.tsx:26-29,63 computes canEdit=userCanEditCase(caseId) and canView=view_case_obligations, so a view-only persona (secretary with view_case_obligations but no edit rights on an unassigned case) renders the block with canEdit=false yet sees fully interactive cells. The edits silently fail server-side: update-obligation-field.ts:67 calls `if (!(await userCanEditCase(caseId))) return {ok:false,error:'unauthorized'}`, and userCanEditCase (permissions.ts:102-122) delegates to the can_edit_case RPC (mig 147) which returns false for view-only — exactly the C-036/R6-inline-actions-1 silent-fail-affordance pattern. ROUND-06-HANDOFF.md:117 explicitly lists 'Incomes / obligations blocks still render edit controls for view-only users' as a known deferred gap, corroborating the finding.\n\nONE reviewer claim is INACCURATE but does not invalidate the finding: 'Incomes/banks/expenses thread a read-only gate into their cells; obligations does not.' Only banks actually threads it (case-bank-inline-row.tsx:68 `disabled={!canEdit}` on the banker_name input). Incomes does NOT — income-row.tsx:109-145 never passes canEdit to EditableField, so EditableField's canEdit defaults to true (editable-field.tsx:16) and renders editable controls. Expenses does NOT — case-expense-row.tsx cells receive no canEdit (only the delete button + ExpenseReceiptCell are gated). So obligations is not uniquely broken; expenses and incomes share the identical gap. The comparison is the only over-stated part; the actual obligations defect is exactly as described.\n\nSeverity Medium is correctly calibrated: same family as R6-inline-actions-1 (Medium) and R8-routes-crosscut-1 (Medium); no unauthorized data write occurs (server + RLS reject), so not High, but it is a genuine violation of the established C-036 UI-edit-gate invariant, so not Low.

#### `CB-authz-1` — case_banks INSERT/UPDATE RLS still uses the legacy guard — excludes associated advisors (not canonicalized on can_edit_case)
- **File:** supabase/migrations/024_rls_layer2_and_constraints.sql:88-125 (latest case_banks_insert/case_banks_update definition); contrast supabase/migrations/190_canonical_can_edit_case_borrower_income_writes.sql
- **Evidence:** case_banks_insert / case_banks_update both gate on:
  public.has_permission('edit_any_case')
  OR (public.has_permission('edit_own_case') AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())
This is the exact LEGACY pattern the project invariant flags as a bug (it predates associated advisors, mig 146/147). Migration 190 re-pointed borrowers/incomes/obligations at public.can_edit_case, and 179 fixed case_properties, but NO migration re-points case_banks. grep for can_edit_case across migrations returns 146,147,179,182,190,123,106,099,065 — case_banks is absent.
- **Why it matters:** An associated advisor (case_associated_advisors, mig 146) legitimately passes userCanEditCase / can_edit_case (which the canonical RPC grants), so all 5 server actions let them through the app-layer check. But the actual DB write then hits these legacy RLS policies which only recognize the *responsible* advisor (assigned_advisor_id) — so the write is silently denied. Net effect: an associated advisor who can edit the rest of the case (borrowers, incomes, obligations, case fields) CANNOT add / edit / delete / set-primary banks. The set_primary_bank RPC is SECURITY INVOKER (mig 118), so it inherits the same legacy policy and fails too. This is an authz inconsistency / broken core flow for associated advisors and the same class of bug R8 fixed everywhere else.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a migration that DROP+CREATE case_banks_insert and case_banks_update using public.can_edit_case(case_id) as the WITH CHECK / USING predicate (mirroring mig 190's income/obligation policies). This widens to associated advisors + admins exactly as elsewhere and never grants a user who lacked edit authority. Verify the two-advisor test as an associated advisor.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code end-to-end.

1. case_banks_insert/case_banks_update (024_rls_layer2_and_constraints.sql:88-125) use the legacy guard verbatim: `public.has_permission('edit_any_case') OR (public.has_permission('edit_own_case') AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())`. No associated-advisor branch.

2. can_edit_case (147_associated_advisor_case_access.sql:81-101) is a strict superset: it adds `OR public.is_case_associated_advisor(c.id)`. So an associated advisor passes can_edit_case but FAILS the legacy case_banks predicate (which only matches assigned_advisor_id).

3. App-layer userCanEditCase (src/lib/auth/permissions.ts:110-121) delegates to the can_edit_case RPC — its own docstring says it does so precisely so it "doesn't drift... which previously over-denied associated advisors."

4. Both case-bank server actions gate on userCanEditCase: addCaseBankAction (src/features/case-banks/actions/add-case-bank.ts:27) and setPrimaryBankAction (set-primary-bank.ts:25). Both then issue a direct case_banks write / RPC that hits the legacy RLS.

5. set_primary_bank is SECURITY INVOKER (118_set_primary_bank_no_delete.sql:25), and set-primary-bank.ts:22-24 explicitly comments "the RPC is SECURITY INVOKER... so case_banks RLS still applies underneath" — so it inherits the legacy guard and also fails for associated advisors.

6. Migration 190 re-pointed borrower_incomes/borrower_obligations INSERT+UPDATE policies and the borrower RPCs at can_edit_case/_assert_can_edit_case, and 179 fixed case_properties — but a full grep of `case_banks_insert`/`case_banks_update` across migrations returns only 022 (created) and 024 (re-created legacy); no later migration re-points them. A grep of `can_edit_case` returns migs 065,099,106,123,146,147,179,182,190 — case_banks is absent from every one, matching the finding's claim exactly.

Net effect is exactly as described: an associated advisor who can edit the rest of the case (cases_update was widened in 147, and borrowers/incomes/obligations/properties in 179/190) is silently denied add/edit/set-primary on banks. This is the same class of legacy-guard bug R8 canonicalized elsewhere; the fix (DROP+CREATE case_banks_insert/update on public.can_edit_case) is correct and SAFE BY CONSTRUCTION (superset, never grants extra authority).

Severity adjusted High->Medium: the impact is a DENY (fail-closed) for a legitimately-authorized user — a broken core flow / authz inconsistency, not a privilege escalation or data exposure (no user gains access they shouldn't). This matches how the project graded the identical class in R6/R7 (Medium "broken core flow for associated advisors").

#### `CB-form-1` — saveCaseBankAction lets the is_primary checkbox be set directly, bypassing set_primary_bank — unchecking primary leaves the case with NO primary bank
- **File:** src/features/case-banks/actions/save-case-bank.ts:43-65; src/features/case-banks/components/case-bank-form.tsx:100-109; trigger in supabase/migrations/006_cases.sql:107-111
- **Evidence:** saveCaseBankAction writes payload = { ...parsed.data, ... } directly via INSERT/UPDATE, and parsed.data includes is_primary (CaseBankFormSchema has is_primary: boolFromForm). The single-primary trigger trg_case_banks_single_primary only fires WHEN (NEW.is_primary = TRUE) — it demotes OTHER rows when one is promoted, but does NOTHING when a row is set is_primary = FALSE. The domain whitelist comment (editable-case-bank-fields.ts:8-10) explicitly states is_primary must go through setPrimaryBankAction → set_primary_bank RPC 'so the trigger that demotes other primaries can run atomically', yet the form edit path bypasses that.
- **Why it matters:** On the /cases/[id]/banks/[bankId]/edit form, unchecking 'is_primary' on the current primary bank (or saving a non-primary edit while the previously-primary state flips) writes is_primary = FALSE with no compensating promotion, leaving the case with zero primary banks — a violation of the 'exactly one primary per case' invariant in the no-primary direction. uq_case_banks_one_primary only prevents TWO primaries, not zero. The case's dashboard 'primary bank' cell then renders empty until someone re-sets a primary.
- **Suggested fix:** Remove is_primary from the saveCaseBankAction write path (and from the form, or make the form route primary changes through setPrimaryBankAction). Promotion/demotion of the primary should only ever happen via the set_primary_bank RPC, consistent with the inline list and the documented rule.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the full chain. (1) CaseBankFormSchema includes `is_primary: boolFromForm` (case-bank.schema.ts:19). (2) saveCaseBankAction builds `payload = { case_id, ...parsed.data, updated_by }` and writes it directly via UPDATE (lines 52-57) or INSERT (61-63) with no filtering of is_primary (save-case-bank.ts:43-65). (3) The edit form renders the is_primary checkbox (case-bank-form.tsx:100-109), pre-checked when editing the current primary (isPrimaryDefault from initial.is_primary, lines 71-73), and is wired into the live route /cases/[id]/banks/[bankId]/edit which renders CaseBankForm with initial=caseBank (edit/page.tsx:54-60). (4) Unchecking the box omits the field from FormData (standard HTML); boolFromForm maps absent/empty/null/undefined to false (form-primitives.ts:189), so parsed.data.is_primary=false is written. (5) The compensating trigger ensure_single_primary_bank only demotes OTHER rows `IF NEW.is_primary = TRUE`, and trg_case_banks_single_primary fires `WHEN (NEW.is_primary = TRUE)` (006_cases.sql:96-111) — it does nothing on a demotion to FALSE, so no promotion occurs. I confirmed this trigger/function is never redefined in any later migration. (6) uq_case_banks_one_primary only prevents TWO primaries (`WHERE is_primary = TRUE AND deleted_at IS NULL`, mig 024:233-235); it permits ZERO. Result: unchecking is_primary on the current primary leaves the case with no primary bank, violating the one-primary invariant. The domain whitelist comment (editable-case-bank-fields.ts:8-10) explicitly states is_primary must go through setPrimaryBankAction -> set_primary_bank RPC (mig 021, which atomically clears+promotes) for exactly this reason, and the inline patch path (update-case-bank-field.ts via isEditableCaseBankField) correctly enforces that whitelist — so saveCaseBankAction is the documented-rule-violating outlier. Migration 190 (cross-referenced) only touches borrowers/incomes/obligations and is irrelevant here. Severity stays Medium: the action is gated by userCanEditCase (save-case-bank.ts:39), so this is a data-integrity/invariant break reachable by a legitimate editor via normal UI (empty primary-bank cell + inconsistent downstream consumers until a primary is re-set), not a privilege escalation. The reviewer's suggested fix (drop is_primary from the write path / route primary changes through setPrimaryBankAction) is correct and consistent with the existing inline-list design.

#### `CB-update-1` — updateCaseBankFieldAction returns ok:true even when 0 rows are affected (false success on wrong-case / soft-deleted / RLS-denied row)
- **File:** src/features/case-banks/actions/update-case-bank-field.ts:72-98
- **Evidence:** const { error } = await supabase.from('case_banks').update(patch).eq('id', caseBankId).eq('case_id', caseId).is('deleted_at', null);
if (error) { ... return {ok:false} }
// no .select() and no rowcount check → returns { ok: true } on 0 affected rows.
Contrast save-case-bank.ts:52-59 and delete-case-bank.ts:23-38, which both .select('id') and return 'unauthorized' when updated.length === 0.
- **Why it matters:** If the row doesn't match (caseBankId belongs to a different case than caseId, the row is soft-deleted, or — given CB-authz-1 — RLS silently filters the UPDATE for an associated advisor), the action reports success and the optimistic UI keeps the edited value while the DB never changed. The user believes a banker_name/phone/email edit saved when it did not. No data corruption (the .eq('case_id') scope prevents cross-case writes), but it's a silent-no-op correctness bug and inconsistent with the sibling actions.
- **Suggested fix:** Add .select('id') and treat 0 returned rows as a failure: if (!updated || updated.length === 0) return { ok: false, error: 'unauthorized' }; — matching save-case-bank and delete-case-bank.
- **Verify:** Confirmed against the code. updateCaseBankFieldAction (src/features/case-banks/actions/update-case-bank-field.ts:72-98) runs `.update(patch).eq('id',caseBankId).eq('case_id',caseId).is('deleted_at',null)` with NO .select() and NO rowcount check, then returns {ok:true} (line 98). On 0 affected rows with no DB error it reports false success. The sibling-inconsistency claim is accurate: save-case-bank.ts:52-59 does `.select('id')` and returns 'unauthorized' when updated.length===0; delete-case-bank.ts:33,38 does the same. The named action is the outlier.

The severity-driving "RLS silently filters for an associated advisor" path is REAL and live. userCanEditCase (src/lib/auth/permissions.ts:102-122) delegates to the can_edit_case RPC, which includes associated advisors (per its doc + migration 190). But the live case_banks_update RLS policy is still migration 024's LEGACY check (024:102-125): `edit_any_case OR (edit_own_case AND assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())` — no associated-advisor support. Migration 190 explicitly re-pointed borrowers/incomes/obligations to can_edit_case but did NOT touch case_banks; grep over all migrations confirms 024 is the last definition of case_banks_update (no later override). So an associated advisor with edit_own_case passes the action's gate, then RLS silently filters the UPDATE → 0 rows, no error → {ok:true}. The action whitelist (domain/editable-case-bank-fields.ts:12-17) covers banker_name/banker_phone/banker_email/bank_id, matching the finding.

The optimistic-UI consequence is confirmed: case-bank-inline-row.tsx:51-54 only toasts on !result.ok and keeps the local edited value on success, re-syncing from props only when the server row changes — which won't happen since the write was a no-op. No cross-case corruption (the .eq('case_id') scope holds), as the finding states. Medium is appropriate: a reachable silent-no-op correctness bug for a legitimate user persona with no error surfaced, but not a security/data-corruption issue. Suggested fix (add .select('id') + treat 0 rows as 'unauthorized', matching the siblings) is correct.

#### `R-ce-authz-1` — case_expenses write RLS + soft_delete_case_expense RPC use the LEGACY guard — excludes associated advisors
- **File:** supabase/migrations/081_case_expenses.sql:58-94 (case_expenses_insert / case_expenses_update) and :98-140 (soft_delete_case_expense RPC, SECURITY DEFINER)
- **Evidence:** Both policies and the RPC gate on `public.has_permission('edit_any_case') OR c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid()` (RPC line 122-125: `edit_any_case OR (edit_own_case AND c.assigned_advisor_id = v_actor)`). Migration 101 explicitly states 'No new RLS' and migration 190 did not touch case_expenses. Receipt upload/remove actions authorize with userCanEditCase (canonical) but then write through these legacy-guarded policies/RPC.
- **Why it matters:** Same canonicalization gap as case_banks: an associated advisor can edit the case (can_edit_case=true, passes every server action's userCanEditCase) but cannot create/edit/delete an expense, nor delete via soft_delete_case_expense — the RPC RAISEs 42501 and the inline cell shows a generic failure. The receipt-upload path also depends on the expense row resolving under the user client, so receipt attach can succeed while the row edit fails, producing inconsistent affordance behavior for the associated-advisor role. Legitimate role + broken core flow.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a migration re-pointing case_expenses_insert/update and soft_delete_case_expense at public.can_edit_case / public._assert_can_edit_case (drop the assigned_advisor_id branch and the redundant cases join), matching migration 190's pattern for incomes/obligations.
- **Verify:** Confirmed against the code. In supabase/migrations/081_case_expenses.sql the INSERT policy (lines 58-70) and UPDATE policy (lines 74-94) both gate on `public.has_permission('edit_any_case') OR c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid()`, and `soft_delete_case_expense` (SECURITY DEFINER, lines 98-140) gates on `edit_any_case OR (edit_own_case AND c.assigned_advisor_id = v_actor)` at lines 122-125 — the LEGACY guard with no associated-advisor branch. The canonical helpers in migration 147 (can_edit_case lines 81-101, _assert_can_edit_case lines 104-131) add `OR public.is_case_associated_advisor(c.id)`, making them a strict superset. Migration 190 re-pointed only borrower/income/obligation writes (verified: it contains zero case_expenses references); grep confirms soft_delete_case_expense and the case_expenses_insert/update policies are defined ONLY in 081 and never re-pointed. Migration 101 explicitly states 'No new RLS' and authorizes receipt upload via userCanEditCase (header comment lines 14-16). Application layer confirms the gap: create-empty-expense.ts (line 21), update-expense-field.ts (line 54), delete-expense.ts (line 21), and upload-expense-receipt.ts (line 62) all gate on userCanEditCase, which delegates to the canonical can_edit_case RPC (permissions.ts lines 102-122). So an associated advisor passes every server-action gate but is then blocked at the DB on insert/update/delete (RPC RAISEs 42501). The receipt path is also inconsistent: the blob lands via the admin client, but the pointer UPDATE at upload-expense-receipt.ts:104-116 runs through the user client → legacy case_expenses_update RLS, so attach can partially fail for an associated advisor. This is fail-closed (over-denies, never over-grants), affects a narrow persona on a secondary light-bookkeeping sub-block, and is not a confidentiality/integrity breach — Medium fits better than the reviewer's High. Suggested fix (re-point at can_edit_case / _assert_can_edit_case, mirroring migration 190) is correct.

#### `R-ob-uigate-1` — Obligation inline table cells render editable inputs for view-only users (C-036 edit-gate violation)
- **File:** src/features/obligations/components/obligation-table-row.tsx:33-85 (cells), :69-82 (only delete is gated)
- **Evidence:** ObligationTableRow receives canEdit but uses it ONLY for the delete button (line 70 `{canEdit && (...)}`). The loan_amount / monthly_payment / end_date / months_remaining / lender cells (NumberCell, DateCell, TextCell) are always rendered as live, focusable inputs with no `disabled` prop and always fire onSaveField on blur. Contrast case-bank-inline-row.tsx:64-75 which correctly does `disabled={!canEdit}`, and editable-bank-cell.tsx:102 which renders a read-only branch when !canEdit.
- **Why it matters:** A user who can view but not edit a case (e.g. a secretary with view_all on an unassigned case — the exact persona behind contract C-036, Round 6) sees fully editable obligation fields, can type into them, and on blur fires updateObligationFieldAction which fails server-side with 'unauthorized'. The edit affordance is shown for an action that always fails at the server — the precise pattern C-036 forbids.
- **Suggested fix:** Thread canEdit into TextCell/NumberCell/DateCell and pass `disabled={!canEdit}` (GroupedNumberInput and the native inputs already accept `disabled`), or render a read-only value span when !canEdit. Mirror case-bank-inline-row.tsx's disabled-input pattern.
- **Verify:** Confirmed against the code. In src/features/obligations/components/obligation-table-row.tsx, ObligationTableRow takes canEdit (lines 18, 33) but applies it ONLY to the delete button (line 70 `{canEdit && (...)}`). All five data cells — NumberCell (loan_amount line 40, monthly_payment 43-46, months_remaining 56-60), DateCell (end_date 49-53), TextCell (lender 63-67) — render live `<input>` elements (text input 110-122, number/GroupedNumberInput 144-187, date input 204-227) with NO disabled prop and always fire onSaveField on blur; canEdit is never threaded into these sub-components. The contrast files exist (paths in the finding said banks/ but they are actually case-banks/): case-bank-inline-row.tsx:68 does `disabled={!canEdit}` and editable-bank-cell.tsx:102 has a `if (!canEdit) return <read-only span>` branch — the obligations row does neither. The persona is real per C-036: CaseObligationsBlock computes canEdit via userCanEditCase (the can_edit_case RPC, permissions.ts:102-122) and passes it down (case-obligations-block.tsx:26-63); a view_case_obligations holder who cannot edit gets canEdit=false yet still sees editable inputs. The server always rejects: updateObligationFieldAction returns {ok:false,error:'unauthorized'} when !userCanEditCase (update-obligation-field.ts:67), so blur edits by a view-only user fail server-side — the exact 'affordance shown for an always-failing action' pattern C-036 forbids. Severity stays Medium (UI edit-gate violation; the server is authoritative so there is no privilege escalation or data leak). Note: the failure is silent — saveField in case-obligations-client.tsx:117-121 rolls back optimistic state on !ok with no toast — so the view-only user sees the value revert with no error, which is worse UX but still not a security hole.

#### `R-ce-uigate-1` — Expense inline cells render editable inputs for view-only users (C-036 edit-gate violation)
- **File:** src/features/case-expenses/components/case-expense-row.tsx:38-81 (cells), :65-76 (only delete gated; receipt cell already gates)
- **Evidence:** CaseExpenseRow receives canEdit but the expense_date / amount / description cells (DateCell, NumberCell, TextCell) are always live inputs with no disabled prop and always fire onSaveField on blur. Only the delete button (line 65) and ExpenseReceiptCell honor canEdit.

- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. The parent case-expenses-list.tsx saveField (lines 89-101) has no client guard either and always calls updateExpenseFieldAction. The finding's comparison points check out: the correctly-gated case-bank-inline-row.tsx uses disabled={!canEdit} on its text input (line 68) with disabled styling (line 75), and obligation-table-row.tsx has the identical un-gated cells (only delete gated, line 70) — confirming the inconsistency. UX-honesty (defense-in-depth)'), which explicitly notes obligations/incomes blocks still need this gate (R8/R9). Severity stays Medium to match the team's own R6 classification of this exact violation class; impact is UX-honesty only (DB/RLS is the real boundary per C-035), so it sits at the low end of Medium.

#### `R9-obl-2` — Dead obligations cluster: saveObligationAction + dialog + per-borrower group + card row + getObligationById are unused
- **File:** src/features/obligations/actions/save-obligation.ts:15; src/features/obligations/components/obligation-form-dialog.tsx:56; src/features/obligations/components/borrower-obligations-group.tsx:45; src/features/obligations/components/obligation-row.tsx:33; src/features/obligations/services/obligations.service.ts:134

No index.ts re-exports them.
- **Why it matters:** Dead code is a maintenance + audit hazard: a reviewer (or future dev) must still verify authz/validation on saveObligationAction even though nothing reaches it, and obligation-row.tsx is the file that breaches the 250-line component limit (see R9-obl-4). It also duplicates the obligation-edit logic that already lives in the table-row path, risking divergence.

- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the files and an exhaustive grep over src. Live UI path: src/app/(app)/cases/[id]/page.tsx:239 renders CaseObligationsBlock -> CaseObligationsClient (case-obligations-block.tsx:58) -> ObligationTableRow (case-obligations-client.tsx:212), wiring createEmptyObligationAction/deleteObligationAction/updateObligationFieldAction — NOT saveObligationAction. No src/features/obligations/index.ts exists, so nothing is re-exported out of tree. Every cross-reference the reviewer claimed checks out. Severity Low is correct: this is genuine dead code (maintenance/audit hazard), not a runtime or security defect — notably saveObligationAction is itself well-guarded (auth + userCanEditCase + Zod safeParse + borrowerIsOnCase), so the dead code is unreachable rather than insecure, which supports keeping it Low rather than escalating.

#### `R9-obl-3` — delete-obligation.ts logs raw error.message instead of the safeDbError helper
- **File:** src/features/obligations/actions/delete-obligation.ts:30-42
- **Evidence:** On RPC failure it does `console.error('[deleteObligation] rpc error', JSON.stringify({ obligationId, borrowerId, caseId, code: error.code ?? null, message: error.message ?? null }))`. The sibling actions create-empty-obligation.ts (line 43) and update-obligation-field.ts (line 99) use `safeDbError(error)`.
- **Why it matters:** Inconsistent with the project's safeDbError convention. It is server-side-only and the helper also keeps `message`, so there is no client leak today; but bypassing the helper means the deliberate `details`/`hint` PII-stripping it documents (release-review PRIV-2) is not centrally applied here, and the next person copying this pattern could log `details`. The returned client error is correctly the generic 'unknown'.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace the inline object with `console.error('[deleteObligation] rpc error', { obligationId, caseId, ...safeDbError(error) })` to match the other two actions.
- **Verify:** Verified against the actual code. delete-obligation.ts:30-42 logs the RPC failure with an inline object `JSON.stringify({ obligationId, borrowerId, caseId, code: error.code ?? null, message: error.message ?? null })` and does NOT import/use safeDbError — confirmed exactly as the evidence states. The two sibling actions DO use the helper: create-empty-obligation.ts:43 `console.error('[createEmptyObligation] db error', safeDbError(error))` (import at line 4) and update-obligation-field.ts:99 `console.error('[updateObligationField] db error', JSON.stringify({ obligationId, caseId, field: safeField, ...safeDbError(error) }))` (import at line 4). So the inconsistency claim is accurate.

The helper (src/lib/supabase/db-error-log.ts:7-28) deliberately drops `details`/`hint` because Postgres embeds row VALUES (national IDs, phones, financials) there — release-review PRIV-2 — and keeps only `code`+`message`. The inline version in delete-obligation.ts already logs only `code` and `message`, i.e. the exact two safe fields the helper returns, and returns the generic 'unknown' to the client (line 41). Therefore there is NO PII leak today and no client leak — the finding correctly acknowledges both of these. The substance is purely a convention/maintainability issue: bypassing the central helper means the PII-stripping intent isn't enforced here and a future edit could add `details`. The suggested fix matches the sibling pattern.

Severity Low is correct; the issue is functionally a no-op for security today (the inline object is equivalent to safeDbError's output) and only carries defensive/consistency value, so Low is if anything generous but appropriate.

#### `R9-obl-4` — File-size limits exceeded: update-obligation-field.ts (108 > 100 lines), obligation-row.tsx (280 > 250 lines)
- **File:** src/features/obligations/actions/update-obligation-field.ts:1-108; src/features/obligations/components/obligation-row.tsx:1-280
- **Evidence:** wc -l reports update-obligation-field.ts = 108 lines (server-action cap is 100) and obligation-row.tsx = 280 lines (component cap is 250).
- **Why it matters:** Engineering Standards mark exceeding the size limit as a SPLIT trigger / auto-reject in review. obligation-row.tsx is also dead (R9-obl-2) so deleting it resolves that one; update-obligation-field.ts is live and slightly over — the EDITABLE_FIELDS whitelist + per-field Zod + the borrower-resolve guard could move a helper into domain/.
- **Suggested fix:** Delete obligation-row.tsx (per R9-obl-2). For update-obligation-field.ts, extract the obligation->case ownership resolution (lines 69-82) into a small service/domain helper to bring the action under 100 lines.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the files and the standard. wc -l reports update-obligation-field.ts = 108 lines and obligation-row.tsx = 280 lines (verified directly). CLAUDE.md:88-93 "File Size Limits (Non-Negotiable)" sets Server Actions max 100 and Components max 250, with "Exceeding limit means SPLIT"; the Anti-Patterns section also lists ">100 for actions / >250 for components" as an auto-reject. So both files genuinely violate a documented project rule (action +8, component +30).

The finding's dependency on R9-obl-2 also holds: obligation-row.tsx's exported ObligationRow COMPONENT (defined at obligation-row.tsx:33) has zero importers — grep for `from '...obligation-row'` returns no matches; every other ObligationRow reference is to the unrelated TYPE alias in ../types. The live debt UI renders ObligationTableRow (obligation-table-row.tsx), imported/used at case-obligations-client.tsx:21,212. So obligation-row.tsx is dead, and deleting it resolves the component-size overage. For the action, the ownership-resolution block at lines 69-82 (the borrower_obligations.select('borrower_id') lookup + borrowerIsOnCase guard, where borrowerIsOnCase already lives in borrowers.service.ts:148) is a clean extract that would bring it under 100 lines, as suggested.

Severity stays Low: this is a mechanical style/limit overage with no behavioral, security, or correctness impact (and half of it is dead code). It is a real, deliberately-enforced standards violation, not invalid, but it is the lowest-impact tier.

#### `CB-add-1` — addCaseBankAction reactivate branch returns ok:true without confirming the row was actually updated (false success when RLS denies the reactivate)
- **File:** src/features/case-banks/actions/add-case-bank.ts:57-68
- **Evidence:** const softDeleted = thisBank.find((r) => r.deleted_at !== null);
if (softDeleted) {
  const { error } = await supabase.from('case_banks').update({ ...fields, deleted_at: null }).eq('id', softDeleted.id);
  if (error) { ...; return { ok: false, error: 'unknown' }; }
  return { ok: true, caseBankId: softDeleted.id };
}
No .eq('case_id', caseId) scope and no rowcount check on this UPDATE.
- **Why it matters:** Two issues: (1) the reactivate UPDATE is scoped only by id, not by case_id (the row was looked up under this case so it is correct in practice, but it diverges from the case-scoped pattern every other write uses); (2) if RLS silently denies the UPDATE (e.g. the associated-advisor gap in CB-authz-1), it returns ok:true and the optimistic row 'sticks' even though nothing was reactivated. Lower severity than CB-update-1 because the soft-deleted-then-readded path is uncommon.
- **Suggested fix:** Add .eq('case_id', caseId).select('id') and verify a row came back before returning ok:true, consistent with save/delete.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. In src/features/case-banks/actions/add-case-bank.ts:57-68 the reactivate branch does `.update({ ...fields, deleted_at: null }).eq('id', softDeleted.id)` with NO `.eq('case_id', caseId)` and NO `.select('id')` / rowcount check, then unconditionally `return { ok: true, caseBankId: softDeleted.id }` when there is no `error`.

Claim (1) — divergence from the case-scoped pattern: confirmed. The sibling writes both scope by case AND verify a row changed: save-case-bank.ts:52-59 does `.update(payload).eq('id', caseBankId).eq('case_id', caseId).select('id')` then `if (!updated || updated.length === 0) return unauthorized`; delete-case-bank.ts:23-38 does the same with `.select('id')` + `if (!deleted || deleted.length === 0) return unauthorized`. The reactivate branch has neither.

Claim (2) — false success on RLS denial: confirmed and genuinely reachable, not theoretical. A Supabase UPDATE that matches 0 rows under RLS returns no error, so the branch returns ok:true even though nothing was reactivated. And RLS CAN deny while the TS guard passes: userCanEditCase (lib/auth/permissions.ts:102-122) delegates to the can_edit_case RPC (mig 147:88-100), which grants associated advisors `edit_own_case AND is_case_associated_advisor(c.id)`. But the case_banks_update RLS policy (mig 024:102-110, the LAST migration to touch case_banks write policies — verified via grep: only 006/022/024 define case_banks_insert/update) uses the LEGACY check `edit_any_case OR (edit_own_case AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())` with NO is_case_associated_advisor branch. This is exactly the legacy/canonical divergence migration 190 was created to fix for borrowers/incomes/obligations — but case_banks was not re-pointed. So an associated advisor (edit_own, not assigned) passes userCanEditCase, the reactivate UPDATE is silently denied (0 rows, no error), and the action falsely returns ok:true; in save/delete the same persona is correctly caught and returned 'unauthorized'.

Severity Low is appropriate: RLS still blocks the actual write (no data corruption / no privilege escalation); impact is a confusing optimistic-row 'stick' for associated advisors only, on the uncommon soft-deleted-then-readded path. Suggested fix (add `.eq('case_id', caseId).select('id')` + verify a row returned) is correct and matches the sibling pattern.

#### `CB-dead-1` — Dead, ungated case-bank read UI (CaseBanksBlock / CaseBankRow) renders an unconditional 'add bank' Link with no canEdit gate
- **File:** src/features/case-banks/components/case-banks-block.tsx:31-38; src/features/case-banks/components/case-bank-row.tsx

Dead code also rots.

Note: the /banks/new and /banks/[bankId]/edit route pages also have no view-only gate — reachable only by direct URL since the linking block is dead — so they too rely solely on the server action's authz; consider a canEdit redirect there.

There is no index.ts barrel in features/case-banks re-exporting them. The live case page instead uses CaseBanksInlineList via case-admin-block.tsx line 164, which threads canEdit (line 168) — matching the finding. No data risk: saveCaseBankAction (save-case-bank.ts) checks auth.getUser() (lines 33-36), userCanEditCase(caseId) (lines 38-41), and scopes the update to .eq('id').eq('case_id') returning 'unauthorized' on 0 rows (line 59) — so this is pure-UX/dead-code, exactly the C-036 latent-trap framing. Secondary claim also holds: /banks/new/page.tsx and /banks/[bankId]/edit/page.tsx only call notFound() for missing/mismatched records and never check userCanEditCase/redirect view-only users, so they rely solely on the action's authz. #### `CB-result-1` — setPrimaryBankAction Result types error as a bare string instead of a literal union
- **File:** src/features/case-banks/actions/set-primary-bank.ts:6
- **Evidence:** type Result = { ok: true } | { ok: false; error: string };  // error is only ever 'unauthorized' | 'unknown'
- **Why it matters:** Weakens the typed Result<T,E> contract the standards require: callers can't exhaustively switch on error, and a typo'd error code wouldn't be caught by the compiler. The other four actions use precise literal unions (e.g. add-case-bank's 'unauthorized' | 'already_linked' | 'unknown').
- **Suggested fix:** Narrow to { ok: false; error: 'unauthorized' | 'unknown' } to match the rest of the feature.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by direct read. src/features/case-banks/actions/set-primary-bank.ts:6 declares `type Result = { ok: true } | { ok: false; error: string };` — a bare string. The action only ever emits two concrete codes: 'unauthorized' (lines 20 and 25) and 'unknown' (line 37), so the precise type would be `error: 'unauthorized' | 'unknown'`. The cross-feature comparison the finding cites is accurate: add-case-bank.ts:9 uses `'unauthorized' | 'already_linked' | 'unknown'`, delete-case-bank.ts:7 uses `'unauthorized' | 'unknown'`, and update-case-bank-field.ts:16-22 uses a five-member literal union; only set-primary-bank.ts uses a bare string. (save-case-bank.ts uses the shared CaseBankActionState action-state type, a different pattern, so 4 of 5 siblings using literal unions is the right framing.) This is a genuine type-hygiene defect that weakens the typed Result<T,E> contract the standards require — callers can't exhaustively switch and a typo'd code wouldn't be compiler-caught. However it causes no runtime bug (all emitted values are valid) and has no security/correctness impact; the can_edit_case gate (line 25 userCanEditCase) and the SECURITY INVOKER RPC are intact. Migration 190 / RLS cross-references are irrelevant to this purely-typing finding. Low severity as rated is correct.

#### `CE-action-order-1` — updateExpenseFieldAction validates the field/value with Zod before checking authorization
- **File:** src/features/case-expenses/actions/update-expense-field.ts:38-56
- **Evidence:** Order is: isEditableExpenseField (line 38) → fieldSchema.safeParse (line 44) → only then userCanEditCase (line 54) and getUser (line 59). CLAUDE.md Server Actions Rules: 'MUST check authentication/authorization at the top.' The sibling write actions in this same feature (create-empty:19-23, remove-receipt:27-29, upload:60-62) do auth first.
- **Why it matters:** No data leak (validation touches no DB and returns only translated field strings), so this is consistency/standards drift rather than a security hole — an unauthenticated/unauthorized caller still gets a generic rejection, just after a wasted parse. Worth aligning so the pattern stays uniform across the feature.
- **Suggested fix:** Move the getUser + userCanEditCase guard above the whitelist/Zod block (matching the other expense actions and the documented 'authz at the top' rule).
- **Verify:** Confirmed against the actual code. In src/features/case-expenses/actions/update-expense-field.ts the order is exactly as claimed: isEditableExpenseField whitelist (line 38) -> fieldSchema.safeParse (lines 43-44, with resolveSchemaErrors on failure) -> userCanEditCase(caseId) (line 54) -> getUser() (lines 58-61). So validation runs before any authn/authz, violating the CLAUDE.md "MUST check authentication/authorization at the top" rule. The three sibling write actions verifiably do auth first: create-empty-expense.ts (getUser 18-19, userCanEditCase 21-23), remove-expense-receipt.ts (getUser 27-28, userCanEditCase 29), upload-expense-receipt.ts (getUser 60-61, userCanEditCase 62 — before the expensive rate-limit/storage work; only cheap FormData-shape checks precede). No data leak: ExpenseFormShape (expense.schema.ts) validation is pure in-memory over date/amount/description, and resolveSchemaErrors (lib/validators/i18n-errors.ts) only maps Zod issue messages to next-intl translation strings — no DB, no policy/constraint/bucket names. can_edit_case is the canonical write gate (migration 190) and RLS backstops the actual write, so an unauthorized caller is still rejected, just after a wasted parse. Genuine consistency/standards drift, not a security hole; reviewer's Low is correct.

#### `UI-bank-form-gate-1` — CaseBankForm renders a fully-editable bank form with no canEdit gate; its host pages don't check userCanEditCase
- **File:** src/features/case-banks/components/case-bank-form.tsx:48-160 ; src/app/(app)/cases/[id]/banks/new/page.tsx:18-51 ; src/app/(app)/cases/[id]/banks/[bankId]/edit/page.tsx:19-63
- **Evidence:** CaseBankForm has no canEdit prop — it always renders the bank select, status select, is_primary checkbox, banker fields, dates, notes and a live SubmitButton. The new/edit pages only do `getRawCaseById(...)` / `getCaseBankById(...)` (which load if the user can VIEW the case via RLS) and never call userCanEditCase before rendering the form: `if (!caseData) notFound();` (new) / `if (!caseData || !caseBank || caseBank.case_id !== id) notFound();` (edit). A view-only user who can see a case (e.g. secretary with view_all on an unassigned case) can navigate directly to /cases/{id}/banks/new or /cases/{id}/banks/{bankId}/edit and is shown the full editable form.
- **Why it matters:** Contract C-036 (Round 6) requires view-only users not be shown edit affordances that fail at the server. The inline banks list correctly hides its '+ add bank' affordance when !canEdit, so the only entry to these form pages is a direct URL — but once there, a non-editor sees a complete, fillable bank form. saveCaseBankAction DOES re-assert userCanEditCase (save-case-bank.ts:39) so there is no data-loss/privilege escalation; the harm is limited to a misleading UI that lets a viewer fill a form only to be rejected on submit (with a generic 'unauthorized' error). Blast radius is limited (server-gated, direct-URL only), hence Medium.
- **Suggested fix:** In both bank pages compute `const canEdit = await userCanEditCase(asCaseId(id));` and `notFound()` (or redirect to /cases/{id} read-only) when false — mirroring how the case detail page gates the inline list. Optionally add a `canEdit` prop to CaseBankForm and render a read-only summary when false, for parity with EditableBankCell's read-only branch.
- **Verify:** Every claim in the finding is substantiated by the code. (1) CaseBankForm (src/features/case-banks/components/case-bank-form.tsx:26-31, 48) has no canEdit prop; its props are only caseId/initial/banks/statuses and it unconditionally renders the bank select, status select, is_primary checkbox, banker fields, date pickers, notes Textarea and a live SubmitButton (lines 80-158). (2) The new page (banks/new/page.tsx:18-21) calls only getRawCaseById + `if (!caseData) notFound()` and never userCanEditCase. (3) The edit page (banks/[bankId]/edit/page.tsx:22-27) calls getRawCaseById + getCaseBankById + `if (!caseData || !caseBank || caseBank.case_id !== id) notFound()` and never userCanEditCase. (4) getRawCaseById (cases.service.ts:98-109) is a plain RLS-gated SELECT, so a view-only user who can SEE a case passes it. (5) The sibling borrower new page (borrowers/new/page.tsx:19-23) DOES gate with `if (!(await userCanEditCase(asCaseId(id)))) notFound();` and its comment cites the exact same secretary/view_all-on-unassigned-case scenario — proving the bank pages are an inconsistent omission of an established pattern. (6) The inline banks list and row correctly hide their add/edit affordances behind canEdit (case-banks-inline-list.tsx:176; case-bank-inline-row.tsx:77,98), and the case detail page threads canEdit=canEditCase into CaseAdminBlock -> CaseBanksInlineList (page.tsx:300; case-admin-block.tsx:164-168), so a view-only user has no UI link into these form pages — direct URL only. (7) saveCaseBankAction re-asserts authorization: getUser then `if (!(await userCanEditCase(caseId))) return {ok:false,error:'unauthorized'}` (save-case-bank.ts:33-41) plus a scoped update/insert, so there is genuinely NO data-loss or privilege escalation. can_edit_case (migration 190; permissions.ts:102-122 via the can_edit_case RPC) is the EDIT guard (edit_any OR edit_own AND assigned/associated + not-deleted), distinct from VIEW, confirming the view-but-not-edit gap. So the finding is real and correctly diagnosed. I downgrade Medium -> Low: the only entry is a hand-typed URL to routes with no UI link anywhere (the linking components CaseBanksBlock/case-bank-row.tsx are dead code — no importers found repo-wide), the server fully blocks the write, and the impact is purely a misleading editable form for a view-only user. It is a legitimate C-036 consistency violation worth fixing by mirroring the borrower-page gate, but the realistic blast radius is cosmetic-only and direct-URL-only on an effectively orphaned route, which is Low rather than Medium.

#### `UI-table-textright-1` — Physical text-right on table header <tr> (overridden by text-start cells) — RTL-leaning inconsistency
- **File:** src/features/obligations/components/case-obligations-client.tsx:201 ; src/features/case-expenses/components/case-expenses-list.tsx:134
- **Evidence:** Both tables render `<tr className="text-right">` for the header row, while each header cell uses the logical `text-start` (case-obligations-client Th:234 `text-start`; case-expenses-list Th:167 `text-start`). The child text-start overrides the inherited physical text-right, so visible alignment is correct in both LTR and RTL.
- **Why it matters:** No functional RTL bug today (cells override it), but a physical `text-right` is exactly the kind of class the project bans for RTL safety; if a future cell drops its text-start override it would silently mis-align in English/LTR. It is also dead styling.
- **Suggested fix:** Remove `text-right` from the header <tr> in both files (the Th cells already set text-start), or replace with the logical `text-start` for consistency with the rest of the codebase.
- **Verify:** Confirmed in code. case-obligations-client.tsx:201 renders `<tr className="text-right">` and case-expenses-list.tsx:134 renders the identical `<tr className="text-right">` for the header row. In both, every header cell uses the logical `text-start` (case-obligations-client Th:234; case-expenses-list Th:167), which overrides the inherited physical `text-right`, so visible alignment is correct in LTR and RTL today. I also checked the data-row cells to confirm no cell relies on the header's physical alignment: obligation-table-row.tsx uses a neutral `<td className="px-1.5 py-1.5 align-middle">` (line 88) with `text-end` (logical) on inputs (lines 161, 181); case-expense-row.tsx uses `text-end` on its `<td>` (line 57) and input (line 153). So the header `text-right` is dead styling — overridden by children, with a latent risk of LTR mis-alignment only if a future cell drops its `text-start`. The finding is accurate and the Low severity is appropriate (purely cosmetic/dead-code, no functional bug). One minor over-statement: CLAUDE.md explicitly bans bracketed-hex literals but I found no documented codebase rule that auto-rejects physical `text-right`/`text-left` classes, so the reviewer's "exactly the kind of class the project bans" is slightly stronger than the written rules support; the technical core stands.

#### `R-ob-test-1` — monthsUntil has zero test coverage despite being the only non-trivial date math in the three features
- **File:** src/features/obligations/domain/months-remaining.ts:13-28 (untested); src/features/obligations/domain/totals.test.ts (only totals are covered)
- **Evidence:** grep for monthsUntil in test files returns nothing. totals.test.ts covers sumMonthlyPayments/sumRemainingDebt only. monthsUntil contains branchy edge logic: null/invalid → null, past date → 0 (Math.max), and a day-of-month rollback (`if (end.getDate() < today.getDate()) total -= 1`).
- **Why it matters:** monthsUntil is wired as the smart default that auto-fills months_remaining when an end_date is picked (case-obligations-client.tsx:127-131), so a regression silently writes wrong months to every obligation. The day-of-month adjustment and the year/month boundary cases are exactly where off-by-one bugs hide, and there is no test to catch them. Project standard explicitly prioritizes domain-layer tests.
- **Suggested fix:** Add months-remaining.test.ts covering: null/'' /invalid → null; today → 0; past date → 0; same-month future day-reached vs not-reached (the -1 branch); cross-year (Dec→Jan); exact N-month boundaries (e.g. 2026-05-27 → 2026-08-27 = 3, → 2026-08-20 = 2).
- **Verify:** Confirmed against the code. (1) Coverage gap is real: grep for `monthsUntil` across all `*.{test,spec}.{ts,tsx}` returns "No files found"; it appears only in src/features/obligations/domain/months-remaining.ts:13 and the two call-sites (obligation-row.tsx:71, case-obligations-client.tsx:127). The feature's sole test file, totals.test.ts, covers only sumMonthlyPayments/sumRemainingDebt (lines 5,37) — monthsUntil is untested. (2) Branchy edge logic is real (months-remaining.ts:14-27): null/undefined/'' → null (L14), NaN date → null (L16), Math.max(0,...) clamps past dates to 0 (L27), and the day-of-month rollback `if (end.getDate() < today.getDate()) total -= 1` (L26). That subtraction is exactly where off-by-one bugs hide — e.g. today 2026-01-31 / end 2026-02-28 yields 0 because 28<31, an arguably wrong result a test would surface. (3) Wiring/blast-radius is real: in BOTH components, picking an end_date computes `monthsUntil(value)` and immediately persists it via updateObligationFieldAction(..., 'months_remaining', months) (case-obligations-client.tsx:127-131; obligation-row.tsx:71-78), so a regression silently writes wrong months to the DB. (4) Project standard is real: 45 domain .test.ts files exist incl. date-math siblings (cases/domain/age.test.ts, target-date.test.ts, greeting.test.ts) and the parallel incomes/domain/totals.test.ts — the convention is clearly to test domain logic, and this function escaped it. The finding holds. I lowered severity from Medium to Low: this is a pure missing-test/coverage gap with no demonstrated incorrect output in the currently-shipped path (no live defect), so it's a process/quality gap rather than a Medium-severity bug, even though the silent-DB-write blast radius keeps it above trivial.

#### `R-ob-cap-1` — end_date smart-default can compute months_remaining above the schema cap (600), persisting end_date but silently dropping the derived months
- **File:** src/features/obligations/components/case-obligations-client.tsx:125-137; cap at src/features/obligations/schemas/obligation.schema.ts:20 (optionalInt(600)); monthsUntil at src/features/obligations/domain/months-remaining.ts:23-27
- **Evidence:** On end_date save the client computes `months = monthsUntil(value)` and calls updateObligationFieldAction(...,'months_remaining', months). monthsUntil is unbounded (returns ~1200 for a 100-year date), but optionalInt(600) caps months_remaining at 50 years, so the months update returns validation failure and is rolled back (line 132-136) while the end_date write already succeeded.
- **Why it matters:** For an end_date >50 years out, end_date persists but months_remaining keeps its previous (stale) value with no user-visible error — the two columns silently diverge. Rare in practice, but it is a correctness inconsistency in the documented 'mutual with end_date' relationship.
- **Suggested fix:** Clamp the derived value before saving (e.g. `Math.min(monthsUntil(value) ?? 0, 600)`), or skip the months auto-write when the computed value exceeds the cap, so end_date and months_remaining never disagree silently.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. In case-obligations-client.tsx:117 the end_date save runs first via updateObligationFieldAction(id, caseId, 'end_date', value) and succeeds (end_date is validated only by optionalDate). Then at line 127 months = monthsUntil(value), and line 131 issues a second updateObligationFieldAction(...,'months_remaining', months). monthsUntil (months-remaining.ts:13-28) is unbounded on the upper end — it floors at 0 via Math.max(0, total) but has no ceiling, so a date >50 years out yields >600. The schema (obligation.schema.ts:20) types months_remaining as optionalInt(600), and optionalInt (form-primitives.ts:127-141) enforces .max(600) returning a 'common.errors.tooLarge' validation error. update-obligation-field.ts:53-62 runs that per-field safeParse and returns {ok:false, error:'validation'} for the over-cap value, BEFORE any DB write — so the months_remaining column is never updated. The client rollback at lines 132-136 resets months_remaining to the prior (stale) value and shows NO toast/error. Net result: DB persists the new end_date while months_remaining keeps its old value, silently diverging, contradicting the documented 'Computed mutual with end_date' relationship (months-remaining.ts comment + schema comment '50-year cap'). The end_date write being committed first (line 117) while the dependent months write is rejected is the load-bearing fact, and it holds. Severity Low is appropriate: it only triggers for an end_date more than 50 years in the future (extremely rare for a debt obligation), causes no crash or data loss, and the inconsistency is benign — the stale months simply fails to refresh. The suggested fix (clamp via Math.min(monthsUntil(value) ?? 0, 600), or skip the months auto-write when over cap) is correct and minimal.

#### `R-ob-tz-1` — monthsUntil mixes UTC-parsed end date with local 'today', a latent cross-timezone off-by-one
- **File:** src/features/obligations/domain/months-remaining.ts:14-26
- **Evidence:** `const end = new Date(endDateStr)` parses 'YYYY-MM-DD' as UTC midnight, while `const today = new Date()` is local. getFullYear/getMonth/getDate then read end's fields in local time. For negative UTC offsets (Americas) UTC-midnight rolls back to the previous calendar day, shifting getDate()/getMonth() and tripping the `end.getDate() < today.getDate()` branch differently than intended.
- **Why it matters:** Harmless for the Israel (UTC+2/+3) deployment where UTC midnight stays on the same local calendar day, but it is a correctness footgun if the app is ever run/tested under a negative-offset timezone (incl. CI) and is the kind of bug a monthsUntil test should pin.
- **Suggested fix:** Parse the components explicitly (split on '-' into y/m/d ints) or compare using UTC accessors on both dates so the comparison is timezone-stable, then add the corresponding test.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading src/features/obligations/domain/months-remaining.ts lines 13-28 and empirically reproducing the behavior across timezones. Line 15 `const end = new Date(endDateStr)` parses the 'YYYY-MM-DD' string (the date-only ECMAScript form) as UTC midnight; line 18 `const today = new Date()` is local; lines 24-26 then read end's fields via getFullYear/getMonth/getDate in LOCAL time. Verified with Node: the same instant 2026-08-01T00:00:00.000Z yields getDate()=1/getMonth()=8 under Asia/Jerusalem but getDate()=31/getMonth()=7 under America/New_York and America/Los_Angeles (UTC midnight rolls back to the previous local calendar day under negative offsets). Demonstrated a concrete divergent output: with today=local Jun 1 and end='2026-09-01', monthsUntil returns 3 in Israel (correct) but 2 in New York/LA (off-by-one), because end parses to Aug 31 there and getMonth() loses the month. The two callers (obligation-row.tsx:71, case-obligations-client.tsx:127) pass <input type=date>/DatePickerPopover 'YYYY-MM-DD' strings, matching the finding's premise. No test pins this: the domain folder contains only totals.test.ts, no months-remaining.test.ts. Severity stays Low and not higher because production is Israel-only (UTC+2/+3), where UTC midnight never crosses the local calendar-day boundary, so the bug is fully dormant in prod; it only surfaces under negative-offset timezones (Americas, mis-configured CI). The migration 190 / can_edit_case / RLS cross-references are not applicable — this is a pure client-side date utility with no DB surface. Reviewer's evidence, impact rationale, and Low grade are all accurate.

#### `R-ob-deadcode-1` — Orphaned obligation full-form dialog cluster (borrower-obligations-group / obligation-form-dialog / obligation-row / saveObligationAction)
- **File:** src/features/obligations/components/borrower-obligations-group.tsx, obligation-form-dialog.tsx, obligation-row.tsx; action src/features/obligations/actions/save-obligation.ts
- **Evidence:** The live page uses CaseObligationsBlock (flat) only (cases/[id]/page.tsx:239). borrower-obligations-group.tsx has no importers; obligation-row.tsx has no importers; obligation-form-dialog.tsx is imported only by the dead borrower-obligations-group; saveObligationAction is imported only by the dead obligation-form-dialog.
