- **Suggested fix:** Remove borrower-obligations-group.tsx, obligation-form-dialog.tsx, obligation-row.tsx, and saveObligationAction after confirming no other importers; retain the grouped listObligationsForCase used by the PDF service.
- **Verify:** Confirmed transitively-dead cluster. (1) The live case page renders only the flat path: src/app/(app)/cases/[id]/page.tsx:239 renders CaseObligationsBlock, which (case-obligations-block.tsx:8,58) renders CaseObligationsClient, which (case-obligations-client.tsx:21,212) renders ObligationTableRow and writes via createEmptyObligationAction/updateObligationFieldAction/deleteObligationAction — saveObligationAction is NOT in this path. (2) borrower-obligations-group.tsx (component BorrowerObligationsGroup) has no importers: a repo-wide grep returns only the component's own definition plus the unrelated *type* `BorrowerObligationsGroup` in types.ts (a name collision; the type is used by the service, not the component). (3) obligation-form-dialog.tsx (ObligationFormDialog) is imported ONLY by the dead borrower-obligations-group.tsx:22. (4) obligation-row.tsx (component ObligationRow) has no source importers — grep for the file path './obligation-row' / 'components/obligation-row' returns nothing (the widely-imported ObligationRow is the type from types.ts; there's no barrel index.ts re-exporting the component). (5) saveObligationAction (save-obligation.ts:15) is imported ONLY by the dead obligation-form-dialog.tsx:23, and indeed logs nothing while returning error:'unknown' on raw db error (lines 56, 65). (6) The reviewer's carve-out is correct: the grouped listObligationsForCase (obligations.service.ts:33) IS still used by src/features/cases/pdf/bank-pdf-data.service.ts:113 and must be retained. Net: 3 dead components + 1 dead action, all transitively rooted in the unreferenced BorrowerObligationsGroup component. Low severity is correct — no runtime, security, or correctness impact; this is maintenance-surface/clarity (one drift-prone duplicate of the obligation write logic). Migration 190, can_edit_case, and RLS were not the locus of this finding (it's pure dead-code), so no schema reading was needed to confirm; userCanEditCase is correctly invoked by the dead action (line 37) but that is moot since the action is unreachable.

#### `R-ob-log-1` — delete-obligation logs raw error.message instead of safeDbError (server-side only; consistency)
- **File:** src/features/obligations/actions/delete-obligation.ts:31-41
- **Evidence:** Logs `message: error.message ?? null` directly, unlike update-obligation-field.ts / create-empty-obligation.ts and the case-banks/case-expenses actions which all route through safeDbError. The client still receives a generic 'unknown' (no leak), so this is purely a server-log consistency nit. Same raw-message logging in delete-expense.ts:36, update-expense-field.ts:80, get-expense-receipt-url is fine.
- **Why it matters:** No client leak (only the server log holds the message), so low risk; but using safeDbError uniformly keeps the redaction/format contract consistent and avoids accidentally logging a constraint/policy name in a future copy-paste.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace the inline `{ code, message }` object with `safeDbError(error)` to match the sibling actions.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. delete-obligation.ts:30-42 logs an inline object on RPC error: `{ obligationId, borrowerId, caseId, code: error.code ?? null, message: error.message ?? null }` and does NOT import safeDbError. Sibling actions do: update-obligation-field.ts imports safeDbError (line 4) and uses `...safeDbError(error)` at line 99; create-empty-obligation.ts imports it (line 4) and uses `safeDbError(error)` at line 43. The finding's consistency claim is accurate. The same inline pattern also appears in case-expenses/actions/delete-expense.ts:30-41 (also flagged correctly). No client leak: delete-obligation returns `{ ok: false, error: 'unknown' }` (line 41) — the message stays server-side only. Importantly, safeDbError (db-error-log.ts:24-28) returns exactly `{ code: error?.code ?? null, message: error?.message ?? null }`, the SAME two fields the inline object already logs; the helper's real value is dropping PII-bearing `details`/`hint`, which the inline object also never includes. So there is no actual privacy/leak delta today — it is purely a contract-uniformity nit (a future copy-paste might inline details/hint). Real but cosmetic; Low is correct, not overstated.

### Refuted (2)

- `CE-action-size-1` uploadExpenseReceiptAction exceeds the 100-line server-action limit — The finding's central evidence is factually wrong. It claims "the action body runs 138 lines total (the function alone spans lines 40-138)." Reading the file, uploadExpenseReceiptAction is declared at line 40 and its closing brace is at line 138 — that is 99 lines inclusive, NOT 138, and it is UNDER the CLAUDE.md 100-line server-action limit. The 138 figure is the TOTAL FILE count, which the reviewer conflated with the function span; that total includes the 3-block import section (lines 1-17), the 7-line UploadReceiptResult type (19-25), and a 13-line JSDoc doc comment (27-39) — none of which is "the action body." Counting non-blank, non-comment lines inside the function body yields 78. So by the natural reading of the rule (a Server Action = one function), the action is compliant (99 <= 100), and by logical-lines it is comfortably compliant (78). Only under a strict "the whole file <= 100" reading is 138 > 100, and even then the overage is driven by a verbose-but-justified doc comment plus the type decl, not by inlined logic. The "inlines everything" claim is also overstated: the Drive mirror is ALREADY extracted to services/receipt-drive.service.ts (verified), the size/mime constants live in schemas/receipt.schema.ts (verified), and filename sanitize is imported from features/documents/domain. The action is genuine orchestration; only the cheap FormData/size/declared-mime guards are inlined. There is no ESLint max-lines-per-function rule configured (eslint.config.mjs only extends next core-web-vitals + typescript), so the "auto-reject in review" framing has no automated enforcement and rests entirely on a guideline the function does not actually breach. Net: the defect as described (a 138-line function over the limit) does not exist in the code.
- `UI-bankcell-default-1` EditableBankCell defaults canEdit to true — a missing prop silently yields an editable cell — The mechanical code facts are accurate: editable-bank-cell.tsx:33 declares `canEdit?: boolean` (optional) and line 41 defaults `canEdit = true` (fail-open); the read-only branch (lines 102-127) renders only when canEdit===false; the sole live caller case-table-row.tsx:135 passes canEdit={canEdit} explicitly (derived from the C-036 gate via canEditCaseRow(editGate, row) at line 43). So there is NO actual defect today — the finding concedes this.

However, the finding's load-bearing rationale is FALSE. It claims "Every other component in this set takes canEdit as a required prop" and tells us to match CaseBankInlineRow / CaseExpenseRow / ObligationTableRow / ExpenseReceiptCell. Those are case-detail BLOCK list-row components — a different set. EditableBankCell's actual peers are the other dashboard inline cells rendered next to it in case-table-row.tsx (status/advisor/target-date/text). I verified all four of those use the IDENTICAL optional + default-true pattern: editable-status-cell.tsx:40, editable-advisor-cell.tsx:48, editable-target-date-cell.tsx:39, editable-text-cell.tsx:33 all read `canEdit = true`. EditableBankCell is therefore the CONSISTENT member of its set, not an outlier.

The suggested fix (make only EditableBankCell required) would actually CREATE inconsistency with its four true peers rather than remove it. Real hardening would mean flipping all five inline-cell defaults to fail-closed, not singling out this one. Given no defect today, a factually-wrong comparison/premise, and a fix that would introduce inconsistency, this does not hold as a valid Low finding as written. The fail-open-default observation has a sliver of defensive-coding merit, but it's too misframed to stand.


## Round 10 — documents / uploads / storage / retention / erasure

**raw 27 -> confirmed 26 / refuted 1  (High 3, Medium 7, Low 16)**

### High (3)

#### `DOC-UP-1-crosscase-path` — finalize-upload never binds storagePath to caseId → cross-case document row (path confusion / IDOR)
- **File:** src/features/documents/actions/finalize-upload.ts:23-34,89-93,170-185
- **Evidence:** `FinalizeUploadInput` carries `caseId` AND `storagePath` as two INDEPENDENT client-supplied strings. The action authorizes ONLY `userCanEditCase(input.caseId)` (line 63) and resolves context on `input.caseId` (line 89), but NOTHING ever checks that `input.storagePath` begins with `input.caseId`. There is no `storagePath.startsWith(caseId)` / `foldername(name)[1] === caseId` guard anywhere in the file (confirmed by grep across the feature). The INSERT then writes `case_id: input.caseId` while `metadata: { storage_path: input.storagePath }` (line 182) can point at ANOTHER case's object. The `documents_insert` RLS (mig 024 lines 135-148) only validates the `case_id` COLUMN against `can_edit_case`-equivalent perms — it does not inspect `metadata.storage_path`, and the INSERT metadata is not write-guarded (mig 027's guard is BEFORE UPDATE only). prepare-upload returns a *correctly* scoped path, but a malicious client ignores it and POSTs an arbitrary `storagePath` to finalize. Concrete exploit: a user who can edit Case A and has `view_all_cases` (e.g. secretary) calls finalize with `caseId=CaseA`, `storagePath="<CaseB-id>/<doc>.<ext>"`; the magic/size checks pass (the signed-read in lines 98-100 succeeds because case_docs_select allows can_view_case(CaseB)); a Case A document row is created whose blob is Case B's file → Case B PII (national IDs, bank statements) surfaces inside Case A's document list and preview (get-document-preview-url.ts signs metadata.storage_path directly).
- **Why it matters:** Cross-case data exposure: a viewer-of-all who can edit only their own case can graft any other case's confidential blob into a case they control, defeating the per-case isolation the storage RLS was designed to enforce. Even where the storage read RLS would later deny a less-privileged attacker, the poisoned row still corrupts case integrity (a Case A document that 404s/leaks on preview) and the same gap means a single typo'd/stale storagePath silently mis-files documents. Violates the STORAGE invariant: 'finalize-upload must verify the object/path belongs to the case the user can edit.'
- **Suggested fix:** At the top of finalizeUploadAction (after auth), assert the path is case-scoped: derive `const expectedPrefix = `${input.caseId}/`` and reject if `!input.storagePath.startsWith(expectedPrefix)` (and ideally that the second segment equals `input.documentId`, since storagePathFor encodes both). Better: don't accept `storagePath` from the client at all — recompute it server-side from `caseId`+`documentId`+sanitized name exactly as prepare did (the value is fully derivable). Same fix applies to finalizeTaskAttachmentUploadAction (src/features/tasks/actions/task-attachment-upload.ts:38-45,169-187) which has the identical missing binding.
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED by reading the code. finalize-upload.ts (src/features/documents/actions/finalize-upload.ts) accepts caseId (line 25) and storagePath (line 26) as two independent client-supplied strings. Auth is ONLY userCanEditCase(input.caseId) (line 63); context resolves on input.caseId (line 89). NOTHING validates that input.storagePath belongs to input.caseId — no startsWith/foldername guard anywhere (grep confirmed no matches). The signed-read (lines 98-100), magic-sniff (107-120), size check (123-141), Drive upload (146-167) and the INSERT (170-185) all run against the attacker-supplied path, and the row is written with case_id: input.caseId but metadata.storage_path: input.storagePath (line 182) pointing at another case's object.

RLS does not save it. documents_insert (mig 024 lines 135-148) and storage case_docs_insert (mig 027 lines 92-105) each validate the case_id COLUMN / path first-segment INDEPENDENTLY; neither inspects metadata.storage_path. The guard_document_trusted_columns trigger (mig 027) that would block cross-case moves is BEFORE UPDATE only (line 79) — it does NOT run on INSERT, so the poisoned metadata is unguarded at creation.

I verified the finding accounts for the CURRENT migration state, not just the cited 020/024/027: mig 040 tightened case_docs_select to gate on can_view_case((foldername(name))[1]) — i.e. the path's first segment (CaseB), not the documents.case_id. can_view_case (mig 039/147) returns TRUE for any user with view_all_cases. So for the stated persona (secretary: view_all_cases + upload_document + edit_own_case on CaseA), the chain works end to end: the finalize signed-read of CaseB's path succeeds (can_view_case(CaseB)=TRUE), the INSERT into CaseA succeeds (can_edit_case(CaseA)=TRUE, metadata unchecked), and the payoff in get-document-preview-url.ts signs metadata.storage_path directly (line 46) — its createSignedUrl on the CaseB path again passes can_view_case(CaseB)=TRUE. Result: CaseB's confidential blob (national IDs, bank statements) surfaces inside CaseA's document list/preview, defeating the per-case isolation the storage RLS write-binding was designed to enforce.

prepare-upload.ts computes the correct path server-side via storagePathFor(caseId, documentId, ...) and returns it (line 91), proving the value is fully derivable; finalize simply trusts the client's copy instead of recomputing — the exact gap the suggested fix closes. The identical missing binding exists in task-attachment-upload.ts: prepare uses storagePathFor (line 77) but finalizeTaskAttachmentUploadAction (lines 96-199) accepts input.storagePath and never validates it against input.caseId.

Bounding nuance (does not refute): an attacker WITHOUT view_all_cases (plain advisor, view_own_cases only) cannot read CaseB — both the finalize signed-read and the preview hit can_view_case(CaseB)=FALSE, so the sniff fetch returns non-OK and finalize fails at line 110-114; the row is never created for that persona. Thus full PII exfiltration requires view_all_cases. But that is a common low-privilege grant (secretary), and the data-integrity harm (silently mis-filed cross-case document via stale/typo'd path) applies even to the narrower persona. Severity High stands: confirmed cross-case PII exposure for a realistic non-admin persona plus a data-integrity hole; fix (recompute path server-side, or assert storagePath.startsWith(`${caseId}/`) and second segment === documentId) is correct and applies to both finalize actions.

#### `R-storage-1` — finalizeUploadAction trusts client-supplied storagePath; never verifies it is scoped to the case being edited
- **File:** src/features/documents/actions/finalize-upload.ts:56-66,98-100,170-185 (cf. prepare-upload.ts:90-95, documents.service.ts:55-65)
- **Evidence:** FinalizeUploadInput.storagePath is a free-form string taken verbatim from the client. The action authorizes on input.caseId (userCanEditCase) but NEVER checks that input.storagePath starts with `${input.caseId}/`. It then signs/sniffs that path (line 98-100) and INSERTs the documents row with case_id=input.caseId but metadata.storage_path=input.storagePath (line 182). prepareUploadAction server-generates a correct path via storagePathFor(caseId, docId) = `<caseId>/<docId>.<ext>`, but finalize re-accepts whatever the client posts back. There is no Zod schema for FinalizeUploadInput and no startsWith(caseId) guard (grep of documents/schemas confirms none). The signed-read at finalize uses the USER session (subject to storage RLS can_view_case), so a user who can VIEW case B but only EDIT case A can finalize a row that attributes case B's blob (national-ID/bank-statement PII) to a document under case A. This violates the project invariant: 'finalize-upload must verify the object/path belongs to the case the user can edit' and the segment-1=case-id storage isolation contract (the stored pointer no longer matches the row's case_id).
- **Why it matters:** Breaks cross-case storage isolation at the application layer. A user with mixed view/edit permissions can plant a foreign case's PII blob pointer onto a case they control, surfacing the foreign document inside case A's UI and breaking the path<->case invariant that the rest of the system (RLS, eraser, purge) relies on. Also lets a stale/replayed prepare path be retargeted.
- **Suggested fix:** In finalizeUploadAction, before any use of input.storagePath, reject unless input.storagePath === storagePathFor(input.caseId, input.documentId, safeFileName) (or at minimum input.storagePath.startsWith(`${input.caseId}/${input.documentId}`)). Better: don't accept storagePath from the client at all — re-derive it from caseId+documentId+fileName server-side (the same way prepare did) so the value is structurally impossible to forge. Add a Zod schema for FinalizeUploadInput while there.
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED by reading the code and the relevant RLS migrations. finalize-upload.ts (lines 23-34, 56-100, 170-185): FinalizeUploadInput.storagePath is a free-form client string. The action authorizes via userCanEditCase(input.caseId) (line 63) but NEVER validates input.storagePath against input.caseId — no startsWith(`${caseId}/`) guard exists (grep over src/features/documents confirms none), and there is NO Zod schema for FinalizeUploadInput (document.schema.ts only has DocumentMetadataSchema for category/borrower/notes/expiry). prepare-upload.ts:91 correctly server-derives the path via storagePathFor = `${caseId}/${documentId}.<ext>` (documents.service.ts:57-65), but finalize re-accepts whatever the client posts back, and the row is inserted with case_id=input.caseId but metadata.storage_path=input.storagePath (line 182).

The attack path is real and not backstopped by RLS: (1) the signed read at line 98-100 uses the user-session client (line 60 getUser()) and storage policy case_docs_select (mig 040 lines 21-26) gates createSignedUrl on can_view_case of the PATH's first segment — NOT input.caseId — so a path under case B succeeds if the user can VIEW B. (2) The documents_insert RLS (mig 024 lines 135-148) checks edit permission against the row's case_id column (=A, editable) but treats metadata->>storage_path as unconstrained JSONB, so the INSERT with case_id=A + storage_path="B/..." passes. Nothing at the DB layer binds the JSONB pointer's first segment to case_id (no trigger; mig 027's guard only fires on UPDATE and only protects status/drive/case_id columns, not metadata path).

Precondition is realistic in this tenant: the secretary persona is view_all + edit_own + NO edit_any (documented in project memory and consistent with the RLS), i.e. exactly a user who can VIEW an unassigned case B but only EDIT their assigned case A. Result: case B's PII blob (national-ID/bank-statement) gets pointer-attributed to a document under case A and surfaces in A's UI. The size cross-check (lines 122-141) does NOT block this because input.fileSize is also client-controlled and the check is skip-on-mismatch only. It also breaks the path<->case invariant the retention eraser depends on (retention-file-eraser.ts:108-164 deletes the blob at metadata.storage_path when case A is purged → would delete case B's real blob).

Severity kept at High: this is a genuine cross-case storage-isolation bypass at the application layer that RLS does not catch, with PII cross-attribution and cross-case data-destruction-on-purge consequences. It requires an authenticated insider with a specific mixed view/edit permission shape (not anon/external), which is the only reason it isn't critical-tier; the documented finalize invariant ('finalize must verify the object/path belongs to the case the user can edit') is squarely violated. Suggested fix is correct: re-derive the path server-side from caseId+documentId+fileName (or at minimum reject unless storagePath starts with `${caseId}/${documentId}`) and add a Zod schema for FinalizeUploadInput.

#### `R10-doc-1` — documents_insert / documents_update RLS still use legacy assigned_advisor_id — EXCLUDE associated advisors (breaks upload + verify + recategorize for that role)
- **File:** supabase/migrations/024_rls_layer2_and_constraints.sql:135-185
- **Evidence:** The final, never-superseded documents_insert and documents_update policies gate writes on `public.has_permission('edit_any_case') OR (public.has_permission('edit_own_case') AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())`. They do NOT call public.can_edit_case (mig 147) and never reference case_associated_advisors. Meanwhile the app actions prepare-upload.ts:81 and finalize-upload.ts:63 (INSERT) and update-document-status.ts:34 (UPDATE) gate on userCanEditCase, which DOES include associated advisors. Result: an associated advisor (edit_own_case, not the assigned advisor) passes the app check, uploads the blob + does the Drive round-trip, then the documents INSERT is rejected by RLS — the upload fails after the work is done (blob then cleaned up at finalize-upload.ts:189). Same for verify/status-change. Note delete-document.ts uses a SECURITY DEFINER RPC so delete works for them — producing inconsistent behavior across operations.
- **Why it matters:** This is the exact bug class the project invariant names ('Legacy assigned_advisor_id = actor OR edit_any_case EXCLUDES associated advisors = a bug'). A legitimate role (associated advisor) cannot upload, verify, or recategorize documents on cases they are explicitly associated with — a broken core flow — while delete works, so the authority model is internally inconsistent.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a migration that rewrites documents_insert/documents_update (USING + WITH CHECK) to use public.can_edit_case(case_id) instead of the inline assigned_advisor_id clause, mirroring what mig 147 did for cases_update and the case_* child tables. Keep the deleted_at IS NULL and the verify/upload permission AND-conditions.
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED by reading the actual code. documents_insert (024_rls_layer2_and_constraints.sql:135-148) and documents_update (024:150-175) are the final, never-superseded write policies — grep across all 189 migrations shows no later redefinition. Both gate writes on the legacy inline clause `has_permission('edit_any_case') OR (has_permission('edit_own_case') AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())`; neither calls public.can_edit_case nor references case_associated_advisors. The helper is_case_associated_advisor appears only in migs 146/147/182, none of which touch document/storage write policies. Meanwhile the app actions gate on userCanEditCase (permissions.ts:102-122 → can_edit_case RPC, mig 147), which DOES include associated advisors: prepare-upload.ts:81, finalize-upload.ts:63 (the actual documents INSERT at lines 170-194), update-document-status.ts:34 (UPDATE). So an associated advisor with edit_own_case (not the assigned advisor) passes the app check, uploads the blob + does the Drive round-trip, then the documents INSERT is rejected by RLS and the blob is cleaned up (finalize-upload.ts:189). Verify/recategorize fail the same way. This is exactly the project's named bug invariant (legacy assigned_advisor_id = actor OR edit_any_case EXCLUDES associated advisors = a bug). The read/write split is corroborated: documents_select was migrated to can_view_case (mig 039:114-121) and storage case_docs_select/delete to can_view_case (mig 040), but the corresponding write policies were left on the legacy clause. Severity High is appropriate — a legitimate, explicitly-shipped role (associated advisor, migs 146-148) cannot upload/verify/recategorize on cases they're associated with, a broken core flow, failing silently after wasted work. ONE INACCURACY in the finding (does not change is_real): it claims delete works for associated advisors, producing inconsistent behavior. That is wrong — soft_delete_document_with_tombstone (mig 027:294-352, SECURITY DEFINER) ALSO uses the legacy assigned_advisor_id clause internally (lines 323-326) and raises 'Document not found or not editable', so delete is broken too. The bug is broader/more uniform, not internally inconsistent as described. The suggested fix is also under-scoped: it should additionally cover storage case_docs_insert/case_docs_update (mig 027:92-133) and the delete RPC, all of which share the same legacy clause.

### Medium (7)

#### `DOC-UP-2-no-rate-limit` — prepare-upload / finalize-upload have no checkRateLimit despite being expensive (signed-URL alloc + 4KB sniff + full download + Drive round-trip)
- **File:** src/features/documents/actions/prepare-upload.ts:60-99; src/features/documents/actions/finalize-upload.ts:56-167
- **Evidence:** Neither action imports or calls `checkRateLimit` (grep for checkRateLimit in src/features/documents returns only sync-drive-documents.ts). prepareUploadAction issues a Supabase signed-upload-URL allocation per call; finalizeUploadAction performs a signed-read + Range fetch (magic sniff), a `storage.list`, AND a FULL `storage.download` of up to 20 MB into function memory followed by a Drive upload (lines 98-167). CLAUDE.md explicitly lists upload among 'Expensive actions go through checkRateLimit'; the bulk export route and sync-drive-documents are already guarded, but the per-file upload path is not.
- **Why it matters:** An authenticated user can loop prepare→finalize to burn Vercel function memory/time (20 MB downloads + Drive API calls) and Supabase signed-URL quota with no throttle — a cheap DoS / cost-amplification vector, and it diverges from the project's stated rate-limit policy for upload actions.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap both actions in `checkRateLimit` with subject `user:<uid>:case:<caseId>` and a window matching the cost (e.g. finalize tighter than prepare). Fail-closed on the limiter. Mirror the pattern already used in sync-drive-documents.ts and the export routes.
- **Verify:** Verified by reading the code. prepare-upload.ts (60-109) and finalize-upload.ts (56-199) neither import nor call checkRateLimit. prepareUploadAction issues supabase.storage.createSignedUploadUrl per call (93-95). finalizeUploadAction does a signed-read + Range magic sniff (98-116), a storage.list (125-127), and a FULL storage.download of up to 20MB into function memory (150-154) before a best-effort Drive upload (155-161). MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES=20MB confirmed (document.schema.ts:28). Grep for checkRateLimit across src/features/documents returns only sync-drive-documents.ts, exactly as the finding claims. The cited precedents are real: sync-drive-documents.ts gates (max 1/30s, fail-closed) and the bulk export route is guarded. Strongest corroboration: the sibling upload action case-expenses/upload-expense-receipt.ts:64-70 already uses the exact suggested pattern (checkRateLimit action='upload_expense_receipt', subject 'user:<uid>:case:<caseId>', max 30, 3600s), proving the project's stated policy applies rate-limiting to per-file upload actions and that the document upload path is the divergent one. CLAUDE.md explicitly lists upload among 'Expensive actions go through checkRateLimit'. No higher-layer throttle exists: proxy.ts only sets a request id and refreshes the session, and the actions are invoked from a client modal (upload-document-modal.tsx), so an authenticated user can loop prepare->finalize. Severity Medium is correct, not higher: both actions are gated by userHasPermission('upload_document') + userCanEditCase, so this is an authenticated-staff cost-amplification / policy-divergence issue (small trusted user base), not an unauthenticated DoS — the same class and rating as the comparable receipt-upload and bank-PDF findings.

#### `DOC-UP-3-storage-insert-rls-excludes-associated-advisors` — Storage case_docs_insert/update RLS still uses legacy assigned_advisor check — excludes associated advisors (drifts from can_edit_case)
- **File:** supabase/migrations/027_production_hardening.sql:92-133 (and 024 documents_insert lines 135-148)
- **Evidence:** `case_docs_insert` / `case_docs_update` (mig 027) and `documents_insert`/`documents_update` (mig 024) gate on `edit_any_case OR (edit_own_case AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())` — the legacy formulation that PREDATES migration 147's associated-advisor branch. The action layer correctly uses `userCanEditCase` → `can_edit_case` RPC (mig 147 lines 81-101) which DOES include `is_case_associated_advisor`. So the action authorizes an associated advisor, prepare issues a signed upload URL (createSignedUploadUrl bypasses object-INSERT RLS via the storage token), the browser PUT succeeds, but the documents-table INSERT in finalize (line 170) is evaluated under `documents_insert` RLS which has NO associated-advisor branch.
- **Why it matters:** Project AUTHZ invariant: 'Legacy assigned_advisor_id = actor OR edit_any_case EXCLUDES associated advisors = a bug.' An associated advisor (who is legitimately allowed to edit the case) gets the upload UI, uploads the bytes successfully, then the finalize INSERT is denied by RLS → orphan blob left in storage (cleanupBlob runs, but the user sees a generic failure for an action they should be allowed). Broken core flow for the associated-advisor persona + storage churn.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a migration that re-states documents_insert/documents_update and the storage case_docs_insert/case_docs_update WITH CHECK clauses to call `public.can_edit_case((storage.foldername(name))[1]::uuid)` / `public.can_edit_case(case_id)` instead of inlining the legacy assigned_advisor expression — same canonicalization mig 190 applied to borrower/income writes (R8). Safe-by-construction: it only widens to the already-authorized associated advisor.
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED by reading the actual code end-to-end. Every link in the finding's chain checks out:

1. can_edit_case INCLUDES associated advisors. supabase/migrations/147_associated_advisor_case_access.sql lines 81-101: can_edit_case() = edit_any_case OR (edit_own_case AND (assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid() OR is_case_associated_advisor(id))). is_case_associated_advisor is a real SECURITY DEFINER fn (mig 146 lines 44-58) keyed on the case_associated_advisors table, distinct from the responsible assigned_advisor_id.

2. The action layer uses the canonical guard. src/lib/auth/permissions.ts lines 102-122: userCanEditCase delegates to the can_edit_case RPC. Both prepare-upload.ts (line 81) and finalize-upload.ts (line 63) gate on userHasPermission('upload_document') AND userCanEditCase(caseId) — so an associated advisor PASSES both action gates.

3. The signed-upload PUT bypasses storage object-INSERT RLS. prepare-upload.ts line 93-95 issues createSignedUploadUrl; upload-document-modal.tsx lines 138-148 PUTs bytes to that signed URL using the embedded token (not the user session), so case_docs_insert (storage RLS) is not the gate that bites.

4. The finalize documents-table INSERT runs under legacy RLS that EXCLUDES associated advisors. finalize-upload.ts line 170 does supabase.from('documents').insert(...) as the authenticated user. The governing policy is documents_insert in migrations/024_rls_layer2_and_constraints.sql lines 135-148: WITH CHECK = upload_document AND (edit_any_case OR (edit_own_case AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())). NO is_case_associated_advisor branch. I grep-confirmed NO migration after 024/027 re-states documents_insert/documents_update or case_docs_insert/case_docs_update (highest mig is 191). The storage policies in mig 027 lines 92-133 carry the same legacy formulation.

Result for an associated advisor who is NOT the responsible advisor and lacks edit_any_case: passes prepare + the PUT + the finalize re-auth, then the documents INSERT is denied by RLS WITH CHECK -> insertErr -> cleanupBlob removes the blob -> generic 'storage' error. Broken core upload flow for a legitimately-authorized persona; matches the project's stated AUTHZ invariant that the legacy assigned_advisor-only check EXCLUDES associated advisors = a bug (same class fixed for borrower/income writes in mig 190 / R8).

Minor calibration note (finding got this right): in THIS flow the storage case_docs_insert policy is NOT the blocking point because createSignedUploadUrl bypasses it; the documents_insert table policy is the actual denial point. Both still drift from can_edit_case and the suggested fix (re-state all four to call can_edit_case / can_edit_case((storage.foldername(name))[1]::uuid)) is correct and safe-by-construction (only widens to the already-authorized associated advisor).

Severity stays Medium: it over-DENIES (no privilege escalation / no data exposure), the orphan blob is cleaned up by cleanupBlob so storage churn is bounded, but it is a broken core flow for the associated-advisor persona and a genuine drift from the canonical authz model — exactly the same severity the team assigned the R8/mig-190 fix. Not High (no security hole), not Low (real broken flow for a shipped feature).

#### `R10-doc-1` — Document soft-delete RPC still uses the legacy advisor check — excludes associated advisors (R8 gap not applied to documents)
- **File:** supabase/migrations/104_ensure_document_delete_rpc.sql:86-89 (and 027_production_hardening.sql:324-325); src/features/documents/actions/delete-document.ts:56-93
- **Evidence:** `soft_delete_document_with_tombstone` (latest definition is mig 104, also in mig 027) gates the FOR UPDATE row lookup on `public.has_permission('edit_any_case') OR (public.has_permission('edit_own_case') AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())` — it does NOT call `is_case_associated_advisor`/`can_edit_case`. But the action layer (delete-document.ts:56) gates on `userCanEditCase(caseId)`, which (via can_edit_case, mig 147) DOES include associated advisors. So an associated advisor with edit_own_case + delete_document passes the action's pre-check, the action's own defense-in-depth fetch (lines 61-67, plain documents_select RLS read = can_view_case) succeeds, then the RPC raises 'Document not found or not editable' (IF NOT FOUND). The action maps that to error:'unknown' and the modal shows the generic deleteFailed message. Migration 190 fixed exactly this legacy-check pattern for borrowers/incomes/obligations (re-pointing them at _assert_can_edit_case) but never touched the document RPC.
- **Why it matters:** An associated advisor who can legitimately edit the case (and is permitted to upload/verify documents, which DO honor associated-advisor access via finalize-upload.ts:63 and update-document-status.ts:34) is silently blocked from DELETING documents on that same case, with a misleading generic error. It is an authz inconsistency (delete is stricter than upload/verify on the same case) and a broken core flow for the associated-advisor persona — the same class of bug mig 190 was written to eliminate.
- **Suggested fix:** Re-point `soft_delete_document_with_tombstone` at the canonical guard: replace the inline `assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid()` branch in the document SELECT...FOR UPDATE with `public.can_edit_case(d.case_id)` (or `PERFORM public._assert_can_edit_case(p_case_id)` before the lookup), in a new migration that CREATE OR REPLACEs the function and NOTIFY pgrst. This makes the DB authority a superset matching userCanEditCase, exactly as mig 190 did for borrower/income RPCs.
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED. The core defect is real and reproducible. Verified by reading the actual code:

1. soft_delete_document_with_tombstone — latest definition is mig 104 (104 > 027; grep shows only those two files define it, no later redefinition). Lines 86-89 gate the SELECT...FOR UPDATE on the LEGACY check `public.has_permission('edit_any_case') OR (public.has_permission('edit_own_case') AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())`. It does NOT call is_case_associated_advisor / can_edit_case.

2. can_edit_case (mig 147 lines 81-101) and the TS helper userCanEditCase (src/lib/auth/permissions.ts:102-122) ARE associated-advisor-inclusive (can_edit_case ORs in is_case_associated_advisor).

3. Reachable mismatch confirmed in delete-document.ts: line 56 gates on userCanEditCase (associated-inclusive); the defense-in-depth fetch at 61-67 is a plain documents_select read = can_view_case which mig 039 made associated-inclusive, so it succeeds; then the RPC raises 'Document not found or not editable' (IF NOT FOUND, mig104:92-94); the action maps deleteErr to error:'unknown' (line 114) → generic deleteFailed modal. So an associated advisor with edit_own_case + delete_document silently fails to delete with a misleading error.

4. Mig 190 explicitly canonicalized borrower/income/obligation writes onto _assert_can_edit_case / can_edit_case for EXACTLY this legacy-check problem (its own header cites mig 146/147 associated advisors) and never touched the document RPC. The suggested fix mirrors mig 190 and is correct.

ONE INACCURACY in the supporting rationale (does not invalidate the finding): the finding claims upload/verify already 'DO honor associated-advisor access' so delete is inconsistently stricter. At the ACTION layer that's true (all three use userCanEditCase). But at the DB enforcement layer, the latest documents_insert + documents_update RLS policies are mig 024 (lines 135-175) — they ALSO use the legacy assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid() check and were NOT re-pointed at can_edit_case (only documents_select was, in mig 039). So upload/verify are ALSO broken for associated advisors at the DB layer (INSERT RLS-blocked; UPDATE silently no-ops). The associated-advisor exclusion is therefore BROADER than delete-only, which strengthens rather than weakens the finding — the 'delete is stricter than upload/verify' framing is wrong, but the underlying defect (document soft-delete RPC over-denies associated advisors via a legacy check mig 190 missed, with a misleading generic error) is genuinely real.

Severity Medium is appropriate: broken core flow for the associated-advisor persona with a misleading error, but it is an over-restriction (denial), not escalation/leak, and only affects associated advisors (responsible/admin/view_all unaffected). Files read: mig 104, mig 027, mig 024 (documents_insert/update legacy check), mig 022 (dropped hard documents_delete), mig 039 (documents_select→can_view_case), mig 147 (can_edit_case + is_case_associated_advisor), mig 190 (borrower/income canonicalization), delete-document.ts, finalize-upload.ts, update-document-status.ts, src/lib/auth/permissions.ts.

#### `R10-doc-2` — Delete/verify UI affordances shown to view-only users — canDeleteDocuments/canVerifyDocuments ignore can_edit_case (C-036 violation)
- **File:** src/app/(app)/cases/[id]/documents/page.tsx:45,111-112; src/features/documents/components/document-preview-actions.tsx:54,59,101
- **Evidence:** The documents page computes `canDeleteDocuments={documentPermissions.delete_document === true}` and `canVerifyDocuments={documentPermissions.verify_document === true}` from the GLOBAL permission set only (userHasPermissions('delete_document','verify_document') at page.tsx:45). There is no `userCanEditCase(caseId)` factor. These flags flow to DocumentPreviewActions, which renders the destructive Delete button (line 101) and the verify/mark-status buttons (line 59) whenever the flag is true. Contrast the upload path, which gates on `userHasPermission('upload_document') && userCanEditCase(...)` (finalize-upload.ts:63, prepare-upload.ts:81), and the case-detail UI-edit-gate invariant (C-036) established in Round 6.
- **Why it matters:** A user with view access but no edit authority on this specific case (e.g. a secretary/advisor holding view_all_cases + delete_document/verify_document but lacking edit_any_case, opening a case they are not the responsible/associated advisor of) sees Delete and verify affordances that always fail at the server (deleteDocumentAction/updateDocumentStatusAction both gate on userCanEditCase). Not a security hole — the server is fail-closed — but it is the exact dumb-component edit-gate violation C-036 forbids: view-only users must not see edit/delete affordances. Produces confusing 'failed' errors on click.
- **Suggested fix:** In documents/page.tsx compute `const canEdit = await userCanEditCase(caseId)` and pass `canDeleteDocuments={canEdit && documentPermissions.delete_document === true}` / `canVerifyDocuments={canEdit && documentPermissions.verify_document === true}` (mirror the upload gate). The server actions already enforce can_edit_case, so this only aligns the UI affordance with actual authority.
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED via full code trace. The documents page (src/app/(app)/cases/[id]/documents/page.tsx:45) computes canDeleteDocuments/canVerifyDocuments from userHasPermissions('delete_document','verify_document') ONLY — the GLOBAL permission set, with no userCanEditCase(caseId) factor (lines 111-112). These flags flow unmodified: page -> DocumentsPageContent (props 50-51, passed at 236-237) -> DocumentPreviewModal (props 30-31, passed at 187-188) -> DocumentPreviewActions, which renders the verify/mark-status buttons whenever canVerifyDocuments (line 59) and the destructive Delete button whenever canDeleteDocuments (line 101), gated only on those flags (line 54).

Server is fail-closed (so NOT a security hole, as the finding states): deleteDocumentAction (delete-document.ts:56-58) and updateDocumentStatusAction (update-document-status.ts:34-36) both call userCanEditCase before mutating. userCanEditCase (lib/auth/permissions.ts:102-122) delegates to the can_edit_case RPC.

The contrast claim is accurate: the upload path gates on userHasPermission('upload_document') && userCanEditCase(...) in BOTH finalize-upload.ts:63 and prepare-upload.ts:81 — so the codebase already knows the correct pattern; the delete/verify affordance gate just wasn't given the same treatment.

The persona is real and grantable. Migration 147 shows can_view_case (page visibility) is satisfied by view_all_cases ALONE (no advisor relationship), while can_edit_case requires edit_any_case OR (edit_own_case AND (assigned OR associated advisor)). delete_document/verify_document are separate, configurable permission keys in the 'documents' category (migs 002:103-104, 004:143), independent of the 'cases' edit permissions. So a role with view_all_cases + delete_document + verify_document but NOT edit_any_case (and not assigned/associated on this specific case) will (a) successfully load the documents page, (b) see Delete + verify buttons, (c) get a 'failed/unauthorized' error on click. This is precisely the dumb-component edit-gate violation (C-036) the Round-6 sweep established for the case workspace; the documents subpage was missed.

Severity Medium is correct — identical category and impact to R6-inline-actions-1 (Medium, user-expanded): a confusing UI affordance / C-036 invariant violation for view-only users, not a data-exposure or write-bypass hole. The suggested fix (compute canEdit = await userCanEditCase(caseId) in page.tsx and AND it into both flags, mirroring the upload gate) is sound and minimal.

#### `R-doc-1` — documents UPDATE RLS still uses legacy assigned-advisor check — excludes associated advisors from changing doc status / category
- **File:** supabase/migrations/024_rls_layer2_and_constraints.sql:150-172 (documents_update); src/features/documents/actions/update-document-status.ts:34; src/features/documents/actions/assign-document-category.ts:35-39

SAFE-BY-CONSTRUCTION: can_edit_case is a superset of the legacy check.
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED by reading the code. (1) documents_update RLS (mig 024:150-175) and documents_insert (mig 024:135-148) gate writes on the legacy `has_permission('edit_any_case') OR (has_permission('edit_own_case') AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())` — no associated-advisor branch. (2) The TS gate is canonical and broader: update-document-status.ts:34 calls userCanEditCase, which (permissions.ts:102-122) delegates to the can_edit_case RPC, and that RPC (mig 147:81-101) DOES include `OR public.is_case_associated_advisor(c.id)`. The broken core flow for the associated-advisor persona is genuine; Medium matches how the identical pattern was prioritized in mig 190.
