#### `R10-doc-3` — finalize-upload trusts client-supplied storagePath without asserting it belongs to caseId (cross-case pointer / blob-delete risk)
- **File:** src/features/documents/actions/finalize-upload.ts:56-205
- **Evidence:** FinalizeUploadInput.storagePath comes from the client and is used to sign/read/list/download the object and is stored verbatim into the row (metadata.storage_path at :182) while case_id = input.caseId (:172). There is no check that input.storagePath.startsWith(input.caseId + '/'). storagePathFor (documents.service.ts:57-65) always prefixes the case id, but finalize doesn't re-validate it. A malicious client could pass another case's path with caseId set to a case they can edit, creating a documents row whose blob pointer references a different case's object; and on a finalize failure cleanupBlob(supabase, input.storagePath) (:189) would attempt to remove that other-case path. Exploitability is bounded by the storage RLS (path seg-1 cast to case uuid) on createSignedUrl/download/remove, but the app layer should not depend solely on that.
- **Why it matters:** The STORAGE invariant explicitly requires: 'finalize-upload must verify the object/path belongs to the case the user can edit'. Without the prefix assertion the DB row and the storage object can point at different cases, undermining cross-case isolation and risking deletion of another case's blob on the cleanup path.
- **Suggested fix:** At the top of finalizeUploadAction, after auth, reject unless `input.storagePath === storagePathFor(input.caseId, input.documentId, safeFileName)` (or at minimum `input.storagePath.startsWith(`${input.caseId}/`)`). Prefer reconstructing the path server-side from caseId+documentId rather than trusting the client value.
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED by reading the code. finalize-upload.ts:56-205 takes storagePath from the client (FinalizeUploadInput.storagePath, :26), uses it verbatim to sign/sniff/list/download (:100,:107,:127,:152), stores it verbatim into metadata.storage_path (:182) while case_id=input.caseId (:172). There is NO assertion that storagePath belongs to caseId (no startsWith(caseId+'/'), no reconstruction). prepare-upload.ts:91 builds the path server-side via storagePathFor (documents.service.ts:57-65) but finalize re-trusts the client value rather than rebuilding it.

The DB documents_insert RLS (mig 024:135-148) gates ONLY on case_id editability, not on metadata.storage_path — so a row with case_id=caseB (editable) + storage_path=caseA/... inserts cleanly. No INSERT trigger validates path/case consistency (guard_document_trusted_columns, mig 027:23-80, is BEFORE UPDATE only and never inspects metadata).

The finding's own caveat is accurate: server.ts uses the cookie-bound anon client, so createSignedUrl/download/list/remove are subject to storage RLS (mig 040 case_docs_select via can_view_case; mig 027 case_docs_insert/update via edit perm; case_docs_delete via delete_document+can_view_case). That bounds the INLINE cleanupBlob remove (:189/:205, errors swallowed by .catch) and means finalize only completes if the attacker can VIEW the source case's blob.

But the finding UNDERSTATES the worst vector, which strengthens it: the retention/permanent-delete erase path bypasses RLS. collectCaseFileRefs (erase-case-files.ts:32-64) uses createAdminClient (admin.ts:19-29, SERVICE_ROLE, 'BYPASSES Row Level Security'), selects metadata.storage_path for every documents row WHERE case_id=caseId, and eraseCaseFiles (:154-181) does admin.storage.remove([...storagePaths]). So when caseB is later purged, a mismatched pointer makes the service role delete caseA's still-live blob — real cross-case data loss not bounded by any RLS.

Severity Medium is right: exploit requires a specific role combo (view source case + edit target case) plus a later purge of the target — not anonymous/trivial — but the consequence is permanent deletion of another case's documents and a DB row whose blob points at another case. Suggested fix (reconstruct path from caseId+documentId, or at minimum assert the `${caseId}/` prefix at the top of finalizeUploadAction after auth) is correct and low-cost.

Files read: src/features/documents/actions/finalize-upload.ts, prepare-upload.ts, delete-document.ts; src/features/documents/services/documents.service.ts; src/features/documents/schemas/document.schema.ts; src/lib/auth/permissions.ts; src/lib/supabase/server.ts, admin.ts; src/features/cases/services/erase-case-files.ts; migrations 020/024/026/027/040.

### Low (16)

#### `DOC-UP-5-finalize-no-zod-on-ids` — finalize-upload validates only metadata via Zod; documentId/caseId/storagePath/fileSize are not safeParsed
- **File:** src/features/documents/actions/finalize-upload.ts:69-78,170-185
- **Evidence:** `DocumentMetadataSchema.safeParse` covers category_id/borrower_id/notes/expiry_date only. `input.documentId`, `input.caseId`, `input.storagePath`, `input.fileSize`, `input.mimeType` are consumed directly (e.g. `id: input.documentId`, `file_size: input.fileSize` at lines 171,176) with no Zod shape. caseId/documentId reach the DB as the row PK/FK so a malformed UUID just fails the INSERT, but there's no `z.uuid()`/finite-number gate at the top as the project standard requires (and fileSize is only compared to storedSize when storedSize is non-null — an attacker-claimed fileSize is otherwise trusted into the row).
- **Why it matters:** Minor robustness/consistency gap vs the 'Zod safeParse, authz at top' server-action invariant; mainly relevant because once DOC-UP-1 is fixed by recomputing the path server-side, fileSize should be read from the stored object metadata rather than trusted from the client at all.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a top-level Zod schema covering documentId/caseId (z.uuid()), fileSize (z.number().int().positive().max(MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES)), mimeType (z.enum(ALLOWED_MIME_TYPES)); and persist file_size from the storage object's listed metadata size rather than input.fileSize, so the DB always reflects the real bytes.
- **Verify:** Verified against the actual code. finalize-upload.ts (C:\Users\shh92\Projects\first-crm\src\features\documents\actions\finalize-upload.ts) lines 69-78 safeParse only DocumentMetadataSchema, which (schema.ts lines 11-16) covers exactly category_id/borrower_id/notes/expiry_date. input.documentId (line 171), input.caseId (line 172), input.storagePath (line 182), and input.fileSize (line 176) are consumed with no Zod shape, matching the finding. One imprecision: input.mimeType is NOT trusted into the row — line 177 persists the server-sniffed sniffed.mime — and the finding itself acknowledges this, so the listing of mimeType is harmless. The size cross-check (lines 133-141) does only fire when storedSize !== null, so a claimed fileSize is trusted into the row when storage list() returns no size metadata (claim 4 = true).

Mitigations make this Low, not higher, exactly as rated: (a) caseId is gated by userCanEditCase(input.caseId) (line 63, uuid-typed can_edit_case RPC) and resolveUploadContext (line 89) before the INSERT, so a malformed caseId fails earlier than the finding states; (b) storage RLS (mig 027 case_docs_insert, mig 040) casts (storage.foldername(name))[1]::uuid and requires edit_any/edit_own case, so the blob itself can't land out-of-scope; (c) the documents.case_id FK + immutable-case_id trigger (mig 027) protect the row; (d) the actual byte ceiling is enforced by the bucket file_size_limit=20971520 (mig 017), so a lying fileSize can't store an oversized file — only the file_size metadata column can be wrong, a display field, not a security boundary. There is a genuine consistency gap vs the CLAUDE.md 'actions MUST validate input with Zod' invariant (documentId/caseId/fileSize sit in no schema), and the DOC-UP-1 forward note (read size from storage object metadata once the path is recomputed server-side) is reasonable. Real, correctly characterized, correctly Low.

#### `R10-doc-3` — Signed preview URL TTL is 300s, contradicting the service's documented 60s PII-exposure baseline
- **File:** src/features/documents/actions/get-document-preview-url.ts:46; src/features/documents/actions/get-document-preview-urls.ts:16,67; src/features/documents/services/documents.service.ts:69-86
- **Evidence:** Both preview actions mint signed URLs with a 300-second TTL (get-document-preview-url.ts:46 `createSignedUrl(storagePath, 300)`; get-document-preview-urls.ts:16 THUMBNAIL_TTL_SECONDS=300). The feature's own signed-URL helper signedUrlFor documents the security rationale for 60s: 'Supabase storage signed URLs are unauthenticated bearer tokens for their entire lifetime, so a URL captured from history / a corporate proxy / a screenshare gives the holder access to PII (national IDs, bank statements) for that window. The iframe preview loads instantly; 60s is plenty.' The preview actions don't use signedUrlFor and pick 5x that window.
- **Why it matters:** A leaked preview/thumbnail URL (browser history, proxy log, screenshare, referer) grants un-authenticated access to borrower PII (ID scans, bank statements) for 5 minutes instead of 1. Read-authz IS enforced at mint time (storage case_docs_select RLS gates createSignedUrl on can_view_case(path-segment-1), and the action runs under the user's session), but once minted the bearer token bypasses RLS for its whole lifetime, so TTL is the only control on a leaked link.
- **Suggested fix:** Lower the TTL toward the documented 60s baseline (or route both actions through signedUrlFor so there is a single source of truth for the PII-exposure window). 300s is defensible for the grid where many thumbnails load, but it should be a deliberate, commented deviation from the 60s baseline rather than an undocumented divergence; consider 60-120s.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. (1) Both preview actions mint 300s signed URLs: get-document-preview-url.ts:46 createSignedUrl(storagePath, 300); get-document-preview-urls.ts:16 THUMBNAIL_TTL_SECONDS=300 used at :67. (2) The documented 60s PII baseline is real and quoted accurately: documents.service.ts:67-78 signedUrlFor(..., expiresInSeconds=60) with the bearer-token/PII comment. (3) Both actions call supabase.storage.createSignedUrl directly, bypassing signedUrlFor, so there is no single source of truth for the PII window. (4) 60s is genuinely the codebase-wide baseline; every other mint uses 60s (finalize-upload.ts:100, case-expenses/get-expense-receipt-url.ts:45, tasks/task-attachment-upload.ts:128, task-general-attachment-upload.ts:100, task-attachment-actions.ts:78) — the two preview actions are the only 300s outliers. (5) Mint-time authz claim verified: migration 040_storage_rls_can_view_case.sql:21-26 gates case_docs_select on has_permission('view_case_documents') AND can_view_case(path-segment-1::uuid); actions run under the user's session, so RLS applies at mint, but the minted bearer token is unauthenticated for its whole lifetime — TTL is the only control on a leaked link. Severity stays Low: not exploitable without a URL leak AND use within the window; read-authz IS enforced at mint; the grid case has a documented UX rationale (lines 13-16). The single-doc modal (document-preview-modal.tsx remounts per open via key={doc.id}, loads one iframe instantly) is the weaker one — its 300 has no TTL comment at all. The finding is a proportionate hardening/defense-in-depth observation, correctly rated Low.

#### `R10-doc-4` — Preview actions skip Zod input validation (standards: actions MUST safeParse input)
- **File:** src/features/documents/actions/get-document-preview-url.ts:11-13; src/features/documents/actions/get-document-preview-urls.ts:29-31
- **Evidence:** getDocumentPreviewUrlAction(documentId: string) and getDocumentPreviewUrlsAction(documentIds: string[]) accept their ids untyped/unvalidated — no z.string().uuid() safeParse, unlike the sibling deleteDocumentAction which validates via DeleteDocumentSchema (delete-document.ts:15-18,47-48). The ids flow into `.eq('id', documentId)` / `.in('id', ...)` (parameterized, so no injection), and an invalid id simply yields not_found, but the project's Server Action rules state input MUST be validated with Zod safeParse.
- **Why it matters:** Pure standards-consistency gap, not exploitable (PostgREST parameterizes and a bad UUID returns no rows). Worth aligning so all document actions follow the same validate-at-top pattern and a malformed id is rejected as a clean validation error rather than reaching the DB.
- **Suggested fix:** Add `const parsed = z.string().uuid().safeParse(documentId)` (and `z.array(z.string().uuid())` for the batch) at the top of each action and return not_found/validation on failure, matching delete-document.ts.
- **Verify:** Verified against source. get-document-preview-url.ts:11-13 declares getDocumentPreviewUrlAction(documentId: string) with no Zod validation; documentId flows raw into .eq('id', documentId) (line 27). get-document-preview-urls.ts:29-31 declares getDocumentPreviewUrlsAction(documentIds: string[]) with no Zod validation; ids flow into .in('id', documentIds.slice(0, MAX_BATCH)) (line 44). The sibling delete-document.ts:15-18,47-48 does validate via DeleteDocumentSchema = z.object({ documentId: z.string().uuid(), caseId: z.string().uuid() }).safeParse(...), confirming the cited inconsistency. All factual claims in the finding are accurate.

Exploitability: correctly stated as none. Both preview actions DO gate access — supabase.auth.getUser() (unauthorized if no user) plus userHasPermission('view_case_documents'), and row access is governed by the caller's RLS (documents_select); ids are parameterized by PostgREST so a malformed UUID just returns no rows -> not_found (single) or an empty url map (batch). No injection, no authz bypass, no data leak. Batch is also bounded by MAX_BATCH=100.

Severity: Low is appropriate (matches the finding's self-rating). This is a pure standards-consistency gap, and the codebase is itself inconsistent on this rule: 8 doc actions use safeParse, assign-document-category.ts uses a manual truthy check returning error:'validation', and toggle-checklist-item.ts (plus these two preview actions) do no input validation at all. So the preview actions are not uniquely deficient — they reflect a broader pattern divergence. The suggested fix (add z.string().uuid() / z.array(z.string().uuid()) safeParse at the top, returning not_found/validation on failure) is correct and aligns them with delete-document.ts. Real but minor.

#### `R-storage-2` — Route named cleanup-orphaned-blobs performs retention erasure, not orphan-blob cleanup — no actual orphan reaper exists
- **File:** src/app/api/cron/cleanup-orphaned-blobs/route.ts:1-52 (calls eraseRetiredFiles)
- **Evidence:** The cron route is named cleanup-orphaned-blobs and the prompt expected an orphan cleaner that could race a still-referenced blob. In fact the route only calls eraseRetiredFiles(), which exclusively targets rows it SELECTs as soft-deleted-past-retention or cascade-doomed (retention-file-eraser.ts:119-145, 219-245) — it never lists the bucket and deletes unreferenced objects. So the 'orphan cleaner deletes a still-referenced blob' race does NOT exist (good), BUT the route name is misleading and there is genuinely NO reaper for blobs left behind when finalize fails after the bytes land or when Drive/Storage erasure is skipped (those are only recorded in erasure_orphan_log for MANUAL cleanup, per erase-case-files.ts:122-146). Leaked blobs from finalize-cleanup failures (cleanupBlob is .catch(()=>undefined), finalize-upload.ts:205) accumulate silently.
- **Why it matters:** Operational/clarity risk: the name implies a safety net that isn't there. Storage can slowly accumulate unreferenced PII blobs (failed finalizes, manual-cleanup orphan-log entries) with nothing automatically reclaiming them, which is a minor GDPR/LEGAL-3 footprint and a cost drift.
- **Suggested fix:** Either rename the route to cleanup-retired-files to match what it does, or add a real orphan sweep that, fail-CLOSED, lists bucket objects whose `<caseId>/<docId>` has NO matching documents/case_expenses row AND whose object is older than a safe grace (so an in-flight prepare->finalize window can't be reaped) before deleting. Keep it idempotent and behind the same CRON_SECRET + retention switch.
- **Verify:** Verified against actual code. The cron route src/app/api/cron/cleanup-orphaned-blobs/route.ts:37 calls ONLY eraseRetiredFiles() (+ recordErasureSuccess), and its own doc comment (lines 9-22) describes LEGAL-3 retention erasure, not orphan-blob cleanup — so the name is genuinely misleading. retention-file-eraser.ts confirms the eraser is strictly row-driven: eraseDocumentFiles (119-145) and eraseExpenseFiles (219-245) SELECT soft-deleted-past-retention or cascade-doomed rows from documents/case_expenses and remove those blobs; neither ever lists the bucket. The disclaimed race (reaper deleting a still-referenced blob) therefore does NOT exist — correct. No orphan reaper exists anywhere: the only storage .list() call in src/ is the single-file size check in finalize-upload.ts:127, and the 6 vercel.json crons (backup, backup-watchdog, cleanup-orphaned-blobs=the eraser, erasure-watchdog=alert-only, status-sla-check, task-reminders) include none that sweeps the bucket for unreferenced objects. Leaked-blob accumulation paths confirmed: finalize-upload.ts:205 cleanupBlob is .catch(()=>undefined) (silent on failure); finalize-upload.ts:190-193 deliberately leaves the Drive copy on insert failure; erase-case-files.ts logOrphans (122-146) records unrecoverable failures to erasure_orphan_log for MANUAL cleanup. Migration 144 (lines 127-135) corroborates: erasure_orphan_log is admin read-only and exists so the leaked file can be cleaned up manually — no automated consumer. Minor citation nit (does not affect validity): erase-case-files.ts is at src/features/cases/services/, not documents/services as implied, but the cited line range 122-146 and content are exact. Severity Low is appropriate: this is an operational/clarity issue plus slow unreferenced-PII-blob drift (minor GDPR/cost footprint), not an exploitable or data-corrupting bug; the SQL retention backstop bounds referenced rows but does not reclaim truly-orphaned blobs.

#### `R-storage-3` — Document pointer-clear is a read-modify-write of the whole metadata JSON (theoretical clobber)
- **File:** src/features/documents/services/retention-file-eraser.ts:172-187
- **Evidence:** After storage.remove() succeeds, the eraser clears storage_path by reading c.metadata captured at SELECT time (line 148-156), spreading it, deleting storage_path, and writing the WHOLE object back per row (update({ metadata: cleared })). A concurrent metadata update between the SELECT and this UPDATE would be silently overwritten. In practice these rows are soft-deleted past the retention window (>=14 days) so no UI path edits them, making the race theoretical; flagged for completeness. (The expense arm uses a column null and is not affected.)
- **Why it matters:** Lost-update on metadata if anything ever mutates a deeply-stale soft-deleted document's metadata concurrently. Low blast radius given the retention age gate.
- **Suggested fix:** Prefer a SECURITY DEFINER RPC that clears only the storage_path key server-side (jsonb - 'storage_path') in a single atomic UPDATE keyed on id, mirroring how the expense column null already works, instead of round-tripping the full JSON through TS.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. retention-file-eraser.ts:148-187 captures documents.metadata at SELECT time, then for each row spreads the captured object, deletes the storage_path key, and writes the WHOLE object back via update({ metadata: cleared }).eq('id', c.id). That is a read-modify-write of a JSONB column, so a concurrent metadata write between the SELECT and this UPDATE would be silently lost. The expense arm (lines 268-269) is genuinely immune: it does update({ receipt_path: null }).in('id', ids), a direct column null with no round-trip, matching the finding's parenthetical and its suggested-fix model.

The Low/theoretical rating is justified by cross-referencing. The eraser only touches (a) documents directly soft-deleted past the retention window (default 14d) or (b) cascade-doomed docs under a soft-deleted case. The only other full-object documents.metadata rewrites are in drive-sync-importer.ts:45-62 and drive-sync-sweeper.ts:31-49. Both operate on existingByDriveId, built in drive-document-sync.ts:96-101 with .is('deleted_at', null) — excluding directly soft-deleted rows. For cascade-doomed rows, both sync entry points are gated against soft-deleted cases: the manual action (sync-drive-documents.ts:37) requires userCanEditCase, and auto-sync runs only from cases/[id]/documents/page.tsx; can_edit_case (mig 147:92) and can_view_case (mig 147:68) both require c.deleted_at IS NULL. So no current path concurrently mutates a row the eraser processes; the lost-update needs a future writer. The SQL backstop framing is accurate: mig 139:107-113 finalizes a doc when metadata->>'storage_path' IS NULL AND drive_file_id IS NULL, which is why the eraser must null the key. Finding accurate, evidence verified, severity Low not overstated; suggested fix (jsonb - 'storage_path' RPC mirroring the expense column null) is sound.

#### `R-doc-2` — assignDocumentCategoryAction is missing the userCanEditCase gate its sibling status action has
- **File:** src/features/documents/actions/assign-document-category.ts:24-39
- **Evidence:** The action checks only `has_permission('verify_document') OR has_permission('upload_document')` and then relies entirely on the RLS .eq('case_id', caseId) match for case scoping. Its sibling update-document-status.ts:31-36 checks BOTH userHasPermission('verify_document') AND userCanEditCase(caseId). assign-document-category never calls userCanEditCase, so the only case-edit authority enforced is whatever the (legacy, see R-doc-1) documents_update RLS provides.
- **Why it matters:** A user who holds verify_document/upload_document globally but is NOT an editor of this particular case is rejected only by RLS, not by the action — inconsistent defense-in-depth, and it inherits the R-doc-1 associated-advisor exclusion. The CLAUDE.md invariant is that document/checklist mutations must check authz at the top; this one checks a feature permission but not case-edit authority.
- **Suggested fix:** Add `if (!(await userCanEditCase(caseId))) return { ok: false, error: 'unauthorized' };` after the user check, matching update-document-status.ts. Combined with R-doc-1 this makes both the action and RLS agree on can_edit_case.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. assign-document-category.ts:25-33 gates ONLY on global has_permission('verify_document') OR has_permission('upload_document') and never calls userCanEditCase; case-scoping is left to the .eq('case_id', caseId) row match plus the documents_update RLS. Its sibling update-document-status.ts:31-36 checks BOTH userHasPermission('verify_document') AND userCanEditCase(caseId), so the siblings are genuinely inconsistent. The R-doc-1 "legacy RLS / associated-advisor exclusion" cross-reference is also accurate: the live documents_update policy is from migration 024 (supabase/migrations/024_rls_layer2_and_constraints.sql:150-174), which inlines edit_any_case OR (edit_own_case AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid()). Migration 147 added the associated-advisor branch to cases_update/can_view_case/can_edit_case/_assert_can_edit_case, and migration 190 realigned borrower/income/obligation RLS to can_edit_case, but NEITHER touched documents_update (verified via grep over all migrations: the last definition of documents_update is migration 024). So the documents UPDATE RLS diverges from can_edit_case and excludes associated advisors. This violates the CLAUDE.md "authz checked at the server boundary / top of action" convention and the defense-in-depth pattern its sibling follows.

Severity downgraded from Medium to Low: this is a defense-in-depth/consistency gap, not an exploitable escalation. The migration-024 documents_update RLS plus the migration-027 guard_document_trusted_columns trigger still block the DB write for a user lacking case-edit authority — the worst observable effect is a generic error:'unknown' instead of a clean error:'unauthorized'. Moreover the RLS divergence is over-restrictive (it would block an associated advisor who legitimately has can_edit_case from re-categorizing), so the direction is a functional over-deny, not an unauthorized write. The suggested fix (add `if (!(await userCanEditCase(caseId))) return { ok: false, error: 'unauthorized' };` after the user check) is correct and would make the action consistent with its sibling; pairing it with realigning documents_update to can_edit_case (R-doc-1) would make action and RLS agree and restore associated-advisor access. Files read: src/features/documents/actions/assign-document-category.ts, update-document-status.ts; src/lib/auth/permissions.ts (userCanEditCase delegates to can_edit_case RPC); migrations 008, 011, 024, 027, 039, 147, 190; UI caller src/features/documents/components/uncategorized-card.tsx.

#### `R-doc-3` — sendDocumentRequestAction sends a client-facing email with no rate limit
- **File:** src/features/documents/actions/send-document-request.ts:22-54
- **Evidence:** The action authorizes via userCanEditCase, resolves the primary borrower email, then calls sendDocumentRequestEmail → sendEmail (Resend) with no checkRateLimit anywhere in the path. CLAUDE.md lists 'sending mail' as an expensive action that must go through checkRateLimit (already applied to export-pdf/xlsx, run-backup, import-cases, sync-drive-documents, lookup-borrower).
- **Why it matters:** An authorized-but-careless or compromised advisor session can repeatedly fire branded emails to a client's inbox (the dialog re-opens on 'unknown', so a held button can resend). No per-user/per-case budget. This is the only advisor-initiated outbound-mail action reviewed that lacks the gate.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap with checkRateLimit({ action: 'send_document_request', subject: `user:${uid}:case:${caseId}`, max: ~10, windowSeconds: 3600, failMode: 'open' }) before the send, returning a typed 'rate_limited' code the dialog maps to a translated message.
- **Verify:** Core technical claim VERIFIED by reading the full path. src/features/documents/actions/send-document-request.ts:22-54 has no checkRateLimit; chain is action -> sendDocumentRequestEmail (services/document-request-email.ts, no gate) -> sendEmail (lib/email/send.ts, no gate) -> Resend. Only gates are DocumentRequestEmailSchema.safeParse and userCanEditCase (can_edit_case RPC, lib/auth/permissions.ts:102). It does send a branded client-facing email. CLAUDE.md convention and the email_simulator_report precedent confirm the gate is expected: emailScenarioReportAction (simulators/actions/email-scenario-report.ts:52-59) gates an analogous advisor->client email at 30/hr, failMode closed, returning a typed rate_limited code -- so the suggested fix is sound and there is a clear consistency gap.

COMPARATIVE CLAIM REFUTED (overstated): finding says this is 'the only advisor-initiated outbound-mail action reviewed that lacks the gate.' False -- sendClientEmailAction (cases/actions/send-client-email.ts:45-104), the general advisor->client email with the same userCanEditCase -> primary-borrower-email -> sendBrandedClientEmail shape, ALSO lacks checkRateLimit. At least two such actions are ungated; this one is not unique.

DIALOG-RESEND CLAIM NARROWER THAN STATED: send-doc-request-button.tsx:97 keeps the dialog open only on error 'unknown' (a FAILED send or parse failure, action lines 50-51); a successful send clears the draft and closes the dialog, and a useTransition pending guard blocks double-fire within one in-flight call. So 'a held button can resend' requires repeated clicks or a failing send, not a single hold.

SEVERITY: real defense-in-depth gap, but bounded -- authz-gated to staff who can edit the case, no anon/public path, recipient fixed to the case's own primary borrower (not arbitrary addresses, so not an open spam relay), and blast radius limited to spamming one known client + Resend cost. Combined with the incorrect 'only one' framing and narrower resend vector, Medium is slightly overstated; Low is appropriate. Fix should ideally also cover sendClientEmailAction for consistency.

#### `R-doc-4` — send-document-request returns 'unknown' for Zod parse failure, causing the dialog to loop instead of stopping
- **File:** src/features/documents/actions/send-document-request.ts:23-24; src/features/documents/components/send-doc-request-button.tsx:88-97
- **Evidence:** On `DocumentRequestEmailSchema.safeParse` failure the action returns `{ ok: false, error: 'unknown' }` (not a 'validation' code — the Result union doesn't even include 'validation'). In the component, `res.error !== 'unknown'` is the only branch that closes the dialog; an 'unknown' result keeps the draft open and shows the generic 'failed' toast.
- **Why it matters:** A structurally-invalid payload (e.g. body > 5000 chars) yields a retryable 'failed' state that can never succeed on retry — the dialog stays open and the user re-submits the same invalid text. Also diverges from the other actions, which return a distinct 'validation' code.
- **Suggested fix:** Add 'validation' to the Result union, return it on parse failure, and map it in the dialog to a non-retryable message (and close the dialog like the other terminal errors).
- **Verify:** The code observations are accurate. In src/features/documents/actions/send-document-request.ts:23-24, a Zod parse failure returns {ok:false, error:'unknown'}, and the Result union (lines 12-14) does NOT include a 'validation' code. In src/features/documents/components/send-doc-request-button.tsx:88-97, the toast-key map sends 'unknown' to the generic 'failed' branch, and line 97 (`if (res.error !== 'unknown') setDraft(null)`) keeps the dialog open only for 'unknown' — so a parse failure produces a retryable-looking 'failed' state with the dialog still open. The divergence claim is also correct: dozens of sibling actions (e.g. post-case-comment.ts:26, edit-case-comment.ts:22, save-borrower.ts) return a distinct 'validation' code. So the finding is a genuine consistency/robustness defect.

However, the finding's concrete harm — "body > 5000 chars yields an unwinnable retry loop" — is essentially unreachable via the UI, so even Low is at the optimistic end. The schema (document-request.schema.ts) requires subject 1-200 and body 1-5000 after trim; the ComposeEmailDialog mirrors every one of those constraints client-side: the body Textarea has maxLength={5000} (compose-email-dialog.tsx:97), the subject Input has maxLength={200} (line 82), and the Send button is disabled when !subject.trim() || !body.trim() (line 106). caseId is a prop (z.string min1/max100), not free input. Thus a normal user cannot construct a payload that fails safeParse, and the described loop cannot occur except by bypassing the client (devtools/scripted call), where the only affected party is the attacker themselves.

Verdict: real as a low-severity code-quality / convention-consistency nit (action should add a 'validation' code, return it on parse failure, and the dialog should treat it as terminal). Not a practically reachable user-facing bug. Severity stays Low (the floor); reachability is the only caveat.

#### `R-doc-5` — assignDocumentCategoryAction validates ids as non-empty strings, not UUIDs, and never validates caseId
- **File:** src/features/documents/actions/assign-document-category.ts:12-17
- **Evidence:** Input check is `if (!documentId || !categoryId) return { ok: false, error: 'validation' };`. There is no Zod schema; documentId/categoryId are not validated as UUIDs and caseId is not validated at all (just passed to .eq('case_id', caseId)). Every sibling action that takes ids uses a Zod schema (ChecklistOrderSchema = z.array(z.string().uuid()), DocumentRequestEmailSchema, AddChecklistTemplateSchema).
- **Why it matters:** Malformed input reaches the DB and fails as a generic 'unknown' (uuid cast error) rather than a clean 'validation', and it's inconsistent with the project Zod-at-the-boundary standard. Not a security hole (RLS + FK still constrain), but a quality/consistency gap.
- **Suggested fix:** Introduce a small Zod object schema { documentId: z.string().uuid(), caseId: z.string().uuid(), categoryId: z.string().uuid() } and safeParse at the top, mirroring the other doc actions.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. assign-document-category.ts:17 validates only with `if (!documentId || !categoryId) return {ok:false, error:'validation'}` — non-empty-string check, no Zod, no .uuid(). caseId is never validated (omitted from the truthiness guard; passed straight to .eq('case_id', caseId) at line 39). The sibling-inconsistency claim is accurate and stronger than stated: the closest parallel deleteDocumentAction (same documentId+caseId shape) uses DeleteDocumentSchema = z.object({documentId: z.string().uuid(), caseId: z.string().uuid()}) with safeParse; cited siblings ChecklistOrderSchema (z.array(z.string().uuid())), DocumentRequestEmailSchema, AddChecklistTemplateSchema all verified, plus sync-drive-documents and reorder-checklist-items. documents.id/case_id/category_id are all UUID columns (008_documents.sql:12-15), so malformed ids produce a Postgres uuid-cast error caught at line 41 and returned as generic 'unknown' rather than clean 'validation' — exactly as described. Severity Low is correct, not under-stated: line 21 requires an authenticated user, lines 25-33 gate on verify_document/upload_document permission, and RLS + the .eq('case_id') constraint + FKs prevent any invalid/cross-case write. Sole UI caller (uncategorized-card.tsx:76) passes server-rendered ids, so the issue only surfaces on crafted requests to this public server-action endpoint. Worst case is a confusing error code — a quality/consistency gap, not a security or correctness defect. (Noted extra: unlike deleteDocumentAction it also lacks a per-case userCanEditCase gate, still Low.) Suggested fix (mirror DeleteDocumentSchema with a 3-field UUID object schema) is appropriate.

#### `R-doc-6` — addChecklistTemplateAction dedup is a racy read-then-insert; concurrent template adds can duplicate manual rows
- **File:** src/features/documents/actions/add-checklist-template.ts:41-74; supabase/migrations/099_case_checklist_items.sql:47-49
- **Evidence:** The action SELECTs existing labels, computes `toAdd = items.filter(label => !existing.has(label.trim()))`, then loops add_case_checklist_item. Template items are inserted as manual rows (source='manual', document_category_id NULL). The only unique index (uq_case_checklist_case_category) is partial WHERE document_category_id IS NOT NULL, so it does NOT cover label-only manual rows. Two concurrent template picks (or a double-click) can both observe the label absent and both insert it.
- **Why it matters:** Duplicate checklist rows for the same document on a case — cosmetic clutter the user must remove manually. Low blast radius (no data loss / cross-case leak), and single-request re-picks are already deduped; only the concurrent/double-submit window is exposed.
- **Suggested fix:** Either debounce/disable the picker while pending in the UI, or add an idempotent insert in the RPC (e.g. a unique index on (case_id, lower(btrim(label))) for manual rows with ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING) so dedup is enforced atomically at the DB rather than in app-level read-then-write.
- **Verify:** Confirmed the core mechanism by reading the code. add-checklist-template.ts:42-58 does a read-then-filter dedup (SELECT label -> Set -> toAdd = items.filter(!existing.has(label.trim()))), then inserts each via the add_case_checklist_item RPC. That RPC (migration 099:207-239) unconditionally INSERTs a manual row (source='manual', document_category_id NULL) with no existence check and no ON CONFLICT. The only unique index, uq_case_checklist_case_category (099:47-49), is partial WHERE document_category_id IS NOT NULL, so it does NOT cover label-only manual rows. A grep confirms case_checklist_items and add_case_checklist_item are defined ONLY in migration 099 — no later migration adds a label unique index or idempotent insert. So the racy read-then-insert window genuinely exists and nothing at the DB enforces label dedup; two truly-concurrent requests can both insert the same label. Finding is real. Severity correctly Low: impact is cosmetic duplicate rows the user can delete via remove_case_checklist_item; no data loss, no cross-case leak; gated behind userCanEditCase + _assert_can_edit_case (staff-only, same-case). One imprecision in the evidence: the 'double-click' vector it cites is already closed in the only UI caller (checklist-template-picker.tsx) — it uses useTransition with disabled={isPending} on both the trigger button (line 72) and every menu item (line 93), so a second click is blocked synchronously before the first action returns. The remaining exposure is only genuinely concurrent multi-client requests (two tabs/devices/users or a non-UI caller) — a narrow window. The suggested fix (lower(btrim(label)) unique index for manual rows + ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING) is the correct atomic remedy.

#### `R-doc-7` — logClientEmail is awaited after the email already sent, adding a round-trip to user-perceived latency
- **File:** src/features/documents/actions/send-document-request.ts:52-54
- **Evidence:** After the send succeeds, the action does `await logClientEmail({...})` before returning ok. logClientEmail is best-effort (its own try/catch, never throws), so the success path waits on a non-critical DB insert. The codebase convention (MEMORY: 'No awaited email/external HTTP in server actions' / use after()) is to keep best-effort side-effects off the response path.
- **Why it matters:** The send-result genuinely must be awaited (it drives no_email/not_configured/unknown), so this is not the prod-bug-class awaited-email issue; but the activity-log write is purely best-effort and needlessly delays the toast. Minor latency only.
- **Suggested fix:** Move the logClientEmail call into next/server `after(() => logClientEmail({...}))` so the success response returns immediately and the log persists out-of-band, consistent with the established best-effort pattern.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. In src/features/documents/actions/send-document-request.ts:49-54, sendDocumentRequestEmail is correctly awaited (line 49) because its result drives the user-facing error codes (not_configured/unknown), but logClientEmail is then ALSO awaited on the response path (line 53) before returning ok. I verified logClientEmail (src/features/case-activity/services/client-email-log.service.ts:66-85) is genuinely best-effort: it has its own try/catch, swallows all errors (console.error only), returns Promise<void>, and its result is never used. It is not free — it does a fresh createClient(), an auth.getUser() round-trip, and an insert, so it adds ~2 round-trips to user-perceived latency before the toast.

The codebase convention is to keep such best-effort side-effects off the response path via next/server after(). This is documented in MEMORY (feedback_no_awaited_email_in_actions: "best-effort side effects ... must run via after(), NOT await") and, decisively, the sibling action send-client-email.ts:79-101 imports `after` and wraps the exact same logClientEmail call (line 89) inside after(), with a comment explaining the dialog spun when the work was awaited. So the suggested fix (after(() => logClientEmail(...))) matches the established pattern.

Refutation attempt failed: there is no correctness reason to await the log (return value unused, never throws). The only counterpoint is that a third call site, src/features/simulators/actions/email-scenario-report.ts:111, has the identical un-deferred awaited-logClientEmail pattern — but that shows the convention is applied inconsistently, not that awaiting is intended. 

Severity stays Low (not adjusted): the finding correctly self-distinguishes this from the prod-bug class (the 10s awaited-Resend issue) — the slow Resend send is correctly awaited here; only a couple of best-effort DB round-trips are needlessly on the response path. Real but minor latency.

#### `R10-doc-4` — assignDocumentCategoryAction skips the canonical userCanEditCase guard used by every sibling doc action
- **File:** src/features/documents/actions/assign-document-category.ts:19-44
- **Evidence:** This action checks only `verify_document OR upload_document` global permissions (via has_permission RPC), then does a direct `documents.update({category_id}).eq('id',documentId).eq('case_id',caseId)`. It does NOT call userCanEditCase, unlike delete-document.ts:56, update-document-status.ts:34, prepare-upload.ts:81 and finalize-upload.ts:63 which all add the per-case edit check. Case scoping here rests entirely on the documents_update RLS (which itself is the legacy assigned_advisor_id policy — see R10-doc-1).
- **Why it matters:** Inconsistent with the documented AUTHZ canonicalization (case-scoped writes canonicalize on userCanEditCase / can_edit_case). It is a defense-in-depth gap: if the documents_update RLS were ever loosened, a user with a global upload/verify permission could recategorize documents on cases they cannot edit. It also means associated advisors are blocked here too (RLS), compounding R10-doc-1.
- **Suggested fix:** Add `if (!(await userCanEditCase(caseId))) return { ok:false, error:'unauthorized' };` after the auth check, matching the other document actions, and validate caseId with z.string().uuid().
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED but severity over-stated (Medium -> Low).

Code facts verified:
- assign-document-category.ts:12-48 checks only the global permissions via has_permission RPC (verify_document at L25-27, upload_document at L28-30, OR at L31-33), then does a direct documents.update({category_id}).eq('id',documentId).eq('case_id',caseId) (L35-39). It does NOT call userCanEditCase. Confirmed.
- The four named siblings all DO call userCanEditCase at exactly the cited lines: delete-document.ts:56, update-document-status.ts:34, prepare-upload.ts:81 (combined `||` with userHasPermission), finalize-upload.ts:63. Confirmed verbatim.
- caseId is never validated (only `if (!documentId || !categoryId)` truthiness at L17); no z.string().uuid(). The suggested-fix point is accurate.
- documents_update RLS: current definition is migration 024 (lines 150-175), USING/WITH CHECK = (verify_document OR upload_document) AND EXISTS(cases WHERE deleted_at IS NULL AND (edit_any_case OR (edit_own_case AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid()))). I grepped all migrations: documents_update is only ever defined in 011 (superseded) and 024 (current). It was NOT re-pointed at can_edit_case by mig 147 (which only touched cases_select/cases_update/can_view_case/can_edit_case/_assert_can_edit_case) nor by mig 190 (which canonicalized borrowers/incomes/obligations onto can_edit_case but left documents alone). So documents_update still uses the legacy assigned_advisor_id check with no associated-advisor (is_case_associated_advisor) branch.

Implications confirming the finding:
1. Defense-in-depth gap is REAL: app-layer case-edit gate is missing here while present on every sibling.
2. The compounding-with-R10-doc-1 claim is ACCURATE: associated advisors who legitimately have can_edit_case ARE blocked from recategorizing because documents_update RLS uses the stale assigned_advisor_id check (the action would return 'unknown' from the RLS rejection).

Why Low not Medium: there is NO live privilege escalation today. The documents_update RLS DOES enforce a case-edit check (edit_any_case OR edit_own+assigned), so a user with only a global upload/verify permission but no case-edit authority cannot recategorize — the direct .update is rejected by RLS and the action returns 'unknown'. The finding's exploit ("if the documents_update RLS were ever loosened...") is explicitly hypothetical/conditional, and the finding itself labels this "a defense-in-depth gap." The present functional bug (associated advisors blocked) is caused by R10-doc-1's stale RLS, not by this missing app-layer guard — adding userCanEditCase here would NOT unblock associated advisors (they'd still hit the legacy RLS). So this item is a consistency/fail-fast/defense-in-depth improvement with no current exploitable impact, which fits Low. The suggested fix (add userCanEditCase + z.uuid() on caseId) is correct and low-risk; it does not by itself resolve the associated-advisor block (that needs the R10-doc-1 RLS fix).

Relevant files: C:\Users\shh92\Projects\first-crm\src\features\documents\actions\assign-document-category.ts; C:\Users\shh92\Projects\first-crm\src\features\documents\actions\delete-document.ts; C:\Users\shh92\Projects\first-crm\src\features\documents\actions\update-document-status.ts; C:\Users\shh92\Projects\first-crm\src\features\documents\actions\prepare-upload.ts; C:\Users\shh92\Projects\first-crm\src\features\documents\actions\finalize-upload.ts; C:\Users\shh92\Projects\first-crm\src\lib\auth\permissions.ts; C:\Users\shh92\Projects\first-crm\supabase\migrations\024_rls_layer2_and_constraints.sql (documents_update at L150-175); C:\Users\shh92\Projects\first-crm\supabase\migrations\147_associated_advisor_case_access.sql; C:\Users\shh92\Projects\first-crm\supabase\migrations\190_canonical_can_edit_case_borrower_income_writes.sql; caller C:\Users\shh92\Projects\first-crm\src\features\documents\components\uncategorized-card.tsx.

#### `R10-doc-5` — UploadDocumentModal: 313 lines (over 250) and embeds the 3-phase upload orchestration (application logic in a component)
- **File:** src/features/documents/components/upload-document-modal.tsx:99-180
- **Evidence:** File is 313 lines (component limit 250). handleSubmit contains the full prepare→PUT→finalize orchestration, FormData extraction, client mirror of size/MIME validation (validateFile :65-72) and server-error-code-to-i18n mapping (mapErrorMessage :91-97). Per the 'dumb components' rule, fetch/orchestration belongs in a hook (e.g. use-document-upload).

- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the file and cross-references. (1) Line count: `wc -l` returns exactly 313 lines, over the 250-line component limit codified in CLAUDE.md — a 25% overage. (2) handleSubmit (lines 99-180) embeds the full 3-phase upload orchestration: prepareUploadAction (l.120) → raw fetch PUT to the signed Supabase Storage URL (l.138, a direct infrastructure call inside the component) → finalizeUploadAction (l.155), plus FormData extraction (l.111-115), pending-state management, and per-phase error branching. This is application orchestration living in a UI component, violating the "dumb components" rule (NO business logic / NO direct data fetching in components). (3) validateFile (l.65-72) is a client mirror of the server-side guards in prepare-upload.ts (l.64-69: size==0, MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES, ALLOWED_MIME_TYPES) — logic that belongs in domain/. (4) mapErrorMessage (l.91-97) is server-error-code→i18n mapping. The suggested fix is viable and consistent with existing patterns: hooks/use-document-previews.ts already wraps a server action in a hook within this same feature, and a domain/ folder exists (sanitize-filename.ts) where validateFile could move. Refutation attempt: the header line cite ':99-180' is actually handleSubmit's range not the file's, but the substantive claims are all accurate and present. Severity correctly Low — this is a maintainability/architecture-conformance issue (file-size limit + layering), not a correctness, security, or data-loss bug; both prepare and finalize actions independently enforce auth (userCanEditCase/userHasPermission) and validation server-side, so the client mirror is purely UX.

#### `R10-doc-7` — Hardcoded non-i18n aria-label "clear" on the upload file-clear button

#### `R10-doc-8` — Stale loading.tsx comment claims the page does a Drive sync before rendering (it no longer does)
- **File:** src/app/(app)/cases/[id]/documents/loading.tsx:4-6
- **Evidence:** Comment: 'The documents page does a Drive sync + 4-way fetch before rendering, so navigation here can take a beat'. The page now fire-and-forgets autoSyncIfStale (page.tsx:32 `void ... .catch`) precisely so first paint is NOT blocked on Drive; it does a 6-way Promise.all of DB reads, not a sync.
- **Why it matters:** Misleading documentation that contradicts the deliberate non-blocking design (page.tsx:26-37), could lead a future maintainer to re-introduce the blocking await.
- **Suggested fix:** Update the comment to: background (non-blocking) Drive freshness check + parallel DB fetch; the skeleton covers the DB fetch latency.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading both files. loading.tsx:3-7 comment states "The documents page does a Drive sync + 4-way fetch before rendering, so navigation here can take a beat". Both clauses are contradicted by page.tsx: (1) the Drive sync is fire-and-forget, NOT awaited before render — page.tsx:32 `void autoSyncIfStale(caseId).catch(...)`, and the adjacent comment (lines 26-31) explicitly documents that it was DELIBERATELY changed from a blocking await so first paint is no longer blocked on the Google API hop ("The page now renders from the DB immediately"); (2) it is not a "4-way" fetch — the Promise.all at lines 39-46 has SIX members (getCaseById, listDocumentsForCase, listDocumentCategories, listBorrowersForCase, getLocale/parseLocale, userHasPermissions) plus a 7th sequential await (getCaseDocumentChecklist, line 53). The loading.tsx comment thus describes the pre-refactor behavior. The risk (a maintainer re-introducing the blocking await) is genuine but indirect and partially mitigated by page.tsx's own counter-comment. Comment-only defect in a skeleton component, no runtime/security/data impact — Low is correctly rated.

### Refuted (1)

- `DOC-UP-4-message-leak-prepare` prepare-upload returns translation-key 'message' for client mapping — fine — but finalize/prepare 'message' field is typed to allow arbitrary strings; ensure only keys flow — Verified against the actual code; the finding describes no real defect and self-admits "No live leak... defensive only."

Facts confirmed:
1. prepare-upload.ts and finalize-upload.ts: every populated `message` is one of three hardcoded i18n KEYS ('fileRequired', 'fileTooLarge', 'fileTypeNotAllowed'). Supabase errors are routed through safeDbError(...) into console.error server-side (prepare:97, finalize:102/188) and the returned object carries ONLY {ok:false, error:'storage'} with no message. So there is zero raw error.message leak today (finding concedes this).
2. db-error-log.ts: safeDbError returns {code, message} only for server logging, and its output is NEVER assigned to the actions' returned `message` field — only ever passed to console.error.
3. The SOLE consumer of the returned `message` is upload-document-modal.tsx lines 132/168, both via mapErrorMessage (lines 91-97), which is an ALLOWLIST: it maps only the three known keys and DEFAULTS any other value to tErr('uploadFailed'). This is a second defense layer the finding did not account for — even a hypothetical future edit assigning err.message to the returned message would be discarded by the UI, never rendered.

The "risk" is therefore doubly mitigated and purely hypothetical (a future-edit footgun). There is no bug, no leak, no incorrect behavior. The compiler-tightening suggestion (narrow message to a key union) is a minor hardening nicety with marginal merit, but it does not describe an existing problem in the code. Marking invalid/not-real per the default-to-false instruction for non-substantiated defects.


## Round 11 — integrations / backup / restore / Google OAuth

**raw 16 -> confirmed 16 / refuted 0  (High 2, Medium 3, Low 11)**

### High (2)

#### `DRIVE-1` — Document write RLS still uses the legacy guard — associated advisors are locked out, orphaning their Drive uploads
- **File:** supabase/migrations/024_rls_layer2_and_constraints.sql:135-175 (documents_insert/documents_update); supabase/migrations/027_production_hardening.sql:92-133 (case_docs_insert/case_docs_update on storage.objects)
- **Evidence:** documents_insert (024:137-148), documents_update (024:150-175), and the storage policies case_docs_insert/case_docs_update (027:100-102, 116-117, 129-130) all inline the LEGACY guard: `public.has_permission('edit_any_case') OR (public.has_permission('edit_own_case') AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())`. Migration 147 (associated_advisor_case_access) updated can_edit_case(), can_view_case(), cases_update, cases_select, and _assert_can_edit_case() to also allow `public.is_case_associated_advisor(id)`, but it NEVER re-pointed these documents-table or storage write policies at can_edit_case(). Meanwhile the application layer authorizes uploads via userCanEditCase, which DOES include associated advisors: finalizeUploadAction (finalize-upload.ts:63), finalizeTaskAttachmentUploadAction (task-attachment-upload.ts:69,103), and syncDriveDocumentsAction (sync-drive-documents.ts:37-38) all gate on userCanEditCase. So an associated advisor passes the app gate, the file is successfully uploaded to Drive via uploadCaseDocumentToDrive (finalize-upload.ts:155-165), and then the documents INSERT at finalize-upload.ts:170 is silently rejected by RLS. cleanupBlob removes the storage object but the Drive file is intentionally left (finalize-upload.ts:190-193 comment), so the case ends with an orphan Drive file and NO documents row.
- **Why it matters:** This is the exact legacy-guard bug the base invariants flag. An associated advisor (a supported, shipped role per migs 146-148) cannot persist any uploaded document or task attachment for a case they are associated with — the upload appears to succeed at the Drive level but no DB record is created, producing a confusing partial failure and an orphan Drive file on every attempt. It is a data-integrity + broken-core-flow defect with the same shape as R8's borrower/income canonicalization fix (mig 190), but documents/storage were missed.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a migration that DROP+CREATE documents_insert, documents_update, case_docs_insert, case_docs_update to gate on public.can_edit_case(case_id) (and the case_docs_* equivalent resolving case id from (storage.foldername(name))[1]::uuid) instead of the inlined assigned_advisor_id check, mirroring how mig 190 canonicalized borrower/income writes. Keep the upload_document / verify_document permission AND-branch; only replace the case-edit branch. Self-register in schema_version.
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED by reading the code. documents_insert (024:137-148) and documents_update (024:150-175) inline the legacy guard `edit_any_case OR (edit_own_case AND assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())`; case_docs_insert/update (027:92-133) carry the same. Migration 147 added the is_case_associated_advisor OR-branch to cases_select/update, can_view_case, can_edit_case, _assert_can_edit_case ONLY — it never re-pointed these four document/storage write policies. Migration 040 re-pointed only case_docs_select/delete (read/delete) at can_view_case, not insert/update. Migration 190 canonicalized borrower/income/obligation writes onto can_edit_case but explicitly did not touch documents or storage write policies; a grep across all migrations confirms the 024/027 definitions are the live ones. App layer: userCanEditCase (permissions.ts:102-122) delegates to the can_edit_case RPC which DOES include associated advisors; prepareUploadAction (prepare-upload.ts:81) and finalizeUploadAction (finalize-upload.ts:63) and syncDriveDocumentsAction (sync-drive-documents.ts:37) all gate on it, so an associated advisor passes the app gate. The blob lands via createSignedUploadUrl (prepare-upload.ts:93) which bypasses case_docs_insert RLS via the signed token; Drive upload succeeds (finalize-upload.ts:155-165); then the documents INSERT at finalize-upload.ts:170 runs under the caller RLS context and is silently rejected by the legacy documents_insert policy. cleanupBlob removes the storage object but the Drive file is intentionally left (lines 190-193), producing an orphan Drive file and no documents row on EVERY associated-advisor upload. Drive sync (drive-document-sync.ts:23,97) uses request-scoped createClient and inserts into documents, so it hits the same lockout. Two minor framing corrections that do not change the verdict: (1) for the signed-URL upload path the case_docs_insert/update storage policies are bypassed by the token, so the documents-table policy is the operative gate there, not the storage policy; (2) the task-attachment path writes to the separate task_attachments table (mig 157, can_view_task RLS), not documents_insert, so that one citation is imprecise. The documents-table + Drive-sync vectors and the orphan-file harm narrative are fully substantiated. High severity upheld: broken core flow for a shipped role (associated advisors, migs 146-148) plus data-integrity orphan Drive files; same shape as the R8 mig-190 fix that missed documents/storage.

#### `BACKUP-1` — Backup omits four persistent business-data tables — silent data loss on disaster-recovery restore
- **File:** src/features/backup/services/backup-snapshot.service.ts:14-43
- **Evidence:** BACKUP_TABLES is an explicit allowlist of 28 tables. It OMITS four tables that hold real, user-entered, soft-deletable business data (verified in src/types/database.ts): case_expenses (id 1594 — amount/description/expense_date/receipt refs, deleted_at), case_checklist_items (id 1518 — is_done/done_by/label/required-at-stage per case, deleted_at), task_comments (id 3413 — author_id/body/event_type conversation threads, deleted_at; the case-comment thread foundation), and case_bank_statuses (id 1344 — per-office bank status config). None of these names appear anywhere in src/features/backup (grep returned no matches), so they are never written to a snapshot. Because the restore RPC only re-inserts tables present in the snapshot AND its hardcoded v_tables, these rows can never be recovered. The allowlist comment claims it excludes only 'ephemeral / bookkeeping' tables, but these are durable financial/checklist/conversation records.
- **Why it matters:** This is the disaster-recovery feature whose entire purpose is to make data loss survivable. After a catastrophic DB loss, a restore from the most recent backup would come back with ALL case expenses, ALL document-checklist progress, ALL task/case comment threads, and bank-status config permanently gone — while the restore reports success (it counts only the tables it knows about). For a mortgage office, expense records and checklist progress are operationally and financially material. The existing parity test (backup-restore-allowlist.test.ts) only guards backup<->restore lockstep; it cannot detect a table that is missing from BOTH lists.
- **Suggested fix:** Add case_expenses, case_checklist_items, task_comments, and case_bank_statuses to BACKUP_TABLES, then add each to the restore RPC's v_tables (new migration, CREATE OR REPLACE of restore_backup_snapshot) in FK-parent-first order (case_bank_statuses early; case_expenses/case_checklist_items after cases; task_comments after tasks). Add the soft-delete ones (case_expenses, case_checklist_items, task_comments) to v_tables_with_deleted_at so restored 'deleted' rows aren't reborn invisible. Verify columns carry no secrets before inclusion (none do). Re-run the parity test. Audit every remaining unlisted public table once and document each exclusion with a reason in the BACKUP_TABLES comment.
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED. backup-snapshot.service.ts:14-43 defines BACKUP_TABLES as a 28-entry explicit allowlist; case_expenses, case_checklist_items, task_comments, and case_bank_statuses are all absent, and a Grep over src/features/backup returned zero matches for any of the four — they are never written to a snapshot. The restore RPC (latest = migration 115_restore_includes_scenarios.sql) iterates a hardcoded v_tables array (lines 37-44) that likewise omits all four; the loop only re-inserts tables present in v_tables, so even a snapshot row for these tables could never be restored. This is the identical silent-data-loss failure mode that migration 115 itself was created to fix for mortgage_scenarios/scenario_tracks (documented in its header), establishing both the bug pattern and its severity as precedent in this codebase.

Durability of the omitted data, verified against migrations + database.ts: case_expenses (migration 081) holds real financial records — amount NUMERIC(15,2), expense_date, description, receipt refs — with soft-delete (deleted_at/deleted_by). case_checklist_items (migration 099) holds per-case document-checklist progress (is_done/done_by/done_at/label, hard-delete). task_comments (migration 120; database.ts:3413) holds conversation threads (author_id/body/event_type, deleted_at). case_bank_statuses (database.ts:1344) is a global bank-status lookup/config table (key/name_he/name_en/color/is_system, no case_id, no deleted_at) analogous to case_statuses which IS backed up. The parity test (backup-restore-allowlist.test.ts:75-89) only compares the two lists against each other and has no whole-schema coverage check, so it genuinely cannot detect a table missing from BOTH lists — as the finding states.

Two minor factual errors in the finding that do not change the verdict: (1) it asserts case_checklist_items has a deleted_at column — it does NOT (migration 099 has no deleted_at; database.ts Row confirms), so the suggested fix to add it to v_tables_with_deleted_at is wrong for that one table. (2) case_bank_statuses is a global config/lookup table, not per-case 'user-entered business data'; its loss impact is lower than the other three. Despite these, the central problem is real and serious: a disaster-recovery restore would permanently drop ALL case expenses (financial), ALL document-checklist progress (operational), and ALL task/case comment threads while reporting success. Blast radius + established precedent justify High.

### Medium (3)

#### `DRIVE-2` — documents_delete RLS + delete RPC still use the legacy guard (associated advisors cannot delete)
- **File:** supabase/migrations/027_production_hardening.sql:280-286 (documents_delete) and 318-326 (soft-delete RPC guard)
- **Evidence:** The documents_delete policy (027:284-285) and the soft-delete RPC guard (027:324-325) both use `public.has_permission('edit_any_case') OR (public.has_permission('edit_own_case') AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())`, never updated to can_edit_case() by mig 147. This is the read/write counterpart to DRIVE-1 on the delete path.
- **Why it matters:** An associated advisor who can edit a case (per userCanEditCase) cannot delete its documents — the UI affordance (gated on can_edit_case + delete_document) will be shown but the server delete fails. Same legacy-guard exclusion class as DRIVE-1, narrower blast radius (delete only).
- **Suggested fix:** Re-point documents_delete and the document soft-delete RPC guard at public.can_edit_case(case_id) in the same canonicalization migration as DRIVE-1.
- **Verify:** PARTIALLY CONFIRMED — core defect is real; one of the two cited targets is wrong.

CONFIRMED (the load-bearing half): The document soft-delete RPC public.soft_delete_document_with_tombstone still uses the legacy guard. Its latest definition is in 104_ensure_document_delete_rpc.sql:86-89 (post-027, pre-147), with WHERE ... AND (public.has_permission('edit_any_case') OR (public.has_permission('edit_own_case') AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())) — no associated-advisor branch. Migration 147's own header (lines 6-11) enumerates exactly 5 objects it re-pointed (cases_select, cases_update, can_view_case, can_edit_case, _assert_can_edit_case); this RPC is NOT among them. Migration 190 (R8 canonicalization) re-pointed the SIBLING soft-delete RPCs soft_delete_borrower_income/obligation at the canonical guard (190:318-417) but did NOT touch the document RPC — so it still drifts. can_edit_case (147:81-101) is a strict superset of the legacy check, so an associated advisor with edit_own_case passes userCanEditCase but fails the RPC's internal WHERE → RAISE EXCEPTION 'Document not found or not editable' → action returns 'unknown'. Verified the real call path: src/features/documents/actions/delete-document.ts:53-58 gates on delete_document + userCanEditCase (so the action proceeds for an associated advisor), then calls the legacy-guarded RPC at lines 89-93 which then fails.

WRONG (the other cited target): The finding's first target — 'documents_delete RLS policy at 027:284-285 with the legacy guard' — is inaccurate. (a) Lines 027:284-285 are the tombstones_insert policy, not documents_delete. (b) The actual documents_delete policy was created only in 011_rls_policies.sql:202 as USING (public.has_permission('delete_document')) — it never had the assigned_advisor_id legacy guard the finding describes — and it was DROPPED in 022_security_hardening.sql:258 and never recreated (grep confirms no later CREATE). So there is no documents_delete RLS policy in the current schema at all; deletes flow exclusively through the SECURITY DEFINER soft-delete RPC. The finding conflated tombstones_insert with documents_delete.

UI-affordance nuance: the finding says the button is gated on 'can_edit_case + delete_document'. Actually canDeleteDocuments is gated ONLY on the delete_document permission (page.tsx:111 / documents/page.tsx). This makes the UI-vs-server mismatch even broader than stated, but the finding's conclusion (affordance shown, server delete fails for an associated advisor) holds.

Net: the substantive vulnerability — an associated advisor who can edit a case cannot soft-delete its documents because the RPC guard predates associated advisors — is genuine and is the delete-path counterpart to DRIVE-1. Fix should re-point only soft_delete_document_with_tombstone (and, for consistency, the tombstones_insert WITH CHECK) at public.can_edit_case; there is no documents_delete policy to fix. Severity Medium is appropriate: it fails closed (deny direction, no data exposure), affects only the associated-advisor configuration, and is a broken affordance rather than a security hole. is_real=true because the named RPC guard genuinely exhibits the legacy-exclusion problem, even though the title's 'documents_delete RLS' target does not exist.

#### `DRIVE-3` — Auto-sync fires on documents page load with no upload-permission gate — relies entirely on RLS to block writes
- **File:** src/app/(app)/cases/[id]/documents/page.tsx:32-37; src/features/integrations/services/drive-document-sync.ts:22-44, 74-204
- **Evidence:** CaseDocumentsPage fires `void autoSyncIfStale(caseId)` for ANY user who can load the page (the page only requires view permission — the Promise.all does not check upload_document). autoSyncIfStale → syncDriveDocumentsForCase, which performs INSERTs (drive-sync-importer.ts:71-85), category-move UPDATEs (importer.ts:45-52), and soft-delete UPDATEs (drive-sync-sweeper.ts:31-50) via the cookie-bound user client. Unlike the explicit syncDriveDocumentsAction (sync-drive-documents.ts:35-52) which checks userHasAllPermissions('view_case_documents','upload_document') + userCanEditCase + rate-limit, the auto-sync path has NO permission check and NO rate-limit at the service layer — only autoSyncIfStale's 10s last_synced_at throttle (drive-document-sync.ts:33-36) and the documents-table RLS gate stop a viewer-only user from mutating rows.
- **Why it matters:** Defense-in-depth gap: the write protection for the auto-sync path lives ONLY in RLS. DRIVE-1 shows that RLS guard is itself already wrong (excludes associated advisors); the inverse risk is that any future RLS regression on documents_insert/update immediately lets a pure viewer's page load mutate document rows. The manual action enforces the same protections in the app layer; auto-sync should not be weaker. Also, every documents page open for a stale case triggers an N+1 Drive listing pass with no per-user/per-case rate-limit at the service boundary (the 10s window is the only brake).
- **Suggested fix:** Have autoSyncIfStale (or syncDriveDocumentsForCase) verify the caller can edit the case (userCanEditCase) + has upload_document before mutating, returning early/no-op otherwise, so view-only loads never attempt writes. Optionally route auto-sync through the same checkRateLimit subject as the manual action.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. page.tsx:32 fires `void autoSyncIfStale(caseId)` unconditionally on render — before the `Promise.all`, before `if (!caseData) notFound()`, and with NO upload_document/userCanEditCase gate (the page's only permission read at line 45 gates UI affordances, not the sync). autoSyncIfStale (drive-document-sync.ts:22-44) -> syncDriveDocumentsForCase (74-204) uses the cookie-bound user client (createClient) and writes: INSERT (drive-sync-importer.ts:71-85), category-move UPDATE (importer 45-52), soft-delete UPDATE (drive-sync-sweeper.ts:31-50). The only brakes are MIN_AUTO_SYNC_INTERVAL_MS=10_000 (drive-sync-types.ts:18) and documents-table RLS.

Asymmetry verified: syncDriveDocumentsAction (sync-drive-documents.ts:35-52) enforces userHasAllPermissions('view_case_documents','upload_document') + userCanEditCase + checkRateLimit('sync_drive_documents', 1/30s, fail-closed) before the identical syncDriveDocumentsForCase call; auto-sync enforces none of these. So write protection for the auto-sync path lives ONLY in RLS — a true defense-in-depth gap, exactly as described.

DRIVE-1 cross-reference is also accurate: documents_insert/documents_update RLS (migration 024:135-175) gate on edit_any_case OR (edit_own_case AND assigned_advisor_id=auth.uid()) with NO associated-advisor branch. Migration 147 widened cases_update / can_view_case / can_edit_case / _assert_can_edit_case to include is_case_associated_advisor but did NOT touch the documents write policies; no later migration redefines documents_insert/_update (grep over migrations confirms only 008/011/024/027 reference them). Hence the documents write RLS genuinely diverges from the app-layer can_edit_case the manual action uses.

Severity Medium is correct, not over/under-stated: not exploitable by a pure viewer today (documents_insert/_update still require upload_document + case-edit in RLS, which a viewer-only user lacks), but the protection is single-layer for auto-sync while the manual path is double-layered, and any future RLS regression on documents writes would let a stale-case page open mutate rows. The N+1 Drive-listing concern is real (no service-boundary rate-limit), with the minor caveat that the 10s per-case throttle does cap frequency — but that throttle is per-case, not a true per-user rate limit, so the framing holds. Files read: page.tsx, drive-document-sync.ts, drive-sync-importer.ts, drive-sync-sweeper.ts, sync-drive-documents.ts, permissions.ts, proxy.ts, drive-sync-types.ts, migrations 008/011/024/027/039/147.

#### `INTEG-1` — restoreBackupAction is an expensive external+DB action with no checkRateLimit
- **File:** src/features/backup/actions/restore-backup.ts:24-85
- **Evidence:** The action does auth + isCurrentUserAdmin + a length check on driveFileId, then unconditionally: downloads up to 20MB from Drive (client.downloadFileText, line 37), AES-256-GCM decrypts (line 50), JSON.parse (line 68), Zod-validates (line 73), and runs the heavy multi-table restore_backup_snapshot RPC (restoreSnapshot, line 76). Its sibling runBackupAction goes through checkRateLimit({action:'run_backup', max:1, windowSeconds:600, failMode:'closed'}) (run-backup.ts:31-38), but restoreBackupAction has no checkRateLimit anywhere (confirmed by grep across src/features/backup). CLAUDE.md mandates 'Expensive actions go through checkRateLimit' and lists run-backup as already covered; restore is strictly more expensive (download + decrypt + full-DB insert) yet is unthrottled.
- **Why it matters:** A button-mash or scripted loop by an admin (or a compromised admin session) can fire repeated 20MB Drive downloads + full-table restore RPCs back-to-back, hammering the Drive API quota and the database with concurrent ON CONFLICT inserts. Admin-only limits the blast radius (this is why it's Medium, not High), but the action is exactly the cost profile the rate-limit rule exists for, and it is inconsistent with the throttled backup path right beside it.
- **Suggested fix:** Add checkRateLimit at the top (after the admin check, before getDriveClientIfConnected) with a fail-closed window, e.g. checkRateLimit({action:'restore_backup', subject:`user:${userRes.user.id}`, max:3, windowSeconds:600, failMode:'closed'}); return {ok:false, error:'rate_limited'} when blocked, add 'rate_limited' to RestoreBackupResult in backup/types.ts, and map it to a toast in backup-restore-button.tsx (the run-backup path already has the toast.error(t('toast.rateLimited')) precedent in backup-panel.tsx:43).
- **Verify:** Verified against the code; could not refute. restore-backup.ts:24-85 does auth (26-27) + isCurrentUserAdmin (28) + driveFileId length check (29-31), then unconditionally downloads up to 20MB from Drive (downloadFileText, 37), AES-256-GCM decrypts (decryptWithKey, 50), JSON.parse (68), Zod-validates (73), and runs the heavy multi-table restore_backup_snapshot SECURITY DEFINER RPC via restoreSnapshot (76; restore.service.ts:15-25, migration 030). There is NO checkRateLimit: it is not imported (imports are lines 1-14) and grep across src/features/backup finds checkRateLimit ONLY in run-backup.ts. The sibling runBackupAction DOES throttle: checkRateLimit({action:'run_backup', subject:`user:${id}`, max:1, windowSeconds:600, failMode:'closed'}) at run-backup.ts:31-38. CLAUDE.md mandates 'Expensive actions go through checkRateLimit' and lists run-backup as covered. Restore is strictly more expensive than backup (download+decrypt+full-table insert), so the inconsistency is real. checkRateLimit (rate-limit.ts:45-64) supports the suggested call shape. Suggested fix is feasible: RestoreBackupResult (types.ts:19-30) lacks 'rate_limited' (present in RunBackupResult line 17) and would need it, and backup-restore-button.tsx (confirmRestore, 32-46) would need a toast branch — precedent at backup-panel.tsx:43-44 toast.error(t('toast.rateLimited')). Severity Medium is correctly calibrated: admin-only gating (lines 27-28) caps blast radius, exactly the reviewer's stated rationale; not High. Confidence high — every factual claim matched verbatim.

### Low (11)

#### `OAUTH-1` — Refresh token placed in revoke-request URL query string; catch-all warn may echo it
- **File:** src/features/integrations/services/google-oauth.ts:155-167
- **Evidence:** revokeToken builds the request as `${REVOKE_URL}?token=${encodeURIComponent(token)}` (line 157) — the OAuth refresh token is carried in the URL query of the POST rather than the body. On a thrown fetch (network error), line 166 does `console.warn('Google token revoke threw:', err)`; a fetch error object can carry the request URL, so the token could land in server logs. The non-throw failure branch (line 163) only logs `res.status res.statusText body` of the revoke RESPONSE, which is safe.
- **Why it matters:** Secrets in URLs are a known weak spot: query strings are routinely captured by reverse proxies, CDN access logs, and APM tooling in ways request bodies are not. Even though this matches Google's documented revoke endpoint shape and the token is being revoked anyway, a leaked-but-not-yet-revoked refresh token (e.g. revoke fetch threw before reaching Google) is a live credential to the office-wide Drive.
- **Suggested fix:** Send the token in the form-encoded body instead of the query: POST to REVOKE_URL with `Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded` and body `token=...` (Google's revoke endpoint accepts both). Keep the catch branch logging only a generic message (e.g. `console.warn('Google token revoke threw')` without interpolating err) so a fetch error carrying the URL can't surface the token.
- **Verify:** Verified against src/features/integrations/services/google-oauth.ts (read full file) + caller src/features/integrations/actions/disconnect-google-drive.ts + src/lib/http/with-timeout.ts.

CONFIRMED (primary claim): Line 157 builds the revoke request as `fetch(\`${REVOKE_URL}?token=${encodeURIComponent(token)}\`, { method: 'POST', signal: timeoutSignal() })` — the OAuth refresh token is in the URL query string of a POST, with NO body. This is the long-lived refresh_token for office-wide Drive (GOOGLE_DRIVE_SCOPES includes the full `drive` scope), passed in from disconnect-google-drive.ts:27 (row.refresh_token). Putting a secret in a URL query string is a recognized anti-pattern: query strings are routinely captured by upstream proxies/CDN access logs/APM in ways request bodies are not. Google's revoke endpoint accepts the token in a form-encoded body (as exchangeCodeForTokens/refreshAccessToken already do, lines 79/120), so the suggested fix is valid and consistent with the rest of the file.

CONFIRMED (response branch is safe): Line 163 logs only res.status/statusText/body of the revoke RESPONSE — no token. Accurate.

PARTIALLY OVERSTATED (secondary claim): Line 166 `console.warn('Google token revoke threw:', err)` interpolates the caught error. The finding says a fetch error 'can carry the request URL' so the token could land in logs. This is speculative for the runtime in use: timeoutSignal() => AbortSignal.timeout(8000) rejects with a generic TimeoutError/DOMException (no URL), and a network failure under Node/undici rejects with `TypeError: fetch failed` whose message/stack do not embed the request URL+query string (at most a hostname via err.cause for DNS errors). So the local console.warn echo vector is largely theoretical. The finding hedges this correctly ('could') and it is secondary to the URL-vs-body point.

Severity Low is correct and arguably the ceiling: the token is being revoked at the moment of the call (intent is to destroy it), which sharply limits impact; residual risk is the narrow window where the revoke fetch leaks the token to a proxy/log before Google processes the revoke. The issue is also out of step with the codebase's own secret-hygiene norms (tokens encrypted at rest, no error.message leakage, exports redact secrets), which supports it being a genuine minor finding rather than invalid. Net: is_real=true, Low, medium confidence (URL claim solid; log-echo claim weak).

#### `OAUTH-2` — OAuth state compared with non-constant-time !== (CRON_SECRET path uses timingSafeEqual)
- **File:** src/app/api/auth/google/callback/route.ts:64-69
- **Evidence:** `const cookieState = cookieStore.get(OAUTH_STATE_COOKIE)?.value; cookieStore.delete(...); if (!cookieState || cookieState !== state) return redirectWithError('state_mismatch');` — the CSRF state is compared with a plain `!==`. By contrast the health route's secret check (src/app/api/health/route.ts:145-150) deliberately uses `timingSafeEqual` for the same class of comparison.
- **Why it matters:** Not practically exploitable here: the state is a fresh `crypto.randomUUID()` per flow stored in an httpOnly+secure cookie the attacker cannot read, and the flow additionally re-checks getUser()+is_admin(). So this is a consistency/defense-in-depth gap, not a real bypass. Flagged Low only because the codebase already establishes constant-time comparison as the house pattern for security tokens.
