- **Suggested fix:** Optional: compare with a constant-time helper (Buffer length check + crypto.timingSafeEqual) to match the CRON_SECRET pattern. Functionally the current check is sound given the random per-flow UUID and httpOnly cookie.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. callback/route.ts:67 compares the CSRF state with a plain non-constant-time string `!==`: `if (!cookieState || cookieState !== state)`. By contrast health/route.ts imports timingSafeEqual (line 1) and uses it for the CRON_SECRET check in isDeepAuthorized (lines 145-150: length check + timingSafeEqual), so the codebase does establish constant-time comparison as the house pattern for security tokens — the inconsistency the finding describes is real.

All mitigating facts in the finding also check out: start/route.ts:31 generates the state as `crypto.randomUUID()` (122-bit random, fresh per flow); it's stored httpOnly+secure(prod)+sameSite=lax with a 10-min maxAge (start/route.ts:33-39), so the attacker cannot read it; the cookie is deleted before the comparison (callback:66) making each state single-use; and the callback re-verifies getUser()+is_admin() (callback:72-76).

This makes the timing channel non-exploitable: a timing oracle only helps an attacker who is brute-forcing/forging a stable secret, but here the attacker controls only the query param, the cookieState is a single-use server-side random value with no stable target, and admin re-auth gates the flow regardless. So it is a defense-in-depth / consistency gap, not a bypass. Severity Low is accurate — the reviewer neither overstated (explicitly calls it "not a real bypass") nor understated it.

#### `OAUTH-3` — Raw Google refresh-error body persisted to last_error and rendered in the admin Settings UI
- **File:** src/features/integrations/services/google-drive.ts:73-80
- **Evidence:** On a permanent refresh failure, `markIntegrationDisconnected(provider, err.message)` is called where `err` is a RefreshTokenError whose message is `Google token refresh failed: ${res.status} ${text}` (google-oauth.ts:130-133, with `text` = raw Google response body). That string is stored verbatim into office_integrations.last_error (integrations.service.ts:196) and then returned to the admin Settings page as `lastError` via getDriveIntegrationView (integrations.service.ts:73,86 → drive-integration-card). The refresh response body does NOT contain the refresh token (the token is only in the request), so no credential leaks; it's a raw upstream error body rather than a generic code.
- **Why it matters:** Violates the project convention of not surfacing raw upstream/Supabase error strings to clients (map to a generic code; UI translates). Audience is admin-only (RLS select is is_admin(); the page redirects non-admins), so blast radius is minimal — but it sets the wrong precedent and could expose internal/quota detail in the UI. The same string also reaches the authorized deep /api/health response (health route:123), which is CRON_SECRET-gated.
- **Suggested fix:** Store a stable reason code (e.g. 'refresh_invalid_grant' / 'refresh_failed') in last_error instead of err.message, and keep the raw `${status} ${text}` only in a server-side console.error. The UI then maps the code to a translated string.
- **Verify:** Partially substantiated, with the finding's central claim refuted. CONFIRMED: RefreshTokenError.message = `Google token refresh failed: ${res.status} ${text}` where text is the raw Google response body (google-oauth.ts:126-133); on a permanent failure markIntegrationDisconnected(provider, err.message) (google-drive.ts:73-79) writes that verbatim into office_integrations.last_error (integrations.service.ts:196). So a raw upstream error body IS persisted, which technically deviates from the project convention of storing/returning generic codes. Also confirmed: the raw last_error reaches the deep /api/health response via checkDrive() detail (health route:123,212), but that path is CRON_SECRET-gated by a constant-time bearer check (route:145-150,156-157) — operator-only. No credential leak: the refresh token is only in the request body, never the response (google-oauth.ts:111-122). REFUTED (the load-bearing claim): the finding says the raw last_error is 'rendered in the admin Settings UI' via getDriveIntegrationView -> drive-integration-card. It is NOT. drive-integration-card.tsx never reads view.lastError (grep: zero matches); the only error it renders is a separate `errorReason` prop sourced from the URL search param params.error (settings/integrations/page.tsx:36), passed through prettifyError which maps known OAuth-flow codes or falls back to errors.generic (card lines 87-89,244-258). view.lastError is dead data on that surface; the other consumer backup-view.service.ts reads only view.status. office_integrations SELECT is is_admin() RLS (mig 018:46-47) and getDriveIntegrationView uses the RLS-bound createClient(); the page also redirects non-admins. Net: a real but minimal convention deviation — storage-only plus an operator/CRON-gated diagnostic endpoint, with NO admin-UI exposure and no credential leak. The finding over-stated impact (claimed UI rendering that does not occur); Low is appropriate, at the very bottom of Low. Suggested fix (store a stable reason code in last_error, keep raw status/text in server-side console.error) remains valid as a convention cleanup.

#### `DRIVE-4` — Mutating Drive calls (createFolder, uploadFile, deleteFile) bypass retry/backoff, so a single 429/503 fails the whole upload
- **File:** src/features/integrations/services/google-drive.ts:142-158 (createFolder), 190-211 (uploadFile), 222-229 (deleteFile)
- **Evidence:** authedFetchRetry (google-drive.ts:112-125) retries 429/502/503 with exponential backoff + Retry-After, but only the read methods (findFolder, findFolderByAppProperty, listFolderFiles*, listSubfolders, downloadFileText) opt in. createFolder, uploadFile, and deleteFile call authedFetch directly (no retry) — the comment at 110-111 says mutations bypass retry 'to stay idempotent'. createFolder/uploadFile are NOT idempotent (a retry could create a duplicate folder/file), so skipping retry there is defensible; but it means a transient 429 during the office's normal upload bursts surfaces as a hard 'Drive upload failed: 429' (google-drive.ts:208) and the file silently never reaches Drive (best-effort path swallows it: finalize-upload.ts:162-166). deleteFile IS idempotent (404 already treated as success at 226) yet still gets no retry, so a transient 503 during eraseDriveTargets (drive-case-uploader.ts:234-241) needlessly logs the id as a failed/orphaned deletion (erase-case-files.ts:210-233).
- **Why it matters:** Drive's quota is tight (per-user 100s/100s windows) and 429s are common under bursts. Uploads dropping on the first transient error increases the orphan-Drive-file / missing-mirror rate; deletions failing on transient errors needlessly inflate erasure_orphan_log. Low severity because Drive is a secondary store and the flows degrade gracefully, but reliability suffers.
- **Suggested fix:** Route deleteFile through authedFetchRetry (it is idempotent — safe to retry). For createFolder/uploadFile, consider a guarded single retry on 429/503 only (uploadFile is effectively idempotent within a sync window because the next sweep dedups by drive_file_id; for createFolder the findFolderByAppProperty lookup already absorbs most dupes). At minimum, honor Retry-After for uploads.
- **Verify:** Verified against the code; every factual claim holds. In src/features/integrations/services/google-drive.ts, authedFetchRetry (lines 112-125) retries 429/502/503 with exponential backoff and honors Retry-After. All read methods opt in: findFolder (136), findFolderByAppProperty (184), downloadFileText (215), listFolderFiles (235), listFolderFilesPaginated (261), listSubfolders (289). The three mutating methods call authedFetch directly with no retry: createFolder (150), uploadFile (197), deleteFile (223). The code comment at lines 110-111 explicitly states "mutations bypass retry to stay idempotent." uploadFile throws a hard `Drive upload failed: ${res.status}` on a transient 429 (line 208); the caller finalize-upload.ts swallows it best-effort (lines 162-166: `if (out.ok)` with no else, leaving driveFileId/driveFileUrl null and silently no Drive mirror). deleteFile is idempotent — 404 is treated as success at line 226 — yet still has no retry, so a transient 503 during eraseDriveTargets (drive-case-uploader.ts:234-241, catch pushes id to failed) is logged as an orphaned/failed deletion by erase-case-files.ts (lines 210-233). All cited line numbers are exact. No outer retry wrapper exists at the call sites (confirmed in finalize-upload.ts). One additional uploadFile caller not mentioned (drive-general-uploader.ts:30) shares the same no-retry path, reinforcing rather than refuting the finding. The reviewer's analysis is self-aware and accurate: it correctly flags that createFolder/uploadFile are not truly idempotent (so skipping retry is defensible) and singles out deleteFile as the cleanest fix candidate. Severity Low is appropriate — Drive is a secondary store, both flows degrade gracefully (best-effort upload, orphan-log fallback for deletion); it is a reliability gap, not a data-loss or security bug.

#### `DRIVE-5` — ensureFolder find-or-create on root/subfolders/general folder has a duplicate-folder race under concurrent first-use
- **File:** src/features/integrations/services/google-drive.ts:160-164 (ensureFolder); src/features/integrations/services/drive-case-uploader.ts:113-133 (ensureSubfolder), 69-76 (ensureRootFolder); src/features/integrations/services/drive-general-uploader.ts:29
- **Evidence:** ensureFolder does findFolder() then createFolder() with no mutex; two concurrent first-uploads for the same case (or the first-ever upload before drive_root_folder_id is persisted) can both miss the find and both create. The case folder is protected by findFolderByAppProperty on a stable caseFolderId appProperty (drive-case-uploader.ts:94-101, comment acknowledges 'most of the duplicate-folder race window'), but subfolders (ensureSubfolder:124) and the general folder (drive-general-uploader.ts:29, comment acknowledges this at 18-20) are resolved by NAME only. The subfolders patch also sends the whole subfolders object (drive-case-uploader.ts:125-130, comment notes the per-key merge race). A duplicate subfolder means files dropped into the 'other' copy won't be scanned by syncDriveDocumentsForCase (it matches NAME_TO_FOLDER_KEY on the first subfolder of that name returned).
- **Why it matters:** Low for Kaufman's ~10-user/80-case volume (concurrency is genuinely low and the comments call it out), but a duplicate subfolder would silently make a subset of manually-dropped files invisible to sync, and duplicate root/general folders fragment storage. Worth tracking rather than fixing now.
- **Suggested fix:** For the root and general folders, persist the id (root already is via persistDriveRootFolderId — just ensure it's written before the first concurrent upload; general folder is not persisted at all). For subfolders, an appProperty (e.g. caseSubfolderKey) + findFolderByAppProperty lookup would make resolution rename/dup-proof like the case folder, and a per-key JSONB merge RPC would close the subfolders write race.
- **Verify:** The core race claim is CONFIRMED in code. ensureFolder (google-drive.ts:160-164) does findFolder()→createFolder() with no mutex; two concurrent first-uses can both miss and both create. The case folder is protected by a stable caseFolderId appProperty (drive-case-uploader.ts:94-101), but subfolders go through name-based ensureFolder (ensureSubfolder:124) and the general folder is name-only with no persistence (drive-general-uploader.ts:29, comment at 14-20 acknowledges it). The subfolders patch DOES send the whole subfolders object (drive-case-uploader.ts:125-130) and update_case_drive_meta (migration 026_metadata_rpcs.sql:36-44) does a shallow `||` merge only at the {drive} key — so a concurrent writer adding a different subfolder key can be clobbered, exactly as the comment states. findFolder uses pageSize=1 so the upload path resolves to one arbitrary duplicate.

HOWEVER, the finding's scariest payoff is REFUTED. It claims a duplicate subfolder makes files in the 'other' copy invisible to sync because sync 'matches NAME_TO_FOLDER_KEY on the first subfolder of that name returned.' That is wrong: syncDriveDocumentsForCase (drive-document-sync.ts:170-178) iterates `for (const sub of subfolders)` over EVERY subfolder from listSubfolders (which returns all same-named folders, no dedup — google-drive.ts:281-299). Both duplicates map to the same folderKey/categoryId and BOTH have their files scanned via safeListFiles and imported. So files in a duplicate subfolder would still be picked up by sync; there is no silent data-invisibility. firstCategoryPerFolder (line 117-122) is keyed by category-side drive_folder, not by Drive subfolder, so it doesn't cause skipping either.

Net: the race genuinely exists and the suggested fixes (persist general folder id, appProperty + per-key merge RPC for subfolders) are sound, but the only real residual impact is duplicate root/general/subfolder creation = storage fragmentation under genuinely-low concurrency, all explicitly acknowledged in code comments as accepted tradeoffs. The data-loss framing is overstated. Low severity stands (the finding itself rated it Low and recommended tracking, not fixing now).

#### `BACKUP-2` — select('*') backup with auto-include semantics relies on REDACTED_COLUMNS staying ahead of new credential columns
- **File:** src/features/backup/services/backup-snapshot.service.ts:93-110, 61-77
- **Evidence:** fetchAllRows does .select('*') (one of the two AUDIT-ACK'd exceptions, comment lines 96-99) so any new column auto-propagates into the encrypted snapshot. The safety net is REDACTED_COLUMNS, a manually-maintained Partial<Record> listing column names to delete per table (profiles tokens/hashes, office_settings.bank_account_number). There is no automated check that a newly-added secret column on an already-backed-up table (e.g. a future profiles.api_key that someone forgets to list, or a credential column added to banks/office_settings) gets added to REDACTED_COLUMNS. redactRow deletes only the named columns; a missed one ships into the backup file. The file IS encrypted with BACKUP_ENCRYPTION_KEY, so this is defense-in-depth rather than an open leak, but the whole point of REDACTED_COLUMNS (per its own comment, lines 52-56) is to survive a key-leak-alongside-backup scenario.
- **Why it matters:** The redaction layer is the last line that keeps live credentials out of a file that, if its key ever leaks, enables replay/impersonation. A silent gap here only surfaces after a leak — exactly when it's too late. select('*') + manual deny-list is structurally fragile compared to the TABLE_FULL_COLUMNS allowlist pattern the codebase mandates elsewhere.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a unit test (sibling to backup-restore-allowlist.test.ts, static/no-DB) that reads database.ts and asserts no column on a BACKUP_TABLES table matches a secret-name heuristic (token|secret|password|hash|api_key|refresh|private_key|mfa|totp) unless it is listed in REDACTED_COLUMNS — failing loudly when a new credential-shaped column lands. Alternatively, switch fetchAllRows to a per-table explicit column allowlist so new columns are an opt-in, reviewable step.
- **Verify:** Verified against the code. The structural facts are all accurate: backup-snapshot.service.ts fetchAllRows uses .select('*') (lines 100-104, AUDIT-ACK comment 96-99) with auto-include semantics; the safety net is REDACTED_COLUMNS, a hand-maintained Partial<Record<BackupTable, string[]>> (lines 61-77) whose redactRow only deletes named columns (81-86); and the sibling static test backup-restore-allowlist.test.ts guards ONLY table-list parity (backup<->restore), NOT column-redaction drift. So the finding's central claim — there is no automated check that a future credential-shaped column on a backed-up table gets added to REDACTED_COLUMNS — is correct, and it contradicts the TABLE_FULL_COLUMNS allowlist pattern CLAUDE.md mandates elsewhere.

However, severity is overstated at Medium. (1) There is NO present-day leak: I grepped database.ts for all secret-shaped names. The only OAuth-token table is office_integrations (access_token/refresh_token, lines 2674-2693), which is EXPLICITLY excluded from BACKUP_TABLES (comment line 11; table list 14-43). The only secret column on a backed-up table is profiles.google_calendar_refresh_token, which IS in REDACTED_COLUMNS. office_settings.bank_account_number is sensitive and IS redacted. banks has no credential columns. The other 6 profiles entries (password_hash, mfa_secret, totp_secret, api_key, session_token, recovery_token) don't exist yet — pre-listed by design (comment 57-59). (2) The whole snapshot is encrypted with BACKUP_ENCRYPTION_KEY (AES-256-GCM) before Drive upload (run-backup.ts lines 58-60), so even a Drive compromise reads nothing. The finding itself concedes both points ('defense-in-depth rather than an open leak'). This is a legitimate forward-looking hardening suggestion (add a static heuristic test, or switch to a per-table column allowlist), not a current vulnerability — Low fits a real-but-speculative gap with encryption already in place.

#### `BACKUP-3` — Backup read errors throw raw Supabase error.message up the stack
- **File:** src/features/backup/services/backup-snapshot.service.ts:104; src/features/backup/services/restore.service.ts:23
- **Evidence:** fetchAllRows does `throw new Error(\`backup read failed for ${table}: ${error.message}\`)` and restoreSnapshot does `if (error) throw new Error(error.message)`. Both raw messages propagate to the caller's try/catch. The action/route callers DO log-and-genericize (run-backup.ts:81 returns {error:'unknown'}, cron route returns 'backup_failed'), so the message does not reach the client today. But the contract 'never surface Supabase error.message' is best enforced at the throw site; a future caller that returns err.message would leak table/constraint/policy names.
- **Why it matters:** Defense-in-depth against the documented anti-pattern (returning Supabase error.message to the client leaks schema/policy internals). The current callers happen to be safe, but the throw sites bake the raw message into the Error, leaving the safety dependent on every caller remembering to genericize.
- **Suggested fix:** Throw a generic message (e.g. `backup read failed for ${table}`) and console.error the full error.message server-side at the throw site, mirroring the safeDbError pattern used elsewhere; same for restoreSnapshot.
- **Verify:** Verified verbatim. backup-snapshot.service.ts:104 throws `new Error(`backup read failed for ${table}: ${error.message}`)` and restore.service.ts:23 throws `new Error(error.message)` — both bake the raw Supabase error.message into the Error. I traced every caller: fetchAllRows is only reached via buildBackupSnapshot, whose two callers (run-backup.ts:44 and api/cron/backup/route.ts:45) both wrap it in try/catch and genericize — run-backup.ts:81-82 console.errors then returns {ok:false,error:'unknown'}; the cron route logs only err.message server-side and returns {error:'backup_failed'}. restoreSnapshot is only called from restore-backup.ts:76, also in try/catch returning {ok:false,error:'unknown'} (line 82-83). So the raw message does NOT reach the client on any current path — the finding explicitly acknowledges this. The issue is purely a future-caller defense-in-depth gap against the documented anti-pattern (returning Supabase error.message leaks constraint/relation/policy names; see CLAUDE.md and lib/supabase/db-error-log.ts which keeps message specifically because it carries constraint/relation names). The suggested fix (throw generic, console.error full detail server-side, mirroring the safeDbError pattern used in 46 files) is consistent with the codebase convention. Low severity is correct and not overstated: no live exploit (admin-only + CRON_SECRET-gated infra services, all callers genericize, message carries no row PII), but a real best-practice gap at the throw site. Confidence high — all claims substantiated directly from the cited code plus all cross-referenced callers.

#### `RESTORE-1` — restore.service throws raw Supabase error.message (project anti-pattern, contained but loses specificity)
- **File:** src/features/backup/services/restore.service.ts:23
- **Evidence:** `if (error) throw new Error(error.message);` re-throws the raw PostgREST/RPC error string. The RPC can raise 'not authorized' (ERRCODE 42501) and 'unsupported backup version' (22023). This violates the documented rule 'NEVER return Supabase error.message to the client / log server-side, return a generic code'. In practice it is CONTAINED: the caller's outer `catch (err)` in restore-backup.ts (lines 81-84) logs `err` server-side and returns `{ ok: false, error: 'unknown' }`, so nothing reaches the browser. The cost is (a) the raw DB message lands in server logs from a non-error-boundary throw site, and (b) the distinct RPC failures all collapse to 'unknown' even though RestoreBackupResult already has 'unauthorized' and 'invalid_file' codes that would map cleanly (e.g. 42501 -> 'unauthorized', 22023 -> 'invalid_file').
- **Why it matters:** Minor: no client-facing leak today (the action's catch swallows it), but it is a latent footgun — if a future refactor surfaces restore.service errors closer to the client, or someone returns the thrown message in a different path, the contained pattern breaks. Also the admin gets a generic 'unknown' for a clearly diagnosable wrong-version file.
- **Suggested fix:** In restore.service.ts log the error server-side (`console.error('[restoreSnapshot] rpc failed', { code: error.code })`) and throw a typed sentinel (e.g. an Error with a stable `.code`), or have the action inspect `error.code` (42501/22023) and map to 'unauthorized'/'invalid_file'. Do not propagate error.message.
- **Verify:** VERIFIED the code. restore.service.ts:23 is literally `if (error) throw new Error(error.message);` — confirmed, and it is the ONLY `throw new Error(...message)` in all of src/ (Grep). Migration 030_restore_backup_rpc.sql confirms the RPC raises 'not authorized' (ERRCODE 42501, line 36) and 'unsupported backup version' (22023, line 40). Containment is fully verified: restoreSnapshot has exactly one caller (Grep: restore-backup.ts:76), inside the try block whose catch(err) at lines 81-84 does `console.error('restoreBackupAction failed', err)` and returns `{ ok:false, error:'unknown' }` — so error.message never reaches the browser. The reviewer correctly self-rated this Low and acknowledged it is contained.

The technical core is REAL: the line deviates from the documented rule's letter ('NEVER ... error.message') and the raw DB string lands in server logs from this throw site; if a future refactor surfaced service errors closer to the client the contained pattern would break (the genuine latent-footgun argument). Severity Low is accurate — not overstated.

However two parts of the rationale are REFUTED / overstated, which is why this stays Low and not Medium: (1) 'the admin gets a generic unknown for a clearly diagnosable wrong-version file' is FALSE — BackupSnapshotSchema (snapshot.schema.ts:9 `version: z.literal(1)`) is safeParse'd at restore-backup.ts:73-74 and returns 'invalid_file' for a wrong version BEFORE restoreSnapshot/the RPC is ever called, so the 22023 path is unreachable from this caller and never collapses to 'unknown'. (2) The 42501 path is shadowed by the action's own isCurrentUserAdmin() check (line 28 -> 'unauthorized') and would only fire on a rare admin-check inconsistency. Also context: the codebase's prevailing service convention is `if (error) throw error;` (dozens of services), all caught at the action layer — so throwing from a service into a containing action catch is the established, accepted pattern here, and this line is actually less leaky than the norm since it drops the code/hint/details. The documented rule targets returning to the CLIENT, which never happens. Net: a legitimate code-quality nit at Low; not a security or correctness bug.

#### `RESTORE-2` — Restore downloads the entire Drive file before enforcing the 20MB size cap
- **File:** src/features/backup/actions/restore-backup.ts:37
- **Evidence:** `const text = await client.downloadFileText(driveFileId);` runs first; only AFTER the full download does `if (text.length > MAX_BYTES) return { ok:false, error:'too_large' }` (line 38). The Drive file's `size` is already known to the panel (BackupFileMeta.size in types.ts:4) but is not pre-checked, and downloadFileText has no byte ceiling. The action is admin-only and not rate-limited (run-backup is, restore is not).
- **Why it matters:** An admin (or a compromised admin session) could point restore at an arbitrarily large Drive file id (the input is validated only for length <=200, not that it is a real backup), forcing the server to buffer the whole file into a string in memory before the cap rejects it. Blast radius is small (admin-only, ~80 cases means legit files are tiny) so this is hardening, not a live exploit.
- **Suggested fix:** Fetch the file's size via Drive metadata and reject > MAX_BYTES before downloading the body, and/or stream-with-limit in downloadFileText. Optionally add checkRateLimit to restoreBackupAction the way run-backup.ts already does (CLAUDE.md flags expensive/external actions for rate limiting).
- **Verify:** Verified against the actual code; every technical claim holds. (1) restore-backup.ts:37-38 downloads the full file (`const text = await client.downloadFileText(driveFileId)`) and only then checks `if (text.length > MAX_BYTES)` (MAX_BYTES=20MB, line 16). (2) downloadFileText (google-drive.ts:214-220) calls res.text() with NO byte ceiling — only an 8s fetch timeout via timeoutSignal(); the whole body is buffered into a string before any size check. (3) The file's size IS known to the panel: BackupFileMeta.size (types.ts:4) is populated by drive-backup.service.ts:50 from listFolderFiles, but the restore button (backup-restore-button.tsx:35) passes only fileId and the action never fetches/checks Drive metadata size first. (4) Input validation at restore-backup.ts:29 only checks driveFileId is a non-empty string of length<=200 — not that it is a real backup file, so an admin can point restore at any Drive file id. (5) restore-backup.ts has NO checkRateLimit (no import, no call), whereas run-backup.ts:31-38 rate-limits run_backup (max 1 / 600s, failMode closed); CLAUDE.md flags expensive/external actions for rate limiting. Severity Low is correct and honestly scoped: the action is double-gated by isCurrentUserAdmin() (lines 27-28), so it requires an admin or compromised-admin session; the realistic blast radius is transient memory pressure on a serverless function from buffering one oversized file, further bounded by the 8s Drive timeout. This is defense-in-depth hardening (pre-check size via Drive metadata and/or stream-with-limit; optionally add checkRateLimit), not a live exploit. Keeping Low.

#### `RESTORE-3` — Restore can fail the whole transaction (all-or-nothing) if the backed-up schema drifted from current NOT NULL columns
- **File:** supabase/migrations/115_restore_includes_scenarios.sql:78
- **Evidence:** Each table is restored via `EXECUTE format('INSERT INTO public.%I SELECT * FROM jsonb_populate_recordset(NULL::public.%I, $1) ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING', ...)`. The backup writer uses `select('*')` (backup-snapshot.service.ts:101) so old snapshots simply omit any column added later. jsonb_populate_recordset leaves missing columns NULL; if a column added after the backup is NOT NULL with no default, the INSERT raises and — because the function body is one implicit transaction with no per-table exception handling — the ENTIRE restore rolls back. The function is correctly atomic (no half-apply), which is good for integrity but means one drifted table blocks recovery of all others.
- **Why it matters:** Disaster-recovery fragility: in the exact moment you most need a restore, a since-added NOT NULL column makes the whole snapshot unrestorable with a raw Postgres error mapped to 'unknown'. The merge (ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING) and atomicity are otherwise correct and safe — this is the downside of the all-or-nothing design plus select('*') snapshots.
- **Suggested fix:** Document this DR constraint and add a migration policy that new columns on backed-up tables get a DEFAULT (so jsonb_populate_recordset's NULL is overridden). Optionally wrap each table's INSERT in a per-table BEGIN/EXCEPTION block that records the failure into the returned counts instead of aborting the whole restore, so an admin gets partial recovery + a clear list of skipped tables.
- **Verify:** Every link in the finding's causal chain is confirmed in the code.

1) Backup writer uses select('*'): backup-snapshot.service.ts line 102 (.select('*') in fetchAllRows; explanatory comment lines 96-99). Finding cited line 101 — off by one but the claim is correct. So an old snapshot omits any column added after it was taken.

2) Restore SQL is exactly as quoted: supabase/migrations/115_restore_includes_scenarios.sql lines 78-81 run `INSERT INTO public.%I SELECT * FROM jsonb_populate_recordset(NULL::public.%I, $1) ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING` per table inside a FOREACH loop (lines 63-85). jsonb_populate_recordset sets JSON-absent fields to NULL (standard Postgres), so a since-added NOT NULL column with no default raises 23502 not_null_violation on INSERT.

3) No per-table exception handling: the loop has no inner BEGIN/EXCEPTION; the plpgsql function is one implicit transaction, so any single table's INSERT error propagates and rolls back the ENTIRE restore (all-or-nothing). Confirmed — atomicity is correct (no half-apply) but one drifted table blocks recovery of all others, exactly as stated.

4) Drift passes validation: snapshot.schema.ts line 12 validates rows as z.array(z.unknown()), so an old/drifted snapshot passes the envelope check and reaches the RPC. The schema does not catch missing columns.

5) Error mapped to opaque 'unknown': restore.service.ts line 23 throws new Error(error.message); restore-backup.ts lines 81-84 catch and return { ok:false, error:'unknown' }. The admin gets an opaque error in a DR moment, as described.

Severity correctly self-rated Low and I agree. This is a LATENT/conditional fragility, not an active bug: it only triggers if a FUTURE migration adds a NOT NULL column WITHOUT a default to a backed-up table. The codebase's own convention already guards against this — all 14 historical `ADD COLUMN ... NOT NULL` migrations pair with a DEFAULT (e.g. 056, 068, 094, 114, 161, 170, 173), and there are zero `SET NOT NULL` migrations. So the failure requires a developer to break an established universal pattern. The finding is also honest that the merge (ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING) and atomicity are otherwise correct. The suggested-fix's documentation angle is partly genuine: docs/RESTORE_RUNBOOK.md documents merge-only behavior and the scenarios gap but does NOT mention this schema-drift NOT-NULL fragility. Real, accurately scoped, correctly Low.

#### `INTEG-2` — Restore downloads an arbitrary client-supplied Drive fileId without confirming it lives in the KFG_Backups folder
- **File:** src/features/backup/actions/restore-backup.ts:29-37
- **Evidence:** driveFileId comes straight from the client (BackupRestoreButton passes b.id) and is validated only for type/length (length 1..200). The action then calls client.downloadFileText(driveFileId) directly. There is no check that the id is one of the files returned by listBackups()/findBackupFolder() (drive-backup.service.ts) — the office Drive client will fetch ANY file the connected Google account can read. Downstream safety is real but indirect: a non-backup file fails decryptWithKey (GCM auth-tag, strict in prod) or BackupSnapshotSchema -> error:'invalid_file', and the restore RPC is additive (ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING). The file content is never returned to the caller (only a row count), so there is no exfiltration channel.
- **Why it matters:** An admin is already fully trusted and gets no usable output from a non-backup file, so this is hardening, not an exploit. But binding restore to the backup folder is cheap defense-in-depth: it prevents a malformed/typo'd or maliciously substituted id from causing a Drive read outside the intended folder and keeps the trust boundary explicit if the action is ever reused from a less-trusted surface.
- **Suggested fix:** Before downloading, resolve the backups folder via findBackupFolder(client) and confirm driveFileId is among listBackups(client, folderId) (or verify the file's parent === backup folder id via the Drive metadata). Reject with error:'invalid_file' otherwise.
- **Verify:** Verified against source. restoreBackupAction (src/features/backup/actions/restore-backup.ts:24-37) takes driveFileId straight from the client and validates ONLY type + length (1..200) at lines 29-31, then calls client.downloadFileText(driveFileId) at line 37 with no check that the id belongs to the KFG_Backups folder. findBackupFolder/listBackups (src/features/backup/services/drive-backup.service.ts:14-54) exist but are never imported or called by the action. The id is client-controlled: BackupRestoreButton passes fileId={b.id} (backup-panel.tsx:127) -> restoreBackupAction(fileId) (backup-restore-button.tsx:35), b.id being a Drive file id. downloadFileText (google-drive.ts:214-220) does GET /files/{id}?alt=media using the office account's OAuth token via getDriveClientIfConnected (drive-case-uploader.ts:31-35), so Drive returns ANY file that account can read. The finding's mitigation analysis is also accurate and complete: non-backup content fails decryptWithKey (secrets.ts:131-133 rejects plaintext in prod/strict; unwrap GCM auth-tag throws on wrong key/tamper, 142-144) -> caught -> error:'invalid_file'; otherwise BackupSnapshotSchema.safeParse rejects (restore-backup.ts:73-74); the restore RPC is additive ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING and re-checks is_admin() (migration 030:35,51); and the action returns only {ok:true, restored:<number>} (types.ts:19-30) -> no file content is exfiltrated. Caller is admin-only (isCurrentUserAdmin line 28 + RPC is_admin). So this is genuine defense-in-depth hardening (bind restore to the backup folder), not an exploitable vuln for an already-trusted admin who gets no usable output from a non-backup id. Low severity is correct and not over/under-stated.


## Round 12 — templates / notifications / push / SLA

**raw 16 -> confirmed 15 / refuted 1  (High 0, Medium 3, Low 12)**

### Medium (3)

#### `NOTIF-1` — Case-mention notification + email is not scoped to who can view the case (parallel fix to mig 188 missing for the case path)
- **File:** supabase/migrations/108_case_comment_mentions.sql:46-64; src/features/case-comments/services/case-comments.service.ts:70-80; src/features/notifications/services/notification-mirror-email.ts:43-83
- **Evidence:** The case-comment mention trigger (notify_case_comment_mentions) inserts a `case_mention` notification for ANY mentioned active user — its only guards are `mentioned_id <> actor` and `is_active` (108:56-57). There is NO check that the mentioned user can view NEW.case_id. The notification `data` carries `preview` = up to 140 chars of the raw comment body (108:39-62). The email mirror then delivers that preview straight to the recipient's inbox (notification-mirror-email.ts bodyParams `case_mention` → preview, lines 99-105; renderSystemEmail body escaped but content fully delivered). Migration 188 (list_task_mentionable_profiles + can_view_task) fixed exactly this for the TASK path (F11), but the case path was never given an equivalent visibility gate. The picker source `listMentionableProfiles()` selects ALL active profiles with the regular client; because `profiles_select_self_or_admin` (011_rls_policies.sql:75) is `USING (id = auth.uid() OR is_admin())`, a manager (admin) gets the full roster and can mention an advisor with no visibility on the case, leaking the comment preview via bell + email. The trigger is the real security boundary and does not enforce case visibility; a hand-crafted `@[name](uuid)` token by any author would also bypass the picker entirely.
- **Why it matters:** Internal case discussion (which may include client PII in the comment text) is delivered to a teammate who has no RLS access to that case, both in the bell and in their email inbox. This is a cross-case isolation / PII-to-wrong-recipient gap of the same class the project already closed for tasks.
- **Suggested fix:** Mirror mig 188 for the case path: (1) replace listMentionableProfiles() with a SECURITY DEFINER RPC (e.g. list_case_mentionable_profiles(case_id)) that returns only active users where can_view_case(case_id) holds, minus the caller; and (2) harden notify_case_comment_mentions to skip any mentioned_id for whom case visibility does not hold (add an EXISTS check against the same predicate used by case_comments_select / can_view_case) so a hand-typed token can't bypass the picker.
- **Verify:** Verified against the code; could not refute it.

(1) Trigger gap confirmed — supabase/migrations/108_case_comment_mentions.sql:46-64: notify_case_comment_mentions (SECURITY DEFINER) inserts a case_mention notification for each mentioned uuid whose only guards are mentioned_id <> actor AND profiles.is_active (lines 56-57). There is NO can_view_case(NEW.case_id) check. The data payload carries preview = up to 140 chars of the raw comment body (lines 39-42, 61).

(2) Case visibility is otherwise strictly enforced — 107_case_comments.sql:38-46 scopes comment SELECT/INSERT to can_view_case (039 defines can_view_case as the canonical cases_select mirror). So a teammate with no RLS access to the case cannot read the thread, yet the mention notification + preview reaches them anyway. Genuine cross-case isolation gap.

(3) Unscoped picker confirmed — case-comments.service.ts:70-80 listMentionableProfiles() selects ALL active profiles (regular client, no case scope); case-comments-block.tsx:30 wires it into the picker. 011_rls_policies.sql:75-76 profiles_select_self_or_admin = (id = auth.uid() OR is_admin()), so a manager/admin gets the full roster and can mention someone with no case access.

(4) Email leak leg confirmed — app/api/push/dispatch/route.ts:108-116 (notifications-INSERT webhook) calls sendMirroredNotificationEmail for case_mention; notification-mirror-email.ts:99-105 maps data.preview into the email body, delivered to the recipient inbox (push is generic/no-PII, but email is not).

(5) Task path DID get the parallel fix the finding references — 188_task_mentionable_profiles.sql adds SECURITY DEFINER list_task_mentionable_profiles(p_task_id) gated by can_view_task + has_permission_for(user,key); task-comments.service.ts:86-112 consumes it. No equivalent exists for the case path. Latest migration is 191; nothing after 188 closes the case gap. Asymmetry confirmed.

(6) No server-side mention filtering before insert — post-case-comment.ts stores body raw; domain/mentions.ts only parses tokens; the trigger is the sole mention boundary, so a hand-typed @[name](uuid) bypasses the picker entirely. has_permission (002_auth_core.sql:221+, used by can_view_case) is auth.uid()-based, so the trigger needs a parameterized predicate (mirroring 188) to check a different user's visibility — validating the suggested fix.

Severity: Medium is correct. Real PII-to-wrong-recipient + cross-case leak via bell and email, same class the project already closed for tasks. Bounded blast radius (140-char preview, not full thread; recipient still cannot open the case; requires an authorized author/manager-roster or a hand-typed token) keeps it Medium rather than High — consistent with how the identical task-path issue (F11/mig 188) was rated. Not over- or under-stated.

#### `SLA-1` — SLA window math uses UTC calendar days, not Israel civil days — premature/wrong-day alerts
- **File:** src/features/sla/services/sla-check.service.ts:49-53, 132, 144
- **Evidence:** `utcCalendarDaysBetween` anchors both dates with `Date.UTC(getUTCFullYear, getUTCMonth, getUTCDate)`, and `nowDate = new Date()` is read in the ambient (Vercel = UTC) runtime. `stage_durations.entered_at` is a TIMESTAMPTZ set at the exact wall-clock instant of the status change (migration 009_tasks.sql:90,122,145). The codebase already established that this exact field's day-bucketing must be done in Israel time: migration 135_statistics_rpcs.sql:246 uses `date_trunc('month', timezone('Asia/Jerusalem', sd.entered_at))`, and `src/lib/utils/israel-time.ts` (with israel-time.test.ts) exists specifically because 'Server Components run in UTC (Vercel) while the office is in Israel'. Concrete skew: a case entered at Israel 2026-06-16 01:00 (summer) = entered_at 2026-06-15T22:00Z → UTC date is June 15 but the operator's Israel calendar day is June 16. With threshold=1, the cron at 05:00 UTC (08:00 Israel) on June 16 computes utcCalendarDaysBetween(Jun15,Jun16)=1 and fires, even though the case has only been in-status ~7 hours by Israel reckoning — a full day premature. This is the same R5 class of bug that target-date.ts:24 was fixed for using israelCivil.
- **Why it matters:** SLA alerts fire on the wrong day relative to what the manager configured and sees. For Israel late-evening status entries the day count is over-reported by 1, so a 1-day threshold can alert the very next morning when the operator considers it same-day. It makes the threshold meaning non-deterministic (depends on the UTC offset of the entry instant) and diverges from the statistics module's Israel-anchored timing on the identical column.
- **Suggested fix:** Compute days-in-status from Israel civil dates: derive both `enteredAt` and `now` via `israelCivil()` from src/lib/utils/israel-time.ts, then diff the resulting (year,month,day) the same way target-date.ts builds `today`/`soonCutoff` with the Date constructor. Drop the UTC-based `utcCalendarDaysBetween`. Add a domain unit test (none exists today) covering a winter and a summer late-evening entry to lock the boundary.
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED by reading the code. The finding is accurate on every cited point.

WHAT THE CODE DOES (sla-check.service.ts):
- Line 132: `const nowDate = new Date()` — read in the ambient runtime TZ (Vercel = UTC).
- Lines 49-53: `utcCalendarDaysBetween` anchors BOTH dates via `Date.UTC(getUTCFullYear, getUTCMonth, getUTCDate)`, so it diffs UTC calendar days.
- Line 142-144: `enteredDate = new Date(stage.entered_at)` then `utcCalendarDaysBetween(enteredDate, nowDate)` → `daysInStatus`, compared to the per-office threshold at line 145.

CROSS-REFERENCES VERIFIED:
- 009_tasks.sql:90,121-122,144-145: `stage_durations.entered_at` is TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW(), inserted at the exact wall-clock instant of the status change by SECURITY DEFINER triggers — exactly as the finding states.
- 135_statistics_rpcs.sql:246: the statistics module buckets the IDENTICAL column with `date_trunc('month', timezone('Asia/Jerusalem', sd.entered_at))` — the established Israel-civil convention for this column.
- src/lib/utils/israel-time.ts + israel-time.test.ts: exist precisely because "Server Components run in UTC (Vercel) while the office is in Israel"; the test (lines 16-24) demonstrates the UTC-vs-Israel day rollover (22:30Z winter → Israel next civil day).
- target-date.ts:24-28: the R5 fix that switched "today" to `israelCivil(now)` for the same class of bug — directly analogous, confirming the codebase already treats this as a real defect class.
- vercel.json:20-21: the cron runs `0 5 * * *` (05:00 UTC = 08:00 Israel summer), and status-sla-check/route.ts:31 calls `runSlaCheck()` with NO timezone normalization — so the finding's concrete 05:00-UTC scenario is exactly how it deploys.
- No SLA test file exists (Glob found none) — the finding's "none exists today" is correct.

I traced the concrete example: a case entered Israel 2026-06-16 01:00 (summer) = entered_at 2026-06-15T22:00Z → UTC date June 15, Israel civil date June 16. Cron June 16 05:00 UTC computes utcCalendarDaysBetween(Jun15,Jun16)=1 → fires at threshold=1, while by Israel reckoning 0 civil days have elapsed (in-status ~7h). A genuine 1-day-premature fire. Skew direction is correctly characterized (Israel late-evening/post-midnight-local entries over-report by 1).

SEVERITY: I keep the reviewer's Medium. It is a real correctness bug that makes a manager-configured threshold non-deterministic (depends on the UTC offset of the entry instant) and diverges from the Israel-civil convention used everywhere else on the same column — the same class already fixed in target-date.ts (R5). Bounded to ±1 day with no data loss, and the affected slice is narrow in practice (entries whose Israel local time is between midnight and ~02:00/03:00, when UTC date < Israel date — rare for a daytime mortgage office), which keeps it from rising to High. Suggested fix (derive both enteredAt and now via israelCivil() and diff y/m/d like target-date.ts) is sound. Confidence high that the defect exists.

#### `SLA-2` — Documented weekly re-fire never happens — the dedupe UNIQUE index has no time component, so each (recipient, case, status-entry) alerts exactly once forever
- **File:** src/features/sla/services/sla-check.service.ts:60-65, 236-243, 296-318 ; supabase/migrations/073_sla_dedupe_index_and_rpc.sql:30-32, 64-66
- **Evidence:** The service docstring states: 'first alert fires when the threshold is first crossed, re-fires once a week until the case leaves the status'. The authoritative dedupe is the partial UNIQUE index `uq_notifications_overdue_dedupe ON notifications (user_id, case_id, ((data->>'enteredAt'))) WHERE type='case_status_overdue'` (073:30-32), and the RPC inserts `ON CONFLICT (user_id, case_id, ((data->>'enteredAt'))) DO NOTHING` (073:64-66). `enteredAt` is constant for the entire time a case sits in one status (a new entered_at is only minted on status change, which is a different stage row — migration 009_tasks.sql:122). Therefore once the first overdue notification for a (recipient, case, enteredAt) is inserted, the index permanently blocks every subsequent insert for that key. The TS-side 7-day `recentKeys` window (since = now-7d, lines 236-243) is moot — even after that window passes and TS would re-attempt, the RPC's ON CONFLICT silently skips it (counted into skippedAlreadyNotified at line 318, not surfaced as an anomaly). Net: exactly one alert per case-status-entry per recipient, never a weekly repeat.
- **Why it matters:** A case that gets stuck in a status for weeks generates a single alert and then goes silent — the opposite of the feature's stated 'nag weekly until it moves' behavior, so a genuinely stuck case can be forgotten. The 7-day read query, REPEAT_DAYS constant, and idx_notifications_case_overdue helper index (mig 068) all exist to support a re-fire that the permanent unique key makes impossible — dead/misleading code masking the gap.
- **Suggested fix:** Decide the intended contract and make index + RPC + TS agree. To support weekly re-fire, add a week/bucket component to the dedupe key (e.g. include floor(days_since_enter / 7) or a `notified_for_week` value in `data`, and put that in both the UNIQUE index columns and the ON CONFLICT target), so each weekly bucket is a distinct key. If single-alert-per-entry is actually desired, delete the misleading 're-fires once a week' docs, the 7-day `since` read, REPEAT_DAYS, and the now-redundant idx_notifications_case_overdue.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading all named files and cross-references. The authoritative dedupe is the partial UNIQUE index uq_notifications_overdue_dedupe ON notifications(user_id, case_id, ((data->>'enteredAt'))) WHERE type='case_status_overdue' (073:30-32), and the RPC inserts ON CONFLICT (user_id, case_id, ((data->>'enteredAt'))) DO NOTHING (073:64-66). The conflict key has NO time component — I grepped the whole sla feature and migrations dir: no week/bucket/created_at participates anywhere. data.enteredAt is set from stage_durations.entered_at (service lines 158, 283), and migration 009_tasks.sql:121-122 confirms entered_at = NOW() is minted ONLY when status_id changes (a different stage row), so it is constant for the entire time a case sits in one status. Therefore the first overdue notification for a (recipient, case, enteredAt) key permanently blocks every later insert with that key. The TS-side 7-day recentKeys window (since = now-7d, lines 236-243) is moot: after 7 days the original row drops out of that read, so the service re-attempts the insert, but the RPC's ON CONFLICT against the permanent index silently skips it, counting it into skippedAlreadyNotified (line 323) indistinguishable from FK/concurrency skips — never surfaced as an anomaly. Net: exactly one alert per case-status-entry per recipient, never the documented weekly repeat. The stated contract 're-fires once a week until the case leaves the status' appears in three places (service docstring 62-63, mig 068:5-7, cron route 15-16) and is unachievable. The secondary claim is also accurate: REPEAT_DAYS, the 7-day since read, and idx_notifications_case_overdue (mig 068:50-52) exist solely to support a re-fire the unique key makes impossible, so they are dead/misleading. Severity Medium is correct: it is a functional gap in a notification/reminder feature (a genuinely stuck case can go silent), not a security or data-loss bug (not High), and degrades a secondary nag feature rather than a core flow (not Low). All line references and cross-references verified accurate.

### Low (12)

#### `TPL-1` — system_email_templates upsert/delete has no RLS row-count guard (defense-in-depth gap)
- **File:** src/features/templates/actions/update-system-email-template.ts:37-52, src/features/templates/actions/reset-system-email-template.ts:30-35
- **Evidence:** Both actions go through the RLS-respecting createClient() and decide success only on `if (error) return {error:'unknown'}`. If a non-admin somehow reached the DB call, the system_email_templates_admin_all RLS WITH CHECK would block the write, but the upsert affects 0 rows WITHOUT raising an error, so the action would still return `{ ok: true }`. Contrast templates.service.ts updateMessageTemplate/deleteMessageTemplate which correctly use a `.select('id')` row-count guard for exactly this reason ("RLS is admin-only, so a non-admin update affects 0 rows with no error — treat that as failed").
- **Why it matters:** Not currently exploitable because both actions already call isCurrentUserAdmin() at the top (the same is_admin() RPC that backs RLS), so the app-layer check is the real gate. But the success signal is decoupled from whether a row was actually written; if the top-level admin check were ever refactored/removed, a non-admin would silently get a false success. The message_templates path already models the correct belt-and-suspenders pattern.
- **Suggested fix:** Mirror updateMessageTemplate: append `.select('template_key')` to the upsert / delete and treat an empty result array as an unauthorized/failed write, so success reflects an actual row change rather than just the absence of an error.
- **Verify:** All factual claims verified against the code. update-system-email-template.ts:37-52 does an .upsert() through the RLS-respecting createClient() and returns success purely on `if (error) return {error:'unknown'}` (line 52) with no .select() row-count guard; reset-system-email-template.ts:30-35 does the same for .delete(). The RLS policy is admin-only: migration 162 line 23-26 defines system_email_templates_admin_all FOR ALL ... USING(is_admin()) WITH CHECK(is_admin()). Postgres/PostgREST behavior is as described — an UPDATE/DELETE that hits zero rows because the WITH CHECK/USING filter excludes them returns no error, so the "no error => ok:true" logic would yield a false success if a non-admin ever reached the call. The contrast claim is exact: templates.service.ts updateMessageTemplate (107-121) and deleteMessageTemplate (123-132) append .select('id') and return `data.length > 0`, with the verbatim comment the finding quotes about RLS-admin-only 0-row writes.

Adversarial check (tried to refute): the finding is honestly self-limiting and NOT a live vulnerability. Both system-email actions DO call isCurrentUserAdmin() before the DB write (update line 32, reset line 28), and isCurrentUserAdmin (permissions.ts:77-80) wraps the same is_admin() RPC that backs the RLS — so a non-admin is rejected at the app layer with error:'unauthorized' and never reaches the upsert/delete. The false-success branch is therefore currently unreachable; there is no exploit, no data-integrity bug, no correctness defect today. The issue is purely a defense-in-depth / pattern-consistency gap: success is coupled to "absence of error" rather than "a row was written," diverging from the belt-and-suspenders model the sibling message_templates service already uses. Impact is hypothetical and contingent on a future refactor removing the top-level admin check. That is exactly a Low-severity hardening/consistency nit — real and accurately described, but minor. Severity Low is correct (not under- or over-stated).

#### `TPL-3` — renderTemplate inserts literal 'undefined' if a future variable is added to the regex but omitted from context
- **File:** src/features/templates/domain/render-template.ts:12-14
- **Evidence:** `text.replace(VARIABLE_PATTERN, (_, key) => context[key as TemplateVariable])` returns context[key] with no fallback. The pattern is built from TEMPLATE_VARIABLES (all 5), and the sole caller (listRenderedTemplatesForCase) always supplies all 5, so it is safe today. But unlike renderSystemTemplateText — which is explicitly missing-field-safe (`hasOwnProperty ? String(v) : token`, with a unit test asserting unknown tokens stay visible) — renderTemplate has no guard: if someone adds a 6th variable to TEMPLATE_VARIABLES (extending the regex) without adding it to the context object, that field renders as the string 'undefined' into the client-facing message.
- **Why it matters:** A latent footgun in client-facing outbound content: a typo'd/forgotten context key would ship 'undefined' to a borrower's WhatsApp/email rather than leaving the placeholder visible to the advisor. The doc comment claims unknown braces are left untouched, but that only covers braces OUTSIDE the known-variable set, not a known variable missing from context.
- **Suggested fix:** Guard the substitution: `(_, key) => context[key as TemplateVariable] ?? `{${key}}`` (keep the placeholder visible) and/or add a unit test for renderTemplate covering a present-vs-missing context key, paralleling the existing renderSystemTemplateText test.
- **Verify:** Verified against the code. render-template.ts:13 does `text.replace(VARIABLE_PATTERN, (_, key) => context[key as TemplateVariable])` with no fallback — if a matched key is absent from context, the callback returns undefined and String.replace coerces it to the literal string "undefined". The regex (line 5) is built from TEMPLATE_VARIABLES (types.ts:5-12, exactly 5 entries). The sole caller listRenderedTemplatesForCase (templates.service.ts:73-82) supplies all 5 keys, so it is genuinely safe today, exactly as the finding states. The contrast claim is also accurate: renderSystemTemplateText (system-email-templates.ts:306-308) is explicitly missing-field-safe via hasOwnProperty ? String(v) : token, with a passing unit test (system-email-templates.test.ts:20-24) asserting unknown tokens stay visible; no render-template.test.ts exists (confirmed via glob). The doc comment ("Unknown braces are left untouched") does overstate safety for the known-variable-missing-from-context case. Mitigating factor lowering real-world probability (but not invalidating the finding): TemplateContext is Readonly<Record<TemplateVariable,string>>, so adding a 6th variable would make tsc flag the context literal as missing a required key — the footgun only fires if someone bypasses the type (as-cast, looser context type, or new untyped caller). This is a latent maintainability footgun, not a present bug; the reviewer correctly characterizes it as safe-today and rates it Low. Severity Low is appropriate.

#### `TPL-4` — escapeHtml does not encode single quotes; safe only because every attribute sink uses escapeAttr
- **File:** src/lib/email/render.ts:91-101
- **Evidence:** escapeHtml() encodes & < > " but NOT the single quote. The only attribute interpolation that could be single-quote-delimited is the CTA href, which correctly uses escapeAttr() (escapeHtml + `'`→`&#39;`) at line 44. All other escapeHtml() uses (heading l.64, footer l.81, ctaLabel l.44, plainTextBodyHtml/textToHtml bodies, intake summaryTable cells) land in element text content where a bare `'` is harmless. So there is no current injection, but the safety depends entirely on every future attribute sink remembering to call escapeAttr rather than escapeHtml.
- **Why it matters:** The escape contract is implicit and order-dependent: a future contributor who interpolates escapeHtml() output into a single-quoted HTML attribute would have an attribute-breakout/XSS hole with no compile-time signal. Email body content is built from admin-authored templates + (for intake) anonymous user input, so the attribute-escaping discipline matters.
- **Suggested fix:** Either make escapeHtml also encode `'`→`&#39;` (cheap, removes the footgun entirely), or add a short comment on escapeHtml stating it is for element-content only and attributes MUST use escapeAttr.
- **Verify:** Verified against source. render.ts:91-97 escapeHtml encodes & < > " but NOT single quote; escapeAttr (l.99-100) adds '->&#39;. The only single-quote-delimitable dynamic attribute is the CTA href (l.44) which is actually double-quote-delimited AND correctly uses escapeAttr. Every other escapeHtml sink lands in element content, confirmed by reading all callers: render.ts CTA label/heading/footer (l.44/64/81) in element text; system-email-templates plainTextBodyHtml l.127 inside <p>; document-request-email l.43 and client-email.service l.49 inside <p>; notification-email l.124-125 (function is contextTable, not summaryTable as the finding said) inside <td>; intake-office-email summaryTable l.84-85 inside <td>, concatenated as afterBodyHtml into bodyHtml -> rendered at render.ts:68 inside <div>. The dir/lang/align attribute interpolations derive from a typed 'he'|'en' locale, not user input. render.test.ts:7 confirms escapeHtml covers only & < > ". So: NO current injection (the finding admits this), but the safety is an implicit, order-dependent contract — a future contributor interpolating escapeHtml output into a single-quoted attribute would get attribute-breakout XSS with no compile-time signal, and email bodies do mix admin templates + anonymous intake input. This is a genuine latent footgun / hardening gap, accurately described (one trivial naming slip: contextTable vs summaryTable for the notification file). Low severity is correctly calibrated — defensive future-proofing, not an exploitable hole.

#### `NOTIF-2` — Email mirror webhook has no per-notification idempotency — a retried/duplicated webhook delivery sends the email twice
- **File:** src/app/api/push/dispatch/route.ts:58-117; src/features/notifications/services/notification-mirror-email.ts:43-83
- **Evidence:** The dispatch route turns each notifications-INSERT webhook into a push + a mirrored email. It always returns 200 (except bad secret) to avoid retry storms (route comment lines 22-24), but there is no dedupe keyed on the notification row id: sendMirroredNotificationEmail re-renders and re-sends unconditionally each time the route is invoked for a given record. Supabase database webhooks can re-deliver (timeout, at-least-once semantics). The notification ROW is deduped at the DB layer for SLA (uq_notifications_overdue_dedupe, mig 073), but the EMAIL send itself is not idempotent — a second webhook delivery for the same INSERT produces a second identical email. The push leg is similarly non-idempotent but is low-impact (a duplicate generic badge).
- **Why it matters:** A redelivered webhook results in a duplicate mention/reminder/SLA email to the recipient. Low blast radius (no data exposure, just an annoyance), but it violates the round invariant that dispatch should be idempotent.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the email leg idempotent: include the notification row id in the webhook payload (record.id) and record sent emails (e.g. a small notification_email_sent table or a sent_at column on notifications) under a unique constraint, short-circuiting if already sent; or rely on a unique (notification_id) insert before calling sendEmail. Keep returning 200 so the webhook still doesn't retry-storm.
- **Verify:** Verified against the actual code. /api/push/dispatch (route.ts:58-117) is the Supabase Database Webhook target on notifications-INSERT (confirmed by mig 150 line 6 and mig 161 line 7). It always returns 200 except on bad secret (lines 59-117) explicitly to avoid retry storms (comment 22-24), and the email leg runs unconditionally each invocation via sendMirroredNotificationEmail (notification-mirror-email.ts:43-83), which re-renders and calls sendEmail with no dedupe. sendEmail (lib/email/send.ts) has no idempotency key — it just POSTs to Resend. The DB dedupe the finding references, uq_notifications_overdue_dedupe (mig 073 lines 30-32), is a partial unique index that prevents duplicate ROWS only for type='case_status_overdue'; it does NOT prevent a duplicate webhook redelivery of the same single INSERT from sending the email twice. The notifications row has an id PK (mig 028 line 13) that could anchor idempotency, but the dispatch payload type (route.ts:70-79) never even reads record.id, and there is no notification_email_sent table or sent_at column. Supabase webhooks deliver via pg_net at-least-once, so a redelivery (e.g. on a slow handler near the 30s maxDuration / 10s Resend timeout) genuinely produces a second identical email. Severity correctly Low: no data exposure, blast radius is one duplicate mention/reminder/SLA email — an annoyance. The reviewer's own caveats (push leg lower-impact; suggested fix using record.id + a sent-tracking unique constraint) are accurate and not overstated. Not refutable.

#### `NOTIF-3` — task_reminder / case_status_overdue notification rows are inserted by cron jobs that have no email-mirror trigger of their own — email delivery depends entirely on an externally-configured Supabase webhook
- **File:** src/features/tasks/services/task-reminders.service.ts:43-59; src/features/sla/services/sla-check.service.ts:301-310; src/app/api/push/dispatch/route.ts:11-24
- **Evidence:** runTaskReminders and runSlaCheck insert notifications via the admin client / insert_overdue_notifications RPC. Their email mirror is delivered ONLY if the operator has wired a Supabase Database Webhook on INSERT public.notifications → /api/push/dispatch with the CRON_SECRET bearer (documented in the route header, not enforced anywhere). There is no in-code path that calls sendMirroredNotificationEmail for these crons; if the webhook is unconfigured or its secret rotates out of sync, the bell still works (DB insert) but mention/reminder/SLA EMAILS silently never send, with no error surfaced. This is a delivery-completeness fragility rather than a code bug.
- **Why it matters:** Email for an entire class of notifications can be silently dropped based on an out-of-band webhook config that the codebase can't verify, making 'preferences honored / no dropped emails' depend on infra wiring with no observability.
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) document this dependency in a health/integrations check and surface a warning when the notifications webhook is absent, or (b) call sendMirroredNotificationEmail directly from the cron services (via after()/best-effort) for the rows they create, so email delivery doesn't hinge solely on the external webhook. If keeping the webhook-only model, add the idempotency from NOTIF-2 so direct + webhook sends can't double up.
- **Verify:** Verified against the code. (1) runTaskReminders (task-reminders.service.ts:43-59) inserts task_reminder rows via the admin client and runSlaCheck (sla-check.service.ts:296-310) inserts case_status_overdue rows via the insert_overdue_notifications RPC — neither calls any email-mirror path. (2) grep confirms sendMirroredNotificationEmail has exactly ONE in-code caller: /api/push/dispatch/route.ts:110. (3) That route is invoked only by an externally-configured Supabase Database Webhook (route header lines 11-24 document the required INSERT public.notifications -> POST with Bearer CRON_SECRET; migration 161 comment line 7 states 'The actual sending rides the notifications-insert webhook (/api/push/dispatch)'; migration 150 comments concur). No SQL trigger, pg_net/http call, or other code posts to the dispatch route — all migrations only INSERT into notifications. So if the webhook is unconfigured or its secret rotates out of sync, the bell still works (DB insert succeeds) but the email mirror for these kinds silently never sends. (4) No observability: grep over **/api/health/** and features/settings for webhook/CRON_SECRET monitoring returned nothing — nothing surfaces a warning when the notifications webhook is absent. The finding's claim is fully substantiated. Severity Low is appropriate: this is delivery-completeness/infra-wiring fragility, not a code bug — the email is explicitly best-effort (notification-mirror-email.ts:80-82 swallows errors), and the in-app bell is unaffected. One nuance (broadens, not weakens, the finding): the same single webhook is the only delivery path for case_mention/task_mention/task_comment email mirrors too (which originate from DB triggers), so the fragility spans more kinds than the two cron-sourced ones named, but the specific cron-kind claim is correct. Suggested fixes (health-check observability, or calling sendMirroredNotificationEmail directly from the crons via after() — which would require NOTIF-2 idempotency to avoid double sends with the webhook) are coherent.

#### `PUSH-1` — Dispatch route is not idempotent — a webhook retry re-fires duplicate pushes/emails
- **File:** src/app/api/push/dispatch/route.ts:58-118
- **Evidence:** The handler reads `payload.record` (user_id, type, case_id, data) but never reads or persists a notification id, and there is no dedup store. It calls `sendPushToUser` + `sendMirroredNotificationEmail` and returns 200. The triggering Supabase Database Webhook is delivered via pg_net at-least-once and retries on a non-2xx / timeout. If the function does its work but the response is lost (e.g. the 30s `maxDuration` elapses after web-push/Resend calls complete but before the 200 returns, or a transient network drop on the response), the webhook redelivers the same INSERT and the recipient gets a second identical push and a second mirror email. Nothing keys on `record` identity to short-circuit a replay.
- **Why it matters:** Duplicate lock-screen pushes and duplicate emails for the same event. Blast radius is small (push is best-effort, the bell is the source of truth, and the retry window is narrow because the normal path returns 200), so this is a quality/robustness gap rather than a security or data-loss bug. It is the one place the round-specific 'dispatch idempotent' invariant is not satisfied.
- **Suggested fix:** Include the notification row id in the webhook payload (it is available as `record.id`) and dedupe on it before sending — e.g. an INSERT into a small `push_dispatch_log(notification_id PK)` guarded by ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING, sending only when the insert affected a row. Alternatively accept the current best-effort behavior and document it explicitly as an accepted trade-off in the route comment.
- **Verify:** Verified against the code. src/app/api/push/dispatch/route.ts:58-118 destructures payload.record as { user_id, type, case_id, data } only (lines 70-79) and never reads or persists a notification id; it runs sendPushToUser + sendMirroredNotificationEmail (lines 108-116) then returns 200 with no dedup check. A repo-wide grep for push_dispatch_log / dispatch_log / notification_id found no dedup store anywhere. The trigger really is a Supabase Database Webhook on public.notifications INSERT delivered via pg_net (documented in migrations 150 and 161 header comments), which is at-least-once and retries on non-2xx/timeout. maxDuration=30 (line 26) makes the "work completes, then the 200 is lost to a timeout/network drop, then the same INSERT is redelivered" window concrete. Both downstream services (push-sender.ts, notification-mirror-email.ts) are explicitly best-effort and have no internal idempotency, so a replay re-fires both legs. The suggested fix is feasible: notifications.id is a UUID PRIMARY KEY (migration 028 line 13), so record.id is present in the standard webhook payload and can key an ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING dedup. Note: migration 073's uq_notifications_overdue_dedupe is row-CREATION dedupe (prevents duplicate notification rows) and does not protect against a replay of an already-existing row's INSERT event, so it does not cover this case. Severity is correctly Low and the reviewer did not overstate it: push is best-effort with the in-app bell as source of truth, the email mirror respects per-user prefs, the normal path returns 200 quickly so the retry window is narrow, and there is no security or data-loss impact — only an occasional duplicate lock-screen push and duplicate mirror email.

#### `PUSH-2` — subscribe upsert unconditionally reassigns an existing endpoint's owner (subscription takeover if an endpoint leaks)
- **File:** src/features/notifications/services/push-subscriptions.service.ts:22-43
- **Evidence:** `upsertPushSubscription` does `table().upsert({ user_id, endpoint, ... }, { onConflict: 'endpoint' })`. The `push_subscriptions` table has `endpoint TEXT NOT NULL UNIQUE` (migration 150:23). Because the conflict target is `endpoint` and the upsert SETs `user_id` to the current caller, an authenticated user who learns another user's endpoint URL can call `subscribePushAction` with it and the row's `user_id` is rewritten to the attacker — re-homing the victim's device subscription to the attacker (victim stops receiving pushes; attacker now receives generic pushes meant for the victim's events). The unsubscribe path is correctly scoped (`deletePushSubscriptionByEndpoint` filters by user_id, per its own test), but the subscribe path has no such ownership guard.
- **Why it matters:** It is an authz/ownership gap on a per-device record. Severity is Low only because the push endpoint is a per-device, non-enumerable URL that is not normally exposed to other users, so exploitation requires first obtaining the victim's endpoint; and the push payload is intentionally generic/no-PII, so even a successful takeover leaks only category-level titles. Still, an upsert that silently transfers ownership of someone else's row is not the behavior the table's RLS-locked, service-role-only design intends.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the upsert non-owner-transferring: either change `onConflict` to `(user_id, endpoint)` (add that composite to the table) so a colliding endpoint owned by a different user inserts/no-ops rather than steals, or do an explicit delete-foreign-then-insert only when the existing row's user_id matches the caller. At minimum, gate the upsert so it refuses to change `user_id` when the endpoint already belongs to a different user.
- **Verify:** Confirmed in code. push-subscriptions.service.ts:27-37 — upsertPushSubscription does table().upsert({ user_id, endpoint, ... }, { onConflict: 'endpoint' }), unconditionally SETting user_id to the passed caller id on conflict. Migration 150_push_subscriptions.sql:23 defines endpoint TEXT NOT NULL UNIQUE, so onConflict:'endpoint' matches by endpoint alone and rewrites the existing row's user_id. subscribe-push.ts:13-37 — the action's Zod schema only validates endpoint as a URL string (no ownership proof), checks auth, then calls upsertPushSubscription(userRes.user.id, parsed.data, ...) with a caller-supplied endpoint. So any authenticated user who submits another user's endpoint re-homes (steals ownership of) that subscription row. The contrast the finding draws is accurate: deletePushSubscriptionByEndpoint (service:52-58) filters .eq('endpoint').eq('user_id') and is explicitly tested (push-subscriptions.service.test.ts:31-42, ref R2-notif-1) and commented as 'the authorization boundary'; the subscribe path got no such guard. Impact chain verified: api/push/dispatch/route.ts:108-109 calls sendPushToUser(record.user_id) → push-sender.ts:48 listUserPushSubscriptions(userId) → service:60-71 selects by user_id, so after takeover the victim's endpoint no longer serves the victim. Severity correctly Low: I grepped all endpoint references (16 files) and found NO read path exposing another user's push endpoint cross-user (table is RLS-locked with no policy, all reads scoped by user_id server-side), so exploitation requires first obtaining the victim's non-enumerable endpoint URL; and the push payload is intentionally generic/no-PII (dispatch route TITLES are category-level only, lines 28-40). Minor imprecision in the finding's impact wording: the takeover misdirects the attacker's OWN generic notifications to the victim's device while denying the victim their pushes (rather than the attacker literally receiving the victim's pushes), but the core defect — an upsert silently transferring ownership of another user's row with no owner guard — is genuine and the rating stands.

#### `PUSH-3` — subscribe/unsubscribe push actions are not rate-limited
- **File:** src/features/notifications/actions/subscribe-push.ts:24-39
- **Evidence:** `subscribePushAction` (and `unsubscribePushAction`) validate Zod + check auth, then write to `push_subscriptions` via the admin client, with no `checkRateLimit` call. The CLAUDE.md standard rate-limits expensive/external/abuse-prone actions; a write that an authenticated client can fire in a loop is a candidate. Compare the dispatch fan-out which is protected by being CRON_SECRET-gated, and other writes (lookup-borrower, exports) which do gate.
- **Why it matters:** An authenticated user could spam upserts/deletes against the table. It is Low because each call is a single small upsert keyed on the caller's own endpoint (the row count per user is naturally bounded by the number of real devices, and onConflict makes repeated calls no-ops rather than row growth), so the abuse ceiling is low. Noted for consistency with the project's rate-limit posture, not as a live exploit.
- **Suggested fix:** Optional: add a light `checkRateLimit('push_subscribe', e.g. 30/hr, subject `user:<uid>`)` to both actions, fail-closed, mirroring the established pattern. Acceptable to skip given the bounded blast radius — flag only for parity with the documented standard.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. subscribe-push.ts:24-39 (subscribePushAction) and unsubscribe-push.ts:18-29 (unsubscribePushAction) both do Zod safeParse + supabase.auth.getUser() check, then write to push_subscriptions via the service-role admin client (push-subscriptions.service.ts: upsertPushSubscription / deletePushSubscriptionByEndpoint). Neither calls checkRateLimit; grep finds zero checkRateLimit usage anywhere under src/features/notifications. The actions are exported server actions consumed by use-push-subscription.ts but are directly invokable by any authenticated client, so no upstream gate exists.

The finding's mitigations are all accurate: migration 150 (150_push_subscriptions.sql:23) declares endpoint TEXT NOT NULL UNIQUE, and the service upserts with onConflict:'endpoint', so repeated subscribe calls are true no-op replacements rather than row growth; per-user rows are bounded by real device count. Unsubscribe deletes are scoped .eq('endpoint').eq('user_id', userId), so no cross-user effect. The table is RLS-on/no-policy, reachable only via the admin client behind the auth check, and idx_push_subscriptions_user exists.

The parity argument is well-founded: the project does rate-limit ordinary authenticated DB writes elsewhere — save-scenario.ts gates a routine scenario upsert at 60/hr with failMode:'closed' — establishing a precedent that a comparable cheap write should also be capped per CLAUDE.md's rate-limit standard. So this is a genuine, correctly-stated consistency gap.

Severity Low is correct and matches the reviewer's own scoping: blast radius is bounded (upserts collapse to no-ops, deletes are self-scoped, both writes are tiny and indexed), there is no row-growth DoS or cross-user impact, only wasted DB round-trips under abusive looping. The finding explicitly frames it as a parity nicety ('acceptable to skip'), which is the right characterization.

#### `SLA-3` — Production env warning under-reports which crons CRON_SECRET gates
- **File:** src/lib/env.ts:213-215
- **Evidence:** `if (!env.CRON_SECRET) warnings.push('CRON_SECRET is unset — /api/cron/backup will refuse every call (nightly backup disabled).')`. The same secret gates /api/cron/status-sla-check (route.ts:21-28), task-reminders, backup-watchdog, erasure-watchdog, cleanup-orphaned-blobs, and /api/push/dispatch (notification email+push mirror). Vercel registers all of them (vercel.json:1-27).
- **Why it matters:** An operator who reads the cold-start warning believes only backup is affected when CRON_SECRET is missing; in reality SLA scanning, task reminders, and the entire push/email-mirror delivery path are all silently disabled too. Misleading failure visibility for an operationally critical secret.
- **Suggested fix:** Reword the warning to name the consequence broadly, e.g. 'CRON_SECRET is unset — every /api/cron/* route and /api/push/dispatch will refuse all calls (backups, SLA scan, task reminders, push/email notifications disabled).'
- **Verify:** Verified against source. src/lib/env.ts:213-214 warns only "/api/cron/backup will refuse every call (nightly backup disabled)" when CRON_SECRET is unset. A grep confirms the SAME secret gates six cron routes and the push/dispatch route, each with an identical `if (!env.CRON_SECRET)` refusal: backup/route.ts:29, backup-watchdog:20, cleanup-orphaned-blobs:28, erasure-watchdog:21, status-sla-check:21 (read in full — returns 503 not_configured), task-reminders:16, and push/dispatch:52 (isAuthorized returns false → 401). push/dispatch/route.ts imports sendMirroredNotificationEmail + sendPushToUser and its docstring confirms it is the notification email+push-mirror webhook target, so a missing secret silently disables SLA scanning, task reminders, two watchdogs, orphaned-blob cleanup, and the entire push/email notification delivery path — not just backup. vercel.json registers all six cron paths. The warning therefore genuinely under-reports the blast radius and would mislead an operator diagnosing a missing secret. Severity Low is correct as stated: this is an observability/messaging defect with no incorrect runtime behavior, no security or data-loss impact — it only makes a misconfiguration harder to diagnose.

#### `SLA-4` — RPC insert-vs-skip count relies on `(SELECT 1 WHERE FOUND)` idiom rather than GET DIAGNOSTICS
- **File:** supabase/migrations/073_sla_dedupe_index_and_rpc.sql:67-71
