- **Evidence:** After `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING`, the RPC counts inserts via `v_inserted := v_inserted + COALESCE((SELECT 1 WHERE FOUND), 0)`. The comment on line 68 says 'ROW_COUNT distinguishes insert (1) from conflict-skip (0)' but the code reads the `FOUND` boolean, not ROW_COUNT. The idiom works (FOUND is true only when the INSERT affected a row, and the scalar subquery reads it before being reset), but it is fragile and the comment is inaccurate.
- **Why it matters:** The returned count drives notificationsCreated vs skippedAlreadyNotified in the cron's JSON result (route.ts:32) — the only operator-facing signal of how many alerts went out. A subtle regression in this idiom would silently miscount without any test (no SLA tests exist).
- **Suggested fix:** Use the canonical form: after the INSERT, `GET DIAGNOSTICS v_rc = ROW_COUNT; v_inserted := v_inserted + v_rc;` and fix the comment. ROW_COUNT is 1 on insert, 0 on conflict-skip, which is exactly what the comment already claims.
- **Verify:** Verified against the code. In supabase/migrations/073_sla_dedupe_index_and_rpc.sql the RPC insert_overdue_notifications counts inserts via `v_inserted := v_inserted + COALESCE((SELECT 1 WHERE FOUND), 0)` (lines 69-71), reading the FOUND boolean — while the comment on line 68 states "ROW_COUNT distinguishes insert (1) from conflict-skip (0)". The code never calls GET DIAGNOSTICS / ROW_COUNT, so the comment is factually inaccurate (comment-vs-code mismatch is real and confirmed). The returned count drives the operator-facing JSON: sla-check.service.ts uses `insertedCount` to compute notificationsCreated (line 322) and skippedAlreadyNotified (line 323), and the cron route spreads `...result` into the response at src/app/api/cron/status-sla-check/route.ts:32 (`return NextResponse.json({ ok: true, ...result })`) — confirming the finding's route.ts:32 citation (path elided but line correct). No SLA tests exist (Glob/Grep for *sla* tests and for insert_overdue_notifications/runSlaCheck in test files returned nothing), confirming the "no test guards this" claim. Migration 073 is the sole definition; no later migration supersedes it. Severity is correctly Low: the finding itself concedes the idiom works, and it does — after INSERT ... ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING, FOUND is true only on a real insert; the scalar subquery `(SELECT 1 WHERE FOUND)` reads FOUND during expression evaluation before the assignment statement updates it, so the count is correct today. There is no runtime miscount — the issue is an inaccurate comment plus a fragile/non-canonical idiom, which is genuinely Low (maintainability), not Medium/High. The suggested fix (GET DIAGNOSTICS v_rc = ROW_COUNT) is the canonical form and matches what the comment already claims. Only flaw in the finding is the elided file path on the route.ts citation; line number and the consumption chain are accurate.

#### `R-TMPL-1` — Bracketed-hex colors in the system-template email-preview pane
- **File:** src/features/templates/components/system-template-dialog.tsx
- **Evidence:** The live preview swatch (lines 204-214) uses raw bracketed hex utilities instead of brand tokens: line 204 `bg-[#f7f4ec]`, line 206 `bg-[#0a0a0a]` and `text-[#c9a961]`, line 212 `bg-[#c9a961]` and `text-[#0a0a0a]`. CLAUDE.md is explicit: 'Any new [#hex] literal in a class is an auto-reject in code review.' #0a0a0a maps to `brand-black`/`bg-brand-black`, #c9a961 maps to `brand-gold`/`bg-brand-gold` + `text-brand-gold`. (#f7f4ec has no exact token — closest is `brand-gold-soft` #FAF8F3; if the email-card warm tint must match the rendered email byte-for-byte, it can stay as an inline style on a div rather than a Tailwind class, but the gold/black ones have direct token equivalents.)
- **Why it matters:** Project anti-pattern (auto-reject in review): bracketed-hex bypasses the brand token system, so a future brand color change won't propagate and the values can drift from the canonical email palette. This is the in-app preview UI (not the email HTML, where inline hex is legitimate because clients strip CSS).
- **Suggested fix:** Replace the gold/black bracketed-hex utility classes with brand tokens: `bg-[#0a0a0a]`→`bg-brand-black`, `text-[#c9a961]`→`text-brand-gold`, `bg-[#c9a961]`→`bg-brand-gold`, `text-[#0a0a0a]`→`text-brand-black`. For the #f7f4ec card tint with no exact token, move it to an inline style attribute (style={{ background: '#f7f4ec' }}) so it isn't a Tailwind bracketed-hex class, or add a token if the warm tint is reused.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading src/features/templates/components/system-template-dialog.tsx. The cited bracketed-hex literals are present exactly as described: line 204 `bg-[#f7f4ec]`, line 206 `bg-[#0a0a0a]` + `text-[#c9a961]`, line 212 `bg-[#c9a961]` + `text-[#0a0a0a]`. CLAUDE.md explicitly designates any new `[#hex]` literal in a class as an auto-reject anti-pattern. Token mapping verified in src/app/globals.css: `--color-brand-black: #0A0A0A` (so #0a0a0a -> brand-black) and `--color-brand-gold: #C9A961` (so #c9a961 -> brand-gold); #f7f4ec has no exact token (closest brand-gold-soft is #FAF8F3). The same file already uses brand tokens elsewhere (bg-brand-gold, text-brand-black, accent-brand-gold, hover:bg-brand-gold-soft on lines 174/189/262), so the bracketed-hex here is an internal inconsistency, not a sanctioned exception. The finding correctly scopes this to the in-app preview pane, not the email HTML (the real email builder is src/lib/email/render.ts, where inline hex is legitimate). One correction to the finding's hedge: the preview's #f7f4ec does NOT need to match the email byte-for-byte because the actual email uses #F3EEE3 (page) and #FFFFFF/#FAF8F3 (card) and never #f7f4ec, so the preview is already not a color-faithful match -- but this only weakens the suggested-fix caveat, not the core finding. Severity Low is correct: convention/maintainability issue in an admin-only settings preview with zero functional or security impact.

#### `R-TMPL-2` — system-template-dialog.tsx exceeds the 250-line component limit
- **File:** src/features/templates/components/system-template-dialog.tsx
- **Evidence:** The file is 268 lines (one main `SystemTemplateDialog` component plus the small `SaveButton` helper). CLAUDE.md Engineering Standards: 'Components: max 250 lines → Exceeding limit means SPLIT, not deferred.' The component carries 5 local useState fields, locale switching, variable insertion, reset transition, the form, and an inline email-preview block.
- **Why it matters:** Documented hard file-size limit; the inline preview block (lines 200-223) and the variable-insertion logic are independently extractable, which would bring the component under the limit and improve readability.
- **Suggested fix:** Extract the email-preview pane (lines 200-223) into a small presentational `SystemEmailPreview` component (props: locale, heading, body, ctaLabel, subject) co-located in the templates feature; that alone drops the file well under 250 lines.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the file. src/features/templates/components/system-template-dialog.tsx is 268 lines (wc -l reports 268; Read shows content through the closing brace of the SaveButton helper on line 268). CLAUDE.md Engineering Standards state "Components: max 250 lines → Exceeding limit means SPLIT, not deferred" and list "God files (>250 lines for components)" as an auto-reject anti-pattern. 268 > 250, so the file exceeds the documented hard limit by 18 lines. The file is a single 'use client' component module: one main SystemTemplateDialog component (lines 35-253) plus a small SaveButton helper (255-268). It carries locale state + 5 content useState fields (subject/heading/body/ctaLabel/enabled, lines 45-49; the finding's "5 local useState" undercounts by one since locale on line 39 is also useState, but this is immaterial), locale switching (selectLocale 76-84 + toggle UI 106-121), variable insertion (insertVariable 64-74 + UI 165-181), reset transition (86-97), the form, and the inline email-preview block. The suggested extraction target — the email-preview pane at lines 200-223 — is verified to be a self-contained presentational block reading only locale/heading/body/ctaLabel/subject, and extracting it would drop the file well under 250 lines. The finding is accurate. Severity Low is appropriate: this is a pure documented-style/maintainability violation with no correctness, security, or runtime impact, and the fix is a low-risk mechanical extraction.

### Refuted (1)

- `TPL-2` listMessageTemplates rethrows the raw Supabase error object — Refuted by reading the code. (1) `if (error) throw error;` at templates.service.ts:37 is the DOMINANT codebase convention for read-side fetch services, not an outlier — it appears 31 times across 15 service files (borrowers, cases, integrations, incomes, case-banks, team, documents, tasks, simulators, case-comments, obligations, leads, banks, task-attachments). The finding's contrast against the one sibling listRenderedTemplatesForCase is misleading; that sibling has a different contract (silently no-op an optional picker). (2) The cited project standard ('NEVER return Supabase error.message TO THE CLIENT ... from a server action') is scoped to server ACTIONS that RETURN error.message to the client. listMessageTemplates is not a server action and does not return error.message — it throws into the React Server Component render path, a distinct mechanism the rule does not govern. (3) Runtime behavior already matches the standard's intent: in production (NODE_ENV=production, no override in next.config.ts) Next.js sanitizes Server Component errors to a digest, so raw .message/.details/.hint never reach the client; the app error boundary src/app/(app)/error.tsx renders a generic i18n'd message (t('title')/t('description')) — not error.message — and logs server-side via console.error + Sentry.captureException. Net = server-side log + generic translated message, exactly the redaction the standard wants. (4) The only caller (settings/templates/page.tsx:14) is admin-gated via isCurrentUserAdmin() redirect at line 11, as the finding concedes. The 'could leak DB internals' concern is speculative and false on the actual production path. The suggested fix (return [] on error) would be a regression — it masks real DB/RLS failures on an admin page, silently showing 'no templates'. The current throw-to-error-boundary is the correct, conventional, safe choice.


## Round 13 — tasks (CRUD / assignment / threads / attachments / reminders)

**raw 26 -> confirmed 24 / refuted 2  (High 0, Medium 8, Low 16)**

### Medium (8)

#### `TASK-REASSIGN-1` — Reassigning with a note double-notifies the new assignee (two bells + two emails for one handoff)
- **File:** supabase/migrations/131_reassign_task_rpc.sql:98-126 (+ 185_task_comment_assignee_notification.sql:36-99, src/features/notifications/services/notification-mirror-email.ts:13-26)
- **Evidence:** reassign_task() performs UPDATE tasks SET assigned_to=... (fires notify_task_change → one 'task_assigned' notification to the new assignee), and when a note is supplied ALSO inserts a row into task_comments with event_type='comment' (lines 113-126). Migration 185 added notify_task_comment_assignee, an AFTER INSERT trigger on task_comments that fires on EVERY 'comment' row and notifies the task's CURRENT assigned_to. By the time the note is inserted, assigned_to is already the NEW assignee, and the author (v_actor=reassigner) is never the recipient, so the dedup guards in 185 (recipient=actor, @mention) do not apply. Result: the new assignee receives BOTH a 'task_assigned' bell AND a 'task_comment' bell for the same handoff. Both kinds are also emailed — 'task_assigned' via the action's after() call (reassign-task.ts:74-82) and 'task_comment' via sendMirroredNotificationEmail (MIRRORED_KINDS includes 'task_comment', notification-mirror-email.ts:20-26). So a single note-bearing reassignment sends the recipient two emails.
- **Why it matters:** Mig 185 (F12 'notify assignee on any comment') was written for the free-text-comment path and did not account for the reassign RPC reusing the same 'comment' event_type for its handoff note. Every reassignment-with-note now produces duplicate bells and duplicate emails to the same person about the same event — notification noise that erodes trust in the bell/inbox.
- **Suggested fix:** Suppress the assignee comment-notification for the note the RPC writes alongside a reassignment. Cleanest: write the handoff note with a distinct event_type (or set a metadata flag like {'system_note': true}) and have notify_task_comment_assignee skip it; or fold the note into the 'reassigned' event row's body/metadata so no separate 'comment' insert happens. Keep the @mention trigger (134) behavior intact for genuine mentions inside the note.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the full chain. reassign_task() (131:93-126) runs UPDATE tasks SET assigned_to=... then, when a note is given, inserts a task_comments row with event_type='comment' (author=reassigner). (1) The UPDATE fires notify_task_change (the trigger lives in mig 159:229-320, not 131 as the finding's prose implies, but the behavior is exactly as described): on the UPDATE branch (266-286) NEW.assigned_to is DISTINCT FROM OLD and from the actor, so it inserts a 'task_assigned' bell to the new assignee. (2) The 'comment' row fires notify_task_comment_assignee (185:36-99); it passes the event_type='comment' gate (50), reads the task's CURRENT assigned_to = the NEW assignee (54-55), recipient != actor(reassigner) so the self-skip (61) doesn't apply, and there's no @mention so the dedup (67) doesn't apply — it inserts a 'task_comment' bell to the SAME new assignee. The 'reassigned' event row does NOT trigger 185 (gate at line 50). So two bells for one handoff: confirmed. Emails: 'task_assigned' is sent by the action's after()→sendTaskNotificationEmail (reassign-task.ts:74-82) and is NOT in MIRRORED_KINDS, so the webhook won't also email it; 'task_comment' IS in MIRRORED_KINDS (notification-mirror-email.ts:20-26) so the notifications-INSERT webhook (/api/push/dispatch:110-115) emails it via sendMirroredNotificationEmail. The two emails are gated by independent prefs — task_assigned→email_task_assigned, task_comment→email_mentions (preferences.service.ts:64-65), both default-true — so no natural dedup. Two emails to the same person for one handoff: confirmed. The early no_change return (131:83-91) means this only happens on a genuine handoff with a note, which is a common flow. Severity Medium is defensible: not a security/authz/data-loss/crash issue, only the reassign-WITH-note path is affected, but it produces user-visible duplicate emails to a real colleague, eroding inbox trust. Minor inaccuracy in the finding: it attributes notify_task_change to mig 131; the function actually lives in 159 — but the described firing behavior is correct.

#### `TASK-REASSIGN-2` — Reassign affordance is shown to view_own_cases advisors who cannot reassign (C-036 affordance/server mismatch)
- **File:** src/features/tasks/components/task-actions-menu.tsx:90-95 (gate is only !task.is_private; cross-ref tasks-list.tsx:153-158, tasks-board.tsx:98,116-123, supabase/migrations/131_reassign_task_rpc.sql:56-63 vs 159_task_assignment_attribution.sql:20-38)
- **Evidence:** The reassign menu item renders whenever onReassign is passed and the task is not private — both the list (TaskRow→TaskActionsMenu) and the board pass onReassign unconditionally for every visible task; there is no authz gate. But the reassign_task RPC only authorizes: assignee (assigned_to=actor), creator (created_by=actor), view_all_cases, or admin (131:56-63). tasks_select (159:20-38) additionally lets a view_own_cases advisor SEE tasks on a case they are the responsible/associated advisor for (case_id branch). So an advisor with view_own_cases (not view_all_cases, not admin) who is the responsible advisor on case X can SEE a task on X that was created by and assigned to a different advisor, sees the 'Reassign' item, opens the dialog, submits — and the RPC returns 'unauthorized' → toast 'reassignFailed'. The user sees an action they are not permitted to perform.
- **Why it matters:** Violates the C-036 edit-gate invariant (view-only-on-this-resource users must not see affordances that fail at the server). It is not a data-leak (the server correctly rejects), but it is a confusing dead-end action for the exact persona the gate exists to protect. Note this is also an intentional asymmetry vs the base 'case-scoped writes canonicalize on can_edit_case' rule — tasks deliberately use an ownership model (mig 129) rather than can_edit_case, so the responsible advisor is NOT a reassign authority; the UI should reflect that.
- **Suggested fix:** Compute a canReassign flag server-side per task (assigned_to===me OR created_by===me OR canViewAll OR isAdmin — mirroring the RPC's authz exactly) and thread it into TaskRow/TaskBoardCard so onReassign is only wired when canReassign is true. Reuse the same domain predicate the create/assignee picker already relies on so the two cannot drift.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code end-to-end. (1) UI gate: task-actions-menu.tsx:90 renders the Reassign item whenever `onReassign && !task.is_private` — no authz check. (2) onReassign is wired unconditionally for every visible task: tasks-list.tsx:67 (TaskRow onReassign={setReassignTarget}) -> task-row.tsx:243 forwards it; tasks-board.tsx:98 (TaskBoardColumn onReassign={setReassignTarget}) -> task-board-card.tsx:111 forwards it. Neither surface filters by per-task authz. (3) RPC authz (131_reassign_task_rpc.sql:56-63) only allows assigned_to=actor OR created_by=actor OR view_all_cases OR is_admin — the responsible advisor is NOT an authority; non-matching callers get error 'unauthorized'. (4) tasks_select (159:20-38, also 148 and confirmed verbatim in 188's mirror) additionally grants SELECT to a view_own_cases advisor who is the case's assigned_advisor_id, so such an advisor genuinely SEES a task created+assigned to a different advisor on their case, sees the Reassign item, and on submit reassign-task.ts:65-66 maps the RPC's 'unauthorized' to a failed Result, and task-reassign-dialog.tsx:70-72 shows toast 'reassignFailed'. So the exact persona the C-036 edit-gate invariant protects (view_own_cases, not view_all_cases, not admin, responsible advisor) is shown a dead-end affordance.\n\nRefutation attempts failed: checked migrations newer than 131/159 (182, 188) — 182 only broadens cases_select/can_view_case (does not narrow tasks_select), 188 only adds the mention RPC; neither changes reassign_task authz nor the tasks_select branches. The board does not pre-filter tasks by assignee/creator either, so every visible card exposes the item.\n\nSeverity Medium is accurate, not over/understated: it is NOT a data leak (the server correctly rejects, returns a generic error code, leaks no Supabase message), but it is a confusing dead-end action for the precise view-only-on-this-resource persona, which is the same class of affordance/server-mismatch the codebase has been rating Medium under the C-036 invariant. The suggested fix (compute canReassign server-side mirroring the RPC authz = assigned_to===me OR created_by===me OR canViewAll OR isAdmin, and thread it so onReassign is only wired when true) is correct and matches the existing edit-gate pattern.

#### `TC-1` — @-mention notification leaks task title + comment preview to a non-viewer (trigger never checks can_view_task)
- **File:** supabase/migrations/134_task_comment_mentions.sql:62-82
- **Evidence:** notify_task_comment_mentions parses every @[name](uuid) token in the body and INSERTs a 'task_mention' notification for each mentioned id whose only gate is `mentioned_id <> actor AND EXISTS(profiles p WHERE p.id = mentioned_id AND p.is_active)` (lines 70-71). It NEVER calls public.can_view_task(NEW.task_id). The notification carries data.taskTitle + data.preview (lines 75-80), which the bell renders (notification-bell.tsx:191-196 -> message.case_mention with `preview = [task, d.preview].join(': ')`) AND is emailed (notification-mirror-email.ts:99-104 includes 'task' and 'preview'). Migration 188 added list_task_mentionable_profiles to scope the PICKER to viewers (its own header: 'Scoping the picker stops a mention/notification from leaking the task...F11'), but the picker only filters UI suggestions — the comment body is free text, so a user who can post on the task (passed task_comments_insert RLS) can hand-craft @[Anyone](uuid) for any active non-viewer and that recipient gets the task title + preview by bell + email. The fix shipped at the UI layer; the authoritative trigger gate was not added.
- **Why it matters:** Private tasks and general/office tasks are exactly the rows a junior advisor/secretary should not see. The mention trigger is the office-wide ground truth for who gets notified, and it leaks the task title + a 140-char body preview (sometimes by email, which can't be unsent) to people with zero access to the task — the precise leak migration 188 claimed to close. Blast radius is limited (requires a crafted token, recipient must be active), so Medium not High.
- **Suggested fix:** Gate the per-recipient INSERT on visibility: inside the FOR loop add `AND public.can_view_task_for(mentioned_id, NEW.task_id)` (a parameterised-by-user can_view_task, analogous to has_permission_for added in mig 188), or at minimum skip mentioned ids that fail a visibility check. Mirror the same fix into notify_case_comment_mentions (mig 108) which has the identical gap.
- **Verify:** Confirmed against the code. notify_task_comment_mentions (134_task_comment_mentions.sql:62-83) loops over every @[name](uuid) token and INSERTs a 'task_mention' notification gated ONLY on `mentioned_id <> actor AND EXISTS(profiles WHERE id=mentioned_id AND is_active)` (lines 70-71). It never calls can_view_task(NEW.task_id). The notification data carries taskTitle + a 140-char body preview (lines 57-60, 75-80).

The picker-scoping fix in 188_task_mentionable_profiles.sql only adds list_task_mentionable_profiles (gated on can_view_task at lines 103-105) for UI suggestions; it touches no trigger, yet its header (lines 1-7) claims to close the "leak the task title/preview" hole. The authoritative trigger gate is genuinely absent.

Attack prerequisite holds: task_comments_insert (140_task_comments_rls_scope.sql:40-49) requires the POSTER to see the parent task (transitive tasks_select), but the body is free text, so a legitimate poster can hand-craft a token for any active non-viewer. The recipient then reads the row with no re-check — notifications_select_own (028_notifications.sql:35-36) gates only on user_id=auth.uid(), not can_view_task. The bell renders it as [taskTitle, preview].join(': ') (notification-bell.tsx:195) and the email mirror includes task+preview, with 'task_mention' present in MIRRORED_KINDS (notification-mirror-email.ts:20-26, 99-104) — so it both bells AND emails, gated only by the recipient's email-preference toggle. Because data is a denormalized snapshot, the leak survives later task soft-delete.

The mirror claim for case comments is also valid: notify_case_comment_mentions (108_case_comment_mentions.sql:56-57) has the identical pattern with no can_view_case check, and can_view_case (mig 039) exists, so the suggested fix is implementable.

Severity Medium is correct (not High): requires a crafted token AND an active recipient, limited blast radius. The poster-must-view-the-task nuance does not weaken the finding because the leak is to the mentioned non-viewer, exactly as stated. The email half cannot be unsent, justifying Medium over Low. Line citations are accurate; the email path matches notification-mirror-email.ts as cited.

#### `TC-2` — Reassign system-event row stores hardcoded Hebrew body that is rendered verbatim to English-locale users
- **File:** supabase/migrations/131_reassign_task_rpc.sql:108-110
- **Evidence:** The 'reassigned' event row is inserted with `body = 'הועברה ל' || COALESCE(v_assignee_name, 'יועץ')` (raw Hebrew literal). SystemEventRow renders `{item.body}` directly (task-thread.tsx:57) with no per-event_type i18n mapping — the component has metadata + event_type available but only ever prints the stored body. An English-locale user opening the thread sees 'הועברה ל<name>' verbatim. CLAUDE.md Definition-of-Done requires user-facing strings go through i18n and the component work in both He (RTL) and En (LTR); this string is locale-baked at write time.
- **Why it matters:** Violates the bilingual requirement for a user-facing string in a core thread UI. The body is frozen in Hebrew at insert time, so it cannot be re-localized — an English user permanently sees Hebrew system events.
- **Suggested fix:** Store the reassign event semantically (event_type='reassigned' + metadata.to_user_id is already present) and localize in SystemEventRow via a tasks.thread.events.* key (e.g. t('events.reassigned', { name })), resolving the assignee name client-side. Same applies to any future system-event body.
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED by reading the code. (1) supabase/migrations/131_reassign_task_rpc.sql:108-110 inserts the 'reassigned' task_comments row with body = 'הועברה ל' || COALESCE(v_assignee_name, 'יועץ') — a raw Hebrew literal baked at write time, plus metadata jsonb_build_object('to_user_id', p_assignee_id, ...). I verified migration 131 is the LIVE definition: it is the only CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION reassign_task in supabase/migrations; migration 132 only redefines notify_task_change (notifications), not the comment body, and migration 159 does not redefine reassign_task either. (2) src/features/tasks/components/task-thread.tsx:57 — SystemEventRow renders {item.body} verbatim. The component has item.event_type and item.metadata available but performs NO per-event_type i18n mapping; it only translates the surrounding chrome via useTranslations('tasks.thread') and passes systemLabel/unknownAuthor down. (3) messages/en.json:2547-2557 confirms a tasks.thread namespace with English strings (title/send/hint/systemAuthor='System'/unknownAuthor) — so English-locale users DO reach this surface and see translated chrome wrapping a Hebrew-baked event body. There is NO events.* key under tasks.thread, confirming 'no per-event_type i18n mapping.' This violates the CLAUDE.md Definition-of-Done (user-facing strings must go through i18n; must work in both He RTL and En LTR). The body is frozen in Hebrew at insert time so it cannot be re-localized. The suggested fix is feasible because metadata.to_user_id already carries the semantic data. Scope note: the reviewer slightly UNDERSTATED scope — the same Hebrew-baked-body pattern exists for every system event type (create-task.ts:74 '✦ נוצרה', complete-task.ts:81 '✓ הושלמה', reopen-task.ts:61 '↩ נפתחה מחדש', snooze-task.ts:66 '⏱ נדחתה ל...', change-task-status.ts:98 'שונה סטטוס ל«...»' with a Hebrew STATUS_LABEL map). The specific TC-2 claim about the reassign RPC is accurate. Severity Medium is correct: a hard violation of a non-negotiable bilingual Definition-of-Done in a core thread UI with no runtime workaround, but it is a secondary surface with no security/data-loss impact and the primary audience is Hebrew-speaking advisors.

#### `TASK-ATT-1` — Case-linked task finalize trusts client storagePath without binding it to caseId — cross-case pointer + service-role blob-delete on purge
- **File:** src/features/tasks/actions/task-attachment-upload.ts:96-199 (finalize), :44 (FinalizeTaskAttachmentInput.storagePath), :171/:181 (insert)
- **Evidence:** finalizeTaskAttachmentUploadAction takes input.storagePath from the client and uses it verbatim to sign (:128), download (:154) and store into the documents row: metadata.storage_path = input.storagePath (:181) while case_id = input.caseId (:171). There is NO assertion that input.storagePath belongs to input.caseId — no `input.storagePath.startsWith(`${input.caseId}/`)`, no re-derivation via storagePathFor(input.caseId, input.documentId, ...). prepare-upload server-derives the path (:77 storagePathFor) but finalize re-trusts whatever the client posts back. This is the exact documents-finalize bug class already CONFIRMED for the documents feature (docs/review/ROUNDS-09-15-FINDINGS.md R10-doc-3, line 392), now reachable through the task-linked attachment path which was not covered by that round. The documents_insert RLS (mig 024:135-148) gates only on the case_id COLUMN editability, not on metadata.storage_path (opaque JSONB), so a row with case_id=A (editable) + storage_path=B/... inserts cleanly. The inline read at finalize is bounded by storage RLS (case_docs_select, mig 040, keys on path-segment-1 via can_view_case), so the attacker must already be able to VIEW case B's blob — but the row still mis-attributes B's blob under case A.
- **Why it matters:** The permanent-delete / retention path bypasses RLS: collectCaseFileRefs (src/features/cases/services/erase-case-files.ts:36-64) uses the SERVICE-ROLE admin client to SELECT metadata.storage_path for EVERY documents row WHERE case_id = A (source-agnostic, includes task-attachment rows), and eraseCaseFiles (:160-163) calls admin.storage.remove([...]) which BYPASSES storage RLS. So when case A is later purged, a forged storage_path=B/... makes the service role permanently delete case B's still-live blob — real cross-case data loss not bounded by any RLS. Precondition is a realistic insider role shape (can view source case B + can edit target case A, e.g. view_all + edit_own without edit_any), exactly the persona the prior round documented. This is the highest-risk item the task instructed me to mirror.
- **Suggested fix:** At the top of finalizeTaskAttachmentUploadAction, after auth, reject unless input.storagePath === storagePathFor(input.caseId, input.documentId, safeFileName) — or better, do not accept storagePath from the client at all and re-derive it server-side from caseId+documentId+fileName (the same value prepare produced), making the pointer structurally impossible to forge. Add a Zod schema (z.uuid for documentId/caseId/taskId) while there.
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED by reading the code. finalizeTaskAttachmentUploadAction (src/features/tasks/actions/task-attachment-upload.ts:96-199) is a 'use server' action directly invokable by the client. It accepts input.storagePath (type FinalizeTaskAttachmentInput.storagePath, :42) and uses it verbatim to sign (:128), download (:154), and persist into metadata.storage_path (:181) while case_id is set from input.caseId (:171). There is NO binding assertion: no input.storagePath.startsWith(`${input.caseId}/`), no re-derivation via storagePathFor(caseId, documentId, fileName). prepare-upload DOES server-derive the path via storagePathFor (:77, confirmed in documents.service.ts:57-65, format `${caseId}/${documentId}.ext`), and the legitimate hook (upload-task-attachments.ts:45) passes prep.path back — but finalize re-trusts whatever the client posts, so the legitimate caller does not constrain a malicious one.

Authz guards present (userHasPermission('upload_document') + userCanEditCase(input.caseId) at :103; taskBelongsToVisibleCase taskId↔caseId at :108) all key on caseId/taskId, NOT on storagePath — none bind the path to the case. The documents_insert RLS (mig 024:135-148) checks only the case_id COLUMN editability, not metadata.storage_path (opaque JSONB), so a row with case_id=A (editable) + storage_path=B/... inserts cleanly. The inline sign/download at finalize use the cookie-bound anon client, so they are bounded by storage RLS case_docs_select (mig 040:21-26, keyed on (storage.foldername(name))[1]::uuid via can_view_case) — the attacker must be able to VIEW case B's blob, exactly as the finding states. The sniff (fileTypeFromBuffer) is not a real barrier since case-B blobs are real documents.

The amplification is real and verified: permanentDeleteCaseAction (permanent-delete-case.ts:37,62) calls collectCaseFileRefs then eraseCaseFiles. collectCaseFileRefs (erase-case-files.ts:32-64) uses createAdminClient (SERVICE_ROLE) to SELECT metadata.storage_path for EVERY documents row WHERE case_id=A (source-agnostic — task-attachment rows included), and eraseCaseFiles (:160-163) does admin.storage.remove([...]) which BYPASSES storage RLS. So purging case A permanently deletes case B's still-live blob = real cross-case data loss not bounded by RLS. Persona is realistic: can_edit_case (mig 190) = edit_any OR (edit_own AND assigned/associated); can_view_case is broader — so view_all + edit_own without edit_any (view source B + edit target A) is a valid role shape, the same persona prior rounds documented. This is the identical class to the CONFIRMED documents-feature finding R10-doc-3 (ROUNDS-09-15-FINDINGS.md:392), now reachable via the uncovered task-attachment path.

SEVERITY ADJUSTED High→Medium: the inline exploit requires viewing the source case's blob (storage-RLS bound) AND editing the target case AND a later purge of the target — a multi-precondition insider chain, not anonymous/trivial. Project precedent is explicit: the identical R10-doc-3 finding, with the SAME service-role-purge amplification reasoning already weighed by its verifier (ROUNDS-09-15-FINDINGS.md:403-405), was rated Medium. Keeping this at Medium is consistent with that precedent; the finding's High over-states it. Suggested fix is correct: after auth, reject unless input.storagePath === storagePathFor(input.caseId, input.documentId, safeFileName), or better re-derive server-side and drop client storagePath entirely, plus add a Zod schema (z.uuid for ids).

Files read: src/features/tasks/actions/task-attachment-upload.ts; src/features/tasks/components/upload-task-attachments.ts; src/features/documents/services/documents.service.ts (storagePathFor); src/features/cases/services/erase-case-files.ts; src/features/cases/actions/permanent-delete-case.ts; supabase/migrations/024 (documents_insert RLS), 040 (storage RLS), 190 (can_edit_case); docs/review/ROUNDS-09-15-FINDINGS.md (R10-doc-3).

#### `TASK-ATT-2` — General task finalize trusts client storagePath without binding it to taskId — mis-attributed task_attachments row
- **File:** src/features/tasks/actions/task-general-attachment-upload.ts:77-153 (finalize), :134-144 (insert)
- **Evidence:** finalizeGeneralTaskAttachmentAction takes input.taskId, input.attachmentId and input.storagePath from the client, checks taskVisible(input.taskId) + upload_document (:87), then inserts task_attachments with task_id = input.taskId AND storage_path = input.storagePath (:135,:140) with NO check that input.storagePath segment-1 equals input.taskId (no startsWith, no re-derivation via taskAttachmentPath(input.taskId, input.attachmentId, ...)). prepare server-derives the path (:66) but finalize re-trusts the client value. Read-side blast radius is genuinely bounded: getTaskAttachmentUrlAction (task-attachment-actions.ts:76-78) signs in TASK_DOCUMENTS_BUCKET whose SELECT RLS (mig 157:104-110 task_docs_select) keys on can_view_task((storage.foldername(name))[1]) — the PATH's task, not the row's task — and the server client uses the user session (anon key, RLS enforced, lib/supabase/server.ts), so a blob the user cannot view cannot be signed even if mis-pointed. Hence no read IDOR, but the persisted task_attachments row can claim task A while its blob lives under task B (both must be viewable by the uploader to get this far).
- **Why it matters:** Breaks the path<->task binding invariant the storage layer relies on: a task_attachments row's storage_path no longer provably belongs to its task_id. Unlike the case path there is no service-role purge that would delete the foreign blob (task_attachments has no retention eraser), so impact is integrity/consistency rather than data loss — but it is still an unbound finalize and should be closed for the same reason as TASK-ATT-1.
- **Suggested fix:** Re-derive the path server-side from taskId+attachmentId+fileName (taskAttachmentPath) instead of trusting input.storagePath, or reject unless input.storagePath.startsWith(`${input.taskId}/`). Add a Zod schema for the finalize input.
- **Verify:** Verified against source. finalizeGeneralTaskAttachmentAction (task-general-attachment-upload.ts:77-153) takes taskId, attachmentId, storagePath, fileName, fileSize all from the client (caller upload-task-attachments.ts:59-66 round-trips prep.path, but the action re-accepts it as an untrusted param). It checks userHasPermission('upload_document') + taskVisible(input.taskId) (:87) then inserts task_attachments with task_id=input.taskId (:136) and storage_path=input.storagePath (:140) with NO binding between them — no startsWith check, no re-derivation via taskAttachmentPath(taskId, attachmentId, fileName). prepare server-derives the path (:66) but finalize re-trusts the client value. No Zod schema (manual if-checks only), violating the project's MUST-validate-with-Zod server-action rule.

Read-side is genuinely bounded as the finding states: getTaskAttachmentUrlAction (task-attachment-actions.ts:69-80) reads row.storage_path and signs it in TASK_DOCUMENTS_BUCKET; the task_docs_select storage RLS (mig 157:104-110) keys on can_view_task((storage.foldername(name))[1]::uuid) — the PATH's task — and createClient (server.ts:16-18) uses the anon key + user cookie session so RLS is enforced. A blob the user cannot view cannot be signed even if mis-pointed → no read IDOR. The row INSERT RLS (mig157:77-83) requires can_view_task(task_id), and storage insert/select RLS (mig157:112-119/104-110) require can_view_task of the PATH's task, so the uploader must be able to see BOTH task A and task B to reach this state. There is no service-role/retention purge for task_attachments (mig157:85-86 comment + deleteTaskAttachmentAction is the only deleter, RLS-gated) — so impact is integrity/consistency (a row's storage_path no longer provably belongs to its task_id), not data loss.

The sibling case-linked action correctly preserves the invariant via server-derived storagePathFor + taskBelongsToVisibleCase (task-attachment-upload.ts), making this an inconsistency in the general path. Finding is accurate in every particular including its own self-limitation. Severity Medium is defensible but sits at the Medium/Low boundary: exploit requires dual-visibility precondition, read-side fully bounded, no priv-esc, no cross-tenant read, no data loss — the defect is a broken path<->task binding invariant worth closing, not an exploitable IDOR. Affirming the reviewer's Medium.

#### `TASK-ATT-3` — task-documents bucket has no file_size_limit / allowed_mime_types and general finalize records the client-claimed size — size is unenforced (up to global 50MiB)
- **File:** supabase/migrations/157_task_attachments.sql:100-102 (bucket); src/features/tasks/actions/task-general-attachment-upload.ts:48-50,138; src/features/tasks/actions/task-attachment-upload.ts (finalize, no size check)
- **Evidence:** The task-documents bucket is created with only (id, name, public) — NO file_size_limit and NO allowed_mime_types — unlike case-documents which sets file_size_limit=20971520 (20MB) + a MIME allowlist (mig 017:27-48). The global cap is 50MiB (supabase/config.toml:112). Both task finalize actions sniff magic bytes server-side (good) but NEITHER cross-checks the stored object size against the client-declared input.fileSize, and the general finalize persists file_size = input.fileSize verbatim (general:138). The canonical documents finalize DOES do a storage.list size cross-check (finalize-upload.ts:122-141). So a client can prepare with fileSize <= 20MB (passing the metadata gate at general:49 / case prepare), then PUT a file up to 50MiB to the signed URL (the PUT enforces no size on the general bucket), and the row records the small lie.
- **Why it matters:** Storage-abuse / cost-amplification and an inaccurate file_size column: the app advertises a 20MB ceiling (MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES, document.schema.ts:28) but the general bucket allows ~2.5x that, and the recorded size can be wrong. Bounded by authenticated staff + the 50MiB global cap, so not High, but it diverges from the documents baseline and the bucket should match the 20MB/MIME-allowlist hardening.
- **Suggested fix:** Set file_size_limit=20971520 and allowed_mime_types on the task-documents bucket (ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE, mirroring mig 017) in a new migration; and in both finalize actions read the real size from the storage object's listed metadata (storage.list) rather than trusting input.fileSize for the persisted file_size, matching finalize-upload.ts.
- **Verify:** All load-bearing claims verified against the code. (1) The task-documents bucket is created in mig 157:100-102 with ONLY (id, name, public) and ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING — no file_size_limit, no allowed_mime_types; no later migration adds them (grep across supabase/migrations confirms). (2) By contrast case-documents (mig 017:27-48) sets file_size_limit=20971520 + a 10-type MIME allowlist via ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE — the documents baseline. (3) Global cap is 50MiB (config.toml:112). (4) Both task finalize actions sniff magic bytes (general 98-116, case 126-148) but NEITHER does a storage.list size cross-check; both persist file_size = input.fileSize verbatim (general:138, case:175), and the prepare-time size gate only checks the client-claimed input.fileSize (general:48-50, case:54-57). (5) The canonical documents finalize DOES cross-check stored vs claimed size and rejects with fileTooLarge (finalize-upload.ts:122-141, with an explicit comment at :52). (6) The advertised ceiling MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES=20MB is in document.schema.ts:28. So a client can pass the 20MB prepare gate, then PUT up to 50MiB to the signed URL on the unbounded task-documents bucket, and the row records the smaller claimed size. The flow is reachable from the UI (upload-task-attachments.ts PUTs to the signed URL). One minor imprecision: the finding implies BOTH finalize actions allow the 50MiB bypass, but the case-bound action (task-attachment-upload.ts) uploads to the case-documents bucket which enforces the 20MB hard cap — so the unbounded-size + recorded-lie exploit genuinely applies only to the general path (task-documents). The general path is exactly where the finding's headline and primary evidence sit, so this doesn't refute it. Severity Medium is appropriate: real divergence from the documents hardening baseline (storage abuse / cost amplification to ~2.5x advertised + inaccurate file_size column), but bounded to authenticated staff and the 50MiB global cap — a hardening/consistency gap, not a sharp security breach. The suggested fix (set file_size_limit + allowed_mime_types on task-documents via ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE mirroring mig 017, and read the real size from storage.list in both finalizes) is correct.

#### `TASK-ATT-4` — Case-task attachment storage PUT is denied for associated advisors (case_docs_insert RLS uses legacy assigned_advisor check, app uses can_edit_case)
- **File:** src/features/tasks/actions/task-attachment-upload.ts:69,103 (userCanEditCase); supabase/migrations/027_production_hardening.sql:92-105 (case_docs_insert)
- **Evidence:** prepareTaskAttachmentUploadAction and finalizeTaskAttachmentUploadAction both gate on userCanEditCase(input.caseId), which delegates to the can_edit_case RPC (lib/auth/permissions.ts:102-122) and INCLUDES associated advisors (mig 147 + is_case_associated_advisor). But the case-task blob lands in the case-documents bucket, whose INSERT RLS (case_docs_insert, mig 027:92-105) still uses the LEGACY clause `edit_any_case OR (edit_own_case AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid())` with NO associated-advisor branch. createSignedUploadUrl requires storage.objects INSERT permission, so for an associated advisor (edit_own_case, not the responsible advisor) the prepare action passes the app gate but createSignedUploadUrl is denied -> returns error:'storage'. This is the same legacy-guard drift already CONFIRMED for the documents path (ROUNDS-09-15-FINDINGS.md DOC-UP-3 / R-doc-1, lines 299-334), now also breaking the task-attachment-on-a-case flow for that persona.
- **Why it matters:** Project AUTHZ invariant: the legacy assigned_advisor_id-only check EXCLUDES associated advisors = a bug. A legitimately-authorized associated advisor cannot attach a file to a task on a case they are associated with — a broken core flow that fails after the app already authorized it. Fails safe (over-deny, no escalation), hence Medium, matching how the team rated the identical documents-path drift.
- **Suggested fix:** Canonicalize case_docs_insert/case_docs_update (and documents_insert/update) onto public.can_edit_case((storage.foldername(name))[1]::uuid) / can_edit_case(case_id) in a migration (mirrors mig 190's borrower/income canonicalization). Safe-by-construction: only widens to the already-authorized associated advisor. Note: fixing this BEFORE TASK-ATT-1 widens the forgeable-path surface to associated advisors, so land the storagePath-binding fix together.
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED by reading the code. Chain verified end-to-end:

APP GATE (passes for associated advisor): src/features/tasks/actions/task-attachment-upload.ts:69 (prepare) and :103 (finalize) both gate on userCanEditCase(input.caseId). That helper (src/lib/auth/permissions.ts:102-122) delegates to the can_edit_case RPC, defined in mig 147 (147_associated_advisor_case_access.sql:81-101) as edit_any_case OR (edit_own_case AND (assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid() OR is_case_associated_advisor(id))). is_case_associated_advisor (mig 146:42-54) reads case_associated_advisors. So an associated-only advisor (edit_own_case, not responsible, no edit_any_case) passes the app gate.

RLS GATE (denies the same persona): prepare calls supabase.storage.from(DOCUMENTS_BUCKET='case-documents').createSignedUploadUrl(path) (lines 77-80), which requires INSERT on storage.objects. The live INSERT policy is case_docs_insert from mig 027 (027_production_hardening.sql:92-105): edit_any_case OR (edit_own_case AND c.assigned_advisor_id = auth.uid()) — NO associated-advisor branch. I verified no later migration re-points it: grep of all migrations shows the last redefinition of case_docs_insert/update is 027; mig 040 (the only later storage migration) explicitly says (lines 4-9) the insert/update policies were 'already made explicit in 027' and only re-states case_docs_select/delete onto can_view_case. The associated-only advisor satisfies neither legacy branch -> INSERT denied -> action returns error:'storage'.

RLS client is genuinely RLS-enforced (refutation #1 fails): src/lib/supabase/server.ts uses the ANON key + session cookies, not service-role — so storage and table RLS both apply to the caller.

PARALLEL DRIFT CONFIRMED: the documents-table documents_insert (mig 024:135-148, latest definition) has the identical legacy assigned_advisor_id check, so finalize's documents.insert (line 169) would ALSO be RLS-denied for the same persona — corroborating the over-deny.

Refutation attempts (all failed): (a) a later mig canonicalizing the storage policy — none exists; (b) service-role bypass on upload — not used; (c) associated advisors also matching the legacy assigned check — they don't (separate table). Mig 190 already canonicalized the analogous borrower/income paths onto can_edit_case, establishing the exact fix precedent the finding cites.

SEVERITY: fails safe (over-deny, no escalation) and breaks a legitimate flow for a genuinely-authorized persona (associated advisor attaching a file to a task on their case). Matches the team's prior Medium rating of the identical documents-path drift. Medium is accurate — not over- or under-stated. Suggested fix (canonicalize case_docs_insert/update + documents_insert/update onto can_edit_case) is correct and safe-by-construction (only widens to the already-authorized associated advisor).

### Low (16)

#### `TASK-1` — due_date is a TIMESTAMPTZ column but validated/treated as a date-only (YYYY-MM-DD) value — timezone-fragile round-trip
- **File:** supabase/migrations/009_tasks.sql:52 ; src/features/tasks/schemas/task.schema.ts:39 ; src/features/tasks/domain/task-state.ts:12-20,80-87
- **Evidence:** The DB column is `due_date TIMESTAMPTZ` (009_tasks.sql line 52). The form schema validates it with `optionalDate` = `z.iso.date()` which only accepts `YYYY-MM-DD` (task.schema.ts line 39 -> form-primitives.ts optionalDate). create-task.ts line 55 and update-task.ts line 68 write that bare date string straight into the timestamptz column, so Postgres coerces `'2026-05-21'` to `2026-05-21T00:00:00` in the DB session timezone (typically UTC). On read-back PostgREST returns a full timestamp and the domain layer recovers the date with `task.due_date.slice(0,10)` (task-state.ts isOverdue line 19, formatDueDate line 84), with a comment asserting 'due_date is a DATE-only value'. The comment is wrong: the column is timestamptz, so the stored instant is midnight UTC, and `.slice(0,10)` of a `+00:00` timestamp can land on the previous calendar day for a user east of UTC (Israel is UTC+2/+3) only if the DB ever returns it in a non-UTC offset, and conversely isOverdue compares that UTC-derived date against `todayLocalDate()` (machine-local). The two clocks (DB-stored UTC midnight vs server-local 'today') are not guaranteed to agree at day boundaries.
- **Why it matters:** Overdue detection and the displayed due date can be off by one day around midnight depending on the server/DB timezone, mislabeling a task as overdue (or not) — a correctness bug in a core task-list signal. It is currently masked because the app runs in Frankfurt/UTC, but it is a latent data-model mismatch (date semantics stored in a timestamp column).
- **Suggested fix:** Either change the column to `DATE` (a migration; matches how the app actually uses it and how every read slices it), or stop treating it as date-only and store/compare a real timestamp consistently. At minimum, make isOverdue/formatDueDate timezone-explicit and correct the misleading 'DATE-only value' comments.
- **Verify:** Verified all cited locations. CONFIRMED facts: due_date is TIMESTAMPTZ (009_tasks.sql:52); the form schema validates it as date-only YYYY-MM-DD (task.schema.ts:39 -> form-primitives.ts:91-95 optionalDate = z.iso.date()); create-task.ts:55 and update-task.ts:68 write the bare date string into the timestamptz column; the domain layer reads it back with task.due_date.slice(0,10) (task-state.ts:19 isOverdue, :84 formatDueDate) under a comment asserting "due_date is a DATE-only value" (task-state.ts:15). So the data-model mismatch (date semantics in a timestamp column) and the technically-inaccurate comment are REAL.

However the asserted ACTIVE consequence ("overdue detection / displayed date can be off by one day") does NOT hold and is over-stated. Postgres timestamptz is stored as a UTC instant and PostgREST renders it back in the session TimeZone. Supabase's default session TZ is UTC; no migration sets a session default (the Asia/Jerusalem references in migs 135/136/187/191 are explicit timezone(...) casts inside statistics RPCs, never a session default). Write-TZ == read-TZ == UTC, so '2026-05-21' round-trips to '2026-05-21T00:00:00+00:00' and .slice(0,10) recovers '2026-05-21' losslessly. Vercel serverless also runs in UTC, so todayLocalDate() (machine-local) agrees with the DB-derived UTC date — the "two clocks disagree" scenario requires a non-UTC Node runtime, which is not the deployment.

The finding's directionality is also internally confused: it worries about rolling to the PREVIOUS day "for a user east of UTC," but a positive (eastward, Israel +2/+3) offset shifts wall-clock time forward, which can only roll the date to the NEXT day, never back — and since the stored instant is UTC midnight with the date in the leading slice, even switching the session TZ to Asia/Jerusalem would still yield '2026-05-21T02:00+02' -> '2026-05-21' (unchanged). So no off-by-one materializes for this app's actual or office timezone.

The developers clearly reasoned about this: formatDueDate deliberately parses as a local calendar date (task-state.ts:82-85) and isOverdue deliberately compares zero-padded YYYY-MM-DD strings lexicographically (task-state.ts:15-18) precisely to avoid the new Date('YYYY-MM-DD') UTC-midnight trap. Existing tests (task-state.test.ts) cover the day-boundary cases.

Net: the column-type/semantics mismatch and the misleading comment are genuine and worth a cleanup (change column to DATE, or fix the comment), so is_real=true — but it is a latent data-model/documentation smell with no demonstrable correctness impact in the current or office configuration, not a Medium correctness bug. Downgraded to Low.

#### `TASK-3` — System task-event bodies are hardcoded Hebrew strings rendered verbatim — breaks English (LTR) i18n
- **File:** src/features/tasks/actions/create-task.ts:74 ; complete-task.ts:81 ; reopen-task.ts:61 ; change-task-status.ts:14-20,98 ; snooze-task.ts:61,66 ; src/features/tasks/components/task-thread.tsx:57
- **Evidence:** The actions write hardcoded Hebrew (with dingbat glyphs) into task_comments.body: create '✦ נוצרה' (create-task.ts:74), complete '✓ הושלמה' (complete-task.ts:81), reopen '↩ נפתחה מחדש' (reopen-task.ts:61), status change `שונה סטטוס ל«${STATUS_LABEL[...]}»` with a Hebrew STATUS_LABEL map (change-task-status.ts:14-20,98), snooze `⏱ נדחתה ל${presetLabel}` with Hebrew preset labels (snooze-task.ts:61,66). task-thread.tsx line 57 renders `{item.body}` directly. An English-locale user sees these Hebrew system labels (and the change-status metadata old/new status are stored values, but the body sentence is Hebrew-only).
- **Why it matters:** Violates the i18n invariant (no hardcoded user-facing strings) and the bilingual Definition of Done (must work in English LTR). The system-event labels are app-generated UI text, not user-entered DATA, so they should be localized at render time, not frozen as Hebrew in the DB.
- **Suggested fix:** Store a stable machine code in body/metadata (or rely on event_type + metadata) and translate at render time in task-thread via next-intl, rather than persisting Hebrew sentences. Also drop the dingbat glyphs in body (✦/✓/↩/⏱) — the thread already renders a per-event icon (EVENT_ICON), and emojis/dingbats in UI are an anti-pattern.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. Hardcoded Hebrew system-event bodies are written into task_comments.body verbatim: create-task.ts:74 ('✦ נוצרה'), complete-task.ts:81 ('✓ הושלמה'), reopen-task.ts:61 ('↩ נפתחה מחדש'), change-task-status.ts:14-20 (Hebrew STATUS_LABEL map) + :98 (`שונה סטטוס ל«${...}»`), snooze-task.ts:61 (Hebrew preset map שעה/3 שעות/יום) + :66 (`⏱ נדחתה ל${presetLabel}`). The thread renders these raw: task-thread.tsx:57 outputs {item.body} inside SystemEventRow with no translation — useTranslations('tasks.thread') is used only for fixed chrome (empty/send/hint/systemAuthor/unknownAuthor). messages/en.json tasks.thread has NO keys for these event strings, so an English (LTR) user sees Hebrew system rows, violating the i18n invariant and the bilingual Definition of Done. The dingbat glyphs (✦/✓/↩/⏱) are also redundant since EVENT_ICON (task-thread.tsx:25-33) already renders a per-event icon, and emojis/dingbats in UI are a stated anti-pattern. The suggested fix is feasible: task_comments persists event_type (CHECK enum, migration 120 lines 30-40) and metadata (jsonb), and the service selects both (task-comments.service.ts:19-20), so translation can be driven off event_type + metadata at render time. Severity Low is correct (not adjusted): the office is Hebrew-primary (RTL is the primary locale), the strings live only in the secondary task-thread activity log, the impact is cosmetic (untranslated author-generated UI text, no functional/security/data effect), and it only surfaces for an English-locale user viewing the thread.

#### `TASK-4` — Toggling a task to private while editing someone else's task force-reassigns it to the original creator and hides it from the editor
- **File:** src/features/tasks/actions/update-task.ts:59-71
- **Evidence:** In update-task.ts, when `is_private` is set true the assignee is forced to `existing.created_by` (line 60), not to the actor. The DB CHECK (mig 098 tasks_private_self_assigned) requires assigned_to = created_by for a private task, and the `tasks_update` WITH CHECK is `true` (mig 129), so the update succeeds even when the actor is a view_all_cases holder editing a colleague's task. After the write the task is private + assigned to the original creator, so tasks_select (`is_private = false OR created_by = auth.uid()`, mig 159) hides it from the editor.
- **Why it matters:** A privileged editor can accidentally make another user's task private (and lose their own visibility of it) via a single checkbox, with no warning. Limited blast radius (requires editing a task you don't own and checking private), but it is surprising data-mutation behavior.
- **Suggested fix:** Either disallow toggling is_private on a task the actor did not create (return validation/unauthorized), or hide the is_private control in the edit form when the actor is not the creator (C-036 edit-gate). At minimum, base the forced self-assignment on whether the actor is the creator before honoring is_private.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code and all cross-referenced migrations. update-task.ts:60 sets `assignee = isPrivate ? existing.created_by : parsed.data.assigned_to ?? null` — when is_private is toggled on, the task is force-assigned to the ORIGINAL CREATOR, not the actor. This contrasts with create-task.ts:48, which forces assignment to the actor (`userId`); the divergence is the crux of the bug. The UI (task-form-dialog.tsx:278-290) renders the is_private checkbox unconditionally in edit mode with no creator gate, and checking it disables the assignee select (line 293 `disabled={isPrivate}`). The Edit action is offered to anyone who can see the task (task-actions-menu.tsx:86, no owner gate). DB layer accepts the write: CHECK tasks_private_self_assigned requires assigned_to = created_by (mig 098:21-22) — satisfied because the patch sets assigned_to = existing.created_by; tasks_update WITH CHECK is `true` and USING allows view_all_cases holders (mig 129:29-35); the guard trigger (mig 029) doesn't block (created_by is not changed by the patch, and the reassign target is the active creator). After the write, tasks_select (`is_private = false OR created_by = auth.uid()`, mig 159:22) hides the now-private task from the non-creator editor. So a view_all_cases holder (e.g. secretary/manager) — or even a non-creator current assignee — editing a colleague's task and checking the private box force-reassigns it to the creator and loses their own visibility, with no warning. Severity Low is correct: it requires editing a task you don't own AND deliberately checking private; blast radius is limited, there is no data loss or privilege escalation (the creator still owns/sees the task, and it is recoverable). Reviewer's file/line refs and the migration mechanics are all accurate.

#### `TASK-5` — No status-transition validity model — any status can move to any other (including completed -> snoozed, cancelled -> completed)
- **File:** src/features/tasks/actions/change-task-status.ts:26-58 ; src/features/tasks/domain/task-state.ts
- **Evidence:** changeTaskStatusAction accepts any value in TASK_STATUS_VALUES and applies it with the only logic being completion-stamp set/clear (change-task-status.ts lines 50-58). There is no allowed-transition matrix; the domain layer (task-state.ts) exposes isActive/isCompleted/isOverdue but no `canTransition(from,to)` guard, and there is no .test.ts asserting transition rules. So a cancelled task can be flipped straight to completed, a completed task to snoozed, etc. snooze-task.ts similarly parks ANY task (even completed/cancelled) into snoozed (it has no status precondition; only the UI gates canSnooze in task-actions-menu.tsx:61).
- **Why it matters:** Without a transition guard the data can reach states the UI doesn't expect (e.g. a snoozed-but-completed-stamp-cleared row from cancelled). Low risk today because the UI constrains the entry points, but the server boundary is the source of truth and currently enforces nothing.
- **Suggested fix:** If arbitrary transitions are intended, document it. Otherwise add a pure `isValidTaskTransition(from,to)` to domain/task-state.ts (with a .test.ts) and enforce it at the top of changeTaskStatusAction and snoozeTaskAction (reject with 'validation').
- **Verify:** Substantiated by reading the code. changeTaskStatusAction (src/features/tasks/actions/change-task-status.ts:26-58) validates only that `status` is a member of TASK_STATUS_VALUES; after the same-status short-circuit (line 48) the only logic is set/clear completion stamps (lines 50-58). No from->to transition matrix or guard exists, so any status can move to any other (cancelled->completed, completed->snoozed, etc.). snoozeTaskAction (snooze-task.ts:25-46) parks ANY non-deleted task into 'snoozed' with no status precondition (it selects only id, case_id and never reads current status), so a completed/cancelled task can be snoozed at the server boundary. The domain layer (domain/task-state.ts) exposes isActive/isCompleted/isOverdue/isImmediateTask but no canTransition(from,to); domain/task-state.test.ts only tests isOverdue/formatDueDate/capCompletedTasks — no transition tests. UI is the sole constraint: task-actions-menu.tsx:59-61 gates canSnooze to pending|in_progress, and task-row.tsx:53-55 LIST_STATUSES offers any status minus the current one. The DB layer enforces nothing beyond membership: migration 009_tasks.sql + 032_task_in_progress_status.sql define `CHECK (status IN (...))` only; no CHECK or trigger enforces transition validity (trigger 088 line 63 only fires on the ->completed transition for notifications). Severity Low is correct and well-justified by the reviewer: no security/RLS bypass and no data-corruption — completion stamps stay internally consistent across any transition (so the cited 'snoozed with cleared completion stamp' is in fact the normal stamp state for a snoozed row), the only impact is reaching logically-odd-but-consistent states the UI doesn't surface. Confirmed is_real=true at Low.

#### `TASK-REASSIGN-3` — getTaskAssignmentHistoryAction does not validate taskId as a UUID before querying
- **File:** src/features/tasks/services/task-assignment-history.service.ts:15-29
- **Evidence:** The action takes taskId: string and passes it straight into .eq('task_id', taskId) with no Zod/uuid validation (unlike reassign-task.ts which runs ReassignTaskSchema.safeParse first). RLS via the task_assignment_history_select policy (can_view_task) still protects the data, so this is not a leak, and the caller (TaskAssignmentHistory component) always passes a real task.id. A malformed value would surface as a Postgres 22P02 error that is caught and mapped to the generic 'unknown'.
- **Why it matters:** Project standard is 'server actions MUST validate input with Zod (safeParse), authz CHECK AT THE TOP'. The auth check is present but the input is unvalidated, leaving the action one refactor away from a uuid-cast error path and inconsistent with the sibling reassign action.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a small z.uuid() safeParse on taskId at the top of getTaskAssignmentHistoryAction (return { ok:false, error:'unknown' } on failure) to match ReassignTaskSchema's discipline and fail fast before the DB round-trip.
- **Verify:** Verified against the code. In src/features/tasks/services/task-assignment-history.service.ts:15-29, getTaskAssignmentHistoryAction(taskId: string) takes a raw string and passes it straight into .eq('task_id', taskId) (line 23) with only an auth.getUser() check (line 18) and no Zod/uuid validation. The sibling reassignTaskAction (src/features/tasks/actions/reassign-task.ts:46) does run ReassignTaskSchema.safeParse first, and ReassignTaskSchema (src/features/tasks/schemas/task.schema.ts:60-66) validates taskId via z.uuid(), so the inconsistency claim is accurate. The mitigations the reviewer cites are all real: (a) RLS protects the data — migration 159 (supabase/migrations/159_task_assignment_attribution.sql:98-100) gates SELECT on task_assignment_history via can_view_task(task_id), which enforces full task visibility (lines 42-70); (b) the only caller passes a real task.id from a TaskWithRelations object (src/features/tasks/components/task-assignment-history.tsx:29), never user-controlled text; (c) a malformed value surfaces as a Postgres 22P02 error that is caught (line 26), logs only error.code not error.message (line 27 — no leak), and returns generic 'unknown' (line 28). So there is no data leak and no current exploit path. The finding is genuine but purely a consistency / defense-in-depth gap against the project standard 'server actions MUST validate input with Zod (safeParse)'. The more security-critical half (authz at the top) is already satisfied. Low severity is correct: not Medium (no security/data impact, RLS fail-closed, error path leaks nothing), not invalid (the standard does require Zod input validation and the sibling action follows it). The suggested z.uuid() safeParse fix is minimal and appropriate.

#### `TC-3` — addTaskCommentAction has no rate limit despite firing fan-out bell + email notifications per insert
- **File:** src/features/tasks/actions/add-task-comment.ts:35-49
- **Evidence:** The action inserts a task_comments row with no checkRateLimit (grep over src/features/tasks shows zero checkRateLimit usages). Each insert fires two AFTER-INSERT triggers: notify_task_comment_mentions (134) — one notification per mentioned user — and notify_task_comment_assignee (185) — one to the assignee; both are mirrored to email via the dispatch webhook. CLAUDE.md: 'Expensive actions go through checkRateLimit' and best-effort email is a known submit-hang/cost vector. A body can mention many users, so one rapid loop can fan out many emails.
- **Why it matters:** A comment that mentions N teammates triggers N bell rows + N emails; unbounded posting is a notification/email-spam amplifier. Low because it requires an authenticated insider and the per-recipient cost is bounded by active-user count, but it's the documented class of action the project rate-limits.
- **Suggested fix:** Add checkRateLimit('add_task_comment', e.g. 60/min, subject `user:<uid>`) at the top of the action (fail-closed), matching the pattern already applied to other expensive actions.
- **Verify:** All factual claims verified. add-task-comment.ts:35-49 inserts task_comments with no checkRateLimit (grep over src/features/tasks = zero usages). Migration 134 (notify_task_comment_mentions, lines 62-83) inserts one task_mention notification per mentioned active teammate; migration 185 (notify_task_comment_assignee, lines 81-90) inserts one task_comment notification to the assignee. Migration 161 (email_mentions DEFAULT TRUE, sent via /api/push/dispatch notifications-insert webhook) confirms each bell mirrors to an email. So N mentions => N bells + N emails. CLAUDE.md does say expensive actions go through checkRateLimit. Severity correctly Low and confirmed, but the finding OVERSTATES the framing: the directly analogous peer postCaseCommentAction (src/features/case-comments/actions/post-case-comment.ts:24-53) fires the identical fan-out class (case_mention per mentioned user via mig 108, same email mirror via mig 161) and ALSO has no checkRateLimit. The project deliberately leaves human-paced comment-insert actions ungated; every action it DOES rate-limit is a heavy compute/IO op (export/PDF/backup/Drive) or an enumeration/brute-force oracle (login/reset/invite/intake), neither of which a single-row comment insert is. The fan-out is async in DB triggers + webhook (the action does not await any email, so no submit-hang vector here). It is a real, bounded (active-user count), insider-only defense-in-depth suggestion, not a gap against an established pattern as the finding implies. Kept Low; would be reasonable to add but is consistent with current convention not a defect.

#### `TC-4` — System-event rows use decorative Unicode glyphs as icons instead of Lucide icons
- **File:** src/features/tasks/components/task-thread.tsx:25-33,52
- **Evidence:** EVENT_ICON = { created:'✦', assigned:'→', reassigned:'⇄', status_changed:'◈', completed:'✓', reopened:'↩', snoozed:'⏱' } and SystemEventRow renders `{icon}` as text. CLAUDE.md anti-patterns: 'Emojis in production UI (Lucide icons only)' and 'NEVER emojis in UI'. These are decorative pictographic glyphs used exactly as status icons, the case the rule targets; they also render inconsistently across fonts/RTL. (Only 'reassigned' is currently produced — mig 131 — so most entries are dead too.)
- **Why it matters:** Direct violation of the project's Lucide-only icon rule and a cross-platform rendering risk for glyph-as-icon; auto-reject category in this codebase's review standard.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace the glyph map with a Lucide icon per event_type (via the shared icon wrapper) and drop the unused entries, or key off event_type with proper components.
- **Verify:** Core issue confirmed. C:\Users\shh92\Projects\first-crm\src\features\tasks\components\task-thread.tsx lines 25-33 define EVENT_ICON with decorative Unicode glyphs; SystemEventRow renders {icon} as text at lines 52+55 (inside a span styled as a status icon column). I extracted the exact codepoints: U+2726 (created), U+2192 (assigned), U+21C4 (reassigned), U+25C8 (status_changed), U+2713 (completed), U+21A9 (reopened), U+23F1 stopwatch (snoozed). These are dingbat/arrow/technical glyphs used as status icons; U+23F1 and U+2713 commonly render with emoji presentation, and symbol glyphs render inconsistently across fonts/RTL. CLAUDE.md states the auto-reject rule "Icons: Lucide React (NEVER emojis in UI)" (line 21) and "Emojis in production UI (Lucide icons only)" (line 373). The same file already imports Loader2/Send from lucide-react, so the violation is concrete and the fix trivial — confirming the rule applies and the issue is genuine.

However, the reviewer's supporting sub-claim is FALSE and over-stated: it says "Only 'reassigned' is currently produced — mig 131 — so most entries are dead too." In fact emitTaskEvent (src/features/tasks/lib/emit-task-event.ts) is called by FIVE server actions — create-task ('created'), snooze-task ('snoozed'), complete-task ('completed'), reopen-task ('reopened'), change-task-status ('status_changed') — plus 'reassigned' via mig 131's RPC. That is 6 of 7 event types actively produced (only 'assigned' may be unused, and migration 120 defines the full CHECK set). So the entries are mostly LIVE, not dead; the dead-code rationale is wrong.

Net: the icon-rule violation is real (is_real=true), but it is correctly Low severity — purely a style/brand-consistency issue with no functional or security impact — and the reviewer's dead-code argument should be disregarded. Reviewer's suggested fix (swap glyph map for per-event Lucide icons) is sound; the unused 'assigned' entry could be dropped, but 'created'/'snoozed'/'completed'/'reopened'/'status_changed'/'reassigned' must be kept.

#### `TC-5` — Server actions placed in a *.service.ts file (Application logic mislabeled as Infrastructure service)
- **File:** src/features/tasks/services/task-comments.service.ts:31,86
- **Evidence:** task-comments.service.ts is `'use server'` and exports getTaskCommentsAction and getTaskMentionableProfilesAction — both are server actions called directly from the client component (task-thread.tsx:17-20). Per CLAUDE.md layer/naming conventions, server actions live in actions/ (verb-named files like add-task-comment.ts, which exists alongside), and services/ is the Infrastructure layer for external integrations. Sibling case-comments puts its reads in case-comments.service.ts too, so this is an established-but-inconsistent pattern, not isolated.
- **Why it matters:** Minor layer/naming drift; makes it ambiguous whether the file is an action (Application) or an infra service. No functional impact — authz and PII handling in the file are correct (admin client selects names only: id, first_name, last_name).
- **Suggested fix:** Move the two server actions into actions/ (e.g. get-task-comments.ts, get-task-mentionable-profiles.ts) or document the convention that task/case comment reads intentionally live in services/.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. src/features/tasks/services/task-comments.service.ts:1 is `'use server'` and exports two Action-suffixed async server actions: getTaskCommentsAction (line 31) and getTaskMentionableProfilesAction (line 86). Both are imported and called directly from the client component task-thread.tsx:17-20 via useTransition (lines 147, 158), so they function as server actions, not infra services. CLAUDE.md's naming-conventions table maps Server Actions to actions/ (verb-named files) and reserves services/ for Infrastructure/external integrations; the parallel write action add-task-comment.ts correctly lives in actions/ alongside 12 other task actions, confirming the convention is established in this very feature. The 'established-but-inconsistent' claim also checks out: case-comments puts reads in services/case-comments.service.ts (listCaseComments) while writes go in actions/ — though that file is NOT 'use server' and exports a plain camelCase fn for a Server Component, making the tasks file the clearer violation. Authz/PII handling is correct as stated: admin client selects names only (id, first_name, last_name, lines 61-64) and the mentionable RPC runs on the user session client to respect can_view_task RLS (lines 93-100). Refutation failed: nothing makes these Infrastructure — they are Application-layer DB reads, and using the admin client doesn't reclassify them (other actions in actions/ also use admin clients). Real, purely cosmetic layer/naming drift with no functional impact. Low severity is accurate.

#### `TASK-ATT-5` — runTaskAttachmentUploads is not atomic across files — a mid-batch failure leaves earlier files persisted while the user sees a failure
- **File:** src/features/tasks/components/upload-task-attachments.ts:25-69
- **Evidence:** runTaskAttachmentUploads loops files sequentially and throws on the FIRST failed prepare/PUT/finalize (:39,:49,:57,:66). If file 1 finalizes successfully and file 2 fails, file 1's blob + documents/task_attachments row remain committed, but the caller (task-form-dialog.tsx:144-151) shows a single attachmentError and closes nothing back out. There is no rollback of already-finalized files.
- **Why it matters:** Not fail-closed as a unit: the user is told the attachment step failed while some files actually landed, producing a confusing 'failed but partially uploaded' state. No security/data-loss impact (every persisted file is correctly bound and authz-checked), so Low — a UX/consistency gap worth a note rather than a blocker.
- **Suggested fix:** Either report per-file results (succeeded N of M, list the failures) instead of throwing on the first, or accumulate successes and surface a partial-success message; at minimum document that earlier files are kept. No need for true transactional rollback given the low file count (client caps at 5, task-form-dialog.tsx:461).
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the actual code. runTaskAttachmentUploads (src/features/tasks/components/upload-task-attachments.ts:30-68) loops files sequentially with a plain `for...of` and throws on the first failure: prepare (`!prep.ok` at :39/:57), the blob PUT (`putBlob` throws 'uploadFailed' at :16 when `!res.ok`), and finalize (`!final.ok` at :49/:66). There is no try/catch inside the loop and no accumulation of per-file results, so the function is not atomic across files. Each finalize action (task-attachment-upload.ts:169-198 inserts the `documents` row; task-general-attachment-upload.ts:134-149 inserts the `task_attachments` row) commits the blob + DB row before returning ok. Therefore if file 1 finalizes and file 2 fails, file 1's blob and row remain persisted with no cross-file rollback (cleanupBlob only undoes the in-flight file's own blob on a single-action failure, not earlier successes). The caller (task-form-dialog.tsx:144-151) catches the throw and sets a single `attachmentError`, surfacing no per-file detail — producing the 'failed but partially uploaded' state the finding describes. Severity Low is correct: every persisted file is re-authz'd at finalize (getUser + userHasPermission('upload_document') + userCanEditCase/taskBelongsToVisibleCase for the case path, taskVisible for the general path), magic-byte sniffed, and bound to task_id, so there is no security or data-loss impact — purely a UX/consistency gap. The 5-file cap (validateAttachmentFiles at task-form-dialog.tsx:461) bounds the batch, making true transactional rollback unnecessary, consistent with the suggested fix. Evidence line numbers (:39,:49,:57,:66, caller :144-151, cap :461) all match; the only minor imprecision is that the PUT throw lives in putBlob at line 16 rather than a numbered line inside the loop, which does not affect the conclusion.

#### `TASK-ATT-6` — Task attachment upload actions are not rate-limited despite signed-URL alloc + 4KB sniff + full download + Drive round-trip
- **File:** src/features/tasks/actions/task-attachment-upload.ts:51-199; src/features/tasks/actions/task-general-attachment-upload.ts:42-153
- **Evidence:** Neither prepare nor finalize (case or general) imports or calls checkRateLimit. Each finalize does a signed-read + Range sniff, a full storage.download of the blob into function memory, and a best-effort Drive upload (case:152-167, general:121-132). CLAUDE.md lists upload among 'expensive actions go through checkRateLimit', and the sibling case-expenses/upload-expense-receipt.ts:64-70 already uses the pattern (subject user:<uid>:case:<caseId>). This matches the documents-feature gap already filed as Medium (ROUNDS-09-15 DOC-UP-2) — kept Low here only because it is the same authenticated-staff cost-amplification class on a tiny trusted user base and is consistent with the un-rate-limited documents baseline.
- **Why it matters:** An authenticated user can loop prepare->finalize to burn Vercel function memory/time (up to 50MiB downloads on the general bucket) + Drive API calls + signed-URL quota with no throttle — cost-amplification, and a divergence from the project's stated rate-limit policy for upload actions.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap both finalize actions (and optionally prepare) in checkRateLimit, fail-closed: subject 'user:<uid>:case:<caseId>' for the case path and 'user:<uid>:task:<taskId>' (or 'user:<uid>') for the general path, window matching the cost. Mirror upload-expense-receipt.ts.
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED as a real gap, severity Low correctly stated.

Code verified:
- src/features/tasks/actions/task-attachment-upload.ts: neither prepareTaskAttachmentUploadAction (51-94) nor finalizeTaskAttachmentUploadAction (96-199) imports or calls checkRateLimit. Imports are only userCanEditCase/userHasPermission, no @/lib/rate-limit. finalize does createSignedUrl read (126-128) + Range-byte sniff fetch (135-144) + full supabase.storage.download into function memory (152-154) + best-effort uploadCaseDocumentToDrive (155-167) with zero throttle.
