- src/features/tasks/actions/task-general-attachment-upload.ts: same pattern — prepare (42-75) and finalize (77-153) have no rate-limit; finalize signs (98-100), sniffs (105-112), downloads (121-123), Drive-uploads (124-132). Line cites in the finding (case:152-167, general:121-132) are accurate.
- Sibling src/features/case-expenses/actions/upload-expense-receipt.ts:64-70 DOES call checkRateLimit with subject `user:${user.id}:case:${caseId}`, action 'upload_expense_receipt', 30/3600s — exactly the pattern the finding says to mirror. So the divergence is real within the same upload-action family.
- src/lib/rate-limit.ts confirms the API (action/subject/max/windowSeconds/failMode) the suggested fix would use.
- CLAUDE.md explicitly states 'Expensive actions go through checkRateLimit' and lists upload-related actions (export-pdf/xlsx, import-cases, sync-drive-documents) — the policy basis is genuine.
- No proxy/middleware rate-limit (src/proxy.ts has none), and the actions are invoked directly from a client component (upload-task-attachments.ts), so an authenticated user fully controls the prepare->finalize loop — the cost-amplification vector is reachable.

Severity calibration — Low is correct, not under/overstated:
- This is authenticated-staff-only (requires upload_document permission + can_edit_case / visible task). Trust boundary is the ~80-case office staff, not the public.
- It is consistent with the broader un-rate-limited documents upload baseline: I confirmed src/features/documents/actions/finalize-upload.ts and prepare-upload.ts also lack checkRateLimit (grep found no matches), so this is the same class as the separately-filed DOC-UP-2, kept Low here for that reason as the finding states.

One evidence inaccuracy (does not change the verdict): the finding says 'up to 50MiB downloads on the general bucket'. The task-documents bucket (migration 157_task_attachments.sql:100-102) is created with only (id, name, public) and NO file_size_limit, but the application caps both prepare actions at MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES = 20MB (document.schema.ts:28). So the realistic per-call download is ~20MB, not 50MiB. This overstates the per-call cost but does not affect the existence of the gap.

Net: real, correctly Low, suggested fix (wrap both finalize actions in checkRateLimit, fail-closed, subject user:<uid>:case:<caseId> for the case path and user:<uid>:task:<taskId> for the general path, mirroring upload-expense-receipt.ts) is sound.

#### `TASK-ATT-7` — listTaskCaseDocumentsAction filters documents.metadata->>task_id with no supporting index (sequential scan)
- **File:** src/features/tasks/actions/task-attachment-actions.ts:45-51
- **Evidence:** listTaskCaseDocumentsAction runs .eq('metadata->>task_id', taskId).eq('metadata->>source','task_attachment') against the documents table. Grep across supabase/migrations shows no expression/GIN index on documents.metadata->>'task_id' (the FK indexes in mig 051 cover columns, not JSONB keys). Every open of an edit-task dialog runs this as a sequential scan over documents.
- **Why it matters:** CLAUDE.md requires indexes on frequently-filtered columns. At ~80 cases the documents table is small so the scan is currently cheap — hence Low — but it grows with document volume and is a deliberate-index gap worth noting per the project's DB standards.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a partial expression index, e.g. CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY (own migration file) idx_documents_task_attachment ON public.documents ((metadata->>'task_id')) WHERE metadata->>'source' = 'task_attachment' AND deleted_at IS NULL. Or skip if document volume is expected to stay small — call it a documented deferral.
- **Verify:** VERIFIED real, but genuinely Low. The query exists exactly as described in src/features/tasks/actions/task-attachment-actions.ts:45-51: listTaskCaseDocumentsAction selects from `documents` with `.eq('metadata->>task_id', taskId).eq('metadata->>source','task_attachment').is('deleted_at', null)`. I confirmed it runs on every edit-task-dialog open: task-attachments-list.tsx:44-49 fires it from a useEffect on mount (TaskAttachmentsList) alongside listTaskAttachmentsAction.

No supporting index exists. The documents table (mig 008_documents.sql:34-38) indexes only columns: case_id, borrower_id, category_id, status, expiry_date (all partial WHERE deleted_at IS NULL). Mig 051_fk_indexes.sql:27-28 adds uploaded_by, verified_by. A full grep across all migrations (1..191) for `ON public.documents`, plus a `gin`/`metadata` index search, returns ZERO expression or GIN index on documents.metadata or its `task_id`/`source` keys. The two JSONB-expression filters are thus unindexed.

The RLS policy (039_explicit_child_rls.sql:115-121, documents_select) adds `deleted_at IS NULL AND has_permission('view_case_documents') AND can_view_case(case_id)`. Note can_view_case(case_id) is a per-row function call, not an indexable equality on a specific case_id, so the case_id index does not save this query — confirming the planner will seq-scan / filter on the JSONB expressions. So the sequential-scan characterization is accurate.

Severity stays Low (reviewer correctly self-rated). At ~80 cases the documents table is small and the scan is cheap today; the cost grows only slowly with document volume. CLAUDE.md's "index frequently-filtered columns" rule is about columns, not JSONB keys, and the project explicitly tolerates small-table scans. The reviewer's own framing — partial expression index OR a documented deferral — is appropriately calibrated. This is a legitimate, well-substantiated but minor deliberate-index gap, not an urgent issue.

#### `TR-1` — task-reminders cron has no dedupe — concurrent runs double-insert task_reminder bells (regresses the mig-073 hardening)
- **File:** src/features/tasks/services/task-reminders.service.ts:26-59
- **Evidence:** runTaskReminders() does a plain read-then-write: SELECT snoozed tasks where snoozed_until<=now (l.26-32) -> bulk UPDATE status='pending', snoozed_until=null (l.37-41) -> build inserts from the PRE-UPDATE snapshot `dueTasks` (l.43-54) -> single supabase.from('notifications').insert(inserts) with NO onConflict (l.57). There is NO partial unique index on notifications for type='task_reminder' (grep of supabase/migrations: only uq_notifications_overdue_dedupe mig 073 and uq_notifications_backup_stale mig 128 exist). Two overlapping cron invocations both pass the SELECT before either UPDATE commits, both insert the full notification set -> duplicate bells. The header comment claims 'one-shot ... so no dedupe table is needed', but that only protects against sequential re-runs, not concurrency. This is the exact race mig 073 was written to fix for the SLA cron ('two concurrent runs both pass the dedupe SELECT and both INSERT').
- **Why it matters:** A snoozed reminder can fire twice (or N times) as a duplicate bell + duplicate best-effort email mirror to the owner. Limited blast radius (annoyance, not data loss), but it is a real correctness regression versus the established, already-hardened sibling cron, and the in-file comment asserts a safety property that does not hold under concurrency.
- **Suggested fix:** Mirror mig 073: add a partial UNIQUE INDEX on notifications keyed to the resurface instant (e.g. (user_id, task_id, ((data->>'resurfacedAt'))) WHERE type='task_reminder') and insert via an ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING RPC, OR scope the INSERT to only the rows THIS run actually flipped (return the updated rows from the UPDATE .select() and notify from that set instead of the pre-update snapshot). Either makes the cron race-safe and genuinely idempotent.
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED in code. task-reminders.service.ts:26-59 is a plain read-then-write: SELECT snoozed tasks (l.26-32) -> bulk UPDATE status=pending/snoozed_until=null (l.37-40) -> build inserts from the PRE-UPDATE `dueTasks` snapshot (l.43-54) -> supabase.from('notifications').insert(inserts) with NO onConflict (l.57). Verified there is NO partial unique index for type='task_reminder': grep of supabase/migrations shows only uq_notifications_overdue_dedupe (073, case_status_overdue), uq_notifications_backup_stale_unread (128), uq_notifications_erasure_stale_unread (144). The in-file header comment (l.19-20) does claim "one-shot ... so no dedupe table is needed," which only guards sequential re-runs, not concurrency, exactly as the finding states. Mig 073 is genuinely the established sibling hardening for this identical race ("two concurrent runs both pass the dedupe SELECT and both INSERT") on the SLA cron, so the regression-vs-sibling framing is fair. Blast radius is real and confirmed: a duplicate notifications row triggers the per-INSERT DB webhook (/api/push/dispatch route.ts:58-117) which fans out a duplicate Web Push AND a duplicate email mirror (notification-mirror-email.ts handles task_reminder with no idempotency). 

SEVERITY DOWNGRADED Medium -> Low. Adversarial probability check: the cron is `*/15 * * * *` with maxDuration=60 (route.ts:8, vercel.json:24-26); the work is one SELECT + one UPDATE + one INSERT, sub-second in normal operation. Two scheduled invocations overlapping requires a run to exceed 15 minutes (implausible for this workload). The realistic trigger is only Vercel at-least-once/retry delivery or a manual+scheduled overlap. Additionally the UPDATE narrows the race window to milliseconds (between this run's SELECT and its UPDATE commit), since the second run's SELECT filters status='snoozed' and the flipped rows leave the result set once committed. Combined with the reviewer's own acknowledgement of "limited blast radius (annoyance, not data loss)", low-probability x low-impact = Low. Note: the suggested-fix `resurfacedAt` field does not exist today (current data is {taskTitle, actorName}), and the alternative .select()-the-flipped-rows fix is not fully race-safe either (the .in('id',ids) matches by id regardless of status, so two runs could both return overlapping rows) — the truly race-safe remedy is the unique index, as in mig 073. These are fix-detail nuances and do not affect the validity of the underlying finding.

#### `TR-3` — isOverdue / formatDueDate compute the day boundary in the ambient server TZ (UTC), not Israel — the documented project convention
- **File:** src/features/tasks/domain/task-state.ts:4-20
- **Evidence:** todayLocalDate() builds 'today' from new Date().getFullYear()/getMonth()/getDate() (l.5-9), i.e. the runtime's ambient timezone. On Vercel/Frankfurt server runs that is UTC. isOverdue (l.12-20) is invoked server-side in tasks/page.tsx (overdueCount + focusedTasks, l.98/108). The codebase has a dedicated helper, src/lib/utils/israel-time.ts (israelCivil), whose docstring states server components run in UTC while the office is Israel (UTC+2/+3) and 'a default new Date() today disagrees with what the user sees' — created precisely for this. task-state does not use it. Israel is ahead of UTC, so a task due yesterday (Israel) is NOT flagged overdue for the first ~2-3h of the new Israel day. The unit test (task-state.test.ts) also uses local time, so it cannot catch this.
- **Why it matters:** Overdue badges and the overdue KPI/focus filter lag the office's calendar by up to ~3 hours each day boundary, inconsistent with the rest of the app (welcome banner, case-activity feed, target-date logic) which already standardize on israelCivil.
- **Suggested fix:** Derive todayLocalDate() from israelCivil() (format year/month/day as zero-padded YYYY-MM-DD) so the overdue boundary matches the office. Add a vitest case that freezes time near the Israel/UTC day-rollover to lock the behavior.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. src/features/tasks/domain/task-state.ts:4-10 builds todayLocalDate() from new Date().getFullYear()/getMonth()/getDate(), i.e. the ambient runtime TZ, which on Vercel/Frankfurt is UTC. isOverdue (l.12-20) compares due_date.slice(0,10) lexicographically against that UTC "today". src/app/(app)/tasks/page.tsx is an async Server Component (no 'use client') and calls isOverdue at l.98 (overdueCount KPI) and l.108 (overdue focus filter) on the server, so those run in UTC. Since Israel is UTC+2/+3, during the first ~2-3h of each Israel day UTC is still on the previous date, so a task due "yesterday" (Israel) compares equal-not-less and is NOT flagged overdue until UTC also rolls over — the reviewer's direction and ~2-3h magnitude are correct.

The codebase has the purpose-built helper src/lib/utils/israel-time.ts (israelCivil), whose docstring states precisely this UTC-vs-Israel server-render problem. The sibling calendar-boundary domain helper src/features/cases/domain/target-date.ts:18-31 (getTargetDateState) was deliberately migrated to israelCivil(now) for its overdue/soon boundary (cites R5-domain-logic-1/2), establishing the in-app convention that task-state ignores — so the inconsistency claim holds. The unit test src/features/tasks/domain/task-state.test.ts:7-14 derives offsets from local new Date(), so it cannot reproduce the rollover gap (confirmed).

Caveat on scope (not refuting, just precision): isOverdue is also consumed in client components task-row.tsx:64 and task-board-card.tsx:35, where ambient TZ is the user's Israel browser and the result is correct; the defect is specifically the server-render path (KPI strip, overdue focus list, and the initial server-rendered per-row badge before any client correction). Severity Low is appropriate: transient, ~once-per-day cosmetic/triage lag with no data, authz, or correctness-of-persisted-state impact; fix is trivial (derive todayLocalDate from israelCivil and add a rollover-time vitest case).

#### `TR-4` — task-form-dialog.tsx is 481 lines — nearly 2x the 250-line component limit
- **File:** src/features/tasks/components/task-form-dialog.tsx:1-481
- **Evidence:** wc -l = 481, hard limit for components is 250 (CLAUDE.md Engineering Standards). The file also carries co-located non-render logic — validateAttachmentFiles (l.456-470), mapAttachmentError (l.472-481), getGenericError (l.445-454) — and a large controlled-state seeding block (l.158-201).
- **Why it matters:** Documented file-size limit is non-negotiable per CLAUDE.md ('Exceeding limit means SPLIT'); the attachment validation/error-mapping helpers are domain-ish logic that belongs outside the JSX file.
- **Suggested fix:** Extract the attachment file-validation + error-mapping helpers into a sibling module (e.g. ./task-attachment-validation.ts) and split the case-picker subsection into its own component; bring the file under 250.
- **Verify:** Verified by reading the file and running wc -l. File is exactly 481 lines (confirmed: Read output ends at line 481, wc -l = 481), versus CLAUDE.md's hard component limit of 250 lines ("Components: max 250 lines"; "God files (>250 lines for components)"). 481/250 = 1.92x, so "nearly 2x" is accurate. Cited helpers verified at exact lines: getGenericError (445-454), validateAttachmentFiles (456-470), mapAttachmentError (472-481) — all are pure, non-JSX functions; validateAttachmentFiles encodes attachment-rule logic (count<=5, size, MIME allowlist) and mapAttachmentError maps error codes to i18n, both legitimately extractable to a sibling module. The controlled-state seeding/derivation block (158-201) is real too: the seedKey/seededKey re-seed pattern (168-182) plus case-filter derivation (184-201). The case-picker subsection (305-344) is a self-contained subcomponent candidate. The finding is factually accurate on every point. Severity Low is correct and not overstated: this is a code-organization/file-size nit with no correctness, security, or behavioral impact. Note: SubmitButton (429-443) is also co-located but is reasonably so because useFormStatus must run inside the <form>; even excluding it the file far exceeds 250 lines. The suggested fix aligns with the codebase's own conventions (the file already cites the compose-email-dialog re-seed pattern at line 167).

#### `TR-5` — task-row.tsx (272 lines) and change-task-status.ts (121 lines) exceed their file-size limits
- **File:** src/features/tasks/components/task-row.tsx:1-272
- **Evidence:** task-row.tsx wc -l = 272 (component limit 250); it inlines two startTransition handlers (handleToggleComplete l.74-85, handleStatus l.87-92) plus a local CheckIcon SVG component (l.257-271). Separately, src/features/tasks/actions/change-task-status.ts wc -l = 121 (server-action limit 100).
- **Why it matters:** Both breach the documented hard limits; the action in particular mixes status patch, email mirror, activity-event emit, and own-notification mark-read in one >100-line file, which the standard says to split into domain helpers.
- **Suggested fix:** Extract CheckIcon to components/check-icon.tsx (or use a shared icon) to bring task-row under 250. For change-task-status.ts, move the completion-stamp patch builder and the mark-read sweep into a small domain/lib helper so the action body is under 100 lines.
- **Verify:** Verified by reading both files and confirming with wc -l. task-row.tsx = 272 lines (component limit 250, 22 over); change-task-status.ts = 121 lines (server-action limit 100, 21 over). CLAUDE.md states these are hard limits ("Exceeding limit means SPLIT, not deferred") and lists "God files (>250 for components, >100 for actions)" as a strictly-forbidden auto-reject anti-pattern, so the limits cited are real and documented.

Every specific evidence claim checks out exactly: handleToggleComplete is a startTransition handler at l.74-85; handleStatus a second startTransition handler at l.87-92; the local CheckIcon SVG component is at l.257-271. change-task-status.ts genuinely mixes four concerns in one >100-line action: completion-stamp patch builder (l.50-58), best-effort email mirror via after() (l.73-92), activity-event emit (l.94-100), and own-notification mark-read sweep (l.106-113).

Adversarial checks: (1) No shared check-icon exists in app code — the only other CheckIcon hits are lucide imports inside shadcn primitives (dropdown-menu.tsx, select.tsx), so the inline SVG is a real local duplication that the suggested extraction would address. (2) The action is genuinely splittable along the lines suggested (patch builder + mark-read sweep into domain/lib helpers). emitTaskEvent and sendTaskNotificationEmail are already extracted to ../lib and ../services, confirming the codebase pattern of pulling sub-logic out of actions.

Severity correctly stated as Low: pure code-quality/maintainability breach of documented file-size limits, no functional, correctness, or security impact, and the overages are modest (22 and 21 lines).

#### `TR-6` — Duplicated status-color maps across three files
- **File:** src/features/tasks/components/tasks-list.tsx:22-28
- **Evidence:** STATUS_COLOR (tasks-list.tsx l.22-28: pending #C9A961, in_progress #6366F1, snoozed #F59E0B, completed #10B981, cancelled #A1A1AA) is duplicated verbatim as ACCENT in task-board-column.tsx (l.10-16), and the same status palette is independently re-expressed as Tailwind classes in domain/task-state.ts STATUS_BADGE (l.61-67). Three sources of truth for one concept.
- **Why it matters:** A status palette change must be made in three places or the board, the grouped list, and the badge will drift. Anti-pattern: duplicated constants/logic.
- **Suggested fix:** Define the status-accent color map once in domain/task-state.ts (e.g. statusAccentColor(status)) and import it in both tasks-list and task-board-column, keeping a single source of truth alongside STATUS_BADGE.
- **Verify:** Verified against code. tasks-list.tsx l.22-28 defines STATUS_COLOR (pending #C9A961, in_progress #6366F1, snoozed #F59E0B, completed #10B981, cancelled #A1A1AA), used at l.126 for the grouped-list accent dot. task-board-column.tsx l.10-16 defines ACCENT with byte-for-byte identical keys+hex values, used at l.50 for the board column dot — a true verbatim duplicate (grep over the four distinctive hex values returns exactly these two files). domain/task-state.ts l.61-67 defines STATUS_BADGE, a third per-status palette re-expressed as Tailwind badge classes (statusBadgeClass at l.69). The finding accurately distinguishes: STATUS_COLOR/ACCENT are verbatim duplicates; STATUS_BADGE is independently re-expressed (different visual language — badge bg/text classes, not accent hex), so it does not overstate the case. No shared helper exists (grep statusAccentColor = empty). task-state.ts already centralizes sibling color helpers (priorityBadgeClass, priorityEdgeColor, statusBadgeClass), confirming it as the natural single source of truth the reviewer proposes. Genuine duplicated-constant anti-pattern with real drift risk (two accent maps must be edited in lockstep). Severity Low is correct: maintainability/DRY only, no runtime or correctness impact.

### Refuted (2)

- `TASK-2` Task soft-delete is not manager-only — any assignee/creator/view_all holder can delete; UI shows delete to everyone — All raw code facts in the finding are accurate, but the underlying "manager-only task delete" invariant is misapplied, so this is NOT a real authz bug.

Verified facts:
- src/features/tasks/actions/delete-task.ts (15-53): deleteTaskAction has no role/manager check; it authenticates the user (21), confirms the task exists (24-30), UPDATEs deleted_at (34-41), and reads back .select('id') to detect RLS denial (47 → 'unauthorized' on 0 rows). Authorization is delegated entirely to RLS. CONFIRMED.
- supabase/migrations/129_tasks_update_allow_reassign.sql (27-35): tasks_update USING = assigned_to=auth.uid() OR created_by=auth.uid() OR has_permission('view_all_cases') OR is_admin(), WITH CHECK(true). Soft-delete is an UPDATE of deleted_at, so it rides this policy → an advisor who is assignee or creator CAN soft-delete. CONFIRMED. (Mig 029 lines 100-107 deliberately dropped the FOR DELETE policy, leaving soft-delete to tasks_update.)
- src/features/tasks/components/task-actions-menu.tsx (113-126): delete item renders unconditionally, no manager gate (contrast onReassign at 90 which is gated). CONFIRMED.

Why it is NOT a bug (refutation): The round invariant "manager-only delete" applies to COMMENTS, not tasks. The actual product decision (memory project_task_conversation.md line 16): "manager-only delete OF OTHERS' COMMENTS" — and it is implemented exactly so via soft_delete_task_comment RPC, admin-only (120_task_comments.sql 69-88). The intended model for TASKS is the opposite and is documented in code: migration 129's header states the office rule "anyone with access to the case can hand a task to anyone with access to the case," and that broad assignee/creator/view_all/admin set is the deliberate edit authority. The finding's own NOTE acknowledges this is "likely an intentional broader model, not a bug." No spec entry (searched Kaufman-Finance-Spec.md) requires whole-task deletion to be manager-only. So the implementation matches the documented intent; the only artifact is a stale round invariant, not a security/data-availability gap. Marking severity invalid because the authz claim does not hold against the actual model. The doc-reconciliation note (correct the round invariant) is valid housekeeping but is not a code defect.
- `TR-2` task-reminders is fail-OPEN on partial failure: resurface commits but a single notification FK error drops ALL reminders for the run — REFUTED. The finding's structural description of task-reminders.service.ts is accurate (resurface UPDATE at l.37-41 commits, then a single atomic bulk notifications.insert at l.57, no shared transaction; a throw -> route 500 at route.ts:32 with no rollback). And the cited primitives exist: notifications.user_id is NOT NULL REFERENCES profiles(id) (028_notifications.sql:14), and the per-row error-skipping insert_overdue_notifications RPC pattern (073) is real. BUT the finding's load-bearing causal claim is factually wrong about the schema. It asserts "tasks.assigned_to FK is SET NULL on profile delete leaving a stale id in flight." Checked 009_tasks.sql:53 and 009_tasks.sql:65: both assigned_to and created_by are `REFERENCES public.profiles(id)` with NO ON DELETE clause = default NO ACTION (not SET NULL). No later migration alters these FKs (grepped all ALTER TABLE tasks). Therefore: (1) You cannot end up with assigned_to/created_by pointing at a deleted profile. profiles.id CASCADEs from auth.users (002:141), but the only auth.users delete in app code is the invite-rollback deleteUser on a just-created user with zero tasks (invite-member.ts:84,101). (2) Member deletion is a SOFT delete: delete-member.ts header (l.20-22) says the profiles row is KEPT; admin_delete_member (170:118-120) sets deleted_at + is_active=FALSE and never removes the row. The RPC reassigns only status='pending' tasks (170:110-111) to the acting admin and does NOT touch snoozed tasks, so a snoozed task can keep assigned_to=<soft-deleted-member-id> -- but that id is a real, existing profiles row, so the notification FK is satisfied (it merely lands in an inactive user's bell, which the code comment treats as intended historical attribution). (3) Even a raw auth.users delete on a user with snoozed tasks would be BLOCKED by the NO ACTION constraint, not silently orphan the column. With `if (!recipient) continue` guarding NULL user_id (l.45-46), type a string literal, and data provided, no constraint on the insert can fire in this codebase. The architectural fail-open is thus purely hypothetical -- there is no real trigger for the FK rejection it depends on, and the finding invents a SET NULL cascade that does not exist. Severity invalid: not a real defect as described.


## Round 14 — case-comments / case-activity / statistics

**raw 13 -> confirmed 11 / refuted 2  (High 1, Medium 1, Low 9)**

### High (1)

#### `ACT-1` — Soft-deletes are invisible on the activity timeline (SOFT_DELETE/RESTORE actions are never handled)
- **File:** src/features/case-activity/domain/derive-audit-events.ts:70-94 (switch), :90, :128-129, :145-146, :152-153, :170-171, :175-176, :193-194, :197-198
- **Evidence:** The authoritative audit trigger (supabase/migrations/022_security_hardening.sql:107-125) classifies ANY UPDATE that sets deleted_at (null -> not-null) on a table that has a deleted_at column as action='SOFT_DELETE' (and not-null -> null as 'RESTORE') -- it is NOT a hardcoded table list, it is dynamic on column presence (`new_jsonb ? 'deleted_at'`). The audited tables documents, case_banks (mig 024), borrower_incomes/borrower_obligations (mig 076), borrowers, and tasks (mig 022) all soft-delete via UPDATE deleted_at (e.g. soft_delete_document_with_tombstone in mig 104 does `UPDATE public.documents SET deleted_at = NOW()`; delete-task.ts:37 sets deleted_at). For a SOFT_DELETE row: extractChanges() (audit-parser.ts:65) returns null because action!=='UPDATE', and extractWholeRow() (audit-parser.ts:82) returns null because action is neither INSERT nor DELETE. The entry still survives resolveEntries' filter (audit.service.ts:52 keeps it since action!=='UPDATE'). In eventsFromEntry the row hits each table branch with action that is not INSERT and not DELETE, so it falls to `const ch = e.changes ?? {}` = {}, and every check (isNowSet(ch.deleted_at), ch.status, fieldsUpdated with empty changes) yields []. Net: deriveAuditEvents returns NO event. The isNowSet(ch.deleted_at) 'removal' branches in documentsEvents (:175-176) and tasksEvents (:197-198) are dead code -- they assume soft-delete arrives as a plain UPDATE carrying a deleted_at diff, which the trigger never produces.
- **Why it matters:** Removals are a core part of a history/audit timeline ('who deleted this document / removed this bank / deleted this task and when'). For every soft-deletable entity, deletions and restores simply do not appear in the curated activity feed -- the feature silently drops the most accountability-relevant events. This is exactly the 'missing events' failure mode the timeline is supposed to prevent (e.g. a client dispute 'you deleted my uploaded document' has no record on the feed).
- **Suggested fix:** Handle SOFT_DELETE (and RESTORE) in the derivation. Either (a) normalize in audit.service.resolveEntries by mapping action 'SOFT_DELETE'->'DELETE' equivalence for display while preserving wholeRow (extractWholeRow already has the full OLD row available for SOFT_DELETE since the trigger does NOT store the whole row for SOFT_DELETE -- so prefer option b), or (b) add explicit SOFT_DELETE/RESTORE arms in eventsFromEntry/each table handler that emit record_removed / a restore kind, sourcing the subject from the live context maps (documentNames/bankNames/incomeSubjects/etc.) since wholeRow is null for SOFT_DELETE. Note the trigger currently writes NO changed_fields for SOFT_DELETE, so the subject must come from ctx; consider also having the trigger record the whole row (or at least the label FK) on SOFT_DELETE so removals can be labelled even after the live row is purged. Add a derive-audit-events.test.ts covering SOFT_DELETE/RESTORE for documents, case_banks, incomes, obligations, tasks.
- **Verify:** Verified the full chain end-to-end; the finding holds.

TRIGGER (authoritative def is mig 045 supersedes mig 022 — both identical on this logic): audit_log_change classifies an UPDATE that sets deleted_at null->not-null as action='SOFT_DELETE' and not-null->null as 'RESTORE', based dynamically on `new_jsonb ? 'deleted_at'` (column presence), NOT a hardcoded table list (045:86-99). The skip-noise guard only skips when action_type='UPDATE' (045:129), so SOFT_DELETE rows ARE inserted into audit_log.

WRITE PATHS confirmed to do `UPDATE ... SET deleted_at` (so they classify as SOFT_DELETE): delete-task.ts:34-39; soft_delete_document_with_tombstone mig104:96-98; delete-case-bank.ts:26; soft_delete_borrower_income/obligation mig190:355-361 & 402-408. All these tables have the audit trigger attached (mig 012:99-126), so they produce audit rows.

TS PIPELINE: extractChanges (audit-parser.ts:65) returns null unless action==='UPDATE' -> SOFT_DELETE gets changes=null. extractWholeRow (:82) returns null unless action is INSERT/DELETE -> SOFT_DELETE gets wholeRow=null. resolveEntries filter (audit.service.ts:52) keeps the row (action!=='UPDATE'), so it survives but is empty. In eventsFromEntry (derive-audit-events.ts:70-93) the SOFT_DELETE row hits its table branch, is neither INSERT nor DELETE, falls to `ch = e.changes ?? {}` = {}, and every check (isNowSet(ch.deleted_at), ch.status, fieldsUpdated over empty changes) yields [] -> NO event. Net: deriveAuditEvents emits nothing for soft-deletes/restores. case-activity.service.ts:44 calls deriveAuditEvents directly with no SOFT_DELETE->DELETE remapping.

DEAD CODE confirmed: the isNowSet(ch.deleted_at) 'removal' branches (derive-audit-events.ts:175-176 documents, 197-198 tasks) are unreachable — e.changes only populates for action==='UPDATE', and a null->notnull deleted_at transition is classified SOFT_DELETE by the trigger, never plain UPDATE, so a plain-UPDATE diff can never carry that transition.

FEATURE IS REAL & DISPLAYED: record_removed events + `removed.*` translations exist (he.json:1188-1198, e.g. documents='מסמך נמחק', tasks='משימה נמחקה') and are rendered (activity-event-line.tsx:112 via removed.${event.entity}). So the entire removal-display pipeline exists yet soft-delete removals/restores silently never appear on the curated activity timeline — the accountability events that matter most.

ONE MINOR INACCURACY (in the suggested-fix notes only, not the core bug): the finding states the trigger writes NO changed_fields for SOFT_DELETE. Actually it DOES — the diff aggregation (045:101-111) runs for every UPDATE-op including SOFT_DELETE, so audit_log.changed_fields contains {deleted_at:{old,new},...}; the TS layer just discards it because extractChanges gates on action==='UPDATE'. This makes fix option (a) viable too, but does not affect the bug's existence.

Severity High is appropriate: deletions and restores of documents, banks, incomes, obligations, and tasks are entirely absent from the audit/history timeline, which is exactly the accountability the feature is meant to provide (e.g. a 'you deleted my document' dispute has no record). No test covers derive-audit-events (no *.test.ts under case-activity).

Relevant files: src/features/case-activity/domain/derive-audit-events.ts; src/features/audit/domain/audit-parser.ts; src/features/audit/services/audit.service.ts; src/features/case-activity/services/case-activity.service.ts; supabase/migrations/045_audit_trigger_id_fallback.sql; supabase/migrations/022_security_hardening.sql; supabase/migrations/012_audit_triggers.sql; supabase/migrations/104_ensure_document_delete_rpc.sql; supabase/migrations/190_canonical_can_edit_case_borrower_income_writes.sql; src/features/tasks/actions/delete-task.ts; src/features/case-banks/actions/delete-case-bank.ts; messages/he.json:1188-1198; src/features/case-activity/components/activity-event-line.tsx.

### Medium (1)

#### `CC-1` — @-mention notifies + emails a comment preview to teammates who cannot view the case (cross-case PII leak)
- **File:** supabase/migrations/108_case_comment_mentions.sql:46-63 ; src/features/case-comments/services/case-comments.service.ts:70-80 ; src/features/notifications/services/notification-mirror-email.ts:99-104 ; src/features/notifications/components/notification-bell.tsx:186-190
- **Evidence:** The composer offers ALL active teammates as mention targets — listMentionableProfiles() selects profiles WHERE is_active = true with no case scoping (case-comments.service.ts:70-80) — and the case-comments-block passes that unscoped list straight into the thread/composer. The notify_case_comment_mentions trigger (mig 108:46-63) then drops a notifications row for every mentioned active user, gated ONLY by 'is_active AND <> author', NOT by whether the mentioned user can view the case. The row's data.preview is a 140-char snippet of the comment body (mig 108:39-42). That preview is then surfaced verbatim: the bell renders d.preview (notification-bell.tsx:189) and the email mirror sends it to the recipient's inbox (notification-mirror-email.ts:99-104), both gated only by the per-user email_mentions toggle + active status (preferences.service) — never by can_view_case. listRecentNotifications filters solely on user_id = me (notifications.service.ts:11-29), so RLS adds no case scope here. Net: an advisor can @-mention a teammate with no access to the case (e.g. an advisor who isn't the responsible/associated advisor and lacks view_all) and that teammate receives, in their bell AND off-platform email, a snippet of internal client chatter for a case they're forbidden to open. The deep-link click itself is harmless (/cases/{id} RLS-404s), but the preview text already leaked.
- **Why it matters:** Breaks cross-case isolation for the one field that carries free-text client PII ('client is hiding a second mortgage', salary figures, etc.). The comment thread is the internal-WhatsApp replacement, so previews routinely contain sensitive client detail. Email delivery makes it worse — the snippet leaves the RLS-protected app entirely and lands in an inbox, defeating the whole 'open the RLS-protected app for specifics' design that the push path (route.ts:18-21) deliberately follows.
- **Suggested fix:** Scope mentions to case viewers at BOTH layers. (1) listMentionableProfiles should take a caseId and return only teammates who can view that case (or filter the composer list against case access) so non-viewers can't be picked. (2) Defense-in-depth in the trigger: before INSERTing the notification, skip mentioned_id who cannot view NEW.case_id. Since notify_case_comment_mentions is SECURITY DEFINER, can_view_case (SECURITY INVOKER, mig 147/182) would evaluate against the function owner, not the mentioned user — add a small SECURITY DEFINER predicate that checks a *given* user's case access (mirrors is_case_associated_advisor / is_case_task_member but parameterized by user id) and gate the INSERT on it. That closes both the bell and the email leak (the email mirror reads the same row that would no longer be created).
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading every cited file plus cross-references. (1) listMentionableProfiles() (case-comments.service.ts:70-80) selects profiles WHERE is_active=true with NO case scoping; it is fetched in case-comments-block.tsx:30 and passed block→thread (case-comments-thread.tsx:143)→composer, which filters only by name substring (case-comment-composer.tsx:31-35). No case-access filter anywhere in the chain. (2) The notify_case_comment_mentions trigger (mig 108:56-62, SECURITY DEFINER) inserts a notification gated ONLY by mentioned_id<>actor AND profiles.is_active — never can_view_case. data.preview is a 140-char snippet of the comment body (mig 108:39-42,61). (3) The bell renders d.preview verbatim (notification-bell.tsx:189) and listRecentNotifications filters solely on user_id (notifications.service.ts:16-21), so RLS adds no case scope. (4) The email mirror puts preview into the email and sends it to the recipient's inbox (notification-mirror-email.ts:99-104), gated only by shouldEmailUser→email_mentions toggle + is_active (preferences.service.ts:70-82) — no can_view_case. (5) The asymmetry is real and intentional in the OTHER direction: the push path is explicitly designed PII-free/category-only because it transits FCM/APNs (route.ts:18-21,28-40), while the email deliberately carries specifics off-platform (notification-mirror-email.ts:36-42). (6) The comment thread itself IS correctly RLS-scoped to can_view_case (mig 107:38-46), so the mention notification/email is the sole leak vector, and the deep-link click harmlessly 404s (route.ts:45-47) — the preview text already leaked, exactly as stated. (7) The suggested fix is implementable: can_view_case (mig 147:57-78, updated 182:76-98) and the parameterized SECURITY DEFINER pattern (is_case_task_member, mig 182:36-54) exist as referenced. Refutation attempts failed: the author must be a case-viewer (insert requires can_view_case) but nothing constrains mention TARGETS to viewers; no surface (bell or email) consults case access. Severity Medium is correct: a genuine cross-case PII-isolation break on the free-text comment field with off-platform email egress, but bounded to a 140-char preview + actor name and requiring an authenticated insider with case access to pick a non-viewer from the dropdown.

### Low (9)

#### `CC-2` — JS mention regex is looser than the DB trigger's strict-uuid regex — hand-typed tokens render as pills but never notify
- **File:** src/features/case-comments/domain/mentions.ts:9 ; supabase/migrations/108_case_comment_mentions.sql:50
- **Evidence:** parseMentionBody (mentions.ts:9) matches @[name](X) where X is /[0-9a-fA-F-]{36}/ — any 36-char string of hex digits and dashes, e.g. 36 dashes or 36 'a's. The DB trigger (mig 108:50) matches the strict dashed uuid shape 8-4-4-4-12. A hand-typed token like @[Boss](------------------------------------) parses+renders as a gold mention pill in case-comment-bubble.tsx but the trigger's regexp_matches won't match it, so no notification fires. The reverse can't happen (insertMention always emits a real profile id), so this only affects manually-typed bodies.
- **Why it matters:** A user could believe they pinged someone (sees the pill) when no notification was ever created. Pure display/notify inconsistency — no security impact since real mentions always go through insertMention with a valid uuid.
- **Suggested fix:** Tighten MENTION_RE to the same dashed-uuid shape the trigger uses (8-4-4-4-12) so the render contract matches the notify contract, and an invalid token falls back to plain text instead of a misleading pill.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading both cited files. JS MENTION_RE (src/features/case-comments/domain/mentions.ts:9) is `/@\[([^\]]+)\]\(([0-9a-fA-F-]{36})\)/g` — the uuid group is a character class of hex digits + dash repeated 36x, so ANY 36-char string of hex/dashes matches (e.g. 36 dashes, 36 'a's). The DB trigger's notification loop (supabase/migrations/108_case_comment_mentions.sql:48-52) uses regexp_matches with the strict dashed-uuid shape `[0-9a-fA-F]{8}-{4}-{4}-{4}-{12}`. So a hand-typed token like @[Boss](------------------------------------) satisfies the JS regex and renders as a gold pill (case-comment-bubble.tsx:166-177 maps mention segments to `@{seg.name}` in a brand-gold-soft span), but produces no regexp_matches row in the trigger → no 'case_mention' notification inserted. The render contract is looser than the notify contract: confirmed display/notify inconsistency. Reverse direction is impossible as stated — insertMention (mentions.ts:45-54) builds the token from m.id, and the only caller, applyMention in case-comment-composer.tsx:47 (and task-thread.tsx:203), passes a real profile id from the Member suggestion list, so authored mentions always carry a valid uuid. Thus only manually-typed bodies are affected. Note: the trigger's preview regexp_replace at mig 108:40 actually uses the SAME loose shape as JS, so previews would strip a loose token too — but the notification loop (the bell trigger) uses the strict shape, so the core claim holds. No security impact (no malformed ::uuid cast reaches the trigger; strict shape gates it). Severity Low is correct: requires a user to hand-type a malformed token bypassing the autocomplete UI, purely cosmetic notify/display mismatch.

#### `ACT-2` — Borrower add/remove never produces a timeline event (case_borrowers audit trigger was dropped, borrowers INSERT/DELETE deliberately skipped)
- **File:** src/features/case-activity/domain/derive-audit-events.ts:123-137
- **Evidence:** caseBorrowersEvents (:123-131) builds borrower_added/borrower_removed from case_borrowers audit rows, and borrowersEvents (:133-137) explicitly returns [] for non-UPDATE actions with the comment 'INSERT/DELETE are covered by the case_borrowers link events above'. But migration 014_fix_case_borrowers_audit.sql:10 DROPs trg_audit_case_borrowers (the junction has a composite PK, no `id`, so the audit function couldn't log it) and it was never re-added. So no case_borrowers audit rows are ever produced: the entire `case 'case_borrowers'` branch (eventsFromEntry:73-74) and caseBorrowersEvents are dead code, AND borrowersEvents skipping INSERT/DELETE means attaching a brand-new borrower (borrowers INSERT) or detaching one also yields nothing. listAuditEntriesForCase doesn't even scan the case_borrowers table (audit.service.ts:159-172 has no case_borrowers target).
- **Why it matters:** Adding or removing a borrower from a case is a meaningful, audit-worthy change that the timeline claims to surface (the borrower_added/borrower_removed event kinds exist in types.ts:44-45 and the i18n templates). In practice these lines never appear, so a borrower being added or dropped from a case leaves no trace in the activity feed.
- **Suggested fix:** Decide the source of truth: either (a) re-introduce auditing for case_borrowers by adding a surrogate `id UUID` PK (the mig 014 note lists this as the simple option) so the existing caseBorrowersEvents path activates, or (b) drop the dead case_borrowers branch + caseBorrowersEvents and instead emit borrower_added/borrower_removed from the borrowers INSERT/DELETE audit rows (relax borrowersEvents:135 to handle INSERT/DELETE). Note option (b) misses the 'returning client attached to a new case' path (existing borrower, no borrowers INSERT) -- which is exactly why the code chose the link row -- so (a) is the more correct fix. Add a test asserting a borrower attach/detach yields an event.
- **Verify:** The observable symptom is REAL: adding/removing a borrower produces no line on the case activity ("פעילות") timeline. But the finding's stated ROOT CAUSE is materially WRONG.

WRONG part: The finding claims "trg_audit_case_borrowers was dropped (mig 014) and never re-added, so no case_borrowers audit rows are ever produced." That is false. supabase/migrations/022_security_hardening.sql Section 1 (lines 16-20) adds the surrogate `id UUID NOT NULL DEFAULT gen_random_uuid()` column + unique index to case_borrowers, and Section 5 (lines 170-173) re-creates `trg_audit_case_borrowers` AFTER INSERT OR UPDATE OR DELETE -> audit_log_change(). The rewritten audit_log_change (022:105/140) reads NEW.id/OLD.id, which now exists. Mig 022's header explicitly references finding #40 and mig 014. So case_borrowers audit rows ARE written to audit_log. The finding's suggested fix (a) "add a surrogate id" is already done.

CORRECT part (the actual root cause): listAuditEntriesForCase (src/features/audit/services/audit.service.ts:159-172) builds a `targets` array of tables to scan in audit_log — cases, borrowers, borrower_incomes, borrower_obligations, case_banks, documents, tasks, optional case_financials — with NO case_borrowers target. The case_borrowers query at line 123 only selects borrower_id (to enumerate borrowers); it never scans audit_log for table_name='case_borrowers'. So those audit rows exist but are never fetched into the case timeline. The feed path listCaseActivity -> listAuditEntriesForCase -> deriveAuditEvents (case-activity.service.ts:37,44) therefore never passes a case_borrowers entry to caseBorrowersEvents (derive-audit-events.ts:74,123-131), making that branch dead in this code path, while borrowersEvents (135) deliberately returns [] for INSERT/DELETE. borrower_added/borrower_removed kinds (types.ts:44-45, rendered in activity-event-line.tsx) thus never appear. Confirmed mig 012:94 also audits the `borrowers` table (INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE), so option (b) is feasible but misses the returning-client path, as the finding notes.

SEVERITY downgraded Medium->Low: the data is NOT lost — case_borrowers audit rows are captured in audit_log and are visible system-wide via /audit-log (listAuditEntries, audit.service.ts:76, no table filter). The defect is purely that the per-case activity tab omits attach/detach lines (an observability/UX completeness gap), not a security, authz, data-integrity, or correctness bug. The actual minimal fix differs from the finding's: add a {table:'case_borrowers', ids:<surrogate ids>} target in listAuditEntriesForCase (which currently doesn't even fetch the surrogate id), not "re-introduce the trigger." Real but lower-impact and mis-diagnosed.

#### `ACT-3` — SOFT_DELETE / RESTORE rows render as raw English tokens with empty detail in the full-log tab (RTL/i18n + readability)
- **File:** src/features/audit/components/audit-log-table.tsx:99-103, :136-143; messages/he.json auditLog.actions
- **Evidence:** actionLabel (audit-log-table.tsx:99-103) only translates insert/update/delete; for any other action it returns the raw string, so a SOFT_DELETE/RESTORE audit row shows the literal English token 'SOFT_DELETE' inside the Hebrew RTL audit table (the he.json auditLog.actions object has only keys insert/update/delete). ACTION_STYLE (:10-14) has no SOFT_DELETE/RESTORE entry so it falls back to neutral grey. Because the trigger writes no changed_fields for SOFT_DELETE, both entry.changes and entry.wholeRow are null, so ChangesCell (:143) renders t('values.empty'). The history 'full log' tab (history/page.tsx:78) therefore shows every soft-delete as a bare, untranslated, detail-less row.
- **Why it matters:** The full-log tab is the one place a manager can audit deletions, and it presents them as an untranslated English token with no detail in a Hebrew-primary RTL UI -- inconsistent and hard to read. Even after ACT-1 is fixed for the curated feed, the raw log still needs translated action labels.
- **Suggested fix:** Add auditLog.actions.soft_delete and auditLog.actions.restore to messages/he.json + en.json and extend actionLabel to map them (and add ACTION_STYLE entries, e.g. rose for soft_delete, emerald for restore). Combined with ACT-1's trigger change to capture a label on SOFT_DELETE, the changes cell would then show what was removed.
- **Verify:** Confirmed real, Low severity is correct. Verified against the actual code:

1) actionLabel (src/features/audit/components/audit-log-table.tsx:99-103) only maps insert/update/delete; any other action returns the raw string via `return action`. So a SOFT_DELETE/RESTORE row renders the literal uppercase English token. CONFIRMED.

2) ACTION_STYLE (audit-log-table.tsx:10-14) has only INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE; line 79 falls back to neutral grey for SOFT_DELETE/RESTORE. CONFIRMED.

3) messages/he.json (auditLog.actions, lines 1002-1006) and messages/en.json (lines 1002-1006) each have only insert/update/delete keys — no soft_delete/restore. CONFIRMED.

4) These rows do reach the history full-log tab: history/page.tsx:78 feeds activity.auditEntries to AuditLogTable, sourced from listAuditEntriesForCase (audit.service.ts:99-199), which queries audit_log for `cases` and child tables without filtering action. cases.deleted_at exists (006_cases.sql:27) and a soft-delete is an UPDATE setting deleted_at, which migration 045 (045_audit_trigger_id_fallback.sql:90-93) classifies as SOFT_DELETE. The parser filter (audit.service.ts:52) only drops empty UPDATEs, so SOFT_DELETE rows pass through. CONFIRMED.

5) The detail cell renders t('values.empty') for these rows. CONFIRMED — but the finding's stated MECHANISM is WRONG. The finding claims "the trigger writes no changed_fields for SOFT_DELETE." It actually does: the SOFT_DELETE path runs through the UPDATE branch (045:80-111) and computes the {field:{old,new}} diff, so changed_fields contains at minimum {deleted_at:{old:null,new:<ts>}}. The cell is empty because the CLIENT parser discards it: extractChanges returns null when action !== 'UPDATE' (audit-parser.ts:65) and extractWholeRow returns null when action is neither INSERT nor DELETE (audit-parser.ts:82), leaving both entry.changes and entry.wholeRow null → ChangesCell line 143.

This mechanism error means the finding's suggested fix is partly mis-aimed (it ties the populated cell to an ACT-1 trigger change, but the data already exists in changed_fields; the parser could surface it today by handling SOFT_DELETE/RESTORE). The observable defect — untranslated, un-styled English token with an empty detail cell in a Hebrew-primary RTL manager audit tab — is genuine. It is a readability/i18n polish issue, not functional or security, so Low is the right severity.

#### `STAT-1` — executed_fee_total / executed_expected_income_total use INNER JOIN to case_financials, silently dropping executed cases that have no financials row
- **File:** supabase/migrations/191_statistics_active_fee_total.sql:176-192 (also 187, 136, 135)
- **Evidence:** In get_statistics_summary, both 'executed_fee_total' (SELECT COALESCE(SUM(cf.fee_amount),0) FROM executed e JOIN public.case_financials cf ON cf.case_id = e.case_id) and 'executed_expected_income_total' use a plain INNER JOIN. case_financials is 1:1 with cases (PK = case_id, migration 025) but a row only exists if a fee/expected_income was ever entered (the create-case backfill in 025 only inserts WHERE fee_amount IS NOT NULL OR expected_income IS NOT NULL). An executed case whose financials row was never created contributes nothing — which is the correct numeric result (NULL fee = 0 contribution), so the total is right. The only nuance: 'active_fee_total' (lines 170-175) also uses INNER JOIN against the full active book, so it too excludes cases without a financials row; again the SUM is correct (those cases' fee is unknown/0). No data-loss, no over/under count of money — purely a readability note that these are INNER not LEFT joins.
- **Why it matters:** Not a bug today because every join target contributes 0 when absent and COALESCE wraps the SUM. Worth a one-line comment so a future edit that adds a COUNT or AVG over the same join (where INNER vs LEFT would change the denominator) doesn't silently inherit the filter.
- **Suggested fix:** Optional: leave as-is (numerically correct) or convert to LEFT JOIN public.case_financials for symmetry with the other sub-selects that scan cases directly; add a comment noting the join is intentionally an existence filter, not a row multiplier.
- **Verify:** Verified against the actual code. In supabase/migrations/191_statistics_active_fee_total.sql, all three financial sub-selects use plain INNER JOINs to case_financials: active_fee_total (lines 171-174), executed_fee_total (176-180), and executed_expected_income_total (188-191). The 1:1 relationship is confirmed in 025_case_financials_table.sql:20 (case_id is the PK FK to cases). A financials row can genuinely be absent: the 025 backfill inserts only WHERE fee_amount IS NOT NULL OR expected_income IS NOT NULL (025:32-36), and create-case.ts:63 calls upsert_case_financials only if fee_amount or expected_income is non-null — so a case created with no fee/income has no row.

The finding correctly concludes there is NO numeric bug today: each join target contributes either nothing (row absent) or a value that COALESCEs to 0 (nullable columns), and all three are pure COALESCE(SUM(...),0) money aggregations with no COUNT/AVG, so INNER vs LEFT produce identical totals. The downstream consumer (src/features/statistics/components/financial-summary.tsx:34) uses these only as money sums (netFee = executed_fee_total − executed_payout_total; tithe/fifth are fractions of net) — no denominator that would change under LEFT JOIN.

This is a legitimate, accurately-scoped readability/maintainability note, not a defect. The reviewer explicitly states 'No data-loss, no over/under count of money — purely a readability note,' rates it Low, and offers an optional/leave-as-is fix. The latent risk (a future COUNT/AVG over the same join silently inheriting the existence-filter) is real and the one-line-comment suggestion is reasonable. Could not refute it; the code does exhibit the described INNER-join existence-filter pattern and the characterization is precise. Low severity is correct — no current functional impact, so a higher severity would over-state it.

#### `STAT-2` — avg_cycle_days measures creation→execution but executed cases are matched by first execution entry within the window, so a case that bounced into execution in a prior period and re-entered in this period inflates the period average
- **File:** supabase/migrations/191_statistics_active_fee_total.sql:66-101
- **Evidence:** The 'executed' CTE selects MIN(sd.entered_at) but only over rows WHERE sd.entered_at >= v_from AND sd.entered_at < v_to. If a case entered 'execution' last month, bounced back, and re-entered execution this month, MIN over the windowed rows = this month's re-entry, so the case is counted as executed_in_period for this period AND its avg_cycle_days = (re-entry − created_at), a larger-than-real cycle time. The comment on lines 65-66 ('first entry in the window if it bounced') acknowledges this is the intended windowing rule. Because stage_durations inserts a fresh row on every status change (migration 009 trigger, lines 120-122/143-145), re-entry is possible. This is a definitional choice, not an arithmetic error: 'executed in this period' legitimately means 'entered execution during the window'.
- **Why it matters:** For a back-and-forth case the cycle-time KPI overstates duration and the case may be counted in two different periods' executed counts across the year. Given Kaufman's ~80-case book and that execution is near-terminal, the practical incidence is low, but the manager should know avg_cycle_days = creation→(first execution-entry in window), not creation→(first-ever execution).
- **Suggested fix:** If the intent is true first-time-to-execution, compute executed_at as the global MIN(entered_at) per case across all time and then filter that MIN into the window (so a case counts in exactly one period — its first-ever execution). Document whichever definition is chosen in the schema comment for executed_in_period / avg_cycle_days.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. In supabase/migrations/191_statistics_active_fee_total.sql:66-101, the `executed` CTE does `SELECT sd.case_id, MIN(sd.entered_at) AS executed_at FROM stage_durations sd JOIN es ... WHERE sd.entered_at >= v_from AND sd.entered_at < v_to GROUP BY sd.case_id` — the MIN is taken over WINDOWED rows only, so it yields the first execution-entry within the period, not the first-ever execution. Re-entry is structurally possible: the track_stage_duration() trigger in 009_tasks.sql:111-123 inserts a fresh stage_durations row on every status change (NEW.status_id IS DISTINCT FROM OLD.status_id) with NO uniqueness constraint on (case_id,status_id), so a case can have multiple execution-entry rows (the finding's cite of migration 009 lines 120-122/143-145 is accurate; the file is named 009_tasks.sql but does contain the stage_durations table+triggers). Both consequences are arithmetically sound: a case that entered execution in a prior period, bounced, and re-entered this period (a) is counted in executed_in_period for BOTH periods, and (b) gets avg_cycle_days = (re-entry − created_at), overstating true creation→first-execution. Both KPIs are surfaced to the manager-only stats dashboard (kpi-grid.tsx:52,64). Severity Low is correct, not over/understated: it is a definitional/labeling choice (the code comment 'first entry in the window if it bounced' shows it is intentional), incidence is low on Kaufman's ~80-case book given execution is near-terminal and the bounce must straddle a period boundary, and the suggested fix (global per-case MIN filtered into the window + a doc comment) is appropriate. Minor nuance: this windowing is verbatim identical to migration 187 (and traces to 135/136), so 191 inherited rather than introduced it — but the finding correctly cites 191 as the current live definition, which does not change the verdict.

#### `STAT-3` — Net fee, tithe and fifth are derived in the client component; payouts can exceed gross fee making net (and tithe/fifth) negative with no guard
- **File:** src/features/statistics/components/financial-summary.tsx:34-36
- **Evidence:** netFee = financial.executed_fee_total - financial.executed_payout_total; tithe = netFee * 0.1; fifth = netFee * 0.2. case_payouts.amount (migration 186) is an independent NUMERIC with no constraint tying it to the case fee, and executed_payout_total sums ALL non-deleted payouts for executed cases (191:183-187). If recorded payouts exceed the agreed fee for those cases, netFee goes negative and the displayed tithe/fifth become negative numbers. formatCurrency renders negatives fine (no crash), so this is a display-meaning issue, not a fault. Note also this is light business logic living in a 'use client' component rather than domain/ (CLAUDE.md 'dumb components' rule); it is trivial arithmetic but technically a calculation in JSX-adjacent code.
- **Why it matters:** A negative 'tithe to charity' figure is nonsensical to the manager and could be read as a data error. Low blast radius (manager-only, visual). Also a minor layering nit per the dumb-components rule.
- **Suggested fix:** Clamp at zero for the tithe/fifth derivations (e.g. const base = Math.max(netFee, 0)) or surface net explicitly when negative; consider moving the net/tithe/fifth computation into domain/metrics.ts to keep the component dumb and unit-testable.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code and all cross-references.

1) financial-summary.tsx:34-36 (a 'use client' component) derives netFee = financial.executed_fee_total - financial.executed_payout_total, tithe = netFee*0.1, fifth = netFee*0.2 — verbatim, with no clamp.

2) Migration 186_case_payouts.sql line 21: amount NUMERIC(15,2) with NO CHECK constraint tying it to the case fee. The write path confirms no fee-relative cap: payout.schema.ts bounds amount only by CURRENCY_MAX_ILS (per-field), update-payout-field.ts validates one field at a time, and there is no aggregate guard. So recorded payouts can independently exceed the agreed fee, per-row and in total.

3) Migration 191_statistics_active_fee_total.sql lines 183-187: executed_payout_total = SUM(cp.amount) over case_payouts joined to executed cases WHERE cp.deleted_at IS NULL — sums ALL non-deleted payouts, with no relation to executed_fee_total (lines 176-180). Therefore if payouts > fee, netFee (and the displayed tithe/fifth) go negative.

4) format-currency.ts: formats any finite number; negatives yield a valid negative string (no crash). So this is a display-meaning issue, not a fault — exactly as the reviewer stated.

5) Layering nit also holds: src/features/statistics/domain/metrics.ts exists and already houses pure derivations of this same nature (computeDelta, splitPipeline), yet the net/tithe/fifth arithmetic lives inline in JSX-adjacent client code, contrary to the CLAUDE.md dumb-components rule.

Severity Low is correct: manager-only (case_payouts and get_statistics_summary both gated by is_admin() RLS / EXCEPTION), visual-only, no crash, no security or data-integrity impact; only manifests on an unusual but plausible data-entry case. The suggested fix (clamp base = Math.max(netFee, 0) and/or move to domain/metrics.ts) is appropriate.

#### `STAT-4` — No bypass of the manager-only gate exists through the service or route — confirmed defense-in-depth (positive finding)
- **File:** src/features/statistics/services/statistics.service.ts:36-79; src/app/(app)/statistics/page.tsx:22-25; supabase/migrations/191_statistics_active_fee_total.sql:28-30
- **Evidence:** Three independent layers: (1) page redirects non-admins via isCurrentUserAdmin() before any RPC call (page.tsx:22-25); (2) both RPCs RAISE EXCEPTION USING ERRCODE='42501' when NOT public.is_admin() at the very top, before any data is read (191:28-30, 135:222-223); (3) GRANT EXECUTE only TO authenticated with REVOKE ALL FROM PUBLIC (191:199-200, 135:270-273). is_admin() itself (002_auth_core.sql:283-300) is SECURITY DEFINER checking auth.uid() against roles.key='admin' AND profiles.is_active. The service uses the request-scoped createClient() (server.ts, not a service-role client), so the RPC runs under the caller's auth — a non-admin call raises, is caught at service.ts:48-51, logged server-side, and returns null (never the raw Postgres message, satisfying the no-error.message-to-client rule). No code path calls the RPC with elevated privilege or skips is_admin().
- **Why it matters:** Documents that the manager-only invariant holds across service, route and DB; no action needed. Recorded so the verifier can confirm rather than re-derive.
- **Suggested fix:** None — gate is correct and layered. Keep the is_admin() check as the first statement in any future CREATE OR REPLACE of these functions (it is currently preserved across 135→136→187→191).
- **Verify:** Verified every claim against the code; all are accurate. This is a positive/no-defect finding documenting that the manager-only gate is correctly layered with no bypass.

(1) Page gate: src/app/(app)/statistics/page.tsx:22-25 calls isCurrentUserAdmin() and redirect('/cases') for non-admins before any RPC call. Confirmed.

(2) RPC gate: get_statistics_summary (191:28-30) and get_statistics_monthly_trend (135:222-224) both start with `IF NOT public.is_admin() THEN RAISE EXCEPTION 'not authorized' USING ERRCODE = '42501'` as the first statement, before any data read. I also confirmed the gate is preserved across the function's CREATE OR REPLACE chain: 136_statistics_custom_range.sql:30-31 and 187_statistics_net_fee.sql:29-31 carry the identical check. Confirmed.

(3) Grants: 191:199-200 and 135:270-273 do `REVOKE ALL ... FROM PUBLIC` + `GRANT EXECUTE ... TO authenticated`. Confirmed.

(4) is_admin(): 002_auth_core.sql:283-300 is SECURITY DEFINER (and STABLE), checking auth.uid() against profiles JOIN roles WHERE r.key='admin' AND p.is_active=TRUE. Confirmed (finding cited 283-300 exactly).

(5) Request-scoped client: src/lib/supabase/server.ts createClient() uses NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY + the caller's cookies (not a service-role key), so the RPC runs under the caller's auth — a non-admin call raises. The service (statistics.service.ts:48-51, 68-71) catches the error, logs server-side via console.error, and returns null / [] — never the raw Postgres message, satisfying the no-error.message-to-client rule. Confirmed.

(6) No bypass: grep shows the only TS consumers of getStatisticsSummary/getStatisticsMonthlyTrend are the gated page.tsx and the feature barrel index.ts; the only callers of the RPCs are the two service functions. No service-role/elevated client and no alternate route/action calls these RPCs. Confirmed.

The finding's description of the code is fully accurate and there is no defect. Severity kept at Low (effectively informational) to match the reviewer — it self-classifies as no-action/positive, with suggested fix 'None'. Not refuted: the described defensive posture genuinely exists exactly as stated.

#### `STAT-1` — FinancialSummary computes net/tithe/fifth business math inside the component (dumb-component violation)
- **File:** src/features/statistics/components/financial-summary.tsx:34-36
- **Evidence:** const netFee = financial.executed_fee_total - financial.executed_payout_total; const tithe = netFee * 0.1; const fifth = netFee * 0.2; -- these derived financial figures (net fee, 10% maaser, 20% chomesh) are calculated inline in the JSX component. There is no domain helper for them (grep confirms the 0.1/0.2 constants exist only here).
- **Why it matters:** CLAUDE.md is explicit: 'NO calculations inside components (compute in domain/ or via hook)' and lists 'Mixing UI and business logic in the same file' as an auto-reject anti-pattern. These are real domain rules (charity ratios on the executed net fee) that belong in src/features/statistics/domain/ where they can be unit-tested on boundary inputs (zero fee, payouts > fee producing a negative net, huge values). As written they are untested and duplicated if ever needed elsewhere (e.g. a PDF/export).
- **Suggested fix:** Move to a pure domain function, e.g. domain/financials.ts: `export function deriveCharity(executedFee: number, payout: number) { const net = executedFee - payout; return { net, tithe: net * 0.1, fifth: net * 0.2 }; }`, and have the component consume the result. Keep the component purely presentational.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading src/features/statistics/components/financial-summary.tsx. Lines 34-36 compute netFee = executed_fee_total - executed_payout_total, tithe = netFee * 0.1, fifth = netFee * 0.2 inline in the body of a 'use client' component, then render them at lines 71-73. These are real business/domain rules (net executed fee, 10% maaser, 20% chomesh charity ratios), not display formatting. CLAUDE.md explicitly forbids this: "NO calculations inside components (compute in domain/ or via hook)" and lists "Mixing UI and business logic in the same file" as an auto-reject anti-pattern. The statistics domain layer exists (src/features/statistics/domain/metrics.ts holds analogous pure derivations like computeDelta/splitPipeline) but has no financial helper — confirming the natural home is empty. Grep for the 0.1/0.2 constants and tithe/fifth shows the only computation site is this component (other hits are i18n labels in messages/*.json and docs/UI_FIXES_BACKLOG.md), so the reviewer's "constants exist only here" claim is accurate. Inputs are genuine schema fields (executed_payout_total in statistics.schema.ts:60, sourced from migrations 186/187/191). The finding is a true positive. I keep it Low, matching the reviewer: the math is trivial (one subtraction + two literal-constant multiplications), has no branching or edge-case correctness risk (negative net still computes correctly via the linear formula), is used in exactly one place, isn't currently duplicated, and carries no security/data-integrity/user-facing-correctness impact. The "would be duplicated in a future PDF export / untestable" rationale is hypothetical. It is a legitimate code-organization/dumb-component violation of an explicit project rule with negligible functional impact.

#### `ACT-1` — activity-event-line.tsx exceeds the 250-line component limit (313 lines)
- **File:** src/features/case-activity/components/activity-event-line.tsx:1-313
- **Evidence:** wc -l reports 313 lines. The file bundles the exported ActivityEventLine plus 6 sub-components (EventIcon, FromToPills, EmailSentDetail, FieldDiffs, EventDetail) and several mapping helpers (iconFor, toneFor, sentenceFor, subjectFor with per-kind switch statements).

The kind→icon/tone/sentence/subject mapping is also presentation-mapping logic that would read better extracted (it is effectively a small view-model layer living in the JSX file).
