CLAUDE.md (lines 88-93, 360) explicitly defines this as: "Components: max 250 lines", lists ">250 lines for components" under "God files" as an auto-reject anti-pattern, and states "Exceeding limit means SPLIT, not deferred." The file genuinely co-locates the exported ActivityEventLine plus several sub-components (EventIcon L142, FromToPills L146, EmailSentDetail L165, FieldDiffs L201, EventDetail L229) AND per-kind presentation-mapping helpers with switch statements (iconFor L54, toneFor L88, sentenceFor L107, subjectFor L122) plus the ENTITY_ICONS const (L42). These are pure view-model/presentation mapping that read better extracted, exactly as the finding describes; the suggested split is consistent with the feature's own discipline (sibling files case-activity-feed.tsx=81, case-history-tabs.tsx=75). No ESLint rule enforces or exempts the limit; it is the documented project standard. One minor reviewer inaccuracy: the finding says "6 sub-components" but only 5 distinct ones exist — the over-count does not affect the substance. Severity Low is correct: it is a real, mechanical violation of an explicit non-negotiable standard (genuinely actionable in review) but is purely a maintainability/style issue with no correctness, security, or runtime impact.

### Refuted (2)

- `STAT-5` Israel-TZ date-range math is correct across all preset and custom branches (positive finding) — STAT-5 is a self-declared POSITIVE finding ("Israel-TZ date-range math is correct... no remediation needed"), not a defect report. It describes no actionable problem, so is_real=false (there is no bug for the code to "exhibit") and severity is invalid (a Low severity label on a non-defect is meaningless). I verified every technical claim against the actual code and all check out:

Migration 191 (supabase/migrations/191_statistics_active_fee_total.sql):
- v_month_start (L33-36) uses the canonical double-timezone idiom: inner timezone('Asia/Jerusalem', now()) returns naive Jerusalem wall-clock timestamp, date_trunc('month',...) gives start-of-month, outer timezone('Asia/Jerusalem', ...) reinterprets the naive value AS Jerusalem-local timestamptz. Correct.
- this_month=[v_month_start, +1mo) (L55-56); last_month=[v_month_start-1mo, v_month_start) (L44-46); last_3_months=[v_month_start-2mo, v_month_start+1mo) = current+2 prior calendar months (L47-49); this_year anchored to date_trunc('year', Jerusalem now()) (L50-52). All correct half-open ranges.
- custom branch (L38-41) only fires on p_period='custom' AND both dates non-null AND p_from<=p_to, producing [from 00:00 JLM, (to+1) 00:00 JLM) — inclusive-day half-open. Bad ranges fall to the ELSE/this_month default.
- All window comparisons (sd.entered_at L71, created_at L84, converted_at L105) are timestamptz vs timestamptz — no implicit-tz hazard.
- avg_cycle_days (L94-101) is SQL ROUND(AVG(...)::numeric,1); AVG over the empty executed set returns NULL (not NaN).

Cross-references confirmed:
- schemas/statistics.schema.ts L45: avg_cycle_days is z.number().nullable().
- components/kpi-grid.tsx L64: renders '—' when avg_cycle_days===null.
- domain/metrics.ts L29: computeDelta guards previous===0 (returns pct null).
- lib/utils/format-currency.ts L23: formatCurrency returns '—' for null/undefined/!Number.isFinite.
- domain/period.ts L25-45: parseCustomRange validates ISO_DATE regex + UTC round-trip + rejects from>to (lexical compare valid for zero-padded ISO).
- services/statistics.service.ts L43-58: safeParse on RPC output, returns null on parse/error so no NaN/raw-message reaches UI.

The finding's claim that "there are currently no statistics tests" is also confirmed — Glob/Grep found zero test files under src/features/statistics or matching period/parseCustomRange/computeDelta/avg_cycle. The optional suggested fix (add a unit test pinning boundary instants) is reasonable but explicitly not required. No defect; nothing to remediate.
- `STAT-2` Chart data re-shaping done inline in client components rather than via a domain/presenter — The factual claims are accurate: monthly-trend-chart.tsx:26-30 maps trend→{month: formatMonthLabel(...), opened, executed} inline, and pipeline-funnel.tsx:28-33 maps pipeline→{key, name: statusName(...), count, color: status.color ?? FALLBACK_COLOR} inline; the heavy split (splitPipeline) and formatters (formatMonthLabel domain/period.ts:53, statusName domain/metrics.ts:47) are pure and live in domain/. However the finding mischaracterizes the project norm and is not a genuine problem. (1) The inline maps are NOT business logic, calculations, or data fetching — the three things CLAUDE.md's dumb-component rule actually forbids. They are pure adapter/key-renaming that binds already-computed domain values to recharts' dataKey contract, invoking domain helpers for every non-trivial part. (2) The finding's claim that 'the project keeps this presenter mapping out of JSX elsewhere' is directly contradicted by the codebase: sibling recharts components mix-chart.tsx:23 and payment-breakdown-chart.tsx:34-38 do the identical pattern (call pure domain helper sampleAnnualCurve, then inline-map to recharts rows, including a unit conversion agorotToNis and key-renaming — more shaping than the statistics components). This is the established, consistent convention, not a deviation. (3) The reviewer self-refutes: the suggested fix is explicitly 'Optional'/'Low priority' and concedes 'the current form is already using domain helpers for the non-trivial parts.' This is a stylistic preference contradicted by the codebase's own consistent practice, not a defect.


## Round 15 — simulator calc engine + persistence

**raw 13 -> confirmed 13 / refuted 0  (High 1, Medium 2, Low 10)**

### High (1)

#### `SIM-PERSIST-2` — Case mix simulator page renders the fully-editable autosaving workspace to view-only users (no can_edit_case UI gate)
- **File:** src/app/(app)/cases/[id]/simulators/mix/page.tsx:19,52-60
- **Evidence:** The page guards only `if (!(await userHasPermission('view_simulators'))) redirect('/cases')` (line 19) and then unconditionally mounts <MixWorkspace ... caseId={id} /> (52-60). MixWorkspace → MixCalculator wires useScenarioAutosave (mix-calculator.tsx:74-85) with NO read-only prop: title/money/track/conclusion inputs are always editable (mix-calculator.tsx:99-135) and silently autosave on a 1200ms debounce (use-scenario-autosave.ts:27,95-99). There is no save button to hide — the whole flow is implicit-save. Because the server RPC authorizes on can_view_case (see SIM-PERSIST-1), those autosaves SUCCEED for a view_all-but-not-edit user, so this is a C-036 edit-gate violation where the affordance does NOT fail at the server — it persists.
- **Why it matters:** C-036 requires that users who can view but not edit must not see edit/upload/delete affordances. Here a view-only user sees a live, mutating editor and any field change writes to the DB. Combined with SIM-PERSIST-1 it is the visible half of the same data-integrity hole; even after the RPC is hardened, the page would still show a non-functional editor that throws on save unless gated.
- **Suggested fix:** In the case simulators pages (mix + compare/scenario/tax under cases/[id]/simulators), compute canEdit = await can_edit_case(caseId) (via the existing userCanEditCase helper) and pass a readOnly flag down through MixWorkspace → MixCalculator that disables inputs, hides the '+' new-tab button, and skips wiring useScenarioAutosave when read-only. This mirrors the canEditCase gating already threaded through the case-detail page (R6 / contract C-036).
- **Verify:** Every link in the finding's chain is confirmed by the code.

1) Page has no edit gate: src/app/(app)/cases/[id]/simulators/mix/page.tsx line 19 guards only `userHasPermission('view_simulators')`, then unconditionally mounts <MixWorkspace ... caseId={id} primaryBorrowerId={...} /> (lines 52-60). No userCanEditCase/can_edit_case call anywhere in the file.

2) Editor is always editable + autosaving: MixWorkspace (mix-workspace.tsx) has no readOnly prop and always renders the '+' new-tab button (110-118) and an always-mounted MixCalculator (121-139). MixCalculator (mix-calculator.tsx) wires useScenarioAutosave unconditionally (74-85) and renders always-editable title/conclusion inputs (99-104, 130-134) plus MixInputsBar/TrackTable/BasketPresets with live onChange handlers. There is no explicit save button — useScenarioAutosave persists on a 1200ms debounce on any content change (use-scenario-autosave.ts:27, 92-99), so there is nothing to hide; the only gate would be not wiring it.

3) Server authorizes on can_view_case, NOT can_edit_case — so the autosaves SUCCEED for a view-only user. saveScenarioAction (save-scenario.ts:23) gates on `use_simulators` permission only. The save_mortgage_scenario RPC (mig 097) authorizes the INSERT path on `can_view_case(v_case_id)` (line 111) and the EDIT path on `can_view_case(s.case_id)` (line 61). RLS on mortgage_scenarios (mig 093, INSERT 95-105 / UPDATE 107-124) and scenario_tracks likewise gate on can_view_case. None reference can_edit_case.

4) can_view_case and can_edit_case genuinely diverge: can_view_case (mig 039:30-48) = view_all_cases OR (view_own_cases AND assigned) OR archived+view_archived_cases. can_edit_case (mig 147:81-101) = edit_any_case OR (edit_own_case AND (assigned OR associated)). A secretary/junior with view_all_cases but no edit_* on an unassigned case returns can_view_case=true, can_edit_case=false — exactly the C-036 persona. Such a user's field edits persist to a case they cannot edit.

5) C-036 precedent is real and consistently applied elsewhere but missing here: the case-detail page (cases/[id]/page.tsx:70,86,94-95,186,194,203,229,254,300) computes canEditCase via userCanEditCase and threads it through every edit affordance; sub-routes borrowers/new and borrowers/[borrowerId]/edit even hard-block with notFound() when !userCanEditCase. The userCanEditCase helper the suggested fix names exists at src/lib/auth/permissions.ts:102.

Severity: confirmed High. Unlike the R6 case-detail gap (rated Medium because those affordances failed at the server), here the unauthorized writes SUCCEED and persist — an actual data-integrity/authorization breach, not just a non-functional affordance. Minor caveat (does not reduce severity or is_real): the suggested-fix footnote also lists compare/scenario/tax siblings, but those mount MixComparison/ScenarioCalculator without a caseId/autosave (compare/page.tsx:43, scenario/page.tsx:38 pass no caseId), so they don't persist; the persisting bug is specifically the mix page, which the finding's title and primary evidence scope correctly.

### Medium (2)

#### `SIM-MATH-1` — Partial-ownership purchase tax pro-rates the property value into lower brackets, drastically understating tax (wrong under Israeli law)
- **File:** src/features/simulators/domain/purchase-tax.ts:37 (+ test fixture purchase-tax.test.ts:19-21, caller tax-costs-calculator.tsx:75)
- **Evidence:** calculatePurchaseTax computes `taxableValue = roundAgorot(Math.max(0, propertyValue) * (ownershipSharePct / 100))` then runs the FULL static brackets against that reduced value. The co-located test encodes the result as correct: `calculatePurchaseTax(3_500_000, brackets, 50).totalTax` is asserted toBe 0 — a 3.5M property at 50% ownership yields 1.75M, which falls entirely in the 0% bracket, so the buyer's purchase tax comes out as zero. Under מס רכישה the bracket thresholds are determined by the FULL transaction value; a partial buyer pays their share of the tax computed on the whole property, not the tax on a shrunken value. The real production brackets (tax-costs-calculator.tsx:47-53, single-home 0% up to ~1.98M) make this severe: any partial-ownership purchase below the full-value first bracket is reported as tax-free, and partial shares of expensive homes are pushed down into 0%/3.5% bands that wouldn't apply. Advisors quote this number to clients.
- **Why it matters:** This is the office's purchase-tax estimate shown to clients and (per report-data.service) potentially in generated PDFs. A materially-too-low purchase tax mis-states cash-to-close and financing gap, which feeds an affordability decision worth tens of thousands of shekels. The test fixture actively cements the wrong behavior, so it will never be caught by the suite.
- **Suggested fix:** Compute tax on the full property value first, then apply the ownership share to the resulting tax (and to each bracket row for the breakdown): keep brackets keyed to `Math.max(0, propertyValue)`, then multiply `taxAmount`/`taxableAmount` by `ownershipSharePct/100` per row and on the total. Update the purchase-tax.test.ts partial-ownership expectation accordingly (50% of the full-value tax, i.e. 30,000 for the test brackets, not 0). Also clamp `ownershipSharePct` to (0,100] in the domain function — a share >100 currently inflates the taxable base above the property value, and tax-costs-calculator setNumber only clamps the lower bound (Math.max(0, parsed)), not the upper.
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED at the code level. purchase-tax.ts:37 computes taxableValue = Math.max(0, propertyValue) * (ownershipSharePct/100) and then runs the FULL progressive brackets (calculateBracketTax, lines 42-46) against that reduced value. Under Israeli מס רכישה, bracket thresholds are keyed to the full transaction value and a partial buyer pays their share of the full-property tax, not the tax on a shrunken value, so this systematically understates tax and pushes partial shares into 0%/3.5% bands. The co-located test cements the wrong result: purchase-tax.test.ts:19-21 asserts calculatePurchaseTax(3_500_000, brackets, 50).totalTax toBe(0) (1.75M lands entirely in the 0% bracket), when the correct value is 30,000 = half of the 60,000 full-value tax the sibling test on line 15 already establishes. Production brackets in tax-costs-calculator.tsx:47-53 (single-home 0% up to 1,978,745) make any partial purchase pro-rating below ~1.98M report as tax-free. The clamp gap is also real: setNumber (line 95) does only Math.max(0, parsed) with no upper bound, and the domain fn does not clamp ownershipSharePct, so a share >100 inflates the base above property value. The suggested fix (key brackets to the full value, multiply taxAmount/taxableAmount per row and the total by share/100, clamp share to (0,100]) is the correct Israeli-law treatment.\n\nSEVERITY DOWNGRADED High -> Medium. The finding's claim that this is 'potentially in generated PDFs (per report-data.service)' is NOT substantiated: report-data.service.ts (read in full) never imports or calls calculatePurchaseTax; it maps mix-scenario loan/track fields and re-runs aggregateMix for the ReportDocument. The purchase-tax output flows ONLY to the on-screen TaxCostsCalculator summary card + breakdown on /simulators/tax and /cases/[id]/simulators/tax (both gated on view_simulators). It is an ephemeral scratchpad, not persisted in a saved scenario and not in the client PDF. The bug also only triggers on the non-default partial-ownership path (default ownershipSharePct=100; the in-case page at cases/[id]/simulators/tax/page.tsx:31-36 does not even seed the share). Genuinely-wrong advisor-facing math that misstates cash-to-close warrants a fix, but the scoped, non-persisted, non-PDF, non-default-path blast radius is Medium, not High.

#### `SIM-PERSIST-1` — Case-scoped scenario save/edit/delete authorizes on can_view_case, not can_edit_case — view-only users can write into a case
- **File:** supabase/migrations/096_save_mortgage_scenario_rpc.sql:30-32, supabase/migrations/097_edit_mortgage_scenario_rpc.sql:53-65,111-113, supabase/migrations/093_mortgage_scenarios.sql:94-124 (insert/update policies) + 190-229 (soft_delete_scenario:204-213)
- **Evidence:** Every case-scoped write path gates on public.can_view_case(case_id). save_mortgage_scenario INSERT (096:30) and EDIT (097:61) authorize with `s.case_id IS NOT NULL AND public.can_view_case(s.case_id)`; soft_delete_scenario (093:212) uses the same; the mortgage_scenarios/scenario_tracks INSERT+UPDATE RLS policies (093:103,115,154,172,184) also use can_view_case. can_view_case (migration 147:57-78) is satisfied by has_permission('view_all_cases') — a READ permission. The BASE PROJECT INVARIANT requires case-scoped writes to canonicalize on public.can_edit_case (the edit-permission helper, 147:81-101). Net effect: a user with use_simulators + view_all_cases but NO edit_any_case / edit_own_case (e.g. the documented secretary persona: view_all on an unassigned case, no edit) can create, edit, and soft-delete mortgage scenarios + tracks inside ANY case they can only view. The 097 header comment even claims a caller 'can't move or hijack another advisor's scenario', but the guard it uses (can_view_case) is exactly the read gate, so a view_all user passes it for every case.
- **Why it matters:** Direct authz gap: a view-only role can persist and delete case-attached financial simulations (which feed client-facing PDFs and the in-case total-DTI tile) in cases it has no edit authority over. This is real cross-permission write access, not just a UI affordance — the RPC commits the row. It also contradicts the canonical can_edit_case write rule used everywhere else in the app, so the simulator is the one feature that lets read-only personas mutate case data.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace public.can_view_case(...) with public.can_edit_case(...) in the case-scoped branches of: save_mortgage_scenario (096 INSERT guard, 097 EDIT + INSERT guards), soft_delete_scenario (093:212), and the mortgage_scenarios/scenario_tracks INSERT and UPDATE RLS WITH CHECK/USING clauses (093). Keep can_view_case only for SELECT policies (read). Standalone (case_id IS NULL) writes correctly stay owner-scoped (created_by = auth.uid()). Ship as a new forward migration that re-creates the three RPCs + the two write policies; SELECT policies unchanged.
- **Verify:** CONFIRMED in code. Every case-scoped scenario WRITE path gates on public.can_view_case, not can_edit_case:
- save_mortgage_scenario INSERT guard 096:30-32 (`v_case_id IS NOT NULL AND NOT public.can_view_case(v_case_id)`).
- 097 EDIT guard 097:59-62 (`s.case_id IS NOT NULL AND public.can_view_case(s.case_id)`) and 097 INSERT guard 097:111-113.
- soft_delete_scenario 093:210-213 (same can_view_case branch).
- The mortgage_scenarios INSERT/UPDATE WITH CHECK (093:103, 115, 123) and scenario_tracks INSERT/UPDATE WITH CHECK (093:154-157, 184-186) all use can_view_case for writes.

Helper semantics verified in 147 (the file is 147_associated_advisor_case_access.sql, not the name cited, but content matches): can_view_case (147:64-77) is satisfied by has_permission('view_all_cases') — a pure read perm; can_edit_case (147:88-100) requires edit_any_case OR (edit_own_case AND responsible/associated advisor). They are genuinely different gates, so a view-only actor passes the write guard.

Strongest corroboration: the SAME simulator feature's sibling tables bank_offers/bank_offer_tracks (106:370-435) correctly gate SELECT on can_view_case but INSERT/UPDATE WITH CHECK on can_edit_case — proving the project convention and that the scenario write paths deviate from it. No TS compensating control: saveScenarioAction (src/features/simulators/actions/save-scenario.ts) and deleteScenarioAction only check use_simulators, delegating case authz entirely to the RPC. The 097 header comment claiming a caller 'can't move or hijack another advisor's scenario' is contradicted — a view_all user passes can_view_case for every case.

Severity lowered High->Medium: the gap is not reachable by any DEFAULT-seeded user (004_lookups_seed: senior_advisor has edit_any_case so edit==view; junior_advisor lacks view_all_cases so view==edit scope; secretary has view_all_cases+edit_own_case but is NOT granted use_simulators by 095). Exploitation requires a deliberate (but fully supported) admin configuration: grant use_simulators to a view_all_cases role lacking edit_any_case (the secretary is one toggle away). Real authz/invariant violation with bounded, feature-niche impact and a config precondition — solidly Medium. Suggested fix (swap can_view_case->can_edit_case in the three RPC case-scoped branches + the four scenario write policies; leave SELECT and case_id IS NULL owner-scoped paths) is correct and surgical.

Relevant files (absolute): C:\Users\shh92\Projects\first-crm\supabase\migrations\096_save_mortgage_scenario_rpc.sql; ...\097_edit_mortgage_scenario_rpc.sql; ...\093_mortgage_scenarios.sql; ...\147_associated_advisor_case_access.sql; ...\106_simulator_market_data_foundation.sql (bank_offers contrast); ...\095_simulator_permissions.sql; ...\004_lookups_seed.sql; C:\Users\shh92\Projects\first-crm\src\features\simulators\actions\save-scenario.ts; ...\delete-scenario.ts

### Low (10)

#### `AMORT-1` — Live mix calculator computes on raw, un-Zod-validated React state — degenerate term=0 yields an empty/zero schedule with no user signal
- **File:** src/features/simulators/hooks/use-mix-calculator.ts:79 (with src/features/simulators/components/track-table.tsx:67 and mix-inputs-bar.tsx:38)
- **Evidence:** The live workspace runs `useMemo(() => aggregateMix(mix), [mix])` directly on controlled-input state, bypassing `ScenarioTrackSchema`/`MixInputSchema` (those only gate the save action and the PDF re-aggregation). The term inputs use raw `Number(e.target.value)` (track-table.tsx:67, mix-inputs-bar.tsx:38). Clearing a term field produces `Number('') === 0`; the schedule loops `month <= termMonths` so it emits ZERO rows, making firstPayment/totalCost = 0 and all curves empty. I reproduced this: buildSpitzer with termMonths:0 returns rows.length === 0. The money fields are safe (`nisToAgorot` floors non-finite to 0), and `type=number` browsers coerce bad text to '' (so NaN can't actually reach the domain via the UI), so this is data-quality, not a crash.
- **Why it matters:** A momentarily-empty term field silently zeroes the whole simulation (₪0 payment, blank charts) with no validation message, which is confusing mid-edit. It is not a security or data-loss issue and the save path is Zod-guarded, so blast radius is the live preview only.
- **Suggested fix:** Clamp term/rate inputs at the onChange boundary the way money already is — e.g. wrap term in a `toPositiveInt(value, fallback)` util (mirroring `nisToAgorot`'s `Number.isFinite` guard) so an empty/invalid field falls back to the prior value or 1 rather than 0. Optionally have the hook coalesce `termMonths < 1` to a sane default before aggregating.
- **Verify:** Every technical claim is substantiated by the code.

1. Live calc bypasses Zod: use-mix-calculator.ts:79 runs `useMemo(() => aggregateMix(mix), [mix])` directly on the raw useState `mix` (line 78), never through MixInputSchema/ScenarioTrackSchema. Those schemas only gate the save action (SaveScenarioSchema.mix in simulator.schema.ts:75-105, where termMonths is `z.coerce.number().int().min(1).max(480)` at lines 61 and 79) and the PDF re-aggregation.

2. Raw Number() on term inputs: track-table.tsx:67 `onUpdate(track.id, { termMonths: Number(e.target.value) })` and mix-inputs-bar.tsx:38 `onTermChange(Number(e.target.value))`. Number('') === 0.

3. term=0 yields zero rows: amortization-spitzer.ts:13 loops `for (let month = 1; month <= track.termMonths && balance > 0; ...)` — with termMonths=0, `1 <= 0` is false so the loop never runs and rows.length === 0. summarizeTrack (track-summary.ts:16-22) then returns firstPayment = payments[0] ?? 0 = 0 and totalCost = sumMoney([]) = 0; aggregateMix's maxMonths = Math.max(0, ...[]) = 0 (mix-aggregate.ts:21) so every curve is empty -> blank charts, 0 payment. Reproduction claim confirmed by construction.

4. Money fields are safe: format.ts:13-16 nisToAgorot uses `Number.isFinite(parsed) ? Math.max(0, Math.round(...)) : 0`, so cleared money fields floor to 0 without producing NaN.

5. Severity is correctly Low. No crash (empty arrays are handled with `?? 0` everywhere), no data loss (save path Zod-rejects term<1), no security impact. The blast radius is purely the transient live preview: a momentarily-cleared/zeroed term field silently zeros the simulation with no validation message. The reviewer even acknowledged the mitigations (money safe, type=number prevents NaN reaching the domain). Note the track-level term input (track-table.tsx:67) has NO min attribute, unlike mix-inputs-bar.tsx:38 / loan-base-panel.tsx:41 (min={1} max={480}); regardless, an HTML min attribute does not block reading '' on clear or typing 0, so both paths exhibit the issue. Confirmed real, correctly rated Low.

#### `AMORT-2` — Pure domain has no defensive guard against NaN/Infinity inputs — a non-finite rate produces a 1-row schedule with a NaN balance
- **File:** src/features/simulators/domain/payment.ts:11-13 and amortization-spitzer.ts:13-20
- **Evidence:** If `rate` is NaN, `spitzerPayment` returns NaN, `closeMonth` yields `closingBalance: NaN`, and the loop guard `balance > 0` becomes `NaN > 0 === false`, so the schedule terminates after exactly one row with a NaN balance (reproduced: buildSpitzer with annualRatePct:NaN → rows.length 1, lastClosing NaN). The schema (`pct = z.coerce.number().min(-20).max(100)`, simulator.schema.ts:50-53) DOES reject NaN and Infinity (verified: both `safeParse` return success:false because NaN/Infinity fail the .min/.max comparisons), and the UI can't inject NaN, so no current caller triggers this. It is purely a missing belt-and-suspenders in the pure layer.
- **Why it matters:** The round invariant asks that calculations be correct on boundary inputs (NaN/Infinity). Today every caller happens to sanitize first, so this is latent rather than live — but a future caller that forwards a raw value would get a silently-truncated, NaN-poisoned schedule instead of a thrown error or clean empty result.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a single guard at the top of each `build*Schedule` (or inside `monthlyRate`) returning `[]` when `!Number.isFinite(rate)` / amount / term are non-finite, so the contract is 'garbage in → empty schedule' rather than 'garbage in → 1 NaN row'. Cheap and keeps the domain self-defending.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code and running a throwaway vitest. payment.ts:11-13 (spitzerPayment) does (balance*rate*factor)/(factor-1) with no finite-rate guard; amortization-spitzer.ts:13-21 loops while `balance > 0`. With annualRatePct=NaN, monthlyRate(rate.ts:7-9, no guard) yields NaN, spitzerPayment returns NaN, and the loop guard `NaN > 0 === false` terminates after exactly one row. Empirically: buildSpitzerSchedule({...annualRatePct:NaN}) -> rows.length=1, in-loop balance NaN (stored fields round to null via roundAgorot; same substance: a single truncated/poisoned row). Infinity behaves the same. The schema claim is also accurate: ScenarioTrackSchema (simulator.schema.ts:50-53, pct = z.coerce.number().min(-20).max(100)) safeParse returns success:false for both NaN and Infinity (verified), because NaN/Infinity fail the .min/.max comparisons. So this is genuinely latent: no live caller injects NaN. One nuance the reviewer slightly mis-stated: the live calc path (aggregateMix(mix) in use-mix-calculator.ts) runs on RAW client state inside useMemo, NOT schema-validated data — the schema only guards the save path (save-scenario.ts). The live mix path is actually protected by type=number browser coercion (Number("") -> 0 in track-table.tsx:61, which has no Number.isFinite guard, unlike affordability-calculator.tsx:106 which does). This refines but does not refute: the pure domain truly lacks the belt-and-suspenders guard, the consequence (1-row NaN/null schedule instead of throw or empty) is accurate, line citations are correct, and Low severity is appropriate for a latent defensive-coding gap.

#### `AMORT-3` — Eligibility effective rate is capped at 3% but has no lower floor — a low entered eligibility rate produces a negative effective rate
- **File:** src/features/simulators/domain/rate.ts:21-24
- **Evidence:** `effectiveAnnualRatePct` returns `Math.min(track.annualRatePct - 0.5, 3)` for eligibility tracks. There is no `Math.max(0, ...)` floor, so an entered eligibility rate of e.g. 0.3% yields -0.2% (verified). The `pct` schema floor is -20, so this passes validation. The amortization then computes negative interest. The two tested cases (4.2→3, 2.8→2.3) are correct and pass.
- **Why it matters:** Israeli eligibility-track (זכאות) rates are regulated and bounded below by the government rate; a negative effective rate is not a realistic mortgage and would understate true cost in the comparison. Practical impact is small because real eligibility rates entered by an advisor sit well above 0.5%, so it's an unlikely-input quality gap rather than a live miscalculation.
- **Suggested fix:** Floor the eligibility result, e.g. `Math.max(0, Math.min(annualRatePct - ELIGIBILITY_DISCOUNT_PCT, ELIGIBILITY_MAX_RATE_PCT))`, and add a fixture asserting a sub-discount input clamps to 0 rather than going negative.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. src/features/simulators/domain/rate.ts:21-22 returns `Math.min(track.annualRatePct - ELIGIBILITY_DISCOUNT_PCT, ELIGIBILITY_MAX_RATE_PCT)` for eligibility tracks with no lower floor. constants.ts:5-6 sets ELIGIBILITY_DISCOUNT_PCT=0.5 and ELIGIBILITY_MAX_RATE_PCT=3, so an entered rate of 0.3% yields Math.min(-0.2, 3) = -0.2% (negative). The schema gate does not prevent this: simulator.schema.ts:50-53 defines `pct = z.coerce.number().min(-20).max(100)`, applied to annualRatePct at line 61, so 0.3% (and even negative values down to -20) pass validation. The negative effective rate flows downstream unguarded: amortization-spitzer.ts:10 and amortization-equal-principal.ts:10 both compute `monthlyRate(effectiveAnnualRatePct(track))`, then line 16 `interest = roundAgorot(indexed.balance * rate)` produces negative interest. The balloon path routes through the same buildTrackSchedule dispatcher (track-payment.ts). No clamping exists in track-factory.ts, the hooks, or anywhere upstream. The test file rate.test.ts:27-30 covers only 4.2->3 and 2.8->2.3 (both correct), with no fixture for a sub-discount input, exactly as stated. Severity Low is accurate: real Israeli eligibility (זכאות) rates entered by an advisor sit well above the 0.5% discount, so this is an unlikely-input quality gap producing an unrealistic negative-rate amortization rather than a live miscalculation on plausible inputs. The suggested fix (wrap in Math.max(0, ...) and add a clamping fixture) is correct and well-scoped.

#### `AMORT-4` — No co-located test for curve-sampling, the partial-final-year branch, or CPI-indexed amortization reaching zero
- **File:** src/features/simulators/domain/curve-sampling.ts:9-11 (no curve-sampling.test.ts exists) and amortization-spitzer.test.ts
- **Evidence:** `sampleAnnualCurve` filters `point.monthIndex % 12 === 0 || point.monthIndex === curve.length`; the second clause captures the final stub of a non-12-multiple term. I verified by hand it is correct (350-month curve → 30 points ending year 30; 6-month curve → single year-1 point), but there is no test pinning this behavior, and the `=== curve.length` branch is non-obvious (it relies on the curve being 1-based and dense, which mix-aggregate.ts:58 guarantees). Separately, the Spitzer/equal-principal/balloon tests only cover the non-indexed (`cpiAnnualPct: null`) path; I confirmed CPI-indexed schedules still reach closingBalance 0 at term (even at 15% CPI / 0.5% rate where the balance balloons 6x mid-life), but no fixture guards that.
- **Why it matters:** These are the two areas most exposed to a future off-by-one regression (the partial-year boundary and the CPI negative-amortization-then-payoff path), and they're exactly the cases the round flags as off-by-one / boundary risks. They currently work; the gap is regression coverage, not a present bug.
- **Suggested fix:** Add curve-sampling.test.ts asserting the partial-final-year case (e.g. a 354- or 350-length curve and a 6-length curve), and add a CPI-linked fixture to amortization-spitzer.test.ts asserting `rows.at(-1).closingBalance === 0` and that totalIndexation > 0 for an indexed track.
- **Verify:** Verified against the code. (1) curve-sampling.ts:9-11 filters on `monthIndex % 12 === 0 || monthIndex === curve.length`; the second clause is the partial-final-year stub branch, and it depends on monthIndex being 1-based/dense, which mix-aggregate.ts:57-60 (`monthIndex: index + 1` over a contiguous Array.from) guarantees — exactly as described. (2) No curve-sampling.test.ts exists (Glob + Grep confirm); sampleAnnualCurve is only consumed in three render paths (mix-chart.tsx, pdf/report-page.tsx, payment-breakdown-chart.tsx) with zero direct test coverage. (3) Every test asserting `closingBalance === 0` (amortization-spitzer/balloon/equal-principal, monthly-payment, mix-state) uses a `cpiAnnualPct: null` fixture; no test asserts a CPI-indexed schedule reaches zero. (4) `totalIndexation` is asserted nowhere in the suite (Grep: no matches). The only CPI-indexed amortization tests are indirect (scenario-stress.test.ts:87 cpiAnnualPct:6 for risk; mix-compare.test.ts:53 cpiAnnualPct:2 for flexibility), neither of which checks payoff-to-zero or indexation totals. The finding is honestly scoped: it states the code currently works and the gap is regression coverage, not a present bug. Severity Low is correct — this is a missing-test observation, not a correctness defect.

#### `SIM-MATH-2` — Eligibility effective rate has no lower floor — can go negative when the entered rate is below the 0.5% discount
- **File:** src/features/simulators/domain/rate.ts:21-24
- **Evidence:** `effectiveAnnualRatePct` for an eligibility track returns `Math.min(track.annualRatePct - ELIGIBILITY_DISCOUNT_PCT, ELIGIBILITY_MAX_RATE_PCT)` (discount 0.5, cap 3). The schema allows `annualRatePct` down to -20 (`pct = z.coerce.number().min(-20)`), so an eligibility rate of e.g. 0.3% yields an effective -0.2% with no floor at 0. That negative rate flows into monthlyRate and into blendedEffectiveRatePct (mix-metrics.ts:18 Math.pow(1 + r/1200, 12)) and the amortization schedules, producing a loan that pays the borrower interest.
- **Why it matters:** Real eligibility (זכאות) rates are positive and the cap is the binding side, so this is an unlikely input, but the domain accepts it silently and would produce a nonsensical schedule. Low blast radius because typical inputs never trigger it.
- **Suggested fix:** Floor the eligibility effective rate at 0: `Math.max(0, Math.min(track.annualRatePct - ELIGIBILITY_DISCOUNT_PCT, ELIGIBILITY_MAX_RATE_PCT))`, or document why a sub-discount eligibility rate is impossible and tighten the schema for eligibility tracks.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. src/features/simulators/domain/rate.ts:21-22 returns Math.min(track.annualRatePct - ELIGIBILITY_DISCOUNT_PCT, ELIGIBILITY_MAX_RATE_PCT) for eligibility tracks with no lower floor. constants.ts:5-6 set discount=0.5 and cap=3. schemas/simulator.schema.ts:50-53 define pct = z.coerce.number().min(-20).max(100), applied to annualRatePct at line 60; the only superRefines (lines 66-73) cover CPI-on-linked and grace-on-balloon, so there is NO eligibility-specific tightening — an eligibility track with annualRatePct=0.3 validates and yields effective -0.2%. That negative rate propagates: (1) into blendedEffectiveRatePct (mix-metrics.ts:18 Math.pow(1 + effectiveAnnualRatePct/1200, 12)), and (2) into all three amortization builders via monthlyRate(effectiveAnnualRatePct(track)) — amortization-spitzer.ts:10/16, amortization-equal-principal.ts:10/16, amortization-balloon.ts:10/16 — each computing interest = roundAgorot(indexed.balance * rate), which goes negative (loan pays the borrower). spitzerPayment (payment.ts:5-14) follows the rate!==0 branch with a negative rate, distorting the payment. A grep for Math.max(0,...)/floor/clamp on the rate path found no guard on the rate or interest (the existing clamps are on principal, equity, indexation, costs — unrelated). Severity Low is correct: real Israeli eligibility (זכאות) rates are positive and the cap is the binding constraint, so a sub-0.5% input is economically implausible; blast radius is minimal but the domain accepts it silently and produces a nonsensical schedule, so it is a genuine defect. Suggested fix (floor at 0 via Math.max(0, ...) or tighten the eligibility schema) is appropriate.

#### `SIM-MATH-3` — mixDti receives a stressPayment it never surfaces — dead parameter despite the doc claiming a stress figure
- **File:** src/features/simulators/domain/mix-dti.ts:21-38
- **Evidence:** The function doc says it uses "the peak monthly payment as the stress figure" and the caller passes `stressPayment`, which is forwarded to calculateDtiScenario as `stressMortgagePayment`. But the returned MixDti only contains `totalDtiPct` (from the first payment) and `level`; `result.stressTotalDebtToIncomePct` is computed inside calculateDtiScenario and then discarded. The stressPayment input has no effect on the output.
- **Why it matters:** Not a math error, but misleading: callers may believe the KPI reflects stress, and the wasted parameter invites a future bug when someone wires the stress payment expecting it to matter. The mix-dti.test.ts cases pass identical-ratio data so the dead path is invisible.
- **Suggested fix:** Either include `stressDtiPct` in the MixDti result (surfacing result.stressTotalDebtToIncomePct) and let the level reflect stress, or drop the stressPayment parameter and the stress wording from the doc. Add a test asserting stress is reflected if you keep it.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading the code. mix-dti.ts:21-38: mixDti accepts `stressPayment` (line 23) and forwards it to calculateDtiScenario as `stressMortgagePayment` (line 32). In dti.ts, that input is used ONLY to compute `stressTotalDebtToIncomePct` (lines 28, 35); `riskLevel` is derived from `totalDebtToIncomePct` of the first payment, not stress (lines 36, 48-52). mixDti then returns only `{ totalDtiPct: result.totalDebtToIncomePct, level: result.riskLevel }` (line 37) and the MixDti interface (lines 9-13) has no stress field — so `result.stressTotalDebtToIncomePct` is computed and discarded. Since calculateDtiScenario is pure and the only field touched by stress is the one mixDti drops, changing stressPayment while holding firstPayment constant yields an identical output: the parameter is genuinely dead w.r.t. the result. The doc (lines 15-19) claims "the peak monthly payment as the stress figure," implying stress is part of the signal, which is misleading. The caller (mix-calculator.tsx:65-72) passes calc.result.maxPayment as stressPayment and consumes only dti.totalDtiPct/dti.level, so the value never surfaces in UI. The tests (mix-dti.test.ts) pass stressPayment values but never assert on stress, so the dead path is untested. Severity Low is correct and not overstated — the finding itself notes this is not a math error, just a dead parameter + misleading doc that invites a future bug. One minor wording imprecision in the finding ("identical-ratio data" — the tests actually pass differing stress values) does not affect the core claim that the dead path is invisible to the tests.

#### `R-MIX-1` — compareMixes throws on an empty input array (reduce with no initial value)
- **File:** src/features/simulators/domain/mix-compare.ts:61-67
- **Evidence:** minBy/maxBy both do `items.reduce((best, item) => ...)` with NO initial value. compareMixes calls minBy(rows,...)/maxBy(rows,...) where rows = inputs.map(...). If `inputs` is empty, `rows` is empty and `reduce` throws 'Reduce of empty array with no initial value'. compareMixes is exported as part of the feature public API (src/features/simulators/index.ts:2). The live caller (use-mix-comparison.ts) always seeds MIN_VARIANTS=2 and floors removeVariant at 2, so this is unreachable through the current UI, but the exported pure function is not defensive.
- **Why it matters:** A public domain function that throws on a legitimate edge input (empty list) is a latent crash for any future caller (a new screen, a test, an export path) that does not pre-guarantee a non-empty list. Aggregation helpers in this module (aggregateMix, composeMixByFamily) all handle the empty case gracefully; compareMixes is the lone outlier.
- **Suggested fix:** Guard at the top of compareMixes: `if (inputs.length === 0) return { rows: [], cheapestLabel: '', mostStableLabel: '', mostFlexibleLabel: '', riskiestLabel: '' };` (or have minBy/maxBy seed from items[0] and return undefined for empty). Add a unit test for compareMixes([]).
- **Verify:** Verified against the actual code. In src/features/simulators/domain/mix-compare.ts:61-67, minBy and maxBy both call items.reduce((best,item)=>...) with NO initial value. compareMixes (lines 31-34) feeds them rows = inputs.map(...) (line 28). With an empty inputs array, rows is [] and the first reduce (line 31) throws TypeError 'Reduce of empty array with no initial value' per the ECMAScript spec. compareMixes is exported as public API via index.ts:2, so any future caller can hit it. Confirmed unreachable through the current UI: use-mix-comparison.ts seeds 2 default variants (defaultVariants lines 136-151), removeVariant floors at MIN_VARIANTS=2 (line 106), and no path empties variants, so compareMixes(mixes) (line 73) always gets a 2-4 element array. The reviewer disclosed this caveat honestly. The 'lone outlier' point is accurate: inflexibleSharePct (lines 54-58) reduces WITH an initial value 0 and is empty-safe. mix-compare.test.ts has only two tests, both 2-element arrays, none covering compareMixes([]). All claims substantiated; Low severity is correct because the throw is a latent robustness defect in a pure exported function with zero current runtime impact. Nothing over- or under-stated.

#### `R-MIX-2` — peakMonth seeds max at -1, so an all-negative curve would report month 0 instead of the true peak
- **File:** src/features/simulators/domain/mix-metrics.ts:25-35
- **Evidence:** peakMonth initializes `let max = -1` then only updates when `point.value > max`. For any curve whose every value is <= -1 (all-negative), no point ever exceeds the seed, so it returns month 0 (the 'empty' sentinel) rather than the index of the least-negative point. In practice the only curves passed in are payment/balance curves which are non-negative agorot, so this never triggers today; it is a robustness gap in a pure function, not a live bug.
- **Why it matters:** peakMonth backs MixResult.maxPaymentMonth. If a future curve type could hold negative values (e.g. a delta/savings curve), the reported peak month would silently be wrong. Seeding from the data rather than a magic -1 makes the function correct for any numeric curve.
- **Suggested fix:** Seed from negative infinity instead of -1: `let max = Number.NEGATIVE_INFINITY;` and keep the `month = 0` default for the genuinely empty curve (the loop already leaves month=0 when curve is empty). The existing tests (peak at month 2, ties→first, empty→0) still pass.
- **Verify:** Confirmed by reading src/features/simulators/domain/mix-metrics.ts:24-35. peakMonth seeds `let max = -1` and only updates `month` when `point.value > max` (lines 27-32). For any curve whose values are all <= -1, the `> -1` comparison never succeeds, so `month` stays at its initial 0 and the function returns 0 — the same sentinel used for the empty curve — instead of the least-negative point's index. The abstract logic flaw is real.

It is correctly characterized as a latent robustness gap, NOT a live bug. The only production call site is mix-aggregate.ts:33, `maxPaymentMonth: peakMonth(payments)`, where `payments` is built by aggregateMonthly (lines 52-61) as `sumMoney` over `track.rows[index].payment` — amortization payments produced by buildTrackSchedule (track-payment.ts → spitzer/equal-principal/balloon), which are non-negative agorot. peakMonth is never called on the balance/principal/interest curves either, only `payments`. So no curve passed in today can be all-negative; the bug cannot trigger in the current codebase.

The suggested fix (`let max = Number.NEGATIVE_INFINITY`) is correct: the empty-curve branch still returns 0 (loop never runs), the existing tests in mix-metrics.test.ts (peak at month 2; ties→first month 1 via strict `>`; empty→0) all still pass, and all-negative curves would then report the true peak. Severity Low is appropriate and not overstated — the reviewer accurately notes it never triggers today; it is a correctness improvement for a pure function against future curve types (e.g. a delta/savings curve), not a current defect.

#### `SIM-PERSIST-3` — use-mix-comparison.ts is 151 lines — one line over the 150-line hook file limit
- **File:** src/features/simulators/hooks/use-mix-comparison.ts:1-151
- **Evidence:** `wc -l` reports 151 lines. CLAUDE.md Engineering Standards: 'Hooks: max 150 lines → Exceeding limit means SPLIT'. The file carries the hook plus a module-level defaultVariants() factory (136-151) and the COMPARISON_LABELS/ComparisonVariant declarations.
- **Why it matters:** Marginal but it is a hard, stated file-size rule and an auto-reject criterion in this codebase. Trivial to bring back under the cap.
- **Suggested fix:** Move defaultVariants() (and optionally the DEFAULT_BASE / COMPARISON_LABELS constants) into a sibling module (e.g. ../utils/comparison-defaults.ts) and import them, bringing the hook file under 150 lines. The other three hooks are within limit (use-mix-calculator 133, use-scenario-calculator 104, use-scenario-autosave 102).
- **Verify:** Confirmed against the actual code. `wc -l C:/Users/shh92/Projects/first-crm/src/features/simulators/hooks/use-mix-comparison.ts` reports exactly 151 lines, one over the hard cap. CLAUDE.md "Engineering Standards (Non-Negotiable) > File Size Limits" states "Hooks: max **150 lines**" with "Exceeding limit means SPLIT, not deferred" (also an auto-reject "God files" anti-pattern). The file's structure matches the finding: the useMixComparison hook (lines 59-134) plus a module-level defaultVariants() factory (136-151), DEFAULT_BASE/COMPARISON_LABELS constants (17, 52-57), and ComparisonBase/ComparisonVariant type aliases (21-22). Cross-referenced peer-hook counts are also exact (use-mix-calculator 133, use-scenario-calculator 104, use-scenario-autosave 102 — only this file breaches). The suggested fix (extract defaultVariants/DEFAULT_BASE/COMPARISON_LABELS to a sibling util module) is sound and would drop the file to ~135 lines; these are self-contained with no hook-state dependencies. Could not refute. Severity Low is correctly calibrated: it is a genuine breach of a stated hard rule, but only by a single line with zero correctness/security/behavioral impact — purely a convention nit.

#### `SIM-PERSIST-4` — DEFAULT_REGULATORY_THRESHOLDS.minFixedPct (33.3333) disagrees with the DB column default (33.3334)
- **File:** src/features/simulators/constants.ts:31 vs supabase/migrations/094_simulator_settings.sql:9
- **Evidence:** constants.ts sets minFixedPct: 33.3333; migration 094 seeds the office_settings.regulatory_thresholds default as minFixedPct 33.3334. getRegulatoryThresholds() falls back to the TS constant when office_settings is unreadable/unparseable (settings.service.ts:17,21), so the same office can validate against 33.3333 (fallback) or 33.3334 (stored default) depending on the read path.
- **Why it matters:** Both sit on opposite sides of an exact one-third (33.3333…%) fixed split. regulatory-rules.ts:51 already adds a 0.01pp SHARE_TOLERANCE specifically to forgive this boundary, so it is currently masked — but the two source-of-truth values for the same constant should match to avoid a future regression if the tolerance changes.
- **Suggested fix:** Pick one canonical value (the domain comment in regulatory-rules.ts:46-48 references 33.3334 as the seeded value) and make constants.ts DEFAULT_REGULATORY_THRESHOLDS.minFixedPct match the migration default, or vice-versa.
- **Verify:** All four cited locations verified verbatim. constants.ts:31 sets DEFAULT_REGULATORY_THRESHOLDS.minFixedPct = 33.3333; migration 094_simulator_settings.sql:8 seeds the office_settings.regulatory_thresholds DEFAULT with minFixedPct = 33.3334. The two are genuinely different floats (the other shared value, maxPrimePct 66.6667, agrees in both — isolating minFixedPct as the sole disagreement). settings.service.ts:7-22 confirms getRegulatoryThresholds() falls back to the TS constant on read error (line 17) or parse failure (line 21), otherwise returns the stored value; RegulatoryThresholdsSchema.minFixedPct (simulator.schema.ts:89) is z.coerce.number().min(0).max(100) with NO transform/rounding, so the stored 33.3334 passes through verbatim. Therefore the same office can validate against 33.3333 (fallback) vs 33.3334 (stored) depending on read path — the dual-source-of-truth claim is accurate. Masking is also confirmed: regulatory-rules.ts:51 SHARE_TOLERANCE=0.01 with the check `actual < limit - SHARE_TOLERANCE` (line 61); the 0.0001pp gap between the two threshold values is far inside the 0.01pp tolerance, and a dedicated regression test (regulatory-rules.test.ts:74) exercises the 33.3334 case. So there is NO observable behavioral defect today — this is a latent single-source-of-truth/maintainability nit that would only regress if the tolerance were shrunk below ~0.0001pp. Adversarial refutation attempts failed (values are literally different; schema does not normalize), but the impact characterization (masked, no user impact) is correct. Low severity is accurate and arguably even generous given zero current user-facing effect.

# MASTER SUMMARY (rounds 9-15) — deduped by theme

**Raw confirmed:** 132 (9 High / 31 Medium / 92 Low) across 7 rounds. Many are the
same root issue found by multiple dimension reviewers / rounds; clustered below.
NO code was changed during this scan. STAT-4 is a POSITIVE finding (manager-only
statistics gate confirmed un-bypassable), not a bug.

Per-round: R9 27 (2H/7M/18L) · R10 26 (3H/7M/16L) · R11 16 (2H/3M/11L) ·
R12 15 (0H/3M/12L) · R13 24 (0H/8M/16L) · R14 11 (1H/1M/9L) · R15 13 (1H/2M/10L).

## Theme A — Legacy write-authz not canonicalized on can_edit_case (EXCLUDES associated advisors)  [the biggest cluster; several High]
The R8 fix (mig 190) canonicalized borrowers/incomes/obligations writes on
can_edit_case. The IDENTICAL legacy guard ("assigned_advisor_id = actor OR
edit_any_case") still gates writes in:
- case_banks RLS (mig 024)                     — R9 CB-authz-1 / R-cb-authz-1 [High]
- case_expenses RLS + soft_delete RPC (mig 081)— R9 CE-authz-1 / R-ce-authz-1 [High]
- documents insert/update RLS (mig 024)        — R10 R10-doc-1, R11 DRIVE-1 [High]
- documents storage case_docs RLS (mig 027)    — R10 DOC-UP-3 [Medium]
- documents delete RLS + RPC (mig 027/104)     — R10/R11 DRIVE-2 [Medium]
- task case-attachment storage PUT (case_docs) — R13 TASK-ATT-4 [Medium]
=> ONE migration ("mig 192") extending the R8 canonicalization closes ~6 findings.
Effect: an associated advisor legitimately on a case currently CAN'T add a bank /
expense / document / task file (silent RLS denial of a core flow).

   segment === documentId). The documents one is a real cross-case PII vector for a
   view_all user.
